O vos, tres chiers filz, je vos ai acomplit cest livre qui est li derriens de la science de medicine ensamble l’emplissement de lui, et ai fait la fin per ses expositions et par ses declarations.	I have completed this book, dear son, for you, which is the rear part of the science of medicine along with its filling, and I have brought it to an end through its explanations and declarations.
Et m’est venu en vision que je le vos acomplisse avec cest traitier, qui est partie de l’uevre de mains, c’est a savoir «cyrurgie».	And it came to me in a vision that I should complete this for you with this treatise, which is part of the work of hands, namely "surgery".
Et por ceu que l’uevre de mains est fortraite en nostre region et est etraingie dou tout en tout, si est perie li science et decopee, et n’est riens demorez de li fuers que les petites descriptions en livres des anciens que les mains ont muees.	And because the work of hands is hampered in our region and is entirely foreign everywhere, it is destroyed and dismantled, and nothing remains of its origin except for the small descriptions about ancient practices that have been changed.
Et de ceu est venue li error et li vanitez, et sont closes les ententions et est aloignie li science.	And from this comes error and vanity, and closed are the intentions and alienated is wisdom.
Or me semble que je la vuel vivifier ensamble l’ordination de cest traitier selonc la voie d’exposition et de declaration et de l’abreviation; et venrai ensamble les formes des ferremens de cautere, et des autres estrumens de l’uevre avec l’ajostement de la declaration et de preparation de li, sicom il est mestier.	It seems to me that I will revive it together with the arrangement of this treatise according to the way of exposition and declaration and abbreviation; and I shall come together with the forms of cautery irons, and other instruments of work with the addition of the declaration and preparation of them, as is necessary.
Et por la raison de ceu que nuls boins maistres de mains n’est trovez en nostre tens, est li ars de medicine eslongié.	And because no good master of hands is found in our times, the art of medicine has grown distant.
Et covient celui qui s’en entremet sormonter en la science d’anathomie, si com Galiens dit, tant qu’il saiche la juement des menbres, et les formes et les conjunctions et les separations d’aus, et aient connissance des osses et des nerf et des brais et le nombre d’ous, et le demenement et des voines movans et des reposans, et dou leu de lor issue.	And he who engages in this must master the science of anatomy, as Galen says, to the extent that he knows the judgment of members, and their forms and joints and separations of them, and have knowledge of bones and nerves and sinews and the number of bones, and their movement and the moving and resting veins, and the direction of their outflow.
Et por ceu dist Ypocras que li nons avec le non est mout, et avec l’uevre est poc; et meismement en l’art de main.	And for this reason Hippocrates said that the nose with the thumb is much, and with work is little; and the same in the art of healing.
Nos vos disons en l’introite de cest livre que qui n’est conissans des choses devant dites, si se gart qu’il ne chiece en error et qu’il n’ocie les homes; ensi que j’ai veut maintes fois plusors de ces qui s’entremettent de ceste science et si s’abandonent sen science et sens experiment.	We tell you in the beginning of this book that he who is not knowledgeable about the things mentioned before, let him be careful lest he err and cut men; thus I have seen many times more of those who engage in this science and abandon themselves to science and experience.
Car je vis un fol mire qui copa .i. apostume de scrophules ou col d’une femme, et copa les arteres dou col; por coi tant de sanc issit hors que li femme cheit morte entre ses mains.	Because I saw a foolish man who cut open one abscess of scrofula from a woman's neck, and cut the arteries of her neck; therefore so much blood came out that the woman fell dead in her hands.
Et vis .i. autre mire qui traït une piere d’un home d’eaige, et li piere estoit grans; si emporta avec li une piece de la vessie, et fut mors li hons dedens .iij. jors.	And I saw another man who removed a stone from an old man, and the stone was large; it took with it a piece of his bladder, and the man died within four days.
Et je i avoie ja esteit apelez por lou traire, et vis la disposition dou malaide et la grandor de la piere, et soi bien s’on lou tailloit il en morroit.	And I had already been summoned to treat it, and I saw the condition of the patient and the size of the stone, and I knew well that if it was cut he would die.
Et vis .i. autre mire qui prist en cure .i. duc de nostre terre qui avoit la jambe brisie, et avec la briseure ot plaie; et li mires plains d’ignorance estraint la brisure sus la plaie as esteles par fort lieure, et ne lassa a la plaie point de xalain, et le lassa ensi .i. termine; et li comanda qu’il ne la desliast mie; et demora ensi que li jambe fut toute enflee et li piez et vint a perdition.	And there was another doctor who took care of the leg of one of our land's dukes, which had been broken and caused an injury; and these doctors, full of ignorance, set the break above the wound with great force, and did not leave any splint on the wound, leaving it in such a state; and he commanded that it should not be dislocated again; and it stayed like that until the leg became completely swollen, and the toes rotted away and came to ruin.
Je fuis apelez por venir a lui, et me hastai por venir deslier la jambe; et quant je l’oi desloie si fut em pais et ne sentit point de dolor.	I was called upon to come and loosen the leg; and when I did so, it became peaceful and he felt no pain.
Mais toute voie li corruptions estoit ja confermee ou membre, et ne la poi saner; et ne cessa li corrution d’aler par le membre tant que li membres fut dou tout perdus.	But the corruption was already confirmed in the limb, and it could not heal it; and the corruption continued to spread through the limb until it was completely destroyed.
Et vis .i. autre mire qui effondra .i. apostume enchancreit, et puis enflama per le malice de sa signorie.	And there comes another mirror which collapses an inflamed abscess, and then sets it on fire due to the malice of its power.
Car chancre, quant il est purs d’umor melancolique, ne covient mie qu’on i(l) touche de fer s’il n’est en teil leu c’on puisse toute oster ce que est corrumpus.	For a chancre, when it is full of black bile, it should not be touched with iron unless it can be completely removed that which is corrupt.
Et por ceu, treschier filz, vos est besoig que vos sachiez que oevre de mains est devisee en .ij. divisions: c’est asavoir, huevre ou il a peril en plusors dispositions; et je mostrerai en chescun leu de cest livre ou il a paour et peril.	And for this reason, dear son, it is necessary that you know that the work of hands is divided into two divisions: namely, a surgical operation where there is danger in many dispositions; and I will show in each part of this book where there is fear and danger.
Por coi il est besoig que vos vos en gardez, si que li fol mire ne puissent mal parler de vos.	Because it is necessary for you to take care, so that foolish people cannot speak ill of you.
Si prenez vos armes en cusenson, et entreprenez vos malaides legierement et fermement, et usez de la millor voie si que per la graice de Deu vos venez a salut et soiez loez; et lassiez les maladies espoantables de grief saniteit; et ostez vos armes de ceu que vos fait douter, et aiez foit en vos si que vos puissiez venir de cestui monde a l’autre de gloire.	Take arms in custody, and begin your sick people lightly and firmly, and use the best way so that by the grace of God you may come to salvation and be praised; leave frightening diseases aside due to great health; remove your weapons from those that cause doubt, and have faith in yourself so that you can depart from this world to another of glory.
Galiens dist en aucuns de ses amonestemens: «Ne prenez mie en cure male maladie, que vos ne soiez apelez fol mire.»	Galen said in some of his admonitions: "Do not take care of a bad disease, lest you be called a foolish person."
J’ai deviseit cest traitier selonc .iij. chapitres.	I have devised this treatment according to three chapters.
Li premiers chapitres est des cauteres de feu et dé cauteres de medicine ague, et est li chapitres ordenez de lou chief jusques as piez; et des formes des estrumens, et des ferremens de cautere, et de tout ceu qui est necessaire en l’ueuvre.	The first chapters are about fire and medicine cauteries and they are arranged from the head to the feet; and the forms of instruments, and the cautery irons, and everything that is necessary in the work.
Li secons chapitres si est de taillier et de percier, et des ventouses et des plaies, et des estractions des saiettes, et des semblans choses; et est li chapitres ordenez et les formes des estrumens.	The second chapters are about cutting and piercing, and of the ventouses and wounds, and of the extraction of arrows, and similar things; and they are arranged in order with the forms of instruments.
Li tiers chapitres est de restorer les dislocations et des torcions, et des semblans choses; et est ordeneiz des lou chief jusc’as piez, et des formes des estrumens.	The third chapters are about restoring dislocations and twists, and similar things; and they are arranged from the head to the feet, and with the forms of instruments.
Ainsois que nos nos remembriens de l’uevre, il covient que je die la qualiteit de l’aide et dou nuisement de chescune complexion.	Therefore, remembering the work, it is necessary for me to tell the quality of the aid and the harm of each complexion.
Je dis que li qualiteis de l’aide, et dou nuisement, est li plus longe parole et subtilz science et li secrez reponus; et de ceu parlerent li plusors des saiges, et s’acorderent a ceu; et me soffisent poc lor paroles, car je redous la longesce.	The quality of the aid, and the harm, is a long discourse and subtle science, and the secrets responses; and many wise men spoke about it, and agreed with this; and I do not trust their words much because I reduce the length of it.
Je dis que cautere aide universement a toute complexion ou il a matiere, fuer que .ij. complexions: c’est a savoir complexion chaude sens matere, et complexion seche sens matere.	I say that cauterization helps universally in all complexions where there is matter, whether it be in two complexions: that is to say the hot complexion with matter, and the dry complexion with matter.
En complexion chaude et seche ensamble matiere, deviserent aucun et dirent que cautere i est grans aide; et li autre dirent le contraire: que cautere ne vaut a maladie que vient de chalor et de sechour.	In a hot and dry composition of matter, some said that fire cautery is great aid; and others said the opposite: that fire cautery is not useful for sickness caused by heat and dryness.
Car li nature dou feu si est chaude, et ne doit mie estre cureiz de chaude maladie par chalor, ne per sechour; et dist cil qui dist lou contraire que cautere fait grant aide a maladie chaude et seche que vient en cors des homes.	For the nature of fire is hot and should not be used to cure hot diseases by heat or dryness; and he who said otherwise said that fire makes great aid for hot and dry sicknesses coming into men's bodies.
Car quant tu comperes le cors de l’ome et sa moistor a la complexion dou feu, tu trueves le cors froit.	For when you understand the body and its moisture according to the nature of fire, you find the body cold.
Et je m’acorde a ceste parole.	And I agree to this statement.
Car je l’ai troveit aucune fois per experiment.	For I have found it once by experience.
Et toute voie, ne s’en entremette mie fuers que cil qui l’a esproveit, et qui conoit par lonc usaige le chapistre des cauteres, et la diversiteit des complexions des homes, et les dispositions et les causes de lor maladies, et les sorvenues et l’espaice dou tens; des autres complexions n’avons nos mie paour, meismement em maladies froides et moistes.	And every way, do not interfere unless the one who has tested it and knows by long experience the chapter on cauteries, and the variety of human constitutions, and their dispositions and causes of their diseases, and their symptoms and the space of time; we have no fear for other constitutions, especially in cold and moist diseases.
Et tuit li mire s’asemblerent et s’acorderent au cautere.	And all the physicians agreed and concurred to the cautery.
Et sachiez, filz, que cautere ensamble feu si est des secrez des cures, et de plus grant bonteit que cautere de medicine ardant.	And know, son, that a cautery together with fire is one of the secrets of healing, and of greater goodness than a cautery of burning medicine.
Car li feus est simples, et ne vient mie fuers que au membre qui est cuis, et ne nuit a autre membre se poc nom.	For fire is simple, and does not come out except for the member that is burned, and it harms no other member unless named.
Les medicines ardans vienent de membre a autre en aloignant, et font venir au membre maladies de grief sanation; et par aventure ocit lou malaide.	Burning medicines come from one member to another in spreading, and bring diseases of great suffering to the sick member; and by chance it kills the patient.
Li feus por sa hautece et por la bonteit de sa substance ne fait mie ceu, s’il n’i a superfluiteit.	Fire due to its high nature and the goodness of its substance does not do this if there is no excess.
Et ceu vos ai je troveit par experiment et par la longesce dou servise et de l’estude que j’ai mis en l’art, et esteit sus la verteit des choses; et por ceu je m’escuse de la longesce de la parole, car il ne me plait mie que je vos oste le secreit qui est reponus ou feu, et la qualiteit de l’uevre, coment il deboute les maladies des cors, si com li philosophe le dit en demostrant; or le recevez en vos pensees.	And I have found this for you by experiment and through the length of service and study that I have put into my art, and it is in line with truth; and because of this, I apologize for the length of my words, for I do not wish to deprive you of the secret which is revealed or fire, and the quality of the work, how diseases of the body can be driven away, as the philosopher says in demonstrating; now receive it in your thoughts.
Et sachiez, fil, que il s’acorderent en quel tens doient estre faites les cauteres, et eslirent prientens.	And know, son, that they agreed on what time the cauterizations should be done and chose their assistants.
Et je dis que cautere est covenable en tous tens, por ceu que li nuisemens sorvenans est desoz mis par l’aide dou cautere; et meismement se li cauteres est por dolors necessaires fors et hastans que ne puent atendre le tens que plus grans malice ne veigne au membre.	And I say that a cauterization is useful in all times, because the harm that occurs is kept at bay by the help of cauterization; and indeed, if the cauterizations are necessary for pain, they should not be delayed until greater harm comes to the member.
Et n’i pensez onques, chier fil, si com font li fol mire; car a la maladie qui est sanee par cautere n’a point de revenue; et il le dient ensi; mais il n’est mie si com il cuident, por ce que cauteres nen est que medicine qui mue la complexion, et seche les humors que sont cause de la dolor, et vaut mues que medicine por le hastement de sa valor, et por la vertut de son oevre et de sa signorie.	And never think about it, dear child, as the foolish do; for a disease treated by cautery has no return; and they say thus; but it is not as they believe, because cauteries are not just medicine that changes the complexion, but rather dries the humors that cause pain, and acts more quickly than other medicines due to its potency and the virtue of its work and dominion.
Et possans chose est que li maladie viegne aucune fois selonc la complexion dou malaide et lou leu de la maladie et sa vertut; et sont assemblees en lui les superfluitez par l’aquisition des viandes et des semblans choses, se ce n’est cauteres administrez em leu ou il ait poc de superfluitez et de moistor, si com cauteres de dens por la dolor, et les semblans choses, et teil dolor ne revient mie; mais ce avient poc.	And sometimes the disease comes according to the complexion of the sick and the nature of the disease and its properties; and superfluidities are gathered in him through the consumption of food and similar things, unless cauteries have been administered where there is little superfluity or moisture, such as dense cauteries for pain, and similar things; but this does not often happen.
Et mout de gens n’entendent mie por coi cauteres est apelez li derriens de medecine, et c’est voir; mais il ne croient mie que cauteres vaille aprés medicine, mais lor ententions est fause, et est cauteres li derriens de medicine por ceu que quant nos aministrons manieres de cures en aucune maladie et elles ne valent, adonc administrons nos le cautere, et il vaut.	And many people do not understand why cauteries are called the rear of medicine, and this is true; but they do not believe that cauteries have value after other medicines, but their intentions are false, and cauteries are the rear of medicine because when we administer methods of cure in any disease and they are of no use, then we administer cautery, and it has value.
Adonques apert bien que cauteres est li derriens de medicine, ne mie selonc l’entention des folz mires.	Then it is clearly stated that cauteries are at the rear of medicine, not according to the intention of foolish physicians.
Li ancien dirent que cauteres d’estrument d’or est muedres que de fer, et ne dirent ceu fuers que por la qualiteit de l’or et por la hautece de sa substance; et dirent que li leus de cautere ne fait mie porriture, mais ceu n’est mie voir car je l’ai esprovei, et ai troveit que c’est voir en aucuns homes; et cauteres d’or vaut mues que de fer, si com il lou dirent.	They used to say that cauteries made from gold instruments are more effective than iron ones, and said this only because of the quality of gold and the nobility of its substance; but this is not true, for I have tested it, and found it true in some men; and a golden cautery is as effective as an iron one, as they say.
Et toutevoie quant tu chaufes estrument d’or, tu ne seis mie quant il est chaus par la color de l’or, et s’est tantost refroidiez; et s’on le chaufe trop; si font au feu; et ensi i a assez d’empechement.	And even though you heat an instrument of gold, you do not know when it is hot due to the color of the gold and can suddenly cool; and if heated too much, it causes fire, and so there is enough reason for concern.
Et por ce usons nos de cautere de feir que nos l’avons mues apparilliet a nostre oevre.	And therefore we use the fire cautery, which we have found suitable for our work.
Or vos ai ordeneit cest chapitre des lou chief jusc’a piez, por ceu que li voie soit plus legiere a trover.	I hereby order you this chapter on the head down to the feet, because the veins will be easier to find.
dou cautere olivaire	olive oil cautery
Cist cauteres vaut a moistor et a froidor sus lou cerveil, et en i a dous c’on fait par la cause d’une maladie qui est apelee «soda», et par la cause de maintes humors qui dessendent dou chief as eulz, et as oreilles, et por multitude de songes et dolor de dens et dolor de gorge, et meismement a toutes maladies qui vienent de froidor si com paralisie et sode et apoplexie et semblans maladies.	This cautery is good for both moist and cold conditions on the brain, and it helps with a disease called "soda," as well as many humors that descend from the head to the eyes and ears, and numerous dreams, throat pain, and neck pain, and similarly for all diseases caused by coldness such as paralysis, sode, apoplexy, and similar illnesses.
Li forme de cest cautere si est que li malaides soit espurgiez par medicine solutive mondifiant le chief .iij. nuis ou .iiij., selonc ceu que li vertus et li eaige et li acostumance dou malaide le puet soffrir; et puis fai rere lou chief dou malaide.	The form of this cautery is such that the patient should be purged by a soluble medicine, clearing his head for three to four times or according to what the virtues and age and accustomed tolerance of the sick person can endure; and then make him lie down again on top of the sick man's head.
Et puis le fai seoir croisiet entre tes mains, et mettre ses mains sor som peis; aprés met la racine de ta palme sus la racine de son neis entre ses .ij. eulz; et lai ou venra tes dois moiens, si saigne d’enche puis eschaufe le cautere qui est apelé «olivare», de coi ci est li forme:	Then place him crosswise between your hands and put his hands on a soft place; afterwards place the root of your palm on the root of his nose between his two eyes; and where your thumbs meet, it will bleed, then heat the cautery called "olivare", which is as follows:
Et le met sor le leu signiet d’encre, et fai en dessendant et en estraignant ta main poc et poc en trestornant; puis lieve ta main isnelement, et rewarde le leu se tu vois l’os .i. sol petit; et se tu ne lou vois, si rencomence le cautere tant que tu voies l’os si com je lou t’ai dit; aprés pren .i. poc de seil, et met en awe et molle coton dedens, et met sor le leu, et li laisse .iij. jors; aprés met sus cotun moilliet en burre; et laisse sus tant que li eschaudure soit ostee; aprés cure la plaie de l’oignement qui est apelez «tetrafarmaçon», tant qu’il soit sanez.	Then place it on the spot marked with ink, and move your hand back and forth while turning it over and over; then remove your hand immediately, and watch the spot to see if you can see a small bone; and if you don't see it, continue heating the cautery until you do as I have told you; afterwards take a small piece of oil and put it on a soft cotton inside, and place it on the spot, and leave it for three days; afterwards place soft buttery cotton on top of it; and leave it until the burn is healed; afterwards treat the wound with an ointment called "tetrafarmaçon" until it is healed.
Et se dirent li ancien, que quant plus demoure overte li plaie, plus s’espurge; et por ce si aide mues.	And as the ancients said, when the wound is left open longer, it purges more; therefore, if assisted, it heals faster.
Et dirent aucun de ces que on doit tant lassier le cautere que partie de l’os soit arse, et puis rese on ceu qui est ars de l’os, et soit curez.	And said some that the fire cautery should be allowed to burn part of the bone, then clean and heal what is burned.
Et dient li autre c’on doit le cautere tant lassier sus, et bouter si fort c’on abaite de l’os ausi large comme .i. vertoil que les femmes mettent en lor fusez por ceu que les humors issent mues hors; et doit on lassier la plaie longement overte; aprés le doit on curer et sodeir.	And others say that the cautery should be allowed to burn from above, and strike it so hard that a space as large as a walnut is hollowed out, because the humors flow out; then the wound should be left open for a long time, after which it should be cured and dressed.
Et ces .ij. manieres de cauteres ne me semblent mie estre bones dou tout en tout, fuers qu’en aucuns homes ou il ait voie de paor; et mues me semble que je lou doie laissier; car li chiés li est afoiblis par les solutions continuees de nature, si com nos le tesmoignons ens autres membres; et meisme quant li chiés dou malaide est foibles par nature, et li premiere semblance de cautere est plus salve et muedre por moi, et de celi use je oevre en donques emsamble salut.	And these two methods of cauteries do not seem good to me altogether, except in some men where there is fear; and it seems to me that I should leave them; because the head is weakened by continuous solutions of nature, as we have witnessed in other members; and even when the head of the patient is naturally weak, the first appearance of cautery seems safer and more beneficial to me, and from this use I work for salvation.
de l’anciainne dolor dou chief	of the ancient pain of the head
Quant en tout le chief vient dolor croniques, et dure longement, si doit user li malaides yeris et pilules qui sont apelees «cochie», et d’espurgement de chief et d’oiles et d’emplastres; et s’on li fait le cautere que nos avons devant dit, et il ne vaut.	When the head comes chronic and lasting pain, the patient should use earwax and pills called "cochie", and purge of the head and oils and plasters; and if one does the cautery that we have said before, it is not worthwhile.
Pren warde se li chiés dou malade est de fort nature, et qu’il ne soit trop froit; adonques le cauterize desoz celui cautere un poc que nos avons dit desus.	Take care if the patient's shoulder is strong and not too cold; then cauterize below that fire cautery a small amount as we have mentioned before.
Aprés fai cautere sus chescune corne dou chief jusc’a l’os, si com devant avons dit, et fai .i. cautere ou leu qui est apelez «vasselz»; et est .i. leus en coi on met ventouses; et alige ta main si que tu ne voises mie jusc’a l’os: li malaides sent trop plus grant dolor en cest cautere que as autres, et je em parlerai aillors; et covient que li cauteres des cornes soient plus subtis que cil dont on cautere la moieneteit dou chief, et c’est li forme:	After performing cautery on each temple of the head up to the bone, as we have said before, and perform one cautery called "vasselz"; it is one in which ventouses are placed; align your hand so you do not see past the bone: the patient feels more intense pain in this cautery than others, and I will speak about this later; and the cauteries on the temples should be finer than those used to cauterize the midline of the head, and here is the shape for it:
dou cautere dou chief	the cautery on the head
Quant en une partie dou chief vient dolor sodaine, et est estendue li maladie jusc’a l’oil, et li chiés est espurgiez par medicines mondifians, et on a fait les autres cures que j’ai dit en la division des maladies, et tout ceu ne profite mie: adonques li fai cauteres selonc .ij. manieres, c’est a savoir de medicine ague et de feir.	When sudden pain comes in one part of the head and the disease spreads to the oil, and the head is purged by various medicines, and other treatments as I have said in the division of diseases are performed, but none of it helps; then cauteries are done according to two ways, namely by hot medicine and fire.
Li cauteres de medicine ague si est que tu preignes une doce d’alz, et oste l’escorce et le recope .i. poc as .ij. chiés, et puis fent la temple ou li dolor tient en teil maniere que tu puisses reponre la doce d’alz desoz le cuir; et quant elle sera reponuee si le lie et l’estraint bien et le laisse ensi .xij. houres; et puis le deslie et trait fuers la doce d’ail, et laisse la plaie ensi .ij. jors ou .iij.; puis met sus cotun plongiet en burre tant que porreture en isse.	The cautery by hot medicine is that you take a shallot and remove the skin and place it on two eyes, one piece for each eye, then make an incision in the temple where the pain is located so you can place the shallot under the skin; and when it is placed, press it well and let it stay for 12 hours; then release it and treat the shallot strongly, letting the wound heal for 2 or 3 days; then cover it with a cloth dipped in butter until it becomes dry.
Aprés le cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez; et se tu vues si fai ceu d’aucunes medicines comburans que j’ai escrites ou dozime traitier des medicines comburans.	After the treatment with ointment until it heals; and if you see that this does not work, perform one of the treatments using burning medicines as I have written or the 12th remedy for treating burning medicines.
Li cautere de fer si est selonc ceste meniere. Chaufe le cautere de coi ci est li forme:	The cautery of fire is as follows. Heat the cauterizer according to this shape:
Et est apelez «clos» por ceu que li chief est fait a la forme d’un clo ou il ait .i. poc de corbeure, et em mileu a une petite apparance; et le met sor le leu dolorous, et tien ta main et trestorne le feir un poc legierement, tant que li moitiez de l’espés dou keur soit arse; et lieve ta main que li artere n’arde, que est defuers, et decorre habundance de sanc.	It is called "clo" because the head is made in the shape of a cup with a shallow indentation, and it has a small appearance; place it on the painful area, hold your hand and lightly press the iron until half of the thickness of the iron is burned; remove your hand so that the artery does not burn, that is away from the burn, and draw out the blood abundantly.
Aprés met coton en awe de seil, et met sor le leu par .iij. jors; puis i met coton moilliet em burre, et puis cure le leu d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez; et se tu vuelz cauterize ceste emigraine avec le cautere qui est apelez «cultellare», a tout la pointe, et te garde de coper l’artere en ceste emigraine qui n’est mie anciaine.	After placing cotton on it for two days, then put dampened cotton wool on it, and afterwards heal the wound with ointment until it is healed; and if you wish to cauterize this boil with the cautery called "cultellare", prick it all over, but be careful not to touch the artery in this boil that is not old.
de emigraine	Of emigraine (Translation: From emigrain)
Quant tu cures emigraine si com nos avons devant dit en divisions des maladies, et ne profite mie, et vois que li cauteres devant dis de la medicine et dou fer ne li soffit mie, adonques covient il que tu eschaufes le cautere qui est apelez «cultellare» tant qu’il soit blans; et seigne ainsois sor le leu doillant une ligne de demi doi de lonc, et oste ta main une fois, et l’estrain que tu ne coper l’artere et que ne viegnes jusc’a l’os; et te warde de la mandibule que muet quant on menjut, et li ners n’ait regart que la muet et que spasmus ne veigne a malaide, et te warde de decorrement de sanc de l’artere quant elle sera copee, ou copement ait grant paour et meismement a celui que ne s’i conoit, et qui n’est estudians et esprovez; et laisse l’uevre em mi voie; mais je vos dirai coment on restainche sanc quant li artere est copee, et je vos mostrerai a leu ou il afiert en cest livre.	When you treat emigraine, as we have previously said in the divisions of diseases, and it does not improve, and you find that cauteries before mentioned in the medicine do not help, then it is necessary that you heat the cautery which is called «cultellare» until it becomes white; and hold your hand on the side of a line of half a foot long, and strike once, and strain so as not to touch the artery or come to the bone; and watch for the jaw that moves when eating, and veins should have no sight but the moving one and spasms should not come upon the patient, and beware of the flow of blood from the artery when it is cut, or bleeding too much where there is great fear, especially for those who do not know it and are not trained and experienced; and leave the procedure in progress; but I will tell you how to stop the bleeding when the artery is cut, and I will show you where it should be found in this book.
Et se tu vois que cist cauteres ne soffise mie a la maladie, et li malaides est soffrans, cauterize le enmi le chief ausi com nos avons dit, et cure la plaie tant qu’elle soit sanee; et se tu vues, aministre le cautere que nos avons dit ou chapistre de l’estraction de l’artere, avec le cautere qui ait .ij. coutelz; et est cist cauteres millors de celui et plus aidans.	And if you see that this cautery does not help the disease, and the patient is suffering, cauterize it near the head as we have said, and cure the wound until it heals; and if you find, administer the cautery mentioned or in the chapter of the extraction of the artery, with the cautery that has two knives; and this cautery is better than the one and more helpful.
de la dolor des oreilles de part froidor	From the pain of the ears due to coldness
Quant en l’oreille vient dolor de froit, et on i a ovreit de medicines solutives et des autres cures que nos avons dit en la division, et li dolors ne se muet, adonques eschaufe cest cautere qui est apelez «poins», de coi ci est li forme:	When pain in the ear comes from cold and medicines soluble and other treatments mentioned in the division have been applied but the pain does not subside, then heat this cautery called "poins", here is its shape:
Aprés pointoie tout entor l’oreille malaide, ou entor les .ij. se la dolor tient en ambedous, et t’esloigne un poc ensus de la racine de l’oreille puis que tu as signiet le leu d’enche; et ait .x. poins entor chescune oreille; aprés cure le leu tant qu’il soit sanez.	After pointing all around the sick ear, or in both sides where the pain persists, move away slightly from the root of the ear after you have marked the spot; and place 10 "poins" around each ear; treat the spot until it is healed.
de la torture de la bouche	Of the torture of the mouth
Torture qui doit estre curee par cautere nen est fuers que de celles que muevent de fleume, si com nos avons dit en divisions des maladie; et ne faire point de cautere as semblances que vienent de sechor et de spame de ners.	The torture by cautery can only be applied to those that move due to fever, as we have said in the division of diseases; and never do cautery to similar ones that come from scurvy and internal bleeding.
Quant tu cures ceste semblance de torture qui muet de fleume d’ydres et d’espurgemens de chief et de gargarisme, et ceu ne vaut, adonc covient que tu cauterizes le malaide de .iij. cauteres: l’une en la racine de l’oreille, et l’autre un poc defuers la temple, et le tier en l’ajostement des .ij. levres; et met le cautere en la partie qui apert saine, et li fai cautere endroit le chief de l’oreille desus un poc desoz la corne dou chief, et un autre en la temple ausi longe com uns poce; et laisse le cautere tant sus que li moitiez dou keur soit arse; et c’est li forme dou cautere:	When treating this type of torture caused by fever and purges of the head and gargarism, it is not effective. Therefore, you must cauterize the patient with four cauteries: one at the root of the ear, another a little distance from the temple, and the third in the corner of the lips; put the cautery in the open healthy part, and make it burn towards the ear above a little bit below the forehead, and another in the temple as long as a fist; leave the cautery for as long as half an hour is burned; and this is the form of the cautery:
Et est li semblance dou cutellaire que nos avons mise devant, mais il est un poc plus subtilz et covient que li coutelz soit un poc plus gros; aprés cure lou leu si com j’ai devant dit, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And it is similar to the shape of a surgeon's instrument that we have mentioned, but it is slightly more subtle and requires the knife to be a bit larger; after curing the wound as I have previously stated, let it heal when it is healthy.
Quant apoplexie est ancieinne et tu la cures ensi com nos avons dit, et il ne profite mie, et li malaides n’ait fievre, adonques li fai .iiij. cauteres: .ij. sus les .ij. cornes dou chief, et .i. emmi le chief, et .i. ou leu qui est apelez «vasselz» si com nos avons devant dit, et lou derrien cautere sus la bouche de l’estomac; et soit curez si com nos avons dit devant.	When apoplexy is old and you treat it as we have said, but it does not improve, and the patient does not have a fever, then perform four cauteries: two on the two horns of the head, one on the top of the head, one in the place called "bellybutton" as we have previously mentioned, and the last cautery on the mouth of the stomach; and let it be treated as we have said before.
de litargie	bedridden
A cest maladie covient doner au malaide yeres grans et pilules mondifians le cerveil; aprés reis lou chief dou malaide tout, et li met sus l’occipite l’emplaustre de sinapi qui est escrit ou traitier des emplastres; et c’est li maniere dou cautere: si lou fai si com j’ai dit.	For this disease, give the patient large years and round pills containing cerebrum; afterwards, anoint the head of the patient completely, and place the plaster of mustard (sinapi) on the occiput which is written or treated as plasters; and this is the method of cautery: if done as I have said.
S’il est sanez ensi, boin est; et s’il ne l’est, se li fai .iij. cauteres des emmi le chief en dessendant jusc’a col, et ait d’espaice entre chescun cautere .i. doi de gros; et le cure si com les autres, et se tu i vues ajoster, et li malaides est soffrans, se li fai .i. cautere en mileu; et se mestiers est, .ij. autres sus les .ij. cornes, et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et soit li cauteres qui est apelez «olivare», si com j’ai devant dit.	If it is healthy, it is good; if not, perform four cauteries on the head from the neck to the collarbone, and keep a distance of two between each cautery; heal as with others, and if you see any danger, and the patient is enduring, perform one cautery in the middle; and if necessary, two more on the two horns (temples), and heal until it is healthy; and let the cauteries which are called "olivare", as I have previously said.
de la froidor dou chief	of the coldness of the head
Il covient que li chief soit mundifiez de yeres et de ceu que nos avons devant dit; aprés reis le chief dou malaide, puis li fai cautere emmi le chief et sus chescune corne, et .i. derrier et .iij. sus l’espinee dou col; et se tu en as plus mestier, et li cors est moiste et li malaides est soffrans, et li maladie est fors, se li fai .iiij. cauteres sus l’espinee dou dos; et li laisse tant que li plus dou keur soit ars, et lieve ta main; aprés le cure tant qu’il soit sanez, et soit li cauteres qui est apelez «olivare» que nos avons devant dit.	It is necessary to clean the head (skull) with years and what was said before; afterwards, the head of the patient should be shaved, then make a fire cautery on the head and one at each temple, and one at the back and three on the spine of the neck; if you have more need, and the body is moist and the patient is suffering, and the disease is severe, make four cauteries on the spine of the back; let it be until the most painful part is burned, then wash your hand; afterwards, cure it until it is healed, and heal the cautery that is called "olivare" which was said before.
de l’epilempsie	epilepsy
Li epilentiques ne doit useir de cautere fuers que cil qui est fleumatique, et covient premier mondifier le cerveil de yeres et d’autres cures que nos avons dites en la division quant li malaides est grans et soffrans de penre medicine.	Epileptics should not use fire cautery except for those who are phlegmatic, and it is necessary first to clean the brain with years and other remedies as we have said in the division when the patient is large and suffering from taking medicine.
Et se c’est uns enfes qui ne lou puisse soffrir, se li fai gargarisme et mastication mondifiant le cerveil sovent avec bones viandes; aprés li reis lou chief em mileu, et i fai .i. cautere selonc ce que nos avons dit devant, et .i. cautere sus lou vassel, et sus chescune corne; et se li malaides est fors et soffrans, se li fai cauteres si com j’ai dit a celui qui ait paralisie et mollification de cors, sus l’espinee dou dos et dou col, et soit li cauteres olivier selonc la maniere que j’ai dit.	And if it is an infant who cannot endure it, give him gargarism and frequent mastication of the brain with good foods; afterwards let the head be repositioned, and make one cautery according to what has been said before, and one cautery on the forehead, and on each horn; and if the patient is strong and enduring, make cauterizations as I have said for one who has paralysis and softening of the body, on the spine of the back and neck, and let the cauterizations be olive-shaped according to the manner that I have said.
Se li malaides est enfes, se li fai .i. cautere subtil selonc ceste maniere:	If the patient is an infant, make a subtle cautery in this way:
Quant par la cause de melancolie sunt les superfluitez ou les moistors corrumpues et fleume grosse, adonques lou cauterize de teils cauteres com nos avons dit a celui qui ait paralisie.	When because of melancholy are the superfluidities or corrupted and thick fluids, then make the cautery with such cauteries as we have said for one who has paralysis.
Et se par la cause de melancolie est li superfluitez declinans a melancolie, et est li cors dou malaide moistes, adonc li done a boivre chose par coi li cervelz soit mundifiez, selonc ceu qu’il est devant en la division.	And if due to melancholy the superfluities are descending towards melancholy, and the body of the patient is moist, then give him something to drink that will purify the brain, according to what was mentioned earlier in the division.
Aprés reis lou chief dou malaide; aprés fai .i. torteil de lin bien fait, ausi com .i. cercle, si le met emmi le chief; et li malaides sié croisiez, et soit bien tenus de toutes pars; aprés presente le linement, et vaut mues de burre de berbis ancien; et lou chaufe a feu tempreement, si que li dois s’on li boute le puisse soffrir; aprés vuide le cercle par dedens emmi le chief, et lou laisse refroidier; et fai ce a malaide chescune semaine une fois avec autre governement boin, tant qu’il soit sanez.	Then place the patient's head; make a small linen bandage in the shape of a circle and put it around his head; cross the patient, hold him securely from all sides; apply liniment made of old butterbur, then heat it gently so that he can bear it; empty the circle from within around his head, and let it cool; do this to the patient once a week with good management, until he is cured.
Ou se tu vues cauterize lou en faisant poins plusors a tot le cautere. Ceste maniere de cautere amoistit le cerveil igaument; et puis met sus coton moilliet en burre et en graisse de geline.	Or, if you wish to cauterize him by making multiple punctures throughout the cautery, this method will greatly soften the brain. Then place damp cotton soaked in butter and linseed oil on top.
de l’awe des eulz	From the swelling of the eyes
Quant awe vient premierement as eulz par les signes que j’ai dit en la division, adonques encomence et done boivre au malaide chose mundifiant le chief, et le warde de toutes moistors, et lou fai suer ou bain plusors fois a jeun.	When the swelling of the eyes comes first as I have said in the division, then begin and give the patient something cleansing for the head, and guard him from all moisture, and make it sweat or bathe it more times on an empty stomach.
Aprés li comande a rere son chief, et li fai cautere emmi le chief, et li fai .ij. cauteres sus les .ij. temples se li dessendemens de l’awe est as .ij. eulz ensamble, ou en .i. se li dessendemens est en .i.; et cope a tout le cautere toutes les voines et les arteres que sont desoz le keur, et soient li cautere lonc selon lou large de la temple; et te warde de decorrement de sanc, et se tu vois trop de sanc issir, si li estainche de teil pooir com tu as.	Afterwards, command him to lie on his back, and make a fire cautery on the head, and make two cauteries on the two temples if the swelling is in both eyes, or one if it is in one; and touch all the veins and arteries under the skull with the cautery, and let the cautery be long according to the size of the temple; and be careful not to spill blood, and if you see too much blood flowing out, stop it with your power as you can.
Et je t’enseignerai en l’estraction des arteres et a l’incision la cautele coment tu l’estencheras; et aucune fois fait on cautere ou hatereil desoz les .ij. os derrier.	And I will teach you in the extraction of arteries and in making incisions with caution, how to stop it; and sometimes a fire cautery or hot iron is made under the two bones behind.
dou cors des larmes	The heart weeps
Quant les larmes des eulz sont ancienes et acostumees et sont sus les voines, ou delez les arteres que sont en l’aparance dou chief defors; et on voit que c’est des superfluitez froides fleumatiques, adonques li fai le cautere que j’ai dit en l’encomencement de l’awe dessendant as eulz: .i. cautere emmi le chief, et .ij. cauteres sus les .ij. temples, et .ij. cauteres ou haiterel desoz les .ij. os; et s’il i a besoigne plus, si le cauterize saigement desus le sorcil a tout .i. petit cautere.	When the tears of the eyes are old and accustomed and are above the veins, or from the arteries that appear on the forehead; and it is seen that this is due to cold, fleumatic superfluities, then do the cautery as I have said at the beginning of this work, namely: cauterize in the forehead, and two cauteries on the temples, and two cauteries or cauterize beneath the eyebrows of the eyes; and if there is need for more, cauterize skillfully above the corner of the eye with a small cautery.
dou cors des larmes par dedens les eulz	The heart weeps inside the eyes
Quant tu le medicines selonc ceu que nos avons dit en la division, et il ne profite mie, adonques done a boivre a malaide .iij. nuis cochies; aprés li reis le chief, et li fai cautere ou mileu dou cautere olivaire; et fai .ij. cauteres dou cautere qui est apelez «clavilis» sus les .ij. sorcis, un poc desoz les chevous; et te warde de l’artere que tu ne la coper.	When you treat the patient as we have said in the division, and it does not help, then give the sick person three black eggs to drink; after these, roast the head with olive oil cautery or millet seed cautery; and make two cauterizations called "clavilis" over the two sores, one under the hair; beware of the artery that you do not cover.
Et c’est li forme dou cautere qui est apelez «clavilis»:	And this is the form of the cautery called "clavilis":
Quant li papiere de l’oil est mollifie de maladie et de moistor, adonques la cautarize de cest cautere qui est apelez «olivare». de coi ci est li forme:	When the paper of the oil is softened by illness and moisture, then perform this cauterization with the olive oil cautery. Here is its form:
Et se tu vues si fai .ij. cauteres sus les .ij. sorcis ausi lons com li sorcilz sont; et n’i lassiez mie la main fors que tant que li tierce partie de la papiere soit arse, selonc la maniere que j’ai dit.	And if you wish to perform two cauterizations on the two witches who are long as witches are; and do not leave your hand except when the third part of the paper is burned, according to the manner that I have said.
dou poil qui point l’oil	the hair which pricks the oil
Aucune fois avient que li poil des oilz sont convertit au pardedens, et poignent l’oil, et i fait on cauteres selonc .ij. manieres: c’est a savoir de feu, ou de medicine ardant.	Sometimes the hairs of the eyes are converted into eyelashes and prick the oil; and cauterization is done according to two methods: either with fire, or with burning medicine.
Ou cautere de feu comande au malaide qu’il laisse les poilz tant qu’il soient lons et igals; et s’il le poignent a lor nassance, se li estraint les eulz qu’il ne se muevent tant qu’il naissent.	Instruct the patient to let the hairs grow long and even; and if they prick at their base, hold the eyes steady so they do not move until they grow.
Quant il naissent et i sont igalz, adonques met le malaide en ton sain; aprés seigne sus la papiere des eulz une figure que soit ausi com li fuelle dou mirte, et soit li comencemens dou signe delez les poilz; puis i met coton moilliet en glaire d’uef et muscillaige de persillion sus l’oil, puis eschaufe le cautere de coi ci est li forme:	When they have grown and are even, then place the patient on a paper with a figure shaped like the fennel stalk, and make the incision at the beginning of the sign where the hairs are; then put dampened cotton soaked in egg white and mustard seed oil on the heated cautery, then heat the cautery to this shape:
Aprés cauterize sus la figure que tu as signiet poc et poc mout de fois, que li keurs soit ars lai endroit; et li signes de la santeit de l’uevre est que tu voies la papiere retraite, et les poilz levez a la pointure de l’oil; adonques lieve ta main, et laisse ensi .iij. jors, puis i met coton moilliet en burre tant que li eschaudure soit ostee; aprés le cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez.	After cauterizing on the figure you have marked with small strokes many times until the hairs are burned in that spot; and the signs of the health of the work are when you see the paper shrink, and the hairs rise to the tip of the oil; then lift your hand and let it rest for four days, then soak the cotton in butter until the burn is removed; after treating with ointment until it heals.
Et se aprés ceu vienent li poilz, et li papiere est mollifie adonques rencomence le cautere sus cel leu meisme, si com tu as fait premiers; et se li poil sont defuer, si le cauterize tant que li papiere soit levee a son leu natureil, et soit igals, et ne poignent mie li poil l’oil.	And if afterwards the hairs come, and the paper becomes soft, then repeat the fire cautery on that same place, as you did before; and if the hairs curl, cauterize until the paper is raised to its natural position, and is straight, and does not curl anymore.
Li cauteres de medicine ardant est que tu comandes au malaide qu’il laisse les poilz tant qu’il soient grans et igalz, puis fai de parchemin la forme de la foille de mirte; puis pren de savon fransois et de vive chalz, de chescun une .З., et broie ensamble bien; et le fai hastanment, si qu’il ne refroide, puis en espant sus la forme que tu es fait sicom la foille dou mirte, et met sus la papiere des eulz; et se li maladie tient en .i. oil soulement, si doit on ovrer en .i., et se en ambedous ausi; et met desoz l’oil coton moilliet en abin d’uef; et li chiés dou malaide soit en ton sain et met ton doi mostrant sus la medicine, et presse .i. poc et lou muef toutes les fois que li malaide sent mordication de la medicine, car il sent mordication ausi com de feu.	The hot cautery of medicine is that you instruct the patient to let their hairs grow long and straight, then make a parchment in the shape of a myrtle leaf; then take French soap and hot vinegar, each one .Z., and grind them together well; and apply it hastily, so that it does not cool down, then place the medicine on the parchment with the hairs; and if the patient only feels one oil, you must work with one, and if in both also; put cotton moistened with egg whites under the oil; and the patient's shoulders should be healthy and you place your hand on top of the medicine, pressing it with one finger every time the patient feels a burning sensation from the medicine, because it burns like fire.
Quant tu as ceu fait longement, si oste la medicine a ton doit.	When you have done this for a long time, remove the medicine from your hand.
Et quant li mordication sera passee, si leve le leu d’awe, et rewarde se tu vois la papiere levee ausi com s’ele estoit levee par constraignement de feu ou par incision; et s’il est ensi, si est bien. Se ceu non, si remet encor de la medicine sus lou leu ou li medicine n’ait ovreit, tant que tes ovraiges soit igalz, et tes eulz mis a point; puis met sus coton moilliet en burre tant que li keurs ars soit cheus, aprés cure le leu de l’oignement qui est apelez «dyafenis» et d’autre, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when the bite has passed, lift up the limb and check if the wound is raised as it was by heating or incision; and if it is so, it is good. If not, apply more medicine on the limb, or if no medicine has worked yet, keep your actions equal, and position your hands correctly; then place damp cotton wool on it until the blisters are burnt, afterwards cure the limb with ointment called "dyafenis" and others, until it heals.
Et se t’est mestier que tu te warde bien a ton ovraige par grant warde qu’il ne chiece point de la medicine as eulz.  Et se li papiere devient mole aprés, et li poil poignent en l’oil, si recomence la medicine sus celui leu qui est mollifiez de la papiere proprement, ensi com tu as fait devant; aprés le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et c’est li forme de la fuelle dou mirte:	And if you need to be careful with your work so that the medicine does not seep out from between the hairs. If the wound becomes soft and the hair pricks in the oil, repeat the medicine on that limb which has been properly cleansed; afterwards cure it until it is healed; this is the shape of a mirte leaf:
Et saichés que li eul des homes sont divers en grandor et en petitece, et selonc ceu soit tes constraignemens; et ne soit mie reponue li droite voie a celui cui est li estude de cest art.	And know that the hairs of men are different in size and length, and according to this, apply your efforts; and never deviate from the correct path for those who study this art.
de la cure de fistule par cautere	Treatment of a fistula by cautery
Quant tu cures fistule si com nos avons dit en divisions des maladies, et tes cures ne profitent mie, adonques covient il que tu li fais cautere selonc ceste maniere.	When treating a fistula as previously mentioned in the description of diseases, and your treatment does not help, then it is necessary to cauterize it according to this method.
Comande au malaide qu’il mette son chief en ton sain; et teigne li menistres son chief entre tes mains en teil maniere qu’il ne se mueve, ne ne demoinne son chief; aprés met coton moilliet en abin d’uef ou en jus de persillion sus l’oil; aprés chaufe le cautere qui est teilz: et est chevez au chief si com li forme d’une penne de vouteul, ensamble la queil soit li cautere; se tu vues, si soit apointé des l’un chief dusc’a l’autre, et se tu vues, si soit ausi com une tente; mais toutevoie, cist qui est chevez vaut mues por ton ovraige.	Instruct the patient to place his head on a clean surface; and have an assistant hold the patient's head between their hands in such a way that it does not move or turn; then put cotton soaked in egg white or linseed oil on the area to be cauterized; after heating the cautery until it is hot like iron, place it on the patient's head in the shape of a pen nib, with the cautery also being shaped accordingly; if you see, it should be pointed from one end to the other, and if you see, it should also resemble a tent; but regardless, the one that is shaped like a pen nib is more suitable for your task.
Aprés presse la fistule s’ele est overte, et en trai la porriture, et la seche; et s’ele est close, si la oevre, et trai fuers la bowe; aprés met sus le cautere chaut forment, et tien ta main au cautere a la partie dou neif ensus de l’oil, que ta mains ne faice folie; et met le cautere en la graisse de l’oil, et la corromp.	After pressing the fistula if it is open, drain the pus and dry it; if it is closed, open it and remove the scab; after that, place the heated cautery on it in the shape of a cross, and hold your hand on the cautery at the part near the nail so as not to burn yourself; and place the cautery in the fat of the oil, and corrode it.
Se tu viens au comencement dou cautere jusc’a l’os, si serait bien. Se ceu non, si rencomence le cautere encor une fois, et autre se tu en as mestier, et le laisse .iij. jors; aprés i met sus coton moilliet en burre, et lou cure de l’oignement desiccatif tant qu’il soit sanez, et se .xl. jors passent qu’il ne soit sanez, si met sus medicine ague corrosive tant que li os soit descovers; et lou reis selonc ceu que il venrait en son chapistre.	If you begin the cautery up to the bone, it would be good. If not, restart the cauterization once more, and do this as many times as necessary, and leave for 3 days; after that put soft cotton in butter, and let the ointment with drying properties heal until it is healthy, and if after 40 days it is still not healed, put corrosive medicine on the bone; and the king according to what comes in his chapter.
Et i a une maniere de cautere de fistule que aucun des anciens dirent. Entens a fistule, et fens le leu; aprés met en la fendure .i. camahan subtil de coi ci est li forme:	And there is a way of cauterizing a fistula that none of the ancients spoke about. Understand that by fistula, I mean an opening, and cut open the area; afterwards put one subtle camelidum (camel's fat) into the opening in this form:
et i font a la quantiteit d’une .З. de plonc; et tien ta main ou camahan fermement, et ne se mueve li malaides nes point, que li plons fondus ne corre a son oil; et covient c’on mette sus l’oil a malaide coton moilliet en abin d’uefz ou en awe: li plonc si art lou leu de fistule, et lou saine per mervillouse saniteit.	and they make the quantity of one .5 cubits; hold your hand with camel's fat firmly, and do not let the patient move at all, so that the molten plumb flows into its oil; it is necessary to put linen cloth dipped in egg yolk or oil on the wound: the plumb will heal the fistula by a wonderful healing.
Et se li fistule est sanee per le cautere que nos avons dit, c’est boin. Se ce non, si covient aministrer pertus au neif, et ramener la fistule au cors dou neif selonc ceu qu’il covient en som propre leu.	And if the fistula is healed by the fire cautery that we have mentioned, it is good. If not, it is necessary to administer poultice to the heat, and return the fistula to the body of the heat according to what is needed in its own place.
des crevaices en levres	deep grooves in lips
Mout de fois avienent crevaices en levres que sont apelees «poil», et meismement en levres des enfans.	Many times there are grooves or cracks in the lips, called "hair" and also in children's lips.
Quant tu cures ces crevaices de ceu que nos avons dit en divisions, et li cure ne profite, adonques eschaufe .i. petit cautere cultellaire selonc ceste forme:	When you treat these cavities as we have said in the previous sections and the treatment does not help, then heat a small cautery scalpel according to this shape:
Et le met hastanment en celles crevaices tant qu’il viegne jusc’a font; aprés cure le leu de cerote tant qu’il soit sanez.	And apply it promptly into those cavities until it reaches the bottom; after heating the area with a cautery iron until it is healthy.
de l’aposteme de la goule	of the abscess from the throat
Quant apostume vient en la racine de la goule ou en l’uve, ou ou palais, ou as racines des dens, aprés fait porriture et ront et est enveillis et devient fistule; et tu le cures si com nos avons dit en divisions, et il ne profite mie: adonques covient il que tu aies .i. cautere selonc la quantiteit de la fistule; aprés le bote ou pertus de la fistule, et tien ta main tant que li fer chaus viegne au font de li, et ou derrien leu; et fai ensi une fois ou .ij., aprés le cure de ce que nos avons dit en cures, tant qu’il soit sanez; et s’il est curez ensi, c’est boin; et se ceu non, si covient descovrir le leu et oster l’os corrumput, selonc ceu que vos le troverez en son chapistre.	When an abscess appears at the root of the throat or in the uvula, palate, or roots of the teeth, after becoming pus-filled, growing, and developing into a fistula; and you treat it as we have said in the previous sections, and it does not help: then you must have one cautery according to the size of the fistula; after emptying or puncturing the fistula, and hold your hand until the iron is hot at the bottom of it, and where the last part is; and do this once or twice, after curing as we have said in cures, until it is healthy; and if it heals like this, it is good; and if not, you must discover the area and remove the corrupted bone, according to what you will find in its chapter.
dou movement des dens	The translation for "dou movement des dens" in this context is "the double motion of the teeth".
Quant les gencives sont mollifies par moistor et les dens muevent, et tu le cures per medicines et ceu ne vaut, adonc met le chief dou malaide en ton sain; aprés eschaufe le cautere dont li forme venra ci aprés en teil maniere que tu mettes une cainne sor le dent; et met dedens le cautere chaut hastanment, et tien tant ta main que li malaides sente la chalor venant a la racine dou dent; aprés lieve ta main et rencomence le cautere selonc ta volenteit; aprés emplisse li malaides sa bouche d’awe salee, et la teigne une houre et raiche fuers.	When the gums are softened by moisture and the teeth move, and you cure it with medicine but it does not work, then put the head of the patient in your lap; afterwards heat the cautery in such a way that you place a cane on the tooth; and put the hot cautery inside immediately, and hold your hand so that the patient feels the heat coming to the root of the tooth; afterwards release your hand and continue with the cautery according to your will; afterwards fill the patient's mouth with salt water, and keep it there for an hour and rinse thoroughly.
Et en teil maniere li dens qui estoit movans si est confermez, et li gencive mollifie restrainte, et li moistors corrumpue sechie.	And in this way the moving tooth is confirmed, and the softened gums are kept restrained, and the moist corruptions dry up.
de la dolor des dens	Of the pain of the teeth
Quant dolor de dens vient por froidor, ou il i a froidor ou veir, et les cures de medicine ne valent, adonc i ait mestier de cautere selonc .ij. manieres: et cautere de burre et cautere de feu.	When tooth pain comes from cold or there is cold or fever, and the medicinal remedies do not work, then it is necessary to use cauterization according to two ways: cauterization by bull and cauterization by fire.
Cautere de burre si est telz que tu preignes burre de vaiche, et le bout en une cuillier de fer ou d’arain; aprés pren coton et envolope sus la pointe d’une tente, et la moille en burre bulit, et met sus le dent dolant hastanment et tien tant qu’il soit refroidiez; et ensi fai sovent tant que sa vertus viegne a la racine de la dent, et se tu vues si moille laine et coton en burre froit, et met sus le dent doillant, et met sus .i. fer chaut tant que li feus viegne au chevement dou dent.	Cauterization with bull fat is as follows: take bull fat and put it in an iron or brass container; then take cotton and wrap it around the tip of a tent, moisten it in boiled bull fat, apply it quickly to the painful tooth and hold until it cools; repeat this process until its property reaches the root of the tooth. If you see that the linen and cotton are moistened in cold bull fat, then apply it again and apply hot iron on top of it so the fire penetrates the tooth's crown.
Li cauteres ensamble feu si est telz que tu preignes uns cainne de fer ou d’arain, et soit grosse si que li feus ne viegne a la bouche dou malaide; aprés chaufe le cautere, de coi li forme venra ci aprés, et le met sus le dent et tien ta main tant que li cauteres soit refroidiez; fai ceu sovent, car li dolor sera ostee celui jor meisme ou l’endemain. Et covient que li malaides emplisse sa bouche de boin burre en l’empressement de cel cautere, et puis le raiche fuer; et c’est li forme dou cautere:	The cauteries together use fire if it is such that you take a chain of iron or steel, and it should be thick so that the fire does not reach the patient's mouth; after heating the cautery, its shape will come afterwards, put it on the tooth and hold your hand until the cautery cools down; do this often, for the pain will be alleviated that day itself or the next. And it is necessary that the patient fills his mouth with good butter in the hurry of this cautery, and then blow hard; this is the shape of the cautery:
Et fai cautere dou queil chief que tu voudras, et selonc ceu que tu as pooir; et c’est li forme de la caine:	And make the cautery from whatever material you have at hand; and this is the shape of the chain:
des scrophules	boils
Quant les scrophules sont de fleume et de moistors froides, et ne sont obeissans a digestion par medicines, adonques eschaufe le cautere cheveit de coi ci aprés vient li forme, et ait ij. aovertures por les fumees a issir au cautere de l’autre partie; et met le cautere chaut sus l’apostume une fois, ou .ij. se mestier est, tant qu’il viegne au font de l’apostume; et se li apostume est petis si met cautere selonc la quantiteit de l’apostume, et le laisse ensi .iij. jors; et met sus coton moilliet em burre tant que li arsure soit ostee; aprés cure le leu d’oignemens et de tentes tant qu’il soit sanez.	When scrofulas are of the fluids and cold moistures, and are not obedient to digestion by medicines, then heat the cautery hair from what follows next, and have two apertures for the smoke to issue from the other part; and place the hot cautery on the abscess once, or twice if necessary, until it reaches the root of the abscess; and if the abscess is small, place the cautery according to the size of the abscess, and leave it thus for three days; and put cotton soaked in butter over the wound until the boil is opened; afterwards, cure the affected area with ointments and poultices until it heals.
Quant les moistors vainquent sus les chenals dou pormon, et meismement quant ce vient de froide complexion, adonc covient que li malaides soit voidiez premiers par medicines solutives; aprés li fai cautere a la racine de la gorge, et te garde que tu ne venir mie jusc’a la gorge, et n’ardre dou keur mais c’un poc. Aprés li fai .i. autre cautere a la jointure dou col au chief de l’espinee, et soit li cauteres qui est apelez «clavile» de coi nos avons la forme devant; et cure le leu si com nos avons devant dit tant qu’il soit sanez.	When phlegm prevails over the channel of the throat, and especially when it comes from a cold constitution, then the patient should first be purged with soluble medicines; afterwards, make cautery at the root of the throat, but not reaching the throat, and take care not to burn it too much but just a little. Then make another cautery at the joint between the neck and spine (the "clavicle"), using the form mentioned before; and treat the affected area as previously described until it heals.
de la toust	of the cough
Quant tous et maladie de pormon sont de moistors froides, et li malaides nen ait fievre ne sechor, et est li maladie anciaine, se li fai ij cauteres sus la forcele en leus vuis; et .i. autre cautere emmi le pis entre .ij. mameles; et soit li cauteres qui est apelez «clavile» selonc la forme qui est devant dite.	When all and the disease of pormon are due to cold moistures, and the patient does not have fever or secretions, and the disease is old, make two fire cauterizations on the thigh; and another cautery in the middle between the breasts; and let it be the cautery called "clavile" according to the shape mentioned above.
Et se tu vues, fai cautere en poignant a tot le cautere qui est apelez «poins» de coi li forme est ci devant en la maladie des oreilles; et soient li poins jusc’a .xxx., ou enqui entor. Aprés cure le leu selonc ceu qui est devant dit, et soit li cauteres a .iij. rains selonc ceste forme:	And if you wish, make a puncture (cautery) at the tip of the cautery called "poins", as described above in the disease of the ears; and let the punctures be up to 30 or around it. After curing the place as stated before, let the cauterizations be at four intervals according to this shape:
Et por ceu sont li cautere plus legier, por ceu que tu en fais .iij. a cop.	And because the cauteries are lighter, since you make them in pairs (copies).
de la dislocation de l’ajutoire	of the dislocation of the shoulder
Quant li chiés de l’ajutoire est desaloiez par cause de moistor, et on le remet a leu, et il n’i puet demorer ains revient adés et desalue par petit movement qui avient, si com nos avons esproveit, adonques covient il que tu ramoinnes la dislocation premierement.	When the head of the shoulder is dislocated due to moisture, and it is reset but cannot stay in place, repeatedly dislocating with slight movement as we have experienced, then you must first reset the dislocation.
Aprés soit sovinez li malaides sus son dos et sus son costeit; aprés lieve le keur qui est dedens le titillite as dois de ta main senestre; et se li jointure est desaluee dedens, si eschaufe le cautere qui a .ij. ners douqueil ci est li forme:	After placing the patient on their back and on their side, press the sore with the heel of your left hand, and if the joint is dislocated within, use a heated iron with two nerves as shown here to reset it.
et cauterize lou keur tant qu’il le perce jusc’a costeit, et venrait li fugure dou cautere ensamble .iiij. cauteres; et por ceu est faite cautere avec le cautere qui a .iij. ners, por coi li figure de cauterization sunt sis cauteres; et sont li nerf selonc la subtiliteit d’une tente et c’est li forme dou cautere qui a .iij. ners:	and cauterize the sore up to the ribs, and the figure of the cautery will be accompanied by four cauteries; and this is made with the cautery that has two nerves, because the figures of cauterization are these cauteries; and these nerves follow the subtlety of a tent, which is the form of the cautery that has two nerves.
Et aucune fois est ajostez sus ce .i. nerf por coi il i a .viij. cauteres.	And sometimes it is dislocated above this nerve, for which there are eight cauterizations.
Aprés met sus le cautere porrelz broiez avec seil; aprés fai reposer le malaide, et ne soit meus li membres par lonc tens tant qu’il soit bien confortez.	After apply the cautery, break it with oil; after that let the patient rest and do not move the limbs for long times until they are comforted.
Et s’il est desaloiez desus, liquelz chose avient poc, adonques fait cautere sus l’epaisse dou cautere clavile, ou mout de cauteres en poignant. Car li jointure est refermee, et est ostee li moistor et est sanez li malaides.	If it is dislocated above (the joint), which happens rarely, then make a cautery on the thick part of the large bone or many cauterizations in piercing. For the joint is repositioned, and the moisture is removed and the patient is healed.
dou cautere de pleuresin	the cautery of plasters
Li ancien dirent que on doit faire a pleuresin cauteres de racines d’aristologe, et en teil maniere: pren une racine d’aristologe longe, la plus grant que tu poras troveir, et soit seche, et soit ausi grosse et ausi longe comme tes dois; et la moille en oile, et l’emprens au feu, et cauterize .i. cautere entre la forcele et lou col, et .ij. petis cauteres un poc en dessendant en la partie qui est desoz la barbe; et .ij. cauteres entre la quinte coste et la sisime, en declinant derrier un poc; et .i. cautere emmi le pis, et .i. autre sus l’estomac, et .i. entre .ij. espaules, et .ij. as .ij. costez dou pis defuers le cautere qui est entre .ij. espaules; et ne presser mie ta main, ains fai apertement ausi com en odorant.	The ancient ones said that one should perform cauterizations on pleurisy using roots of aristolochia, and in this way: take a long root of aristolochia, the largest one you can find, and let it be dry, and also as thick and long as your fingers; moisten it with oil, put it into fire, and cauterize one cautery between the armpit and the neck, and two small cauteries a little below in the area beneath the beard; two cauteries between the fifth costal cartilage and the sixth, declining slightly behind a little; one cautery on the side, and one other on the stomach, and one between the shoulders, and two at the sides of the shoulder away from the cautionery that is between the shoulders; do not press your hand tightly, but act gently as when smelling.
Et dirent aucun ancien que aucun home usent de cautere de feir semblant a .i. raseur, et l’eschaufent et le mettent entre les costes, tant qu’il vient a cel aposteme; et saut fuers li dolor, si com nos avons dit en l’aposteme dou foie. Mais en cestui ovraige est paour ou li malaides muert maintenant, ou fistule i vient qui ne puet estre sanee.	And some ancient ones said that a person uses a cautery resembling .i. razor, and they heat it up and put it between the ribs until it reaches an abscess; then the pain subsides, as we have said in the abscess of the liver. But in this work there is fear or the patient dies now, or a fistula comes which cannot be healed.
de la mice	of the mouse
Quant tu cures la maladie de la mice de ceu que nos avons dit as divisions des cures, et il ne profite mie, adonques i afierent .iij. manieres de cautere que tuit sont boin.	When you treat the disease of the mice as we have said in the divisions of treatment, and it does not improve, then there are three ways of cautery that are good.
Desquelz li une maniere si est que tu faices .iij. cauteres, ou .iiij., en lignant selonc la longor de la mice, selonc la figure dou cautere dou foie que nos avons dit devant; et n’apresser mie ta main a tout le cautere, et soit li malaides sovins sor son dos;	The first way is that you make four cauterizations, or eight, in lining according to the length of the mice, according to the shape of the cautery of the liver as we have said before; and do not press your hand on the entire cautery, and let the patient be aware on his back.
et une autre maniere de cautere si est que tu eschaufe le cautere qui a .ij. ners, si com nos l’avons mostreit en la dislocation de l’espaule; et lieve le keur qui est endroit la mice, ou li coutes dou malaide vient devers senestre, et soit li elevations dont tu lieves le keur selonc la keur, selonc la longesce dou cors, et li cautere soient selonc la largesce dou cors.	And another way of cautery is that you heat the cautery with two nerves, as we have shown in the dislocation of the shoulder; and lift the curve which is towards the mice, where the patient's pain comes from the left, and raise the elevations from which you lift the curve according to the length of the body, and the cautery should be according to the width of the body.
Aprés i boute les .ij. ners enflamez tant que li keurs soit perciez de l’autre part, et puis trai fuers le cautere, et ensi en i avra .iiij. Et se tu vues, si cauterize a tot le cautere a .iij. ners. Aprés le cure quant il a geteit porriture par lonc tens, et ce vaut mues que li autre des cures devant dites.	After heating the 2 nerves inflamed to the point where their cores are pierced from the other side, then pull out the cautery and thus it will have 4 (pieces). If you see, cauterize the entire cautery on 3 nerves. After healing when it has discharged pus for a long time, this is worth noting that the other treatments mentioned earlier should be done first.
de ydropisie	After removing the water from the bladder by applying pressure and allowing it to empty, then place a hot poultice on the bladder for three days and nights and cover it with cloths. Then remove the poultice and clean the wound with wine and salt.
Cautere ne vaut a ydropique, fors c’a la maniere qui est apelee «asclytes». Quant tu la cures selonc les manieres que nos avons dit en divisions, et ta cure ne profite mie, adonques covient il que tu li faices .iiij. cauteres entor la boude, et .i. sus l’estomac, et un sus le foie, et .i. sus la mice, et .ij. derrier le dos sus l’espinee, et .i. endroit le pis; et soit li cauteres bien pres de l’espés dou keur.	Cautere is not useful for bladder stones, except in the method called "asclytes". When you treat it according to the methods we have described in divisions, and your treatment does not work, then you must make 4 cauteries around the bladder, one on the stomach, one on the liver, one on the spleen, two behind the back near the spine, and one on the kidney; and let the cauteries be close to the base of the bladder.
Aprés laisse le cautere aovert por giter porriture lonc tens, et ne lassier mie la cure dou malaide aprés le cautere; et sanation se hasterait, et seront ensamble les .ij. ententions avec l’aide de Deu.	After letting the fire cautery heal for a long time, do not neglect the care of the patient after the cautery; and healing would hasten, and the two intentions (healing and God's help) would be united.
Li forme dou cautere por le ventre soit li clavile que nos avons devant mostreit; et cil por le dos soit olivaire, selonc ceu qu’il est ci devant mis.	The form of the cautery for the belly is like the key that we have shown before; and for the back it is olive-shaped, as it has been mentioned before.
de l’enfleure des piez	of the swelling of the feet
Quant li piez sont enflez a celui qui est ydropique, et sont plain d’awe citrine, il covient que tu cauterizes sus le dos dou piet entre l’auriculaire et l’anulaire; et lieve ta main avec le cautere sens torner. Et n’entrer mie trop em parfont, ensi sarrait fuers li awe citrine, et soit li cauteres selonc cest forme:	When the feet are swollen in someone who is edematous, and filled with citrus juice, it must be cauterized on the back of the foot between the little finger and the ring finger; and dip your hand with the cautery without turning. And do not enter too deeply, otherwise the citrus juice will burst out, and let the cautery be shaped as follows:
Aprés fai sus .ij. jambes .ij. cauteres en chescune jambe a la pointe dou cutellaire; et soit li cauteres dou lonc, l’un desoz le genoil devant et l’autre defuers, enmi la jambe; et laisse les cauteres aovers longement sens curer, que li awe en isse; aprés le cure des autres cures que nos avons dit.	After doing two cauteries on each leg with the tip of the knife; let one of the cauteries be behind the knee and the other outside the leg; and leave the cauteries above for a long time to heal, as the citrus juice is in it; after healing the other wounds that we have mentioned.
de la menoison	of the treatment
Quant solution de ventre vient de froidor et de moistor, tant que li vertus retentive et digestive qui est ou stomac et en l’intestine est afleboie, et ne puet estre curez par manieres de cures; et tu vois le malaide bien soffrant et de fort vertut, si fai .i. grant cautere sus l’estomac selonc ceu qu’il en a parleit ci devant ou cautere de l’estomac, au cautere circule; et .iiij. cauteres entor la boude subtilz a tout .i. cautere clavile subtil, et .ij. cauteres sus les hainches.	When the hernia of the abdomen comes from cold and moisture, while the digestive and retentive virtues that are in the stomach and intestine are obstructed, and cannot be cured by means of treatments; and you see the patient suffering greatly and of strong constitution, do this: make one large cautery on the stomach as described earlier, the cautery of the stomach, around the circumference; and four subtle cauteries around the abdomen, one subtle cautery each on the flanks.
Et se tu vois les moistors habundans et le malaide soffrant, se li fai cautere sus le poignil, et .i. cautere sus chaicun yle, et .ij. petis cauteres sus l’estomac delez le grant, car li cure est profitans quant il i a bone aide.	And if you see the moisture abundant and the patient suffering, do cautery on the joint, and one cautery on each finger, and two small cauteries on the stomach in place of the large one, for the cure is beneficial when there is good aid.
de la cure des emorroydes	On the treatment of hemorrhoids
