Quant les emorroydes sont ou fondement, ou une ou plusors, et sont ancienes et sont de grosses humors froides et moistes corrumpues, et sont curees si com nos avons dit en divisions, et il ne profite mie, si fai cauteres: .iij. sus l’espine dou dos, celi qui est tout defuers desoz almecdate poc et poc en triangulant, et .i. cautere desoz la boude. ij. dois;	When hemorrhoids are founded, either one or several, and are old and are of large, cold and corrupted humors, and are cured as we have said in divisions, it does not benefit if cauteries are done: 4 on the spine of the back, which is completely turned out below the coccyx and point by point triangulating, and 1 caution beneath the anus. 2 times;
et se tu penses que ses estomac soit refroidiez, et li viande ne cuise, et on voit enfler la faice, adonques li faice on .i. grant cautere sus le stomac, si com il est devant dit, et .i. autre sus le foie, et i. autre sus la mice a tout le cautere clavile; et laisse le cautere overt lonc tens. Aprés cure le leu tant qu’il soit sanez.	If you think his stomach is cooled and the meat does not cook, and swelling of the face is observed, then one large caution is done on the stomach as previously mentioned, and another on the liver, and another on the spleen with a long incision; and leave the caution open for a long time. After curing the place until it is healed.
de la charnositeit qui est nommee «thelul»	of the flesh growth which is called "thelul"
Quant tu copes althelul, si eschaufe le cautere qui semble .i. raseur, et puis le met tout embraseit sus cel althelul copeit; et i laisse tant ta main que li cauteres viegne a la naissance de la voine, de coi li sans cort; fai ceu une fois ou .ij., et s’il i a mout d’althelul, si cauterize chaicun si com nos avons dit; aprés les cure d’oignemens profitans tant qu’il soient sanez; et se tu cauterizes d’un cautere grant sus alchatim, si avra plus grant aide.	When you apply althelul, heat the cautery which seems like a razor, and then place it entirely over the althelul-coated wound; leave your hand so that the cautery reaches the vein opening, thus burning the wound; do this once or twice, and if there is much of althelul, cauterize each time as we have said; afterwards, cure with herbs until they are healed; and if you cauterize a large cautery over blisters, it will provide more aid.
de plaie mal curee	of an improperly healed wound
Quant li malaides ne puet soffrir tailleure ne overture, que nos raconterons en son leu, si vient teil maladie que ne puet estre sanee fuer que par cautere.	When the patient cannot tolerate incision or opening, as we will explain in its place, this illness occurs that can only be healed by cauterization.
Quant a aucun vient fistule, et est enveillie et giete porriture et moistors corrumpues, si la doies prover a tot une tente subtil, et garde que tu saiches a tot la tente combien elle a de parfont. Aprés eschaufe le cautere qui semble .i. raseur, et le boute en la fistule selonc la quantiteit que li tente i est entrée, et rencomence lou cautere tant que cil cors porris et corrumpus soient ars, une fois, ou .ij. ou .iij., selonc la quantiteit de som besoing; et te warde d’ardre lé nerf qui sunt enqui, et des grans voinnes. se li fistule vait au cors de la vesie et a l’intestine, si te warde de ces leus, et ne faire ceu fuers que en leu charnut, et pense qu’ele n’est mie persans; aprés cure le leu tant qu’il soit sanez, et se li leus est saielez, et les matieres sont ostees lonc tens, adonc saiches que li leus est sanez entierement; et se les matieres ne sont ostees, saiche que li leus est troez, et corrumpus li os au font; et ensi com un de ces que nos dirons en son leu.	When any fistula comes, and it is swollen and filled with pus and corrupt moisture, you should probe it thoroughly with great subtlety, and be aware of the extent to which it has become full. After heating the cautery that resembles a razor, insert it into the fistula according to the size that the pus has entered, and continue the cauterization until the flesh burns and becomes corrupt, once or twice or thrice, depending on the amount of pus required; be careful not to burn the nerves and large veins. If the fistula goes towards the body of the bladder and intestines, be careful with these areas, and do not do anything outside the charnut area, thinking it is not dangerous; after curing the area until it is healed, if the area is ulcerated or the matter has been removed for a long time, then know that the area is completely healed; if the matter has not been removed, know that the area is closed and the bone is corrupted in the process; and so with one of these as we will say in its place.
de la maladie des reins	Kidney disease
Quant dolor de froit vient as rains, et de grosse ventositeit, et ne prent talant de femme, adonc covient il que tu li fais cautere sus les rains d’une part et d’autre au cautere clavile que nos avons devant dit; et se nos le cauterizons em mileu, si avra .iij. cauteres en ligne, et se feront plus grant aide.	When cold pain comes to the kidneys, accompanied by large swelling, and does not take on female form, then it requires cautery over the kidneys on both sides with the cautery described earlier; and if we cauterize it in the middle, it will have four cauteries in a line, and will provide more assistance.
de la vessie	of the bladder
Quant li vessie est mole et foible de froit et de moistor, si que li malaides retient l’urine, adonc li fai cautere en la partie defuers sus la vessie, la ou encomencent li poil dou poignil, et .i. a destre et .i. a senestre, et soit chescuns cauteres si lons com li nous d’un poce; et li fais .i. cautere defuers le dos, ou .ij. se tu en as besoing; et soit li cauteres clavile selon la forme devant dite.	When the bladder is soft and weak from cold or moisture, causing the patient to retain urine, then make a cautery on the area outside of the bladder, where the pubic hair begins, one on the right side and one on the left, both as long as our thumb; and make one incision on the back, or two if necessary; and let the incisions be like the shape mentioned before.
de la marris	of the kidney
Quant li marrix est froide et moiste, et ne laisse mie por ceu a concevoir, et les flors sont corrumpues et lor termines tarde; et quant elles vienent, si sent grant dolor: adonques covient il c’on li faice .iij. cauteres entor la boude, si com nos avons dit ou cautere de la vessie, et .ij. cauteres defuers le dos; et soit li cauteres clavile, si com nos avons dit.	When the matrix is cold and moist and does not allow conception, and the flowers are corrupted and their terms delay; and when they come, they feel great pain: then it is necessary to apply four cauteries around the womb, as we have said (cautere of the bladder), and two cauteries behind the back; and may the cauteries be sharp, as we have said.
de la hainche	When the loins are cold and moist, and do not allow conception, and the seed is corrupted and its term prolonged; and when it comes, it causes great pain: then it is necessary to apply four cauteries around the flanks, as we have said (cautere of the bladder), and two cauteries behind the back; and may the cauteries be sharp, as we have said.
Quant les moistors viscouses dessendent a la boiste de la hainche, et por ceste cause si se muet de son leu, et li signes est que li cuisse est plus longe que li autre quant on le mesure ensamble; et est trovez li leus dou departement vuis, si covient que tu cauterizes le malaide sus la boiste de la hainche a .i. cautere semblant au cercle, et seigne devant le leu entor la boiste si com elle torne, si que li boiste soit dedens le cercle; et si soit li cauteres telz com cil dont on a cauterizeit le stomac.	When the viscous fluids descend into the belly of the loins, and because of this it moves away from its place, and the signs are that one thigh is longer than the other when measured together; and the joints are found to be dislocated, if so you must cauterize the patient on the belly of the loins with one cautery resembling a circle, and sign in front of the joint around the belly so that the belly is within the circle; and may the cautery be like those used to cauterize the stomach.
Et se cist cauteres ne t’est presens, se li fai .iij. cauteres de l’olivaire grans, et soit li cauteres ausi parfont com tous li keurs; et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if this fire cautery is not present for you, make 4 large olive oil cauteries and let them be as perfect as all the others; and apply it until it is healed.
de la dolor de la hainche	of the pain from the hernia
Quant dolor vient en la boiste de la hainche, et c’est de froidor et de moistor, et li malaides est curez de ceu que nos avons dit en la division et li cure ne vaut, et li maladie est anciene: adonc covient il que tu purges le malaide des grosses humors de pilules fetides, ou autres pilules bones semblans.	When pain comes in the area of the hernia, and it is caused by coldness and moisture; and the patient is cured with what has been said in the division, but the treatment is not effective, and the illness is old: then you must purge the patient from the thick humors using fetid pills or other good-seeming pills.
Aprés li fai cautere; et li maniere dou cautere si est selonc .ij. manieres: c’est a savoir ensamble medicines ardans, et cautere de feu. Cautere de feu si est selonc mout de manieres, desquelz li uns est telz: que tu cauterize sus la boiste de la hainche .iij. cauteres triangulalz selonc ceste forme, et i fai bone profunditeit et grant, et ait entre chaicun cautere d’espaice la groissece d’un doi, et soit li cauteres olivaire; aucune fois fait on cautere en mileu sus lou chief de la hainche, por coi il en i a .iiij. selonc ceste forme:	After the cautery, the method of the cautery is according to two ways: namely with burning medicines, and cautery of fire. The cautery of fire is according to many ways, of which one is such: you should cauterize on the boil of the haunch four triangular cauteries according to this form, and make it a good depth and large, and have space between each cautery the size of a thumb, and the cauteries should be olive-shaped; sometimes a cautery is made in the middle on the head of the haunch, for which there are four according to this form:
Et se tu vues, si le cauterize au cautere dou cercle que nos avons devant dit en la dislocation de la hainche; mais fai en teil maniere que li cercles conteigne toute la hainche, et tous li espés dou keur soit ars.	And if you wish, cauterize the cautery of the circle that we have previously mentioned in the dislocation of the haunch, but make it so that the circles encompass the entire haunch, and all the fat surrounding it is burned.
Et c’est li maniere c’on fait en sciatique, quant li dolor tient en la hainche, et ne parvient mie jusc’a la cuisse ne jusc’a la jambe. Et s’ele vient jusc’a la cuisse et la jambe, se li fai .ij. cauteres lai ou li malaides dit que li dolor li tient, et .i. cautere desus la cheville .iiij. dois, a la partie senestre un poc; et soit li cauteres cutellaire, et soit arse li espesseté dou keur; et se li malaides sent que li dolor s’estende jusc’a dois dou piet ou pres d’enqui, se le cauterize la ou il sent la dolor .iij. poins ou .iiij. au cautere qui est apelez «poins».	And this is the method used in sciatica when the pain remains in the haunch and does not reach the thigh or the leg. If it reaches the thigh and the leg, two cauteries are made where the patient says that the pain is, and one cautery above the ankle four fingers wide, on the left side a little bit; and let the cauteries be scissor-shaped, and burn the fat surrounding it; if the patient feels that the pain extends to two fingers or less of the foot, cauterize there where he feels the pain two or three fingers depending on the cautery called "poins".
Et se mestiers est, se li en fai plus; et se il seit que li dolor soit desoz le genoil vers la cuisse, se li fais cautere au cautere cutellaire ou circulaire, et te done bien garde en tous tes cauteres que tu n’i lassier mie tant le cautere que tu brules les ners et les grans arteres, et que tu ne faices au malaide plus grant nuisance et contraction.	And if necessary, do more; and if the pain is below the knee towards the thigh, make a fire cautery with a cutlery or circular cautery, and be very careful in all your cauteries not to let the cautery burn nerves and large arteries, and not to cause greater harm and contraction to the patient.
Et je meisme ai veus plusors qui ont fait cautere sus la cheville dou piet, et li lasserent tant que li jambe fut toute enflee, et li piez ausi, et fut perciez et corrumpus toz li piez. Aprés une solution de ventre dont il ot la mort.	I have also seen many who made a cautery on the ankle of the foot and let it burn too much so that the leg was all swollen, and the toes as well, and they were pierced and corrupted in all the toes. After an abdominal solution, death followed.
Et se li dolors est en .ij. parties ensamble, fai cautere en l’une et en l’autre, selonc ceste maniere. // Et li saige dirent en la cautere de la hainche, de coi ci est li maniere, fai .i. tel fer et soit au chief ausi gros com uns nauvillon de dacte, ou un poc moins, et soit par entrechetres et soit des l’un entrechetres jusc’a l’autre d’espaice la quantiteit d’un nou de poce; et soient li entrechetres aovers de .ij. pars, et soient aussi comme noez, et i ait .i. mainche de fer bien fait; et c’est li forme:	And if the pain is in two places at once, make a cautery in one and the other, as follows. // The wise say about the cautery of the neck, here is how it is done, make a rod of iron that is as thick as a little nail of a thumb or a bit less, and let it be between-the-crossbars or let it be from one between-the-crossbar to the other at a distance equal to a nut of the fist; and let the between-the-crossbars be two fingers wide and shaped like nuts, and there should be a single handle of iron well made; and this is its shape:
Et soit eschaufez tant qu’il soit toz rouges et giete senteles, et puis le mette on sus la boiste de la hainche malaide, et soit tornez sus lou sain costeit; et lou cauterize une fois .i. cautere reont et lou laisse .iij. jors; et puis fai emplaustre de burre, et laisse la plaie aoverte lonc tens; aprés la cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez.	And let it be scorched until it is all red and blistered, and then place it on the sick person's bed, turning it towards the healthy side; and cauterize once with one hot iron and leave it for 3 days; then make a plaster of butter, and keep the wound open for a long time; after that, treat it with ointment until it is healed.
Albucasim dit que nos usons poc de cest cautere por la paor de son regart, et se voions poc qui en usent; et toutevoie ceu est des boins cauteres, qui le puet soffrir, et lai ou il s’afiert.	Albucasim says that we should use this cautery sparingly due to fear of its appearance, and not many seem to use it; nevertheless, this is a good cautery for those who can endure it, and in places where it adheres.
de la dolor dou dos	of the pain in the back
Quant dolor vient au dos, ou par cheoir ou de percussion ou par trop grant evacuation, ou par semblans de matiere espandue froide, a nule de ces semblances ne vaut cauteres, fuer que a celi qui vient de infusion de froide matiere.	When pain comes to the back, whether from falling or from striking or excessive bleeding, or from similar causes of cold matter spreading, none of these cases are worth cauterization except for that caused by infusion of cold matter.
Il covient c’aprés ceu que li malaides est voidiez de pilules fetides ou d’autres semblans, que on li faice sus lou dos, lai ou li dolor tient, trois lignes signies d’enche, et en chescune ligne .v. cauteres ou plus selonc la vertut et la quantiteit que li malaides puet soffrir; et soit fait li cauteres selonc le cautere qui est apelez «poins»; et se tu vues, fai .iij. cauteres ou .iiij. au cautere clavile moien selonc ceste forme:	Afterward, the patient should be purged of foul pills or similar substances applied to the back where the pain is located, three lines marked with incense, and in each line 5 or more cauterizations depending on the potency and quantity that the patient can bear; and the cauterization should be done according to the cauterization called "poins"; and if you see, do 4 cauterizations or 3 according to the medium clavicle cauterization in this form:
Maintes fois vient ceste maladie as petis enfans, et li signes de l’encomencement si est qu’il ont estroite alainne quant il se lievent, et paor; et tu trueves en la derriene espinee dou dos et en nous l’apparance qui vient sus les autres espinees.	Often, this disease comes to small children, and the signs of its beginning are that they have a narrow anus when they defecate, and fear; and you find in the lower spine of the back and in us the appearance that comes above the other spines.
Quant tu vois ceu et tu le vues curer, si le cauterize au cautere de celcle selonc ceste forme.	When you see this and you intend to cure it, if you cauterize it with the cautery of that kind according to this form.
Si que li cautere porpreigne chescune partie de l’espinee egaument. Et se tu vues, si cauterize entor l’espinee au cautere poignant .ij. lignes ou .iij., et soient li poins pres l’uns de l’autre. Aprés cure le leu tant qu’il soit sanez selonc ceu que nos avons dit, et warde que tu n’amenistrer cautere en gilbositeit qui soit en spame de nerf.	The cautery should reach each part of the spine in length. And if you see, if you cauterize around the spine with a pointed cautery .2 or .3 inches, and the points should be close to one another. After curing the place until it is healed as we have said, be careful not to apply caution in a gillboise state that is in the nerve's splay.
de la dolor des jointes	of the pain of the joints
Quant dolor de jointes sunt de moistors que sont espandues a chaicun membre dou cors, et quant dolor vient em piez, que li mire apelent «podagre» proprement, et quant elle est de froide cause et cures de medicines ne la puent curer, si est curez par cauteres en teil maniere: fai li mout de cauteres entor la jointure dou piet, et soit li cauteres olivaire selonc ceste forme:	The pain of the joints is due to swellings which are present in every member of the body. When it comes in the feet (they call it podagry properly), and when it is caused by cold and medicines cannot cure it, then it is cured by cauteries as follows: make the patient ready for the cautery around the joint of the foot, and let the cautery be olive oil-shaped according to this form:
Et s’il i a besoigne que tu poignes sus la faice dou piet, se li fai cautere a tot le cautere c’on claime «point». Et se les dolors viegnent jusc’a genous et as autres jointures, et ceu avient maintes fois, se li fai cautere sus chaicun genoil .iij. cauteres ou .iiij. de chescunne partie, a tout le cautere olivaire; et se tu as mestier de plus, si en fai plus, mais n’i tenir mie ta main fuers que tant que li espés dou keur soit ars.	And if it is necessary to prick on the face of the foot, make a cautery all over the area that people call "point". If pains come up to the knees and other joints (this happens many times), then make a cautery on each knee. Make four olive-shaped cauteries or four for each part, all around the cautery. And if more is needed, do more, but do not hold your hand outside the area longer than the tips of the coals are burning.
Et se les dolors dessendent jusc’a genoil et au dos, se li aministre le cautere que nos avons dit en son chapistre. Et se les dolors sunt as mains, si fai poins entor le foscile .ij. lignes; et s’il remaint point de dolor as dois, si fai poins sus chescune jointe et sus lou poil de la main; et se les dolors vienent jusc’as coutes ou jusc’as espaules, si cauterize chescune partie, et fai boin governement au malaide et penre medicines. Car se tu li fais boin governement et tu purges fleume, si sera saneis a l’aide de Deu.	And if the pains descend to the genitals and back, administer the cautery as we have said in its chapter. If the pains are at the hands, make pricks around the fingernails; and if there remains no pain at the thumbs, make pricks on each joint and on the hair of the hand; and if the pains come to the sides or shoulders, cauterize each part, and pay good attention to the patient and think about medicines. For if you take good care of him and purge phlegm, he will be healed by the aid of God.
de la routure dou syfac	of the swelling of the face
Quant routure vient en angres, et li bouelz dessendent as coions et c’est novelement, si covient que quant tu lou vues curer, qu’il ne menjuce mie celui jor; et qu’il use choses qui laichent lou ventre, si que li fiens dessende de son ventre; aprés le fai seoir sus son dos entre tes mains, et li comande qu’il teigne son alaine tant que li boueil soient repairiet, et les ramoinne a tes dois, et seigne d’enche desoz la routure sus l’os dou poignil, et a tout un signe que soit semblans a la moitiet d’un cercle a desus dou cors; puis eschaufe le cautere de coi ci est li forme:	When swelling comes in anger and the boils descend into the eyes and it is suddenly occurring, if you see it when you want to cure it, you must not let him eat on that day; and he should use things that loosen his stomach, so that phlegm descends from his stomach. After that, make him sit on his back between your hands, and command him to hold his elbow as long as the boils are protruding, and rearrange them to your fingers, and sign on top of the swelling over the bone of the wrist, and at all one sign that is similar to half a circle above the chest; then heat the cautery in the shape shown here:
tant qu’il soit blans et qu’il giete senteles. Puis ramoine les bouels a lor leu; et li ministres teigne sa main sus qu’il ne retornent arrier; et oevre bien les cuisses au malaide, et met desoz lui .i. cussin et .i. serjant sus les cuisses, et .i. autre sus lou pis qui li teigne les mains; puis met le cautere sus lou signe a tout ta main, et lou tien droit et lou tien tant que tu ateignes l’os, et se tu ne l’ateins la premiere fois, si le rencomence encor une autre tant que tu viegnes jusc’a l’os; et te warde subtilment que li boueil ne saille quant tu fais lou cautere; que tu ne le brulasses; et que par ceu li malaides ne muere, ou autre malz.	Keep the hairs long and even while it is white and exudes pus. Then you should realign the dislocated shoulder; and have the assistant hold their hand on top so that they do not return to their original position. Work well on the patient's thighs, put one cushion and one sergeant on the thighs, and another on the affected area where the hands are held; then place the cautery on the affected spot all over your hand, hold it straight and continue until you reach the bone. If you do not reach the bone the first time, try again until you reach the bone. Be careful that the dislocated shoulder does not slip out while performing the cauterization; that you do not burn it; and that the patient does not die or suffer other harm.
Et saiches que quant tu ne viens jusc’a l’os au cautere, tes ovraiges ne vaut rien. Et covient que li cauteres des enfans soit subtilz selonc la mesure d’ous, et des grans gens aussi grans selonc lor mesure; aprés .iij. jors cure lou leu dou cautere de burre tant que li eschaudure soit ostee; aprés le cure d’autres oignemens tant qu’il soit sanez, et gise li malaides .xl. jors sus son dos tant que li plaie soit bien soudee; et covient que ses norrissemens soit lassatis longement, si que li boueil ne saillent quant il se preigdra d’aler en chambres.	And know that when you do not reach the bone with the cautery, your work is worthless. The cauteries for children should be subtle according to their age, and for adults as big as them; after four days, cure the burn caused by the cautery with butter until the blistering is removed; then cure it with other medicaments until it heals, and keep the patient lying on his back for forty days so that the wound heals well. It is necessary that his urine be allowed to flow slowly, so that the dislocated shoulder does not slip out when he tries to get up from bed.
Et aprés .xl. jors, quant il se voudra lever, se li amenistre une faixe bien faite, et la porse .xl. autres jors; et ait boin repos, qu’il se travaille poc et se warde de trop grant repletion de boivre et de mengier, et de trop haut braire; et quant il fait cest enseignement si est sanez entierement. Et je dirai ci aprés la cure de taillier en son chapistre.	And after forty days, when he wants to get up, bring him a well-made splint and let it stay for another forty days; he should have good rest, avoiding excessive work, and watch out for too much drinking and eating, and excessive shouting; if he follows this guidance, he will be completely healed. And I will tell you about the cure of amputation in its chapter later.
de la routure dou ventre	From the rupture of the abdomen
Quant routures vienent en autres ventres et sont connisans, et tu vues qu’elles ne croissent plus, se li fai .j. cautere dou cautere reont selonc sa quantiteit, et soit ars li tiers dou keur; aprés le cure selonc ceu que nos avons dit; et aucun des anciens ont dit c’on le doit cauterizer au cautere a .iij. angles selonc ceste forme:	When ruptures occur in other bellies and are known, and you see that they do not grow anymore, make one cautery incision according to its size, and burn the third part of the body; after that, cure it as we have said; and none of the ancients say that it should be cauterized with a cautery at four angles according to this form:
mais signe premier le leu d’enche et fai une ligne per la largesce desus la routure, et une autre defuers, et main ta main emmi a tout le cautere clavile. Mais li premiers cauteres est plus legiers et muedres.	But first sign the location of the incision and make a line above the rupture, and another below, and place your hand on the entire cautery handle. However, the first cauteries are lighter and more movable.
de dolor anciene en aucun membre	From ancient pain in any limb
Quant dolor vient en aucun membre, ou de cheoir ou de ferir, et cele dolor tient lonc tens, et li cure de medicine n’i vaut, adonc covient qu’il soit cauterizeis au cautere qui est apelez «poins», et soit li cauteres selonc la longesce dou membre et la petitece et sa foibleteit et sa vertut et sa location de torcions et de sa dolor. s’il est sanez dou premier cautere, c’est bien; se ceu nom, recomence .i. autre cautere sus celui, car teilz costume est qu’il se doit muer au membre que li est prochiens, por coi il covient que tu faices les cauteres tant que li malaides soit saneis.	When pain comes in any member, either due to falling or injury, and that pain lasts for a long time, and medicine does not heal it, then it should be cauterized with the cautery called "poins", and the cauteries should be done according to the length of the member, its smallness, frailty, virtue, location of twisting, and pain. If it heals from the first cauterization, that is good; if not, repeat one more cauterization on top of it, for it is customary that it should change in the member that is near, so you must do the cauteries until the patient is healed.
de meselerie	When mixing medicines, be careful to measure each ingredient accurately and mix them well, so as not to create an incorrect or ineffective remedy.
Li meseil sont aidiet aucune fois par cautere par grant aide, et meismement li maladie que vient de la putrefaction de fleume et de melancolie. Cant tu la vues cauterizer, pren warde se li maladie est au comencement, et s’ele est curee selonc ceu que nos avons dit en la division, et ne dessent ne ne demoure, et tu doutes que li corruption ne porpreigne tout le malaide, adonques li fai .v. cauteres sus lou chief: .i. emmi le chief a nouf, et l’autre vers lou front a la fin des chevous; et .ij. sus les .ij. cornes, et .i. derrierre sus le haiterel; et i laise tant ta main que li cauteres viegne jusc’a l’os, et tant que les escorces en issent fors si que les vapors des grosses humors s’en puissent issir; et le cauterize sus la mice selonc ce qu’il est devant.	The following text describes the use of cautery in treating certain diseases, such as those caused by putrefaction of the fluids and melancholy. When cauterizing, it is important to be careful that the disease is at an early stage and has been properly treated according to what has been said in the division. If there is doubt that the corruption will not spread throughout the patient, perform five cauteries on the head: one at the nape of the neck, another at the end of the hairline on the forehead; two on each temple; and one behind the ears. Leave your hand in place so that the cautery reaches the bone and the scabs come out, allowing the vapors of the thick humors to escape. Cauterize the mice according to what is appropriate for its condition.
Et se li meselerie est partout esparse; et elle pert manifestement, si covient que tu lou cauterizes de ces cauteres que nos avons dit ou chief, et .i. cautere en som lou neis, et .ij. cauteres sus l’espinee dou col, et .vj. cauteres sus l’espinee dou dos, et .i. grant sus la crupie et .i. autre delez, et .ij. sus les .ij. espaules; et .ij. sus les coutes, et .ij. sus les tendrons dou pis, et .i. sus chascune jointe des mains et des piez, et sus les fosses des mains; et te warde des ners que sunt sus lou derrien calcant, que tu ne les bruler; et aucune fois fait om cautere sus l’os dou poignil, et .i. autre sus l’os de l’estomac, et .i. autre sus lou foie.	And if the flesh is scattered everywhere; it is clearly rotten, you must cauterize with the cauteries that we have said, namely one cautery on the neck, two cauteries on the spine of the neck, six cauteries on the spine of the back, one large one on the crotch and another small one, two on each shoulder, two on the sides, two on the tendons of the feet, one on each joint of the hands and feet, and on the hollows of the hands; and beware of nerves that are above the last calcaneum, do not burn them; and sometimes a cautery is made on the bone of the thumb, and one other on the bone of the stomach, and one other on the liver.
Et saiches que quant plus i fais de cautere, plus li fais d’aide, et mues li profite; et saiches que li malaides ne sent point de dolor au cautere si com li sain le sentent, por ce que li cors est ja toz corrumpus. Et covient ke li cautere soient grant et petit selonc les membres et les jointures, selonc ceu que vos lou troverez en manieres des fers. Aprés cure lou leu de farine de veces avec miel et autres cures tant qu’il soit saneis.	And know that the more you make of cauterization, the more help it provides, and it benefits him; and know that the sick do not feel pain from cauterization as the healthy do, because the body is already completely corrupted. It is necessary that the cautery be large and small according to the members and joints, according to what you will find in the art of iron-working. After curing the leprosy with flour several times with honey and other treatments until it heals.
de enfleure	inflammation or swelling
Quant enfleure vient en aucun membre et est curee par medicines et oiles et emplastres, et il n’est mie sanez, adonques li fai cauteres sus le membre selonc la grandour et la petitece dou membre; et soit li cauteres un poc entrans en l’espés dou keur; puis le cure d’oignemens tant qu’il soit sanez. Et aucune fois fait on cautere et a la main et au piet et au dos, a l’issue dou nerf que muet le membre, et ensi si est ostee li enfleure; et toutevoie ne s’en entremette nuls s’il n’est conoissans des membres et des issues des ners movans lou cors.	When swelling arises in any member and is treated with medicines, oils, and plasters but remains unhealed, then cauterization should be applied to the member according to its size and smallness; and the cautery should be a small amount inserted into the flesh's depth. Then cure it with herbs until it heals. And sometimes a cauterization is performed on hand, foot, back, at the nerve's issue that stops movement in the member, thus removing the swelling; but no one should interfere unless they are knowledgeable about members and the issues of moving nerves of the body.
de albaras	If a worm falls into the eye, you must put the infected eye into vinegar to make it sleep for a while, and then take out the worm with tweezers; if the worm does not come out, you should apply oil of roses or camomile to the eye.
Quant li maladie qui est apelee «albaras» est enveillie, et li engien de medicine n’i valent rien, adonques le cauterize d’un cautere un poc parfont, selonc la quantiteit de l’espés dou keur, tant que li blenchour soit ostee, et soit muee sa color; puis le cure de farine de veces et de lentilles avec oile roset et foilles de plantain, et sanc de colon et sanc d’alondre, de chescun une partie; et soit mellez tout ensamble, et soit liiez d’un drapel, et soit aers au leu tant qu’il soit sanez.	When the illness called "albaras" appears and the devices of medicine are useless, then cauterize it with a deep cautery, according to the thickness of the flesh, until the white spot is removed, and the color changes; then cure it with flour and lentils with rose oil and plantain leaves, blood of cattle and blood of almonds, each one in equal parts; mix them all together, tie it up in a cloth, and apply it to the place until it heals.
li cure de chancre par cautere	The treatment of syphilis by cautery
Quant chancre vient au comencement, et tu lou vues arrester, si le cauterize au cautere qui semble .i. cercle, tout entor au tour dou chancre.  Et toutevoie li saige dirent que on faice cautere ausi au mileu dou chancre; et toutevoie ceu ne me semble mie boin, car je redous que il ne soit ulcerez et corrumpus, et je l’ai ja veut avenir aucune fois; et plus droituriere chose est qu’il soit cauteriés entor, au cautere qui est apelez «circule», si com nos avons dit en mout de cauteres.	When syphilis begins and you wish to stop it, if you cauterize the cautery that appears as a circle around the edge of the syphilitic sore, according to wise men, they say that you should also cauterize in the middle of the syphilitic sore; but this does not seem right to me, since I fear it will become ulcerated and corrupted, and I have seen this happen once; a more appropriate thing is for it to be cauterized around, using the cautery called "circle", as we said in the section about cauteries.
de l’enfleure qui ne puet meurer	The swelling that cannot heal
Quant aucuns ait une maladie qui est apelee «adubelati», et elle tarde de meurer ou por la superfluiteit qu’ele fait ou por l’eaige dou malaide quant il est decrepites (c’est a dire trop vielz) et il a poc de sanc, ou por lou tens; et tu la vues haster de meurer: adonques le cauterize entor de mout de petis cauteres en poignant; aprés le laisse ensi. Car elle se hastera de meureir.	When someone has a disease called "adubelati", which is slow to heal or due to its superfluity, or because the patient is weakened when old and has little blood, or due to time; and you wish to hasten its healing: then cauterize it with many small cauteries while pricking; after that, leave it. For it will hasten in healing.
Et se tu la vues percier a tout le cautere, si chaufe le cautere de coi ci est li forme:	And if you wish to pierce it with the entire cautery, heat the cautery as follows:
Et met ta main en mileu de cele maladie qui est apellee «adubelati» tant que li cauteres ait perciet lou keur, et soit telz li cauteres que li malaides lou sente defuers en teil maniere que li cours de la porriture soit alegis. Aprés le cure tant qu’il soit sanez parfaitement.	Place your hand in the middle of the disease called "adubelati" until the cautery has pierced the core, and make sure that the cauteries are such that the patient feels it move away from his body in such a way that the course of the pus is cleared. After that, cure it until it is perfectly healthy.
li cure dou feu par fer	The treatment of fire by iron
Une autre maniere de maladie i a qui est apelee «corrodens», et n’est autre chose que une mengeson de membre, car ele menjut les membres ausi com li feus les leignes seches. Se tu vois ceste maladie en leu qui puisse soffrir cautere ensamble feu, adonques eschaufe les cauteres clavile mout petit et grant, selonc ceu qu’il covient au leu ou li maladie est; aprés le cauterize de toutes pars tant que tu erraiche toute la corruption, et nen remaigne rien de li, que tout ceu qui est corrumpus ne soit osteit. Et puis le laisse .iij. jors, et met sus les leus cauterizez soffre broiet avec oile tant que les eschaudures dou feu soient ostees, et toute li corruption. Aprés lou cure d’oignemens engendrans char.  Et se tu vois aprés .iij. jors que chars saine ne naisse, c’est boin; et se ceu non, si rencomence le cautere sus ceu qui est demoreit des leus corrumpus. Et ceste mengeson est aucune fois esteit curee de medicine ague en leu de cautere de feu; mais toutevoie cautere de feu est de plus grant aide, et j’ai ja dit la cure de la medicine ague en la division: pren la quant tu en as mestier.	Another type of disease is called "corrodens," and it is nothing but a rotting of a member, for it eats away at limbs just like fire burns dry wood. If you see this disease in a place that can bear cauterization along with fire, then carefully heat the cauteries, both large and small, according to the place or location where the disease is; after cauterizing all parts until you eradicate all corruption, and nothing of it remains except that what is corrupt is removed. Then let it heal for three days, and apply soothing ointment made from cauterized flesh mixed with oil until the burns caused by fire and all corruption are healed. After the treatment of ointments generates healthy skin. And if you see after three days that healthy skin does not grow, that is good; and if not, repeat the cauterization on the place where the corrupt parts remain. This rotting is sometimes cured with medicines made from wormwood instead of cauterization by fire; but nevertheless, cauterization by fire is more beneficial. I have already said the treatment for the medicine made from wormwood in the division: take as much as you need.
des porrelz qui vienent as piez	sore on the feet
Mout de fois avient que as piez par defuers naist une maladie qui est apelee «clos» selonc nostre entencion, et est une grosse chose fautree qui blece lou piet. Et li cauteres de ceste maladie si est selonc .ij. manieres. C’est a savoir cautere de feu, et cautere d’aigue chaude. Cautere de feu si est que tu eschaufe .i. cautere cheveit ausi com est une penne de vouteul, et soit fait de boin fer a la mesure qu’il puisse porpenre le clou de toutes pars, et qu’il i ait subtilz marges; aprés le met tout chaut sus lou clou, et torne ta main tot entor le clou tant qu’il viegne au font dou clou; et lou laisse ensi .iij. jors tant qu’il encomence giter porriture; puis li fai un emplaustre de malves savaiges broiies avec seil, et laisse l’emplaustre sus toute la nuit, et li clous cherra et sera desracinez de ses racines. Puis cure le leu d’oignement enjanrant char tant qu’il soit sanez.	Very often, in the feet, a disease called "clos" arises according to our understanding, and it is a large thing swelling that afflicts the foot. And the cures for this disease are according to .ij. ways. This includes fire cautery, and water hot cautery. Fire cautery is that you heat .i. cautery comb similar to a feather of a bird, made of good iron of suitable size to penetrate the nail from all sides, and it should have subtle edges; after heating it very hot on top of the nail, turn your hand all around the nail until it reaches the root of the nail; then leave it for 3 days until it begins to emit pus; then make a poultice with foul-smelling herbs ground with oil, and leave the poultice on all night, and the heated iron will become cool and be removed from its roots. Then heal the place with soothing ointment until it is healed.
Et s’il sont convertit par defuers lou cors, et maintes fois avient et en mains et em piez, si covient que tu i amenistres cautere d’aigue chaude; et est en teil maniere: pren une cainne d’arain ou de fer, ou une penne de vouteul, et met sus lou clou et l’althelul, c’est asavoir porrelz verrues; et met la cainne sus si qu’ele porpreigne tout entor, puis i met un poc d’awe chaude, et retien bien ta main, et presse ta main en tornant si que li marge de la cainne viegne a la racine dou clou, et puisse trover l’aigue chaude voie parfonde jusc’a la racine; et soffre li malaides un poc la mordication de l’aigue chaude une houre; puis le laisse ensi, et il se derracinera tous a tout ses racines. Ensi fai un aprés autre, tant que tu esraiches toz ces qui sont au cors, puis les cure des oignemens qui engenrent char.	And if it is converted by the outside of the body, and this often happens in hands and feet, then you should apply water hot cautery; and it is done like this: take a cane made of iron or a feather of a bird, and place it on top of the nail and press it, causing blisters; then place the cane so that it surrounds completely, then put a little hot water there, and hold your hand tightly, pressing your hand while turning so that the edges of the cane reach the root of the nail, and the hot water can penetrate to the root; and let the patient bear the pain of the hot water for an hour; then leave it like this, and it will be uprooted with all its roots. Do the same procedure for all others that are on the body, then heal them with ointments that soothe.
li cure dou trembler	the trembling cures
Quant aucuns tremble de froidor de ners, ou de fievre quartaine ou d’autre, si covient que tu li faices .iiij. cauteres ou .iv. sus l’espinee dou dos, .i. cautere entre chescune espinee; et .i. cautere ou pez, et .i. sus l’estomac au cautere olivaire; si laissera lou trembler, et se hastera li santez de la maladie froide.	When someone shakes from cold or from quartan fever or another illness, you must make 4 or 5 fire cauterizations along the spine of the back, one between each vertebra; and 1 cauterization on the heel, and 1 on the stomach using the olive-oil cauterization; it will stop the trembling, and the health will improve from the cold disease.
des pustules puans	of putrid boils
Aucune fois apperent par defuers le cors bathes, ou pustules puans, que vienent de grosses matieres corrumpues. si covient au premier quant eles apperent que on faice cautere sus chescun chief de la pustule: un cautere subtil de fust de mirte, de coi li pointe soit emprise au feu, ou de racine de aristologe longe, ou au cautere lenticulaire. Et aucune fois les cauterize on au comencement quant il aperent, selonc ceste maniere, et il ne puent croistre des enqui en avant, mais est desrompue li superfluitez dont il vienent, et sont sanez; mais il covient que ceu soit fait aprés l’evacuation de sanc.	Sometimes the body appears swollen with boils that are full of putrid matter. In such cases, at first when they appear, it is necessary to make a cautery on each head of the boil: a subtle cautery made from the myrtle stick, of which the tip is placed in fire or long roots of aristolochia, or with a cauterizing iron. Sometimes they are cauterized at the beginning when they appear according to this manner, and they cannot grow further, but the excess is dissipated from where they come, and they become healthy; however, it must be done after the evacuation of blood.
quant li artere est copee	When the artery is cut
Maintes fois avient grans decorremens de sanc de l’artere qui est copee a la plaie que vient au pardefuers, ou a l’incision de l’aposteme, ou au cautere dou membre, et as semblans choses; et est mout grief chose d’estenchier.	Often there are large internal movements of blood from the cut artery at the wound, or in the incision of an abscess, or in the cautery of a limb, and similar things; it is a very grave thing to let it out.
Et toutevoie quant ceu avient a aucun, si te haste de mettre ton doi indice sus la plaie de la voinne, et l’estrain mout tant que li sans soit apaisiez desoz ton doi, et que goute n’en isse plus; puis met au feu les cauteres olivaire plusors petis et grans tant qu’il soient tuit rouge; puis empren .i., ou grant ou petit selonc la plaie et lou leu en coi li artere est route, et met le cautere sus cele voine ou tu tiens ton doi, et tien le cautere tant sus que li sans soit restainchiez.	Nevertheless, whenever this happens, hasten to put your finger over the opening of the vein, and hold it very tightly so that the blood is stopped under your finger, and no more comes out; then take olive oil-soaked cotton balls of various sizes and apply them until they are all red; then take cotton made from hemp, or large or small according to the size of the wound and the location where the artery is damaged, and apply the cauterized cotton over the vein where you hold your finger, and hold the cauterized cotton in place until the blood is stopped.
Et s’il saut fuers quant tu lieves ton doi desus la voinne, et li cauteres estint, si pren hastivement .i. autre des cauteres qui sont au feu.	And if the limb jumps violently when you place your hand on the vein, and the cautery is applied, take quickly another cautery that is near the fire.
Et ne cesser de faire ceu l’un aprés l’autre tant que li sans soit estenchiez; et warde que tu n’ardes lou nerf qui est delez, et que autre malice ne viegne sus lou malaide; et saiches que quant sans decourt de l’artere, c’on ne lou puet mie bien restenchier meismement quant li artere est grans, se ceu n’est par une des .iiij. manieres que nos avons dit: ou par cautere, ou par extraction quant ele n’est mie traite, ou par fort liement de fil, ou par medicines mises sus qui ont pooir de restenchier sanc; et soit liee et estrainte avennament.	Keep doing one after the other until the blood stops flowing; and be careful not to burn the nerve that is exposed, and ensure no further harm comes to the patient; and know that when the artery is large, it cannot be stopped from bleeding if not through one of the four ways we have mentioned: either by cautery, or extraction if it has not been treated, or by tightly tying a thread, or by medicines placed on it which can stop the blood; and bind and tighten it accordingly.
Qui i amenistrera restenchement de liier estroitement de drapelz ou de metre choses ardans sus, ou autres semblans choses, se n’i profite se poc non.	Whoever brings a tight binding of fabrics or places hot substances on it, or other similar things, if they do not help, will not benefit.
Et se ce avient a aucun et il n’ait mie mire ne medicine present, si doit mettre son doi indice sus la plaie de la voinne si com nos avons dit, et bien estrendre tant qu’il soit restenchiez desus la plaie et desus la voinne; et ne remuer lou doit, mais lou moille d’awe froide sovent que soit mout froide tant que li sans soit congelez et engrossiez et restenchiez; et faice des enqui en avant ceu dont il a mestier de cauteres et de medicines.	And if this happens to anyone who has no mirror or medicine present, you should place your finger on the wound of the vein as we have said, and stretch it out until it is stretched taut over the wound and the vein; and do not move it, but moisten it with cold moisture often so that it becomes very cold until the blood is congealed and thickened and stretched taut; and inquire about the ones in front of whom you need cauteries and medicines.
Ci encomence li secons livre des cures de taille	Here begins the second book of surgical treatments
Nos vos avons dit ou premier chapistre toute maladie en coi il covient cautere de feu, ou de medicine ardans, et les oquisons et les causes et les estrumens et les formes des cauteres; et ai mis celui chapistre des lou chief jusc’a piez, et je irai en cest chapistre par celi meisme voie por ceu c’on trueve plus legierement ceu c’on voura.	We have told you in the first chapter about all diseases in which it is necessary to use fire cautery or hot medicines, and we have explained their types, causes, instruments, and forms of cauterization; and I placed that chapter from the head to the feet, and I will proceed in this chapter along the same path for those who seek it more easily.
Et ainsois que je encomence ceu, il covient, chier fil, que vos aprenez que en cest chapistre a plus de peril et de paor que ou premier des cauteres, et por ceu il covient plus grant cautele.	And therefore, as I begin this, dear son, it is necessary that you learn that in this chapter there is more danger and fear than in the first of the cauteries, and for this reason, greater caution is required.
Car en l’ovraige de cest chapistre avient maintes fois evacuation de sanc a l’ovrir la voinne, et a l’incision sus aposteme, et as cures des plaies, et a l’estraction des saiettes, et a l’incision sus la piere, et les semblans choses; ou il a doutance et paor, et en vient li mors a plusors.	For in the work of this chapter, there is often the evacuation of blood when opening a vein, and incising an abscess, and in the treatment of wounds, and in the extraction of arrows, and in cutting into stones, and similar things; where there is doubt and fear, and many die.
Et je vos amoneste que vos n’entreprenez folie. Car mout de manieres de gens vienent en cures. si vienent de telz qui s’aïrent si avec lor maladie qu’il muerent legierement por la forsenerie qu’il trueve de sa maladie, et de la grandour de son malice; et de ces doit on avoir paor.	And I warn you not to act foolishly. For many kinds of people come seeking cures. Some come who are so sick that they die easily because of the confusion and the greatness of their illness, and of these one should have fear.
Et de ces i a qui te done son sens, et dit: «atendez, je sui garis»; et li maladie est despitouse. Il ne covient mie que vos vos consentez a ces qui vienent a vos qui ont ceste maniere, mais mettez plus grant cusanson en vostre honor qu’en vostre covoitise, et n’ovrez mie folement mais saigement de ceu dont vos estes certain, et dont vos poez avoir pris et los; et usez de pronostication et de indication en cures de vos malaides a coi salus soit convertie; et ceu vos aidera a aquester bone renommee, et gloire, et memoire de loenge.	And of these who give you counsel, and says: "wait, I am healed"; the patient is disdainful. It is not appropriate for you to agree with those who come to you who have this manner, but put greater consideration in your honor than in your desire, and do not rashly but wisely from what you are certain, and from what you can perceive; and use prediction and indication in the treatment of your patients, so that salvation may be converted; and this will help you to acquire good reputation, glory, and memory of praise.
Tres chier fil, Nostres Sires vos doint boin entendement et droiture, et se vos vuelle espireir de la sainte inspiration de sa main, amen.	Dearest child, Our Lords grant you good understanding and righteousness, and if you wish to aspire to the holy inspiration of His hand, come here.
Or je vos ai ordeneit cest chapistre en devisant par chapistres, selonc ceu qu’il est devant ou chapistre des cauteres, que je vos ai deviseit des le chief jusc’a piez, por ceu que vos trovez plus legierement ceu dont vos avrez mestier.	I have arranged this chapter in discussing by chapters, following the order of each chapter of cauteries that I have previously described to you from head to feet, as these are easier for you to understand what you will need.
dou chief plein d’aigue	The full head is swollen with water
Saiches que ceste maladie vient mout de fois as enfans a l’enfanter, et quant li baille estraint trop fort le chief de l’enfant; et aucune fois vient ceu de cause reponue que on ne seit.	This disease often comes to children at childbirth, and sometimes it occurs due to an unknown reason.
Et je ne vis onques ceste maladie fuers qu’en enfans, et a toz ces que j’ai veus se hastait li mors; et por ceu me semble qu’il me vaut mues lassier l’ovraige en teilz cures.	And I have never seen this disease except in children, and all those whom I have seen hurried death; and for this reason it seems to me that it is worthwhile to devote some treatment to certain cases.
Et je vis .i. enfant de coi li chiés estoit plains d’aigue, et li chief engroissoit chescun jor tant qu’il ne lou pooit sostenir; et crut tant li moistor qu’il fut mors, et ceste moistor si est assemblee desoz l’os sus lou syphac, entre lou keur et l’os; et li ovraiges si est telz se li moistor est entre lou keur et l’os, et li apostemes est petis, que tu fendes emmi lou chief une fendure large; et soit ausi longe com .ij. nous, tant que li mostor corre; et vez ci la forme dou spatumile:	And I saw one child whose head was swollen with water, and it grew larger every day until it could no longer support it; and the moisture gathered underneath the skull between the brain and the bone; and the treatment is such that if the moisture is between the brain and the bone, and the abscesses are small, you should make an incision large on the head; and let it be as long as two fingers, so that the moisture flows out; and see the shape of a lancet:
Se li moistor est plus creue, et li aposteme soit plus grans, si fai .ij. fendures en maniere d’une croix, selonc ceste forme:	If the moisture is more swollen and the abscess is larger, make two incisions in the shape of a cross, according to this form:
Et se li moistor est desoz l’os, et li signes que tu vois les commissures dou chief overtes de chescune partie, et li aigue saut fuer quant tu la presses de ta main au dedens, et ceu ne t’est mie reponut: si covient que tu fendes enmi lou chief .iij. fendures selonc ceste maniere:	If the moisture is beneath the bone and you see the signs (of the abscess) as the corners of the head open up from each part, and the pus jumps out when you press it with your hand from within, and it does not heal: then you must make four incisions in the middle of the head according to this manner:
Et aprés l’incision estrai la moistor toute fuers. Aprés estraint les fendures de drapelz et de poudres, et i met vin et oile, et laisse ensi jusc’a cinquieme jor; puis le deslie, et cure la plaie par tentes et par oignemens, et laisse estraindre le chief egaument, et done mengier au malaide viande seche de poc de moistor tant que li membre soit confortez et sanez.	And after the incision remove all moisture completely. After holding open the cuts with fabric strips and powders, put vinegar and oil in it, leave it like that until the fifth day; then release it, and treat the wound by bandages and ointments, and let the wound heal gradually, and give the patient dried meat of a moisturized member as long as the limb is comfortable and healthy.
Et une autre maniere d’incision est que tu regardes ou apert li grandor de l’aposteme, et li assemblé de l’aigue; car aucune fois est elle devant; aucune fois derrier; aucune fois en destre; et aucune fois en senestre.	Another way of incision is that you look for the size of the abscess, and the flow of fluid; because sometimes it is in front, sometimes behind; sometimes on the right, and sometimes on the left.
Taille donques lai ou li aposteme apert, et l’emplissement de l’aigue, et lou fent selonc ce que tu en as le pooir; et warde que tu ne coper l’artere; et veigne flun de sanc, si que li malaides muere dou decorrement de sanc et de l’evacuation de moistor.	Therefore, make the incision where the abscess opens, and empty the fluid, and do as you can; but be careful not to cover the artery; and let a vein of blood flow, so that the patient dies with dignity and from the evacuation of moisture.
de reume	of gout
Quant il avient a aucun une maladie qui est apelee «catarre» as eulz ou au pis, et li maladie est anciainne, et li cure de medicine ne profite mie, adonques li derraine cure si est li cauteres avec ceu c’on li copera les .ij. arteres.	When it happens with any disease called "catarrh" in the eyes or at the worst, and the disease is old and medicine does not help at all, then the last cure is the cautery, namely by cutting two arteries.
Il covient donques, cant tu les vues coper, que li malaides faice rere son chief; aprés li frotte lou leu d’un drapel aspre tant que les arteres aperent, puis estraingne li malaides son col a tout .i. drapel; puis regarde ou li voine bait, et li leus de l’une et de l’autre sont aprés les oreilles, et poc sont reponues; puis signe les leus d’enche, puis cope l’une et l’autre d’un spatumile agut de .ij. pars. tant que li taille veigne jusc’a l’os, et ceu soit par lou large dou chief.	Therefore, when you want to cover them, the patient should lie down with their head back; afterwards, rub the area of a rough cloth on the arteries until they appear; then grab the patient's neck with one rough cloth; then look for where the veins are, and they will be found behind the ears, and the arteries will be opposite each other; then mark the places to cut, then cut one and the other with a sharp spatula of 2 parts. The incision should go as far as the bone, and this should be done by the width of the head.
Et se tu vues, boute le spatumile desoz l’artere et la cope au desus, en taillant ausi com .ij. dois au traver.	And if you want to cut them, push the spatula under the artery and cut it from above, while cutting as deep as 2 fingers through.
Et quant li voinne est copee, si saut li sans en haut continuelment fuers.	And when a vein is cut, it leaps out continually without stopping.
Et se li artere n’apert au sentir, si covient que tu mesures la quantiteit de l’espaice de .iij. dois, puis seigne d’enche et fent jusc’a l’os; et ceu qu’il covient dou sanc mettre fuers si est .vj. c/, et par aventure un poc plus ou moins. selonc ce que li malaides puet soffrir, et la repletion de l’artere; puis regarde la plaie: s’il remaint sus l’os point dou syphac, si le cope que apostemes chaus n’i veigne, puis estrain la plaie et lie, et la cure d’oignement tant qu’ele soit sanee.	And if the artery is not opened to feeling, you must measure the space of 3 fingers, then apply pressure and cut up to the bone; and the quantity of blood that should be let out is 6 cubits, and perhaps a little more or less depending on what the patient can endure and the filling of the artery; then examine the wound: if it remains above the bone point without swelling, if the piece that you cut out does not come out, then press and hold the wound and heal it with ointment until it is healed.
de emigrainne	of immigration
Quant emigrainne anciaine vient, et catarre agut, por les moistors des larmes et les chalors en temples et sode anciene forsenee et semblans choses, et il est medicinez par manieres de cures de medicine et tout ceu ne li profite mie, si estraions les arteres des temples et lou cauterizons, si com nos avons conteit.	When an old migration comes and an acute catarrh, due to moisture in the eyes, heat in the temples and an ancient madness, which seems like other things, and it is treated with methods of medicines, but none of them benefit, we should open the arteries of the temples and cauterize, as we have said.
Et li maniere de l’estraction d’elles si est que li malaides faice rere les poilz de ses temples, et entende a l’artere qui apert en la temple, car elle apert bien par son batement, et est poc reponue fuers que en aucuns homes qui sont trop froit; et s’elle est reponue, si estraigne son col li malaides d’aucuns drapelz, puis frote le leu d’aucun aspre drap, et arose le leu d’aigue chaude tant que li artere apere manifestement; puis pren le spatumile de coi ci est li forme:	And the method of extracting them is that the patient pulls the hairs on his temples, and listens to the artery that opens in the temple, because it opens well with its beating, and is easily found except in some cold people; and if it is found, the patient should strain the neck with some cloths, then rub the place with a rough cloth, and burn the place with hot water until the artery appears clearly; then take the spatumile (a medical instrument) as shown here:
puis escorche le cuir legierement tant que tu veignes a l’artere, puis la trai en haut as pinceures, et la depart bien des toiles que sont desoz li de chescune partie; et se li artere est subtilz, si la torne a la pointe de l’uncine, puis la cope de celle partie selonc la quantiteit des .ij. chiés. Car s’elle n’est copee, si ne saut mie li sans dou tout en tout.	then lightly peel the skin until you see the artery, then pull it up towards the tweezers, and separate well the fabrics that are underneath each part; if the artery is thin, turn it to the point of the tweezers, then cut off that part according to the number of the two hairs. Because if it is not cut off, it will not move at all in any way.
Et trai dou sanc des .vj. c/, jusc’a .iij.; et se li artere est grans, si covient que tu la lies en .ij. leus d’un fil double fort de soie, que porriture n’i veigne devant le soudement de la plaie, et veigne decorremens de sanc; puis cope la superfluiteit qui est entre les .ij. liiens en celle houre meisme, et puis, se tu vues, si lou cauterize dou cautere cutellaire jusc’a l’os tant que li chiés soient copez; et c’est li muedre oevre, se li malaides n’a fievre et il est de chaude complexion.	And draw out the blood from the .vj. c/, up to .iij.; and if the arteries are large, you must tie it with a double strong silk thread so that pus does not come before the wound is sealed, and there is drainage of blood; then cut off the excess between the .ij. ligaments at that same hour, and if possible, cauterize the area with a cautery knife up to the bone until the head is amputated; this is the mutilating work, if the patient does not have fever and has a hot constitution.
Car li cauteres est aide por finir les moistors: por ceu est il de plus grant aide as moistors.	The cauteries are aid for healing wounds: therefore it is of greatest aid to those who are wounded.
Ou il covient por l’estraction des arteres que om emplisse lou leu de viel coton et mette on sus tentes bien faites; et quant on les desliera, si soit curez de medicines seches que font naistre char, et de tentes, tant qu’il soit sanez; et se sans cort de l’artere tant dis com tu i oevres, si te haste dou coper par cautere, ou tu emple lou leu de vitriole et l’estrain a ta main que li sans soit estainchiez; et se tu n’as ceu present, si met sor le leu ton doit tant que li sans soit congelez, et arose le leu d’aigue froide tant que li sans cesse, et soit estraint si com il covient; et ceu qui est muedre et plus legier en l’estraction de l’artere est que tu cauterizes la voinne de cest cautere trenchant de .ij. pars, mais li trenchant soient bien espés por warder plus longement lor chalor.	It is necessary for the extraction of arteries that one fills the area with old cotton and places well-made tourniquets on it; and when they are loosened, one should be cured with dry medicines that produce heat, and tourniquets, until it is healed; and if without cutting the artery as you work, you must hasten to cover it by cauterizing, or use vitriol and hold it with your hand so that it is scorched; and if this is not present, place your thumb on the area until it freezes, and moisten the area with cold water until it stops, and hold as necessary; and the one that is mutilated and easier in the extraction of the artery is that you cauterize the vein of this sharp cautery twice, but the cuts should be wide enough to keep its heat longer.
Car quant li estrumens est trop tenves, si tient moins sa chalor.	For when the straw is too thin, it retains less heat.
Et doit avoir entre les .ij. coutelz .i. doit de gros d’espaice, et puis quant tu as signiet d’enche les .ij. leus, et tu mes lou fer ardant sus tant qu’il viegne jusc’a l’os, et cope la voinne en .ij. leus; et soient esloigniet entre les .ij. chiés car il n’est mie soudez de cest cautere dou tout en tout; et c’est li forme dou cautere:	And it should have between the two knives, one thickness of a finger's space, and then when you have signed up to a depth of two inches, and heat the iron hot enough for it to reach the bone, strike the vein in intervals of two inches; they should be spaced apart as they are not entirely sealed by this fire cautery, and this is the form of the cautery.
des larmes	tears
Quant les larmes des eulz sont dessendans des voinnes que sont sus lou test dou chief de fuer, et il ne profite mie cure de medicine c’on i faice, et tu vois la faice dou malaide enrougir, et sent ou front ambulation si com de fremis; et sui oil sont tenve et moiste si que li poil des papieres sont cheut, et sont eschaufees les papieres, et escorchies de l’ardor des larmes, si ait mestier de ceste cure.	When the tears flow from the eyes that are above the vein on the forehead of the head, and it does not benefit the medicine applied to them, and you see the patient wrinkling his forehead like shivering; and if they are thin and moist so that the hair of the eyebrows falls out, and the eyebrows are burned and scorched by the heat of the tears, this treatment is required.
Et l’apelerent li ancien «cure contuse», et est que tu faices a rere au malaide qui a ceste maladie les poilz qu’il ait ou front, puis li fai .iij. fendures ou front igalment selonc la longesce dou front; et soit l’une des fendures ausi com .ij. doi tout emmi lou front en avalant aval jusc’a neif, et les autres .ij. as .ij. costelz par desus les papieres, et te garde de l’incision des arteres que sont as .ij. costez par desus les papieres; et aloigne ta main de la continuation des .ij. mandibules, et soit chescune plaie la quantiteit de .iij. dois au traver joins;	And they called the ancient one "contused cure", and you must shave the patient's head who has this disease, his hair from the forehead, then make three cuts equally along the length of the forehead; one of the cuts should be as deep as two fingers beneath the brow bone, and the others two at the temples above the eyebrows, and be careful not to cut the arteries which are at the temples above the eyebrows; also keep your hand away from the continuation of the jawbones, and each wound should be of the size of three joined fingers.
et aies apparillie une piece d’esponge et mout de drapelz ses por essuer lou sanc, puis boute le spatumile agut de .ij. pars de coi ci est li forme:	and prepare a piece of sponge and much of bandages to wipe the blood, then insert the pointed spoon of this shape:
des l’incision qui est dever la temple jusc’a la seconde incision; et escorche tout le keur qui est entre les .ij. fendures a tot lou syfac qui est sus l’os, puis fai autreteil des la moiene incision jusc’a l’autre seconde, et puis estrai fuer cest spatumile.	from the first incision which is at the temple to the second incision; and scrape all the core that is between the two cuts to the root of the bone, then continue from the mid-incision to the other second one, and draw out this pointed spoon.
si boute en la premiere fendure l’estrument qui est apelez «cultellaire», et est tresbien trenchans d’une part, et d’autre part est souef, ne mie trenchans, et c’est li forme:	Push the instrument called "cultellar" into the first incision, and it is very sharp on one side and soft but not sharp on the other, and its shape is:
Et met le costeit taillant vers la char aerse au keur, et lou costeit souef vers l’os, et lou boute tant qu’il veigne a la moiene fendure. Et cope toz les vasselz que dessendent dou chief as eulz tant que l’incision soit continue jusc’a ceu qui apert dou keur, et puis autreteil fai en la moiene fendure jusc’a l’autre defuer; et puis estrai dou sanc igalment, et espresse lou leu por le sanc pris; puis met en chescune fendure une tente de viel coton, et met sus drapelz moilliez en vin et en oile et en aisil, et garde que apostemes chaus n’i veigne; et au tier jor deslie lou liien, et i amenistre grant planteit d’aigue tede, puis lou cure d’oignement basilicon avec oile roset, et d’autres cures dont on cure plaies, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And cut the flesh that descends from the hair towards the bone with the sharp side, and the soft side against the bone, and push it until it reaches the middle incision. And gather all the veins that descend from the base of the eyes until the incision is continuous up to where the bone opens, and then make another cut in the middle incision towards the other opening; and press the blood evenly, and express the place for the blood taken; then put a tent of old cotton in each incision, and put on moist cloths soaked in wine and oil and ashes, and ensure that no pus comes out; on the third day unbind the bandage, and apply a large amount of hot mustard plaster, then treat it with ointment made from basilicon and oil of roses, and other treatments for wounds until it is healed.
dou reume des eulz	the root of the hairs
Quant a aucun vienent catarre agut acostumeement, et tu vois les eulz tenves et petis, et afoiblir la veue, et les papieres brulees; et li poil chieent, et ou chief en parfont a dolor ague, et li malaides esternue; adonques saiches par ces accidens que celles matieres et cil catharre ne vient fuer que de maintes voines, et li muedre cure que i est, si est ceste.	When anyone comes with an acute catarrh, you see the eyes becoming swollen and small, blurring the vision, and burned papers; hairs fall out, and a headache ensues due to pain, and the patient coughs; then recognize these symptoms that those substances and this catarrh do not come from anywhere else but multiple veins, and the remedy for this illness is what is needed.
Et est que tu comande au malaide a rere son front, puis fai une grant fendure emmi lou front, et une autre dou large. i. poc. Et comence des la fendure de la temple senestre a la temple destre, et soit li incision jusc’a l’os; et esloigne ta main des ners des temples que muevent au mengier; et quant li os est descovers, si essue tout le sanc a une esponge, et puis desevre entre les .ij. levres de la fendure et i met coton viel, et tentes de lin; puis lie desus drapelz moilliez en vin et en oile, et te garde d’aposteme chaut; quant il est ostez, si covient que tu frottes l’os tant que chars i comence a naistre, puis le cure de choses exiccatives, que font enjanrer char.	And you command the patient to lean back his head, then make a large incision across the forehead, and another wide one. First cut from the left temple to the right temple and let it extend to the bone; keep your hand away from the nerves of the temples that move when eating; when the bone is exposed, drain all the blood with a sponge, then press between the two lips of the incision and put old cotton, and bandage; then cover with dampened cloths soaked in wine and oil, and be careful not to get hot; when it is removed, you must rub the bone until char begins to grow, then cure with things that promote char growth.
En teil maniere: pren .ij. parties de flor de froment, et de colofoine .iiij. parties, et en fai emplaustre; et l’aministre en ces plaies por enjanrer char per tout.	In this manner: take two parts of wheat flour and four parts of colophony, and make a plaster with it; apply it to these wounds in order to promote the growth of char everywhere.
de l’estoupement des oreilles	Of the stoppage of ears
Tout ceu que chiet ens oreilles est une des .iiij. choses: ou grains, ou beste, ou piere de mine ou semblans chose si com fer; ou semence, si com jaisses, feves, pois; ou chose defluans si com aigue et aisilz et semblans choses.	Anything falling in the ears is one of the four things: grains, animals, stone or similar things like iron; seeds such as peas, lentils, beans; or something flowing like water and similar things.
Quant il chiet en l’oreille piere ou autre maniere de chose que ne s’ajoste mie a l’oreille, ne ne croist en l’oreille, si met l’oreille au solel. Se tu vois la piere, si distille aucun poc d’oile violet ou oile de sisament, puis i amenistre extraction; et lou fai esternuer de condisi, et li estoupe les narines quant li esternuemens vient, et met entor l’oreille pieces de drapelz ou laine; et estent l’oreille au desus. Mout de fois vient fuer par ceste cure; et s’elle ne vient fuer, se li amenistre extraction as pinceures subtilz, de coi ci est li forme:	If something falls in the ear that does not fit or grow in the ear, put the ear to the sun. If you see the object, apply a drop of purple oil or camphor oil, then perform extraction; and have the patient cough, and close the nostrils when the coughing starts, and place pieces of fabric or wool around the ear; and hold it upwards. Many times expulsion occurs through this cure; and if it does not occur, extract it with fine tweezers as shown in the following form:
S’elle saut fuer as pinceures, c’est boin; se ceu non, si amenistre extraction a l’oncine subtil de petite doubleure; et s’elle ne saut par ceu, si fai une caine d’arain et boute lou chief de la cainne ou pertuis de l’oreille fort, et estoupe ceu qui est entor la cainne de cire mole si que li vens n’i puisse entrer avec la cainne; puis le trai fuer forment, car mout de fois vient fuer si com nos avons dit; et s’elle ne vient fuer en teil maniere, si prent glut de coi en prent les oisiaus, et met en som aucun estrument qui soit a point por ceu faire, et met un poc de coton entor; puis presse le glut sus la piere ou quel chose que ce soit, et trai fuer.	If it jumps at the hinges, that is good; if not, bring forth extraction with subtle thin forceps of small double curvature; and if it does not jump by this means, make a fishhook of wax and thrust its tip into the ear strongly, and stop up that which is around the hook with soft wax so that the vein cannot enter with the hook; then pull it forth, for it often comes forth as we have said; and if it does not come forth in this manner, take glue of that and take the birds, and put any instrument that is pointed for this purpose, and put a bit of cotton around it; then press the glue onto the stone or something else, and pull it forth.
Et s’elle ne saut fuer de toutes ces choses que nos avons dit, si te haste de fendre l’oreille ainsois que aposteme chalz i veigne, et spasme; et li maniere de la fendure si est que tu faices premier sainier lou malaide de la cephalique, et estrai dou sanc selonc la mesure de sa vertu, puis fai seoir lou malaide entre tes mains et li torne l’oreille au desus, et fent une petite fendure en la racine de l’oreille a la graisse ou leu dependant; et soit li fendure ausi com une lune, tant que tu viegnes a la piere, puis l’oste selonc ton pooir, et la suce hastanment a ta bouche; et la cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	If it does not jump in any of the ways we have said, hurry to cut the ear so that abscess pus and spasm come out; and the manner of cutting is that you first make the patient sneeze from the cephalic vein, and draw blood according to the measure of its power, then seat the patient between your hands and turn the ear upward, and make a small cut in the root of the ear where the fat or flesh depends; let the cut be like a moon until you reach the bone, then break it according to your power, and suck it out quickly with your mouth; and cure it until it is healed.
Et se c’est grains qui est ens et il enfle, si aministre extraction; et si’il ne puet issir, si amenistre .i. spatumile tenve subtil selonc ceste forme:	And if it is a grain that swells, administer extraction; and if it cannot come out, administer one thin, subtle spatula according to this shape:
et amenistre incision de celui grain. Mais ne faire mie ceu quant tu penses que li grains est moistes por la moistor de l’oreille, tant que tu en aies fait maintes pieces; puis l’estrai as pinceures subtilz et au succier, si com nos avons dit, si que li estractions soit aligie.	And make the incision of that grain, but not when you believe that the grain is moist due to the moisture from the ear, until you have made many pieces; then strain it with fine tweezers and extractor, as we have said, so that the extraction is aligned.
En l’aigue donques que chiet en l’oreille covient que li malaides use d’esternuement de condisi premiers, et ample l’oreille de viel coton. Et soit gisans sus celle oreille meisme ou li aigue est. s’elle saut fuer per ceu, c’est boin. se ceu non, si prent maintes pieres selonc li longesce de ton doit tenves et legieres, et les eschaufe un poc au feu; et em mette li malaides une ou pertus de son oreille, et saille sus i. de ses piez d’autre part, et fiere d’une autre piere sus la piere qui est en l’oreille; et ne cesse de faire ceu de piere em piere tant que li aigue isse toute fuer, et ensi saut elle toute fuer; et se tu vues, si prent .i. jonc, et boute l’un des chiés en l’oreille, et l’autre chief emprent de feu tant que li plus dou jonc soit ars; puis refai autreteil d’autres jons tant que li aigue isse toute, si com nos avons dit en la piere.	For the moisture that falls into the ear, the patient should first use ear drops consisting of vinegar and honey, or warm olive oil. Then stuff the ear with soft cotton and let it lie there on top of the ear where the moisture has fallen. If it jumps out because of this, that is good. If it does not, take many small and light pebbles according to the size of your finger, heat one slightly in the fire; then place a piece of cloth or wool into the ear of the patient, hold the stones from the other side, and strike another stone against the stone inside the ear; continue striking one stone with another until the moisture jumps out completely, and it should jump out entirely; if you see, take a string, tie one end to the stone in the ear, and the other end to the fire until the first stone is burned; then repeat this process with other stones until the moisture is completely gone, as we have said earlier.
En l’estraction de la beste, s’elle est de petit cors, si com puce et semblans chose, cure la si com nos avons dit en la division; mais s’elle est de grant cors c’on la puisse sentir, si amenistre extraction de pinceures; et c’est li chose plus legiere a oster qui soit en l’oreille.	In the removal of a beast (insect) that is small like a flea and similar things, treat it as we have said in the previous section; but if it is large and can be felt, make an extraction using tweezers; it is the lighter things that are easier to remove from the ear.
En l’estraction des vers enjanrez as oreilles, quant tu lou cures si com nos avons dit en la division et ou traitier des distillations, et li cure ne profite mie, si covient que tu regardes l’oreille au soleil: s’il i apert nulz vers, si les trai as pinceures subtilz, et s’il n’aperent, si prent la cainne de coi ci est li forme:	In the extraction of worms in the ears, when you cure it as we have said in the division and where to treat distillations, if the treatment does not help, then you should look at the ear in the sun: if any worms open, you should take them with subtle tweezers, and if they do not open, then you should take the cane of which this form is.
Et soit estroite desoz et large desus. Et boute lou plus subtil chief en l’oreille selonc la quantiteit de la soffrance dou malaide, puis succe forment a tot la caine; fai ceu sovent tant que tuit li ver issent.
