Et s’il n’obeissent a issir, si estoupe entor la cainne de coton si com j’ai dit en la piere; et s’il ne saillent fuer si com nos avons dit, si aministre distillations que li ancien ont esprovees en l’ocision des vers, et tu les troveras ou traitier des distillations; et si distille tes oiles et tes medicines en l’oreille a tout cest estrument, de coi ci est li forme si com tu vois:	And it should be narrow inside and wide outside. And insert the most subtle head of the cane into the ear according to the quantity of pain suffered by the patient, then suck firmly all along the cane; do this repeatedly until all the worms come out. If they do not come out, you should stop up around the cane with cotton as I said in the stone; if they do not swell as we have said, administer distillations that the ancients have proven in the elimination of worms and you will find them or treat distillations; and if you distill your oils and medicines into the ear using this device as shown:
Et soit d’argent ou d’arain estrois desoz a .i. petis pertuis, et desus overs por distiller; et por presser dedens la distillation a .i. estrument d’arain bien fait por ceu, et se tu vues pren .i. raseur et envoloupe entor la pointe avenanment coton; puis i giete ton oile ou ton jus, et ceu que tu vues de tes medicines en la cainne, et li caine soit en l’oreille; puis boute dedens lou raseur a tout lou coton, et presse ta main tempreement tant que li oile soit distilleit ou chevement de l’oreille; et lou sente li malaides dedens, et soit li distillations .i. poc eschaufee au feu ainsois c’on la distille en l’oreille; et garde qu’elle ne soit trop froide, car li medicine ne seroit mie si bone.	And it should be narrow inside and wide outside made of silver or lead with one small hole, and above a distillation chamber for distilling; and to press the distillation within this device made of lead, and if you see that you need a scraper, you should wrap cotton around the tip; then pour your oil or juice, and whatever medicine you have into the cane, which is in the ear; then push the scraper into all the cotton and press your hand evenly until the oil distills or moves from the ear; let the patient smell inside, and the distillations should be about one spoonful heated in fire thus it is distilled in the ear; make sure that it is not too cold, for the medicine will not be as effective.
de l’estoupement des oreilles	of the stoppage of ears
Aucun enfant naissent qui n’ont nul pertus ens oreilles; et ceste meisme chose avient as homes par estoupement de plaie, ou de char nee dedens l’oreille, et cist estoupemens vient aucune fois em parfont en l’oreille, si c’on ne lou puet veoir; et aucune fois avient .i. poc defuer lou pertus, et lou voit om bien.	No child is born who does not have any birth defects in the ears; and this same thing happens to adults through ear stoppage caused by pus or pus inside the ear, and this stoppage can sometimes be deep within the ear, which cannot be seen; and sometimes it causes one of the eardrums to move out, which is easily visible.
Celle donques que vient em parfont, si c’on ne la puet veoir, est de grief sanation em plusors dispositions, et en cele c’on voit covient que tu mettes l’oreille dou malaide au soleil; et regarde dedens: se tu vois l’opilation apparent, si la oevre a tot cest spatumile de coi ci est li forme:	Therefore, if it cannot be seen deep within the ear, it is a serious condition in many cases, and in this case you must put the sick person's ear in the sun; look inside: if you see the accumulation clearly, you should use the spatula shaped like this one to remove it:
Et soit agus et trenchans devant et derrier tout plain, si qu’il ne blece l’oreille; se li opilation est de char nee ou cors de l’oreille, si la tien as pinceures subtilz, et la cope legierement, tant que celle chars soit toute ostee.	And let it be sharp and incisive all around, so that it does not pierce the ear; if the opening is of soft flesh or cartilage of the ear, hold it with subtle tweezers and strike gently until all the flesh is completely removed.
Et se li opilations est em parfont en l’oreille, si pren .i. raseur subtil legier et l’eschaufe un petit au feu, puis li met ou cors de l’oreille. Se tu sens l’opilation dont li malaides sent grieteit a l’oïr, perce legierement, et garde que tu ne grever les ners de l’oreille; puis met en l’oreille une tente selonc la largesce dou pertus, et la moille en l’oignement egyptien.	If the opening is deep inside the ear, take a subtle razor and heat it slightly over fire, then apply it to the cartilage of the ear. If you feel the opening that causes pain in the ear, pierce gently, making sure not to damage the nerves of the ear; then put a plug in the ear according to the size of the wound, and moisten it with Egyptian ointment.
Fai ceu aucun jor tant que li plaie soit soudee, ou tu pren une tente et la moille en aigue rose, et poudre sus vitriole broiet; et se tu vois enflee l’oreille, si couvient que tu traies la tente et remue une autre tente moillie en cerote qui soit fait d’oile roset et de cire, tant que li enfleure soit ostee; puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	Do this every day until the wound is healed, or take a plug and moisten it with rosewater, add powdered vitriol; if you see the ear swell, then it is necessary to draw out the plug and insert another plug moistened with roset oil and beeswax until the swelling disappears; then let it heal.
Et se decorremens de sanc vient, si plonge une esponge et drapelz en aigue froide, et le met sus l’oreille, et use d’autres cures qui oste lou decorrement de sanc qui sont ou traitier des destillations.	And if bleeding occurs, immerse a sponge and cold water in it, and place it on the ear, and use other treatments that stop the bleeding which are to treat distillations.
de la char des papieres	of the bark of poplars
Cist althelul que vienent em papieres des eulz quant ils sont moiste et sont sec, si covient que tu les estendes de tenailles et de pinceures, et le cope d’un spatumile de ses racines; puis met sor le leu vitriole broiet.	This is the method that comes in papers from the eyes when they are moist and dry; it must be stretched with tongs and tweezers, and then struck with a spatula at its roots; then place it on the side of vitriol powder.
Et se sans en decort, si le cauterize dou cautere lenticulaire subtil, et li cauterizeir aprés l’incision vaut mues; et maintes fois repairent, cant aucune chose demoure de lor racines; et quant elles sont cauterizees par feu, si sont arses celles racines et ne revienent mie.	And if not dressed (cauterized), the subtle lenticular cautery should be applied to it, and afterwards the cauterization following the incision is worthwhile; and they often heal, because nothing remains of their roots; and when they are cauterized by fire, those roots are burned and do not return.
de la gresle	of the hailstorm
Maintes fois vienent em papieres des eulz unes choses que semblent gresle en sa forme et en sa duresce, et por ceu est ceste maladie apelee «grandine», et est une assemblee de moistor grosse en la papiere desus et desoz; li ovraiges est telz: pren warde se li grandine se muet d’une part et d’autre, et c’est legiere chose a savoir; fent la donques dou large, puis l’escorche de chescune partie legierement, puis la prent as pinceures, et la cope. se tu ne la pues coper sens percier un poc la papiere, si ne grieve rien au malaide; et se li fendure est grans, si l’assemble a une costure, et la cure tant qu’ele soit sanee; et s’elle est petite, si n’i faire point de force, car li oignemens la restoure tantost et enjanre char.	Many times there come to papers hailstones that seem like hail in shape and hardness, and because of this the disease is called "hailstorm", and it is a large assembly of thick moisture on the paper above and below; the process is as follows: Take care so that the hailstone moves neither left nor right, and this is an easy thing to know; then make an incision on both sides, then remove the skin gently from each side, then take them with the forceps, and squeeze. If you cannot cover it without perforating the paper a little, do not worry about the patient; and if the tear is large, gather it together with a stitch, and cure it until it heals; and if it is small, do not use force, because the ointments restore it soon and cause pain.
Et se li grandine est dessendans au dedens de l’oreille vers la partie desus, si enverse la papiere, et estent la grandine a unes pinceures, et la cope et presse d’une part et d’autre; et se li papiere est esloignie par l’incision, ce ne grieve rien; et quant li grandine est copee, si leive l’oil d’aigue salee, et cure le leu de ceu qui enjanre char tant que li malaides soit sanez.	And if the pus is descending within the ear towards the upper part, turn the paper over, and grasp the pus with forceps, then press it from both sides; and if the paper is pushed away by the incision, it does not matter; and when the pus is pressed, apply salty oil to the area where the patient has an infection until the patient recovers.
de la graisse des eulz	of the fat from the eyes
Exinach est une graisse qui est enjanree en toiles des papieres desus, et ce avient plus as enfans c’a nules gens, et grieve mout a lor eulz, et li vienent li catharre as matinees, et ne pueent regardeir la lumiere dou soleil por ceu que les larmes se hastent a lor eulz; et por ceu se couchent il sor lor faices adés, et dorment sus, et sont lor papieres desoz lor sorcilz moistes que li enfleure et li apparance ont covert de l’exinach qui apert en l’oil. Et quant tu presses lou leu a tes dois et sent l’exirnach entr’ous.	Exinach is a fat that is infused in the paper on top, and this happens more often in children than adults, and it causes great discomfort to their eyes, and they come down with catarrh in the mornings, and cannot look at the light of the sun because tears flow rapidly into their eyes; therefore, they lie on their faces immediately and sleep, and their wet paper is covered by exinach which spreads in the oil. And when you press the affected area with your fingers and feel the exinach between them.
Et li maniere de l’ovraige si est que li malaides mette son chief en ton sain; et puis pren .i. drapeil de lin, et appareille une tente em maniere d’un cercle selonc la quantiteit que conteigne exirnach de chescune partie, puis le met sus li; et presse a tes dois d’une part et d’autre, si que li exirnach soit assemblez emmi le cercle; puis fent em mileu de la moistor au spatumile trenchant une fendure dou large, et ne soit mie plus grans que li plaie c’on fait a la sainie de voinne; et fent le cuir em parfont tant que tu veignes a l’exirnach; et em plusors dispositions vient exirnach de la fendure, selonc la forme d’une piece de graisse blainche.	And the method of work is that the patient places their head in your lap; and then takes one piece of linen cloth, and prepares a tent in the shape of a circle according to the size that contains exirnach for each part, then puts it on top; and presses with both hands from one side and another, so that the exirnach is assembled within the circle; then makes an incision in the middle of the moisture with a pointed spatula cutting a slit wide, but not larger than the wound made at the vein opening; and cuts the skin completely until you can see the exirnach; and in various positions, the exirnach comes out from the slit, according to the shape of a piece of white fat.
Estrai la donques a tout une piece de drap charpit entre tes dois au defuer, et torne ta main a destre et a senestre tant qu’il soit espars; et garde que tu n’ajoster en la fendure, que tu ne viegnes a tout le spatumile jusc’a l’oil, que tu ne le bleces.	Then, place a piece of linen cloth between your hands and spread it apart; and make sure you do not displace the spatula in the slit, go up to the oil but do not pierce or cut it.
Et se li exirnach n’apert en l’encomencement de la fendure, si acroi un poc la fendure legierement tant qu’il apere; puis l’estrai si com nos avons dit, puis moille drapelz en aisil et en aigue, et met sus le leu, et estrain de bendelz.	If the exirnach does not open at the beginning of the slit, slightly enlarge the slit until it appears; then pull as previously stated, moisten cloth in oil and water, place it on top, and hold with bandages.
Et si a de tels homes qui broient seil et mettent sus por corrompre cele moistor qui est demoree. Puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez. Et s’il vient au leu aposteme chaut, si lou cure d’emplaustres assouajant tant qu’il soit sanez.	And for such men who grind and apply [something] on top to corrupt the moisture that has remained, heal it until it is healed. If it becomes abscessed hot, then heal it with plasters soothing it until it is healed.
des poilz des papieres	the hairs of the paper
Quant em papieres naissent poilz ajostez autre que li naturez, et sont enveillit, si nuisent as eulz, et font venir manieres de maladies si com larmes acostumees et mollifications des papieres et albugine, tant que c’est cause de la destruction des eulz; et est li cure selonc .iiij. manieres: ou par cautere ensamble feu, ou par medicine ague selonc ceu qu’il est devant ou chapistre de cautere, et est fais ou par incision et costure ou par caines, selonc ceu que je dirai.	When paper hairs grow other than naturally and are nurtured, they harm the eyes and bring on various diseases such as common eye ailments like tears and swelling of the paper and albugine, which cause the destruction of the eyes; and there are four ways to cure it: either by cautery with fire, or with medicine ointment according to what is stated in the previous chapter about cautery, and this is done either by incision and stitching, or with canes, as I will explain.
Il covient que tu mettes lou chief dou malaide en ton sain, puis torne la papiere de l’oil a ta main senestre; s’elle est convertie, c’est boin; se ceu non, si i boute une aguille a tout .i. fil desus; et soit ce delez la marge de la papiere ou li poil naissent delez ces poilz, et trai .i. fil au desus a tout la papiere, et la torne au raseur; puis fent en la partie desoz la papiere, desoz les poilz ajostez, a tout le spatumile copant, des le grant larmier jusc’au petit; puis estrai .i. fil, et met desoz la papiere une petite tente de couton et de drapeil, puis seigne sus la papiere une figure d’enche, si com la fuelle de mirte, et toutevoie il covient que li figure soit selonc la quantiteit que tu vues eslever la papiere qui est devisez a toz.	It is required that you place the patient's head in your lap, then turn the paper of oil on your left hand; if it has been converted, that is good; if not, push a needle through one thread above it; and it should be pierced where the edge of the paper meets the hairs, or where the hairs grow from those hairs, and pull one thread across the whole paper, and turn to the razor; then make in the part beneath the paper, under the hairs adjacent, as wide as a spatula, from the large blister until the small one; then pull one thread, and place a small tent of cotton and linen underneath the paper, then mark on the paper a sign of a thorn, as a bunch of myrtle, and it is necessary that the figure be according to the quantity you wish to lift the paper which has been designated for all.
Et si a teil qui a mestier c’on cope grant quantiteit de la papiere selonc ceu que li papiere est mollifie; puis fent a tout le spatumile sus les .ij. lignes que tu as signiet, et comence des lou grant larmier jusc’a petit; et soit li une des fendures pres des poilz naturez en la groissece d’un raiz, puis boute l’oncine en l’un des .ij. angles dou keur, puis l’escorche toute; puis assemble les .ij. levres a une costure d’une aguille a tout .i. fil de laine subtil, et essue le sanc, et fai aerdre la superfluiteit des filz sus les .ij. sorcilz a tout aucunes choses gluans, se tu vues faire ce; et se ce non, si n’en aies cure, puis laisse la costure et les filz jusc’a .iij. jors ou .iiij.; puis cure la plaie sens costure de choses sechans et constrignans, car li papiere se relive au soudement de la plaie et l’assemblement de li, mais li costure est muedre (si com dirent li ancien), et c’est ovraiges sens paor;	And if it is necessary to use a large quantity of the paper according to what the paper has been softened; then make on both lines that you have marked, and begin from the large blister until small; and let one of the cuts be close to the natural hairs in the thickness of a root, then insert the needle into one of the two corners of the keyhole, then peel all; then sew together the two lips with a thread made of subtle linen and an awl at one filament, and squeeze the blood, and make it dry the excess threads above both scissors, if you want to do this; and if not, have no concern, then leave the stitching and threads for 2-4 hours; then treat the wound without stitching with things that are drying and tightening, because the paper will rise to the wound's edge and join it, but the stitching is rotten (as the ancients say), and this is work without fear.
et si a une autre maniere: et est que tu seignes la papiere d’une figure qui soit ausi com li fuelle de mirte, si com nos avons conteit, a .iij. oncines desevrez selonc la forme qui est ci:	and in another way: and it is that you mark the paper with a figure that is like the bunch of myrtle, as we have said before, with four needles pierced according to the form shown here:
puis cope ceu qui sormonte as petites forces igalment selonc la forme qui est ci:	Then bind equally with cords, according to the shape shown below:
Et se tu n’as pooir de tenir les tenailles, et li chose n’est mie igalz, si prent une aguille ou il ait .i. fil, et la boute emmi la figure; et boute .i. autre fil delez lou grant larmier, et lou secont fil delez lou petit, et assemble entre tes dois les filz igalment; puis lieve ta main igalment, et lieve tout le cuir sus coi tu as signiet, si com nos avons conteit, puis assemble les .ij. levres de la plaie par costure, et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et se aposteme vient a ton incision, si l’apaise de cerote et de semblans oignement assouajans;	And if you do not have the ability to hold pincers and the shape is not even, take a needle with one thread and insert it into the figure; and take another thread from the large incision, and the second thread from the small, and bring them together between your hands equally; then bind your hand equally, and bind all the skin above which you have sewn, as we have stated, then suture the two edges of the wound with stitches, and heal it until it is healed; and if an abscess comes to your incision, soothe it with cerote and similar ointments.
et aucune fois avient que li poil de la papiere sont convertit: si covient que tu uses ceu que nos avons dit de l’incision; mais li costure en l’une et en l’autre est plus artificialz.	And sometimes the hair of the papyrus becomes converted: if you need to use what we have said about incision, but stitching in one and the other is more artificial.
Li cure des caines si est selonc ceste forme: et est que tu convertisses la papiere et la fent dedens selonc ceu que j’ai dit, et puis fai .ij. caines par art, et .ij. liiens subtilz ausi lonc com li papiere et li largesce dou spatumile est; et cope as .ij. chiés de .ij. pars ou tu tiens les filz; puis assemble l’un et l’autre subtilment sus ceu que sormonte de la papiere de l’oil, et estrain les .ij. cainnes des .ij. parties forment; et le laisse ensi aucuns jors, et li cuir qui iert estrainte morra et nercira et porrira, tant qu’il cherra par lui.	The cure for bites is as follows: You are to fold the paper and place it inside as I have said, and then make 2 stitches with art, and 2 subtle threads of the same length as the paper and width of the spatula; take 2 pieces of each piece where you hold the threads; then bring together one and the other delicately on top of the paper oil, and bind the 2 stitches of the 2 parts; leave it for some days, and the skin that is bound will rot and die, until it dries up.
S’il tarde, si le cope aunes forces, puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et quant li plaie iert soudee, et si ert levee li papiere, et ne poindront plus li poil; et c’est li forme des .ij. cainnes que tu feras selonc ceste figure, et selonc ceste quantiteit de lonc et de large:	If it is slow or if you need to force it, then cure it until it heals; and when the wound is closed, and no more hair can be felt, this is the shape of the 2 stitches that you will make according to this figure, and according to this length and width:
li ovraiges est telz que tu preignes une aguille subtil, et i boute .i. fil de soie souef et subtil; puis assemble les chiés et noe l’un et l’autre subtilment, et soit li longesce des filz une palme de lonc; puis ordene en la chasse .i. autre fil subtil de soie briément, et noe les chief dou fil; puis mette li malaides son chief en ton sain; et soit delez lou soleil si que li ovraiges soit declairiez, car c’est uns ovraiges subtilz et menus, puis boute l’aguille a tout la chasse en la racine dou poil ajosteit, et la fai percier en la papiere hastanment tant que tu la traies desus lou poil natureil; puis estrai le poil jusque sus la chasse, et boute en la chasse celui poil, s’il en i a .i. ou .ij. ou .iij. ou plusors; puis estrai ta main tant que li poilz veigne fuers a tout la chasse en la papiere avec lou poil natureil.	The work is such that you take a subtle needle and insert one thread of fine silk; then assemble the pieces and join them delicately, and let the length of the threads be about a span; then arrange another fine silk thread briefly, tie the threads together; then make the patient put his head in your healthy one; and place it in the sun so that the work is exposed, for this is a subtle and delicate work, then insert the needle all along the root of the hair next to it, and pierce through the paper quickly until you pull up the natural hair above; then pull out the hair up to the needle, if there are one or two or three or more hairs; then hold your hand until the hairs come out fully with the natural hair.
Et se li chasse est traite et li poilz ne vient fuer avec li, si trairas la chasse au desoz a tout le fil que tu i as ordeneit, tant que li chasse veigne fuer dou pertus desus et que tu la voies par la vision de l’oil; adonques si trairas la chasse et le fil, et clo l’oil et lou laisse clo .ij. jors ou .iij., tant que li poil s’aerde en son leu et naisse li char sus; et se li poilz est petis, si acompaigne .i. poil lonc des chevoulz naturez, et soit alevez avec celui ou tu le laisse, tant qu’il soit eslongiez et puis le lieve.	And if the wound is treated and the hairs do not come forth with it, you shall draw out the arrow beneath to its full length that you have ordered, until the arrow comes forth from the flesh above and you see it by the vision of the eye; then you shall draw out the arrow and the string, and close the eye and leave it closed for two or three days, until the hair grows in its place and new flesh is formed; and if the hairs are small, one long hair of a goat's beard should accompany it, and let it be raised with this until it is distanced and then cleanse it.
de la porriture de l’oil	Of the boils on the eye
Quant ceste maladie qui est apelee «aleacrati» ou li porriture vient en l’oil, si en i a de .ij. manieres: l’une natureil, et l’autre innatureil.  Et avient par soudement de plaie, ou de tailleure ou de cautere, et par semblans choses.	When this disease which is called "aleacrati" or boils appear in the eye, it comes in two ways: natural and unnatural. And it often occurs due to a wound, or from cutting or cautery, and similar things.
Et li maniere de l’ovraige en li est que tu fendes celle soudure, et dessevre les levres de li, et met dedens tentes de lin, et la lie tant qu’elle soit sanee; et ne covient mie que tu uses en la cure de li de choses que sechent et restraignent. Car se tu fais ceu, si revient li maladie pire que li premiere; mais i oevre de choses amollissans, si com fenugreic; et l’arose d’aigue ou altee et semence de lin soient cuites, et oignemens dyaquilon fondut en aucun des oiles, et i envoloupe une tente, et le cure de ceu.	And the method of work in it is that you cut through that joint, separate the sides of it, and put threads of flax inside and keep it until it heals; and you should not use anything in its treatment that dries and constricts. For if you do this, the disease returns worse than before; but the treatment with softening things, such as fenugreek; and the broth of water or oil and flaxseed cooked, and immediately dissolve alum in one of the oils, and wrap it in a linen bandage, and treat it with this.
Et li tresors de ta cure si est que tu te dones en garde qu’ele ne soude mie selonc la forme qu’elle fut devant; et cist ovraiges que nos avons dit nen est fuers que adresemens de ceste maladie, qu’elle ne reviegne selonc la forme qu’elle fut devant.	And the treasure of your care is that you do not allow it to heal in its previous form; and this treatment that we have said is only appropriate for correcting this disease, so that it does not return in its previous form.
de la char qui vient en l’oil	of the fat that comes in oil
Ceste maladie que est desoz qui vraiement est apelee «axacrati», et est naturelz et accidens. Li accidens vient de plaie et de fendure et de cautere et de choses semblans; et li voie de l’ovraige en li si est que tu preignes un aguille, en coi il ait .i. fil double, et la fiche en la char, et li fai percier des le senestre larmier tant c’a destre, si que li filz veigne en .ij. chiés de la char; puis estent la char au desus a tout l’aguille, et la cope a .i. spatumile large.	This illness that is below, which is truly called "axacrati", is both natural and accidental. The accidental part comes from wounds and fractures and cauterizations and similar things; and the work process in it is that you take a needle, with it having one double thread, and pierce it into the flesh, entering from the left tear duct to the right, so that the threads come out in two heads of the flesh; then lift the flesh above the whole needle, and press with one spatula wide.
Et se li figure de la papiere revient selonc ceu qu’il covient, c’est boin; se ceu non, si pren .i. raseur et le met en la fendure, et torne la papiere, et fent .ij. fendures ou costeit dedens la papiere; et soient li chiés des .ij. fendures des .ij. angles de l’incision que tu as copeit, et soit fais uns angles si que quant elles sont assemblees, que li figure soit ausi com li figure d’une lettre qui a non «.j. griesche»; puis oste celle char, selonc la quantiteit que ses costez est agus desoz, de ceu qui enseut la papiere, puis ajoste les .ij. parties desevrees, et les cout d’un fil de lainne; puis lou cure de ceu que nos avons dit des medicines mollifians, et de tentes, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the shape of the paper returns as it should be, that's good; if not, take one rasp and put it in the fracture, turn the paper, and make two fractures where there is bone inside the paper; and let the edges of the two fractures from the two angles of the incision you made meet, and make an angle so that when they are assembled, the shape will be like the shape of a letter with no "i"; then remove the flesh according to the thickness that its sides are sharp under the paper, and join the two separated parts with a thread of linen; then treat this as we have said of medicines softening, and of tenets, until it heals.
Et se li maladie vient de fendure ou de costure ou de cautere, si covient que tu fendes une fendure plainne desoz les poilz des papieres, et selonc ceu qui est ci devant; puis desevre entre les .ij. leivres d’une tente, si com j’ai dit; et doit on faire l’ovraige selonc la forme de la maladie, car elle est mout diverse en forme, et li saiges maistres appareille engien de tout som pooir coment il faice revenir la figure a sa forme natureil; et li malaides meisme, selonc ceu qu’il i covient d’ovraige et d’estrumens em plusors dispositions.	And if the illness comes from a fracture or sewing or cauterization, then you must make a full incision under the hair of the paper, as mentioned before; then separate between the two leaves of a bandage, as I have said; and it is necessary to do the work according to the shape of the illness, because it is very diverse in shape, and the wise masters prepare devices with all possible skill to bring the figure back to its natural form; and the patients themselves, according to what is required for the work and instruments in various positions.
dou soudement de la papiere	swiftly of the paper
Quant ceste soudure avient a mains homes en teil maniere que li papiere desus est sodee avec le blanc de l’oil, et ne puet movoir ne faire ses ovraiges naturez, si covient donques que tu i boutes la pointe d’un raseur desoz la papiere, et la lieve en haut; et l’estent as pinceures, tant que tu copes ceu qui est aert au spatumile subtil, qui ne soit mie trop agus ne trop trenchans, si que li malaides ne puisse soffrir que li spatumile trop agus ne blecent l’oil; et soit ton incision, dont tu escorche celle assemblee, legierement, si que li papiere reviegne selonc sa forme natureil; et est sanee toute celle assemblee, et font aucune fois en l’oil aigue salee, et le leve d’aigue douce, et de coliere; puis met entre la papiere et l’oil une tente de lin, et met sus l’oil laine moillie en abun d’uef; et aprés le tier jor use dou coliere et des choses soudans tant qu’il soit sanez.	When this adhesion occurs in the hands of men in such a way that the paper above is glued with white oil, and cannot move or perform its natural functions, it is necessary to insert the tip of a razor beneath the paper, lift it up; and hold it with pincers until you reach the cartilage that is subtle, which should not be too sharp nor too jagged, so that the patient does not suffer from too sharp spatula piercing the oil; and make your incision, from which you scrape the assembly, lightly, so that the paper returns to its natural form; and the entire assembly heals, and sometimes becomes infected with foul oil, and lifts of sweet oil and colirium; then place between the paper and the oil a tent of linen, and put on the oil wool moistened abundantly with egg; and after the third day use the colirium and other healing substances until it is healed.
de l’ungle de l’oil	of the nail of the oil
Saiches que li ungle est selonc .ij. manieres: elle est nervouse et semblans a .i. dur syfac, et une autre qui n’est mie nervouse, mais est semblans a blainche moistor congelee, que quant on la touche de fer et on la cuide panre as pinceures, si ne puet om; et l’une et l’autre semblance encomence devers le grant larmier, et croist poc et poc tant qu’ele cuevre toute la veue et toute la lumiere et le movement de l’oil.	Know that the nail is of two kinds: it is nerve-like and resembles a hard horn, and another which is not nerve-like but resembles white solidified moisture, such that when it is touched by iron and boiled with pincers, it cannot be moved; and both seem to start from the great root, and grow little by little until it covers the whole eye and light and the movement of the oil.
Et li maniere de l’incision si est que li malaides mette son chief en ton sain, puis li oevre les eulz; et lieve la papiere a ta main, puis coil l’ungle as pinceures de petite doubleure, et l’estent au desus; puis pren une aguille, et i met .i. poil de cheval, ou de vaiche, ou de buef, et .i. fil fort; et double la pointe de l’aguille un poc et la fiche emmi l’ungle, et la perce a tout l’aguille, et lie l’ungle d’un fil et l’estent au desus, et escorche a tout lou poil le costeit de l’ungle qui enseut la prunele et la soie au poil jusc’au chief, puis cope lou remanant en la racine dou larmier a tout lou spatumile subtil et as petites forces, et laisse la char natureil ou larmier, si que par l’incision ne veigne li cors des larmes acostumeement; et aucune fois s’estent li ungle a l’oncine soulement, et au fil, si com nos avons dit; puis l’escorche on a tout le spatumile souef de coi ci est li forme:	And the method of incision is that the patient places his head in your hand, then you open the eyes; take paper into your hand, then hold the nail with small pincers and lift it up; then take a needle, put one hair from a horse or cow or ox, and a strong thread; bend the tip of the needle slightly and insert it into the nail, piercing it all the way through, and tie the nail with the thread and lift it up; then scrape off all the hair on the side of the nail that follows the root and the silk to the hair until the skin, then cut the remaining part in the root of the finger as finely as possible with a small knife or tweezers, leaving the natural flesh at the root of the finger so that by the incision no blood comes out as usual; and sometimes the nail is held only on the end, and along the thread, as we have said; then scrape off all the soft tissue of this shape:
Et garde que li spatumile ne touche la toile charnue et la rompe, et que li prunele ne soit percie; et aprés l’incision giete en l’oil un poc de seil broiet, et dou coliere fait de litargire, et le laisse jusc’a l’autre jor; puis le cure de ceu qu’il i covient tant qu’il soit sanez.	And be careful that the soft tissue does not touch the flesh and tear it, and that the pulp is not pierced; and after the incision pour oil a little bit of broken sebum, and let it sit until the next day; then treat it as necessary until it heals.
Et se li ungle n’est mie nervouse, et tu ne pues bouter l’aguille, et li uncines n’i puet entrer, maintes fois est curee ceste semblance d’ungle de medicines; et naissent sicom j’ai conteit en la division, et se tu la vues coper, si oevre l’oil dou malaide, et pren le spatumile legier poc agut selonc ceste forme:	And if the nail is not nerveous and you cannot insert the needle, and the unguents cannot enter, many times this appearance of the nail is cured with medicines; and they grow as I have said in the division, and if you see it covered, it works the oil of the sick person, and take the spatumile lightly pointed according to this form:
Et reis l’ungle desus subtilment, et se tu vois qu’elle amenuise point et li rasion i apresse, si distille de ta bouche en l’oil coliere fait de litargire et dou coliere rouge et seil broiet, et estoupe l’oil jusc’a l’autre jor; puis rencomence l’autre ovraige selonc ceste meisme oevre, tant qu’elle soit toute ostee.	Gently press the nail upwards, and if you see that it does not shrink at all and the reason persists, distill from your mouth into the collyrium oil made of litargyre and red collyrium powder, and strain the oil until the next day; then repeat the work according to this same procedure until it is completely healed.
Se aucune chose ne t’est contraire en l’oil, si com aposteme chaus, adonques la lait, et cure premier l’aposteme chaut tant qu’il soit sanez, puis rencomence l’ovraige si com devant, tant qu’il soit sanez.	If nothing goes against you in the oil, as a general rule of abscesses, then milk it, and first heal the abscess hot until it is healed, then repeat the work as before, until it is healed.
Et se li apparance de la chair dou larmier nuit en l’oil par grant nuisement, si la sospent a l’oncine, et en cope une partie et non mie tot, que cors de larmes n’i viegne; puis distille en l’oil coliere rouge qui est fais de litargire.	And if the appearance of the flesh at the wound worsens greatly in oil, suspend it on a hook, and cut off a part but not all, so that tears do not come forth; then distill in the oil collyrium made from litharge.
de la char qui naist sus la prunelle	And if the growth arises on the eyelid
Es eulz d’aucuns homes naist aucune fois char rouge, et cuevre la prunele et restraint sus les papieres et les torne au defuer, et semble une rose de balauste; et li ovraiges si est que li malaides mette son chief en ton sain, puis li oevre les eulz, et coil toute celle char as uncines convenaubles a ceu, et la sostien a la force; puis cope la premiere char, et vai tout copant au raseur jusc’a la fin, et te garde que tune bleces l’oil a l’ovraige; et soit li incision dou spatumile que nos avons dit en l’incision de l’ungle et as petites forces de coi on oste lou sebel, si com li forme aprés cest chapistre lou demostre;	In some men, a red growth may arise on the eyelid and cover the eye and be held on the paper and turned inward, resembling a rosebud of balustrade; and such treatment is that the patient puts his head in warm water, then opens the eyes and removes all that red growth with appropriate scissors as needed, taking care not to damage the oil gland during the procedure; it should be the incision of the spatumile as mentioned in the incision of the nail and the small forces used for removing the scab, as shown by the form after this chapter.
et quant li incision est acomplie et ostee toute li char, si emple l’oil de seil broiet ou tu i distille coliere rouge et semblans medicines corrosives, et met sus l’oil defuer coton avec abin d’uef, si qu’il soit asseurez d’aposteme chaut; et s’il i demore rien, et li sans chaus te sormonte, et tu doutes aposteme chaut, si laisse l’oil et cure l’aposteme de choses apaisant aposteme chaut; puis revien a ton ovraige tant qu’il soit sanez, et ensi fai cant chars est ajostee en l’oil par ceste semblance.	And when the incision is completed and all the flesh is removed, use oil of sulphur broken or you distill red collyrium and similar corrosive medicines, and put cotton soaked with egg white on top to ensure that it stays hot; and if anything remains, and the wound becomes swollen, and you doubt that it is hot, leave the oil and treat the abscess with cooling agents for the abscess; then return to your work until it is healthy, and do the same for all wounds that are soothed in oil by this method.
Mais toutevoie il covient que tu aliges la cure de chescun oil foible de la voie natureil; et de la voie accident, en ovraige de fer; et ne bouter mie ta main en aucun de ces ovraiges tant que tu voies que cist membres soit soffrans celui ovraige.	But you must alleviate the cure of each oil with weak natural remedies; and in the work of iron, alleviate with hot remedies; and do not put your hand into any of these works until you see that this member is strong enough for that work.
des voines des eulz	the veins of the eyes
Sebel sont voinnes rouges que sont covertes sus l’oil, et tolent a la veue son ovraige et afoiblissent l’oil toz jors. Mestier est donques au premier que tu regardes se li oil, en coi sebel est, est fors, et n’i a autre maladie fuers que lou sebel; adonques le coil en teil maniere: comande au malaide qu’il mette son chief en ton sain, puis sospent celles voines a tout l’oncine selonc sa sapience, et soit li oncines subtilz double selonc ceste forme:	When the veins that are covered over oil become red and their work can be seen by the eye and weaken the oil every day. Therefore, it is necessary for you to first examine if the oil, in which the vein is located, is healthy and has no other disease besides the one; then squeeze the oil in this manner: instruct the patient to place his head on your healthy hand, then press those veins all along their entire length according to your wisdom, and make the incisions subtle, double as shown in this form:
Et soient dui oncine par degrez en .i. cors selonc ceste forme:	And be two incisions by degree in one body according to this form:
puis c’on coil as forces celles voinnes subtilment, et essue lou sanc houre aprés autre, tant que tu voies removoir celles voines fuers de l’oil; et garde que tu ne blecier l’oil as pointes des spatumiles, et fai cest ovraige a houre de midi devant lou soleil, et soies mout fervans en ton ovraige si que tu ne copes fuer que celles voinnes; et quant tu avras ce fait, si distille en l’oil coliere vert et rouge por corrumpre ceu qui est demorez dou sebel.	Then squeeze those veins gently, and suck out the blood hour after hour until you see them move away from the oil; and be careful not to prick the oil with the points of the spatula, and perform this task at noon before the sun, and be very warm in your work so that you do not cut anything but those veins; and when you have done this, if it distills green and red collector oil for correcting those remaining with the sebel.
Et se tu n’as pooir de coillir tout ceu en celle houre, si fai emplastre sus l’oil de choses apaisans la dolor des eulz, et le laisse aucuns jors tant que li dolors soit apaisie et soit asseurez d’aposteme chaut, puis rencomence selonc ceste maniere qui est devant tant qu’il soit sanez; et c’est li forme des forces:	And if you do not have the power to hold it all in that hour, apply a plaster over oil of soothing things on the eyes, and leave it for some days until the pain is eased and assured of abscess healing, then resume as before until it is healed; this is the form of strength.
de la fistule de l’oil	And from the fistula of oil
Li mire si nomment «arissati» fistule: quant tu la cures per cautere et par medicine ague ardant selonc ceu que j’ai devant dit, et elle n’est mie sanee, si est engien en li que tu fendes sus l’aposteme, lai ou il doit meurer, et trai toute la moistor que i est, tant que li os soit descovers.	The mirror is named "arissati" fistula: when you cure it with cautery and burning medicine as I have previously said, and it is not healed, there is an engine in it that you cut open above the abscess where it should die, and drain all the moisture that is there until the bone is exposed.
Et quant li os iert descovers, et tu verras la corruption et la noiror, si la reis a tout l’estrument de coi ci est li forme; et est apelez «aspre chief», et soit fait de feir inde a .i. chief reont, et soit pointoiez si com une lime si com il est en la presente forme:	And when the bone is exposed, and you see corruption and blackness, if it requires all the tools as stated here; it is called "rough head", and one should make a hole in it, exactly round, and point it like a chisel as shown in the current form.
Et met sus lou leu de l’os corrumput, puis le torne entre tes dois, et presse ta main un poc tant que tu saiches que celle corruption est rese; et fai ceu aucune fois, puis restoure lou leu de medicines exiccatives.	And place the tool on top of the corrupted bone, then turn it between your hands and press your hand slightly so you know that the corruption is removed; do this once, then restore the position of the medicinal tool.
se li leus est soudez, et char i naist, et li cors de la bowe est soudez, et remaint ensi xl. jors, et il ne renovele et n’est mie apostemez, et accidens mavais n’i vient, saiches qu’il est sanez; se ceu non, si n’i a autre engien que de ramener la fistule au pertus dou neif selonc ceste forme: et est que tu descuevre de l’os la seconde fois par fer, et par medicines agues, et quant il iert descovers si prent .i. foret selonc ceste forme, et soit li chiés de fer a .iij. angles, et li fust soit atenuis jusc’a chief si com tu vois ci:	If the joint is swollen and pus forms, and the bone of the bow is also swollen and remains so for 40 days without healing or becoming an abscess, and no evil accident occurs, knowing it is healthy; if not, there is no other means but to bring back the fistula to the pit of the neck according to this form: And you uncover the bone a second time with iron, and with medicines that burn, and when it is exposed take a foret according to this form, and let the head of the iron be at four angles, and the shaft be shortened up to the head as you see here:
puis le met sus l’os delez lou larmier, et esloigne ta main de l’oil .i. poc, puis torne a tot le foret tant qu’il perce l’os et le sent li malaides par ceu que li vens en ist s’il tient sa main sus son neif; et puis restoure lou leu de medicines seches, si com je t’ai ensigniet, et quant li char naist et endurcist li leus, si vait li matiere au neif; si est plus legiere chose au malaide.	Then place it on the dislocated bone at the elbow, and move your hand away from the oil (i.e., fat). Then turn the screw (foret) completely until it pierces the bone and the patient feels it if they hold their hand on their elbow; and then restore the joint with dry medicines as I have taught you, and when the flesh hardens and strengthens the joint, the matter goes to the elbow; it is a lighter thing for the patient.
de l’issue de l’oil	of the oil issue
Quant li eulz apert fuer dou tout en tout, et il ne vient point de destorbier au nef, ne amenuisement, si covient que tu lies lou malaide; puis le saine, puis li met ventouses ou haterel sens ferir por succier, puis met sus l’oil .i. liien fait d’acaice et de aloe et d’encens et de sarcocolle, et puis estrain l’oil, et l’emplaustre sus de bendes et de drapelz; et li maniere des drapelz si est que tu preignes drapelz assez molz, et double chescun en .iiij., et puis met l’un sus l’autre selonc la quantiteit que li eulz en ait mestier; puis l’estrain par desus d’un bendeil dur forment, et rencomence les ventouses por succier sens ferir; puis oste les ventouses et laisse l’oil estraint jor et nuit, et se li liiens amolist, si covient que tu l’estraignes mout; puis oste lou liien aprés le jor et la nut, et se tu vois l’oil repairier, c’est boin; se ce non; si rencomence l’emplaustre et les drapelz et lou liien et les ventouses tant qu’il soit sanez.	When the eyes are wide open all around and there is no dislocation or decrease in size, it is necessary to hold the patient; then clean it, apply leeches or cauterize to aid healing, then place oil made of acacia, aloe, incense, and sarcolaxis on it, and tie it with a bandage, and then wrap it with strips and cloths; the manner of the cloths is that you take soft cloths, fold each one in four, and then put one on top of another according to the quantity that the eyes require; then bind it with a durable bandage form and repeat the leeches or cauterization without cutting again; then remove the leeches and leave the tied oil for a day and night, and if the lien becomes loose, you must tighten it; then remove the lien after the day and night, and if you see the oil healing, that is good; if not, repeat the application of the poultice and cloths and the lien and the leeches until it heals.
dou derrompement de toile uvee	The broken separation of a ruptured membrane
Quant disruptions vient en la toile uvee, puis apert, et vient fuer des papieres si com .i. grain de resins, et est espoantauble a veoir; adonques se tu la vues coper, li ovraiges est telz que tu boutes une aguille en la racine des la partie desoz jusc’a celi desus, puis boute une autre aguille ou il ait .i. fil double des la partie dou larmier; et la fai percier, et laisse la premiere aguille selonc la disposition; puis cope lou leu dou fil double et lie une partie de l’uve entor, et l’estraint bien, puis estrai l’aguille et met sus l’oil lainne moillie en abun d’uef; et le laisse tant que li filz chiece avec l’uve, puis cure l’oil de choses confortans tant que li plaie soit sanee; et aucune fois li plaie est restrainte par l’uve chescune part d’un cercle de drap, tant qu’elle soit sanee.	When disruptions come in the ruptured membrane, it opens and is forced out like grains of paper, which are frightening to see; then you cover it over. The procedure for this is that you insert an awl into the root of the affected area up to where it ends above, followed by another awl or a double-threaded needle from the tear edge; and make it perforate, leaving the first awl as it was; then hold the eye of the double thread and tie a part of the umbilical cord around it, tighten it well, then remove the awl and apply moistened linen oil over it; and let it remain until the threads adhere to the umbilical cord, then treat the oil with soothing things until the wound is healed; and sometimes the wound is restrained by the umbilical cord on both sides of a circular piece of cloth, until it is healed.
Et se li eulz done grant apparance, si le perce au spatumile subtil qui viegne em parfont de l’oil, et corre la moistor albuginé et dessende li eulz, et entre ens tantost; puis l’estrai tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the eyes appear large, pierce with a fine spatula that comes from oil, and remove the moisture and soften the eyes, then insert it immediately; then pull it out when it is healed.
de la bowe de l’oil	From the bone of the oil [it is made]
Ceste maladie qui est apelee «alcunnati» nen est fuers que bowe qui est assemblee en l’oil, semblant a aigue dessendant, et ce n’est mie aigue; et li maniere de l’apparance de l’ovraige si est que tu faices seoir lou malaide sus .i. siege appareilliet et droit, puis prent le chief entre tes mains de .ij. pars, et lou muef tant que tu voies la bowe venir au desus a tes eulz; puis soit ens fichie, et ne dessende et soit descombree li lumiere, et voie li malaides les choses si com il soloit; et s’elle ne dessent desoz, saiches que c’est aigue, et se li dessendemens de la bowe n’est appareilliez si com nos avons dit. si fai seoir lou malaide entre tes mains, puis prent le spatumile subtil et fent sus la toile cornee .i. poc par la continuation de la conjunctive avec la toile cornee et la corone, tant que li bowe isse; et quant elle ert issue, si distille en l’oil aigue chaude mellee a miel, ou aigue ou fenugreic est boillis et miel, puis soit curee d’autre cure tant qu’elle soit sanee.	This disease called "alcunnati" is not far from the bone that is assembled in the oil, resembling an abscess descending, but it is not an abscess; and the manner of its appearance in the work is that you make the patient sit on a chair arranged and straight, then take the head between your two hands, and move it until you see the bone appear above your eyes; then it should be pierced, and the opening should not be reduced and the light removed, and let the patient observe things as he is used to; and if it does not descend below, know that it is an abscess, and if the descent of the bone is not prepared as we have said. Then make the patient sit between your hands, then take the subtile spatumile [instrument] and apply it on the horned cloth .1 inch along the continuation of the conjunctive with the horned cloth and the corona, until the bone issues; and when it has issued, it should be distilled in hot, sweet oil mixed with honey, or hot oil or fenugreek boiled and mixed with honey, then cured with another remedy until it is healed.
des aigues de l’oil	From the waters of the oil
Nos avons jai les semblances des aigues en la division, et ceu qu’il covient por percier; si en oevre selonc la santeit. Il covient que tu faices seoir lou malaide entre tes mains croisiet, fuers de la lumiere por le soleil, et li lie l’oil sain et estreint mout fort; puis met la papiere de l’oil a ta main senestre se li eulz est senestres, ou a ta main destre se li eulz est destres; puis prent en ta main destre, se li eulz est senestres, l’estrument qui est apelez «almagda», ou a ta main senestre, se li eulz est destre; puis met la pointe de l’estrument delez la corone par la groissece d’un rait en celle blenchor de l’oil a la partie dou menor larmier, puis boute l’estrument qui est apelez «almagda» vertuousement, et trestorne ta main tant qu’il perce en la blenchor de l’oil, et sente que almagda viegne a la chose vuide; et covient que li mesure de la voie almagda soit au parfont de la mesure des l’espaice qui est des la prunele jusc’a la fin de la noirour; et c’est li corone de l’oil; si verras l’os en celle papiere por la clarteit de la toile cornee, et pues met l’estrument jusc’a leu ou li aigue est, puis l’espresse desoz une voie aprés autre. se li aigue dessent maintenant, si voit li malaides devant lui et l’estrument en son oil.	1. We have the appearance of the eyes in division, and that which is required to pierce; if you work according to its health. You must make the patient sit between your hands crossed, away from the light due to the sun, and let him hold the oil sanitary and press it very hard; then take paper of oil with your left hand if the eyes are on the left side, or with your right hand if the eyes are on the right side; then take in your right hand (if the eyes are on the left side) the instrument called "almagda", or in your left hand (if the eyes are on the right side); then place the point of the instrument next to the cornea by a ray's thickness into the white part of the oil at the lower part of the inner corner, then push the instrument called "almagda" skillfully, and hold your hand as long as it pierces through the white part of the oil, and feel that almagda comes to an empty place; and the measurement of the path of almagda should be at the full length of the measure of the space from the pupil to the end of the iris; this is the cornea of the eye; you will see the bone in that paper due to the clarity of the horn-coated cloth, then place the instrument up to where the eye is, and press it down through another opening. If the eye moves now, the patient will see before him and the instrument in his oil.
Aprés repose .i. petit, et se li aigue remonte la seconde voie, met la fuer avec l’estrument, et quant elle est ens fichie et ele ne monte, si estrai almagda legierement en tornoiant ta main poc et poc; et puis remette en aigue un poc de seil gemme, et leive de ceu l’oil dedens. Puis met par defuer l’oil estoupes ou lainne moillie en oile roset et en abun d’uef, et lie avec l’oil sain.  Nos, et cil qui sont de nostre tens, mettons sus comin broiet avec abun d’uef.	After a short rest and if the eye rises again through the second path, place force with the instrument, and when it is fully inserted and does not rise again, hold almagda gently while rotating your hand slowly; then insert a small amount of gemstone oil again, and remove the oil inside. Then put on the outside either damp cloth or wet and oiled linen, and bind with the sanitary oil. We, and those from our times, put comfrey with abundant egg white on top.
Et se almagda n’i puet entrer en l’oil par sa duresce, car il i a de teilz homes qui ont trop durs les eulz, si covient que tu preignes l’estrument qui est apelez «alberit», de coi ci est li forme:	And if almagda cannot enter into the oil due to its hardness, for there are some people who have excessively hard eyes, then you must take the instrument called "alberit", which is as follows:
Et perce donques la conjunctive soulement, et n’aler mie trop em parfont, mais fai .i. leu subtil, puis i boute almagda, si com nos avons dit; et au complissement de l’uevre appareille au malaide .i. dorteur avenant, en coi il dorme sus son dos en .j. leu tenebrous; et soit deveez de toz movemens, et preigne legieres viandes, et ne mueve son chief ne a destre ne a senestre, et soit liiez selonc sa disposition jusc’a tier jor; puis le deslie en cele maison meisme tenebrouse, et esprueve sa veue, et lou fai veoir aucunes choses, et puis li remet lou lien jusc’a septime jor; et ne covient mie que tu faices ceu en l’oure de la cure ou aprés l’incision maintenant, mais il covient que tu aliges ceu, por ceu que li aigue monte hastanment.	And therefore pierce only the conjunction [joint], and do not go too deep, but make it subtle, then apply alum, as we have said; and when the work is completed, arrange a pillow for the patient, in which he sleeps on his back in 2 cushions; and be careful of all movements, and take light foods, and do not move his head neither to the right nor to the left, and bind him according to his position until the third day; then unbind him in the same dark place, and test his sight, and let him see certain things, and then rebind him for up to seven days; and it is not necessary that you do this during the time of care or after the incision, but it is necessary that you alleviate this, because the pain increases quickly.
se apostemes chaus vient, que tu desliies l’oil devant le septime jor, et l’adrece de ceu qui assouaige aposteme; et quant il est apaisiez, si deslie la veue et met sus sa faice .i. orilliet por covrir aucun jor, et soit adés en celle maison tenebrouse. Et puis isse de la maison poc et poc, et se convertisse en ses cas; et saiches que nulz deciples ne se doit entremettre en cest cas.	When the abscess comes out, you unbind the oil before the seventh day, and direct those who soothe the abscess; and when it is soothed, unbind the sight and put 1 eyepatch over his face to cover any day, and remain in that dark place. Then gradually leave the house little by little, and convert in his case; and know that no disciples should interfere in this case.
Et uns vint a nos qui estoit de la Yrach, qui nos dist que en som pais faisoit om almagda perciet, a coi on succe l’aigue, mais toutevoie je n’en vis onques nul en nostre terre, ne je ne lou lis onques en livres des anciens; et par aventure c’est une novele chose.	And one came to us who was from Iriha, who told us that in his country people pierce alum, so that the pain subsides, but I have never seen anyone do it on our land, nor have I ever read it in the books of the ancients; and perhaps it is a new thing.
Et ce sont les semblances des formes de almagda, por ceu que cil qui ne les conoit les voie; et soient d’arain proprement:	And these are the appearances of forms of almadga, for this reason those who do not recognize them will see them; and they are of iron properly speaking:
Et soient li chief d’aus de ceste meisme subtiliteit, et li derriene en .iij. angles ague.	And their heads are of the same subtlety, and the points in four angles are sharp.
de la char sor le neis	from the flesh on the neck
Aucune fois naissent ou neis chars ajostees diverses, de coi il i a aucunes qui semblent scorpions a mout de piez; et si i a de telz ou il ait char enchancree de fuxe color, et si a char souef de bone color. En celle donques de ces chars qui est souef, et ne mie enchancree, covient que tu faices seoir lou malaide entre tes mains encontre lou soleil; et oevre ses narines, et giete l’oncine a celles chars, et les trai fuers; puis cope ceu que tu em pues sostenir au spatumile subtil agut d’une part, tant que tu saiches que celle char est toute ostee.	Never are born or grow necks with different shapes, for this reason there are some that resemble scorpions in many places; and if there is a neck swollen of a certain color and the flesh soft of good color, then you must make the patient sit between your hands facing the sun; and open his nostrils, and pour vinegar on those necks, and pull them out; then hold what you can grab with the subtle pointed spatula, until you know that that neck is completely severed.
Et s’il en remaint aucune chose c’on ne puisse coper, si l’ovrez a tout .i. des estrumens subtil legierement, si qu’il n’i demoure rien; et se sans te sormonte, ou aposteme chaus, si lou secort si com il covient; et se c’est apostemes malignes, si te haste et lou cauterize tant que li sans soit estainchiez et soient ostees toutes les chars, puis giete ou neis aisil et aigue ou vin.	And if there remains any matter which cannot be covered, open it all with subtle and light instruments, so that nothing remains; and if without your protection or abscess covering, it should break, assist it as necessary; and if the abscess is malignant, hurry and cauterize it until the pus is drained and all the charring is removed, then pour in oil or warm water or wine.
Se li neis oevre, et moistors en vient jusc’a palais, saiches qu’il est sanez; et se moistors ne perce si com il covient, saiches qu’il i a char nee en l’os desus, acoi li estrumens ne vient mie por taillier: adonques covient il que tu i boutes .i. fil de lin un poc gros, et soit noez de mains nous, et ait entre chescun nout d’espaice .i. doit ou moins; et mette li malaides lou chiés dou fil en son neif a som pooir, et traie en odorant tant qu’il viegne par lou neif dedens la bouche; et maintes fois font ensi li enfant as escoles, et c’est legiere chose a celui qui le vuet faire; puis tien le chief qui vient par lou neif a une main, et l’autre chief qui vient par la bouche a l’autre main, et saiche l’un aprés l’autre en soiant as nous qui sont ou fil. Fai ceu tant que tu saiches que li nout ont corrompue celle char, puis trai lou filz, essue le sanc, et moille lou fil en oignement egiptien, et le remet derechief au neis si com devant; fai ceu .iij. jors ou plus, tant que li oignemens corrode tout ceu qui est demorez de char; et puis met ou neis une caine de plonc aucuns jors tant qu’il soit sanez, et s’il a mestier de medicines sechans, si en use; et c’est li forme de l’estrument por purgier lou chief, a coi on distille les oiles et les medicines ou neis:	If the nostril opens and moisture reaches the palate, know that it is healthy; and if moisture does not pierce as necessary, know that there is pus in the bone above, so instruments do not come to cut: then you must place a thick thread of flax, knotted at regular intervals, between each knot a space of one finger's width or less; and insert the thread through the nostril into the patient's mouth as far as possible, and pull while smelling until pus comes out through the nose; and children in school often do this, and it is easy for those who wish to perform it; then hold the head which comes out through the nose in one hand, and the other head which comes out through the mouth in the other hand, and know one after the other while we are those who hold the thread. Do this until you know that the threads have corrupted the pus, then pull the threads, squeeze out the blood, and moisten the thread with Egyptian ointment, and put it back into the nose as before; do this for four days or more, until the ointment has corroded everything remaining of the pus; and then put oil in the nostril for several days until it is healthy, and if there is a need for drying medicines, use them; and this is the form of the instrument to purge the head, as one distills oils and medicines through the nose.
Et soit d’argent ou d’arain, semblant a une lampe overte, si com une cainne, et li conduis ausi; et se tu vues, si fai une cainne close, et soit li estrumens plains por espurgier lou chief; et ait .i. mainche au chief por lou tenir quant on chaufe l’oile ou aucune liquor.	And it is made of silver or brass, resembling a lamp with an open top, like a funnel, and guide it in this way; and if you see, make a closed funnel, and have the instruments full for purging the head; and have one handle on the head to hold when heating the oil or any liquid.
de la char sor le neis	Of the flesh on the neck
Maintes fois naist au chief dou neis une maladie qui est apelee «telul», et croist et devient grans adés, tant qu’il est vis chose au regarder; et por ceu covient que tu lou copes au comencement, et l’oste tout fuer, puis met sor leu lou cautere ou la medicine ardant; et s’on le tarde a coper tant qu’il soit grans, si pren warde s’il est durs, de fuxe color, de povre sens: si ne lou touchier mie de fer car c’est uns apostemes enchancrez, car quant on le cope aucune fois, si en vient grant malice au malaide; et se li apostemes est de soef touchement, non mie de fuxe color, et tu vois c’on le puisse tout coper, si vuide le malaide et lou cope sens paor, et cure le leu de choses sechans et restraignans.	Many times a disease called "telul" arises on the head of the neck, which grows and becomes large enough to see; and because of this, you must cut it at the beginning, excise all of it, then put fire cautery or burning medicine on the place; if it is delayed until it becomes large, if it is hard, blackish, with poor sensation: do not touch it with iron as it is an enlarged abscess, for when it is cut once, it causes great harm to the patient; and if the abscess is of soft touch, not blackish, and you can cover it, then empty the patient and cauterize with fear, and treat the place with drying and constricting agents.
quant li neis est copez et cosus	when the neck is cut and sewn up
Saiches que quant solutions de continuation vient en une de ces cartillagines ovraiges, i profite poc, fuer que en aucuns homes. Il covient donques cant ceu avient a aucun, si regarde se li plaie est fresche a tout son sanc; et adonques ajoste les .ij. levres a une costure, puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et se les levres sont ja desevrees d’une part et d’autre, si covient que tu escorches toutes les parties de lor keur tant qu’elles sainent, puis assemble les .ij. levres a une costure, et l’estraint, et poudre sus poudre de sanc de dragon, et encens broiet; et met sus les poudres une piece d’emplaustre de fort ou d’autre emplaustre soudant, et le laisse tant qu’il chiece par lui, puis le cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez.	Know that when solutions of continuation come to one of these cartilage joints, it benefits little, except in some men. Therefore, whenever this happens to anyone, you should check if the wound is fresh with all its blood; and then bring the two lips together with a stitch, heal it until it is healthy; and if the lips are already separated from both sides, you must sew up all the parts of their joint as much as they heal, then bring the two lips together with a stitch, tighten it, and sprinkle powder of dragon's blood powder on top, and incense ground; and place some plaster of strong or other plaster on top of the powders until it hardens by itself, then heal it with ointment until it is healthy.
Li maniere de la costure si est que tu assembles la solution: ou par aguilles, si com nos avons dit en la costure dou ventre; ou par fil, si com je le t’ai fait savoir.	The method of stitching is that you bring the solution together: either with needles, as we have said in the abdomen stitch; or with thread, as I have told you.
des apostemes des levres	abscesses of the lips
A mains homes avient dedens les levres aposteme dur, semblans a grains de veces, et menor et plus grant; adonques couvient que tu tornes les levres, et fendes sus chescun nout, et le prent as pinceures et le cope en chescune partie; puis emple lou leu aprés l’incision de vitriole broiet, tant que li sans soit estainchiez; et puis lou leive d’aisil, et cure lou leu de choses seches tant qu’il soit sanez.	In the hands of men, there often forms an abscess deep within the lips, resembling grains of wheat, smaller or larger; then you must turn the lips, and cut open each side, take it with tweezers and squeeze in each part; then apply the powdered vitriol to the wound until the pus is drained; and then apply alum to the wound, and treat the wound with dry things until it heals.
de la char des gencives	of the gums (of the teeth)
Maintes fois naist sus les gencives char ajostee, que li ancien apelent «albulus»; si covient que tu la sostienes as tenailles, et la cope a sa racine, et laisse corre la bowe ou le sanc; puis met sor le leu vitriole broiet, ou autres poudres restraignans et desiccatives; et se celle char revient aprés l’incision, et maintes fois avient, si la cope la seconde fois, et la cauterize: si ne revient mie aprés le cautere; et ce sont les formes des estrumens por coper.	Many times a pimple appears on the gums, which the ancients called “albulus”; then you must hold it with tweezers, and squeeze its root, and let the blood flow; then apply vitriol powder or other powders that restrain and dry it; and if the pimple returns after the incision, and this happens often, then squeeze it again and cauterize it; it will not return after the cautery; and these are the instruments to cover (the wound).
des sordens	The sores
Aucunes fois sont assemblees au chief des dens, dedens la bouche entre les gencives, escorces qui sont laides et aspres; et aucune fois sont li dent noir et citrin et vers, tant que li corruption vient a la gencive, et sont li dent puant; si covient que tu faices seoir lou malaide entre tes mains, et ses chiés soit en ton saint, et reis les dens ou les escorces aperent, tant qu’il n’i demore rien; et ensi fai de la noiror et de la verdor, et de la jaunice et des autres taiches, tant qu’elles soient mondees; et s’on oste ceu que i est a la premiere rasion, c’est boin; se ceu non, si rencomence a rere le secont jor et lou tier, tant que tu aies tout reis; et saiches que li dent ont mestier de diverses formes d’estrumens por reire, selonc ceu que li oevre lou demoustre, por ceu que li raseur dont on reit defuer les dens ont autres formes que cil dont on reit entre les dens; et cestes formes et autres soient avec toi appareillies.	Sometimes there are sores around the teeth, inside the mouth between the gums, rough and harsh sores; and sometimes the teeth are black and yellow and decaying when corruption comes to the gum, and the teeth stink; you must make the patient sit between your hands, and his head should be in your lap, and you should remove the sores or the roughness that appear, until nothing remains; and do the same for the blackness and greenness, and the yellow and other spots, until they are cleaned; and if you remove what is there at first sight, it is good; but if not, start again on the second day and third, as long as you have completely cleaned them; and know that the teeth need different forms of instruments for cleaning, according to what the work demonstrates, because the instrument used to clean the teeth has other forms than that used between the teeth; and these forms and others should be prepared with you.
Il covient quant tu cures lou dent de sa dolor que tu tardes dou traire tant com tu pues, car ce ne doit om mie faire; car c’est une substance mout haute jusc’a donc c’on n’ait point d’excusation dou raier.	It is necessary when you treat the tooth of its pain that you delay drawing it out as much as possible, for this should not be done at all; for this is a very high substance up to which there is no excuse for scraping.
Adonques quant li malaides est constrains dou traire, si covient que tu soies certains dou dent doillant. Maintes fois desoit li dolor lou malaide, et cuide qu’elle soit ou dent saint, et fait traire le boin dent; et toutevoie ne se depart mie li dolor per ceu, tant que li malvais estrais, car nos l’avons ja veut faire a ces sainors; et quant tu es bien certains dou dent doillant, si covient que tu escorches entor lou dent a tout i. spatumile fort por warder la gencive de toutes pars; puis le mues a tes dois ou as tenailles subtilz au premier poc et poc, tant qu’il soit bien eslochiés, puis i afferme bien les tenailles; et soit li chiés dou malaide en ton saint entre tes genous, et lou tien bien si qu’il ne se mueve.	Then when the patient is compelled to draw a tooth, it is necessary that you are certain of the correct one. Many times, despite the pain, the patient believes it is a good tooth and draws out the healthy one; yet the pain does not cease until the bad one is removed, as we have experienced with such patients; and when you are absolutely sure of the tooth to be drawn, first scrape around the tooth entirely with strong spatula to protect the gum from all sides; then grasp it with your fingers or fine pliers at the base of the tooth, and gradually loosen it until it is well dislodged; then firmly hold the pliers; and keep the patient's head steady in your lap, so that it does not move.
Aprés estrai lou dent droitement sens brisier, et s’il ne saut fuer, si prent aucun de ces estrumens et le boute dedens de chescune part legierement, et lou remuef si com tu as fait premier. Et se li dens est perciez et mengiez, si covient que tu l’emplisses de drapelz, lai ou li pertus sont; et si l’estraint subtilment as tenailles, que il ne brise a l’estraindre; et covient mout saigement ovrer entor la gencive por deschaucier lou dent.	After drawing the tooth correctly and if it does not break out on its own, take any of these instruments and gently push it in from each side, and move it as you have previously done. And if the tooth is perforated and broken into pieces, it is necessary to fill it with fabric or cloth where the fracture has occurred; and grasp it subtly with pliers, so that it does not break while being extracted; and work very skillfully around the gum to extract the tooth.
Et te done bien en warde que tu ne le brises, et en remaigne une partie, et reveigne au malaide par la malice de la racine plus grans dolors de la premiere. Et te warde que tu ne faices mie ensi com font li ignorant sainor, qui par lor haste et par lor hardiesce brisent aucune fois le charreit, et n’i amenistrent mie ceu que nos avons conteit; mais font venir aucune fois par l’oquison de ceu grant maladie por les racines que i demorent, ou por lou charreit qu’il brisent, si com nos avons sovent veut; et quant li dens est trais, si lavez lou leu de vin ou d’aisil et de seil; et se decorremens de sanc i vient, que sovent avient, si emple lou leu de vitriole broiet; et se ceu ne vaut, si le cauterize.	And take care that you do not break it and leave a part behind, and return more pain to the patient through the root's malice than the original pain. And beware that you do not act as ignorant doctors who in their haste and recklessness sometimes break the chariot and do not achieve what we have described; but sometimes they bring about great disease due to the roots that remain or because they break the chariot, as we have often seen; and when the tooth is drawn, wash the area with wine or oil and soap; and if bleeding persists, which frequently occurs, use vitriol powder; and if it is not effective, cauterize.
Les formes des estrumens, a coi om muet les dens premier, soient a longes pointes et a gros mainches, qu’il ne doublent mie quant tu trairas le dent; et ce sont les formes:	The forms of the instruments, with which one silences the teeth first, should have long points and large handles, so they do not double when you extract the tooth; and these are their shapes:
Et soient de gros membres si qu’il ne ploient mie au traire, et soient de fer inde bien fait, et soient dentez por mues tenir.	And should be large handles so they do not bend when pulling, and made of good iron, and have teeth for holding on.
de la racine des dens	of the root of the tooth
Quant li racine demoure au traire, si covient que tu mettes sor le leu coton moilliet em burre .i. jor ou ij., tant que li leus soit amolis, puis i boute les tenailles qui sont apelees «algefri», de coi li chiés semblet bec de soigne; et soient dedens faites ausi com une lime et c’est li forme:	When the root remains after pulling, then you must put cotton soaked in butter on it for 1 to 2 days until the area is softened, and then insert the tongs called "algefri", which look like a tweezers for this purpose; they should be made inside like a chisel and this is their shape:
Et se les racines ne vuellent issir a tout ces tenailles, si covient que tu descuevre la char tot entor la racine, et i met l’estrument qui est apelez «althali», c’est a savoir palainche, de coi ci est li forme:	And if the roots do not want to come out with all these tools, then you must expose the flesh entirely around the root, and place the instrument called "althali," which is known as palancha, of this form:
Et soit fors et gros si qu’il ne brise mie, et se li racine saut par ceu, c’est boin; se ceu non, si t’aide de toz les estrumens, de coi les formes vienent ci aprés:	And it should be thick and large so as not to break it, and if the root jumps out through those tools, that is good; if not, help with all the instruments, from which the shapes come after:
Et si s’aide on de cest estrument qui ait .ij. rains, de coi ci est li forme:	And if you use an instrument with two prongs, of this form:
et d’autres ferremens qui sont devant en la rasion des dens, et de cest estrument qui semble unes grans tenailles, dont ci est li forme:	And other instruments which are before the teeth, and of this tool that seems like large pincers, whose shape is as follows:
Et soit cist estrumens fors qu’il ne puisse brisier, et saiches que mout d’estrumens de dens sont; et ausi d’autres estrumens, qui ne sont mie contez; et li saiges maistres subtilz trueve par soi meisme son estrument, selonc ceu que ses ovraiges et li maladie li demoustre, car il i a de teilz maladies ou li ancien n’enseignerent point d’estrument por la diversiteit d’au;s et s’om brise point dou charreit ou des autres os, ou il porrit, si i cerche as estrumens qu’il i covient, que je t’ai dit, et t’aide des gestes, de coi ci est li forme:	And it should not break, and know that many instruments of the teeth are; and also other instruments, which are not counted; and the wise masters find their tools by themselves, according to what their work and the illness indicate, for there are such diseases where the old masters did not teach any tool because of the diversity of ailments, and if it breaks a chariot or another bone, or if it could, then seek the instruments that are required, which I have told you, and help with gestures, as follows:
Et soient gros et bien tenant por tenir l’os, qu’il n’eschaipe, mais le puisse tenir et oster; et puis restoure lou leu de medicines convenant a ceu, et s’il ait en l’os porriture, et elle est petite, si la reis a tout cest estrument:	And they should be large and sturdy to hold the bone and not slip, but it can hold and extract; then restore the joint with appropriate medicines, and if there is pus in the bone, and it is small, use this entire instrument:
Quant li dent apperent ne mie selonc lou cors natureil, et li forme est laide, et meismement en femmes puceles, si covient que tu saiches se li dens est neis aprés lou dent, et n’est mie en droit leu, et on ne lou puet soier ne limer: adonques lou raie; et s’il est aers avec lou dent, si prent cest estrument dont ci est li forme, et est semblans a .i. petit bec, et soit de fer inde agut en som:	When teeth appear not according to natural shape, and the form is ugly, even in girls, you should know that if the tooth is not born after the gum, and it is not correctly positioned, and cannot be straightened or filed: drill (it); and if it is exposed with the tooth, take this tool whose shape is like a small beak, made of hard steel at the tip:
Et lou cope poc et poc em mains jors por la duresce dou dent, et por ceu que tu ne mueves les autres, et s’il est apparans c’on le puisse limer, si lou lime d’une teil lime com ci est li forme:	And the handle of the copper instrument is held for long hours due to the hardness of the tooth, and because you do not move the others; if it appears that one can file it, then file it with a small flat file like this shape:
et est ausi com li lime de coi on fait les aguilles; et en lime lou dent poc et poc em mains jors legierement, si qu’il ne se mueve tant qu’il chiece; puis la plaine en la fin a tout aucun raseur, et se li dens est trop trenchans et il blece la lengue, si covient limer l’aspreteit tant qu’il soit igalz, si qu’il ne blece la lengue ne ne corrompe la parole.	and is similar to the file used to make needles; and file the tooth gently for long hours until it stops hurting; then plane the end with any rasp, and if the tooth is too sharp and bites the tongue, you must file the sharpness until it is even, so that it does not hurt the tongue or corrupt the speech.
quant li dent lochent	When the teeth fall out
