Quant li dent devant lochent, ou par percussion ou par cheoir, et li malaides ne puet presser sus ceu qu’il menjue qu’il ne chient, et tu les as curez de medicines restrignans, et ceu ne vaut; si les covient restraindre d’un fil d’or, car li filz d’argent devient vert et porrit, mais li ors ne se mue onques; et soit li filz moiens ne trop gros ne trop menus, selonc la quantiteit de l’espaice entre les dens; et se tu vues adrecier les dens, si pren lou fil et lou boute double entre les .ij. dens sains, puis met les chiés entre les dens meus, s’il en i a .i. ou plusors, tant que tu veignes saigement jusc’au dent sain d’autre part; puis rencomence la coverture jusc’a la partie ou tu encomensas, et estrains ta main subtilment et saigement, tant qu’il ne se mueve point; et soit ta lieeure a la racine dou dent si qu’il ne puist eschaper. Puis cope les chiés dou fil a unes tenailles, et les assemble, et les repont entre le dent sain, et le met ensi qu’il ne blece la lengue; et puis le laisse ensi estroit tant com il puet demorer, et s’il deslie, ou li filz ront, si l’estraint d’un autre fil; si demorrait et servira ensi tout son tens, et c’est li forme des dens et li figure de l’adrecement des .ij. dens sains, et des .ij. meus, si com tu vois:	When the teeth fall out, either by percussion or by falling, and the patient cannot force it back up for chewing, you should treat them with medicines that tighten, but this is of no use; instead, they must be held together with a gold wire, as silver wire becomes green and rots, but gold does not change; neither too thick nor too thin, according to the space between the teeth; and if you want to align the teeth, take the wire and place it double between two healthy teeth, then put the roots between the misaligned teeth, whether there is one or more, as long as you see clearly up to the healthy tooth on the other side; then cover back up to the part where you started, and hold your hand subtly and skillfully, so that it does not move; and hold your grip at the root of the tooth so that it cannot escape. Then grab the roots with the pliers, and assemble them, and place them back between the healthy tooth, and make sure it does not bite the tongue; then leave it so tight as it can remain for a time, and if they come loose or the wire breaks, hold it together with another wire; if it remains and serves for a time, and this is the shape of the teeth and the alignment of the two healthy teeth and the two misaligned ones, as you see:
Et quant li dent chiet, si lou remet on en son leu, de fres en fres, si com nos avons dit; et ne s’en entremette mie qui n’est saiges et soffrans, et aucune fois fait on la forme d’un dent d’os de vaiche, et lou met on au leu ou li defaute est, et l’estraint on si com nos avons dit, et demore et sert ensi lonc tens.	And when the tooth falls out, put it back in its place, as we have said; and let no one interfere who is not wise and patient, and sometimes the shape of a bone tooth is made and placed where the lack exists, and hold it together as we have said, and remain and serve for a long time.
de coper lou liien de la lengue	To cover the ligament of the tongue
Aucune fois est cist liiens qui vient desoz la lengue ou naturez, que on naist ensi; ou par accident de plaie soudee; et li ovraiges est telz que tu oevre la bouche dou malaide, et ait sa teste en ton sain, et li lieve la lengue; puis cope lou liien nervous dou large, tant que li lengue soit desloie de son tenement, et se il i a duresce ou nout, et c’est de soudement de plaie, si i boute l’uncine et cope dou large celui liement; et garde que li fendure ne soit mie trop em parfont, por l’artere qui est desoz; et quant tu as fait, si leve le leu d’aigue rose et d’aisil, ou d’aigue froide, puis met desoz la lengue une tente de lin; et la teigne li malaides chescune nuit, que li leus ne puisse soder. Et se decorremens de sanc vient, si met sor le leu vitriole broiet; et se li sans te vaint, si le cauterize au cautere lentiginout, qui est boin a ceu; puis le cure d’autre cure tant qu’il soit sanez,	Sometimes this ligament comes under the tongue due to nature or birth defect, or by accident due to a wound; and these treatments are as follows: open the patient's mouth, hold his head steady, and lift the tongue; then cover the nerve-like ligament widely, until the tongue is dislocated from its place, if there is stiffness or not, and it is due to a deep wound, you press the unguent and widen the ligament; be careful that the incision is not too deep, for the artery that is beneath; and when done, lift a piece of fresh lambskin or a piece of fresh cold rose and place it under the tongue; and bind the patient's mouth so that it does not heal. If blood discharge occurs, apply vitriol powder; if the wound weeps, cauterize with a gentle cautery, which is good for this purpose; then treat it with another remedy until it is healed.
et se tu lou vois de fusse color ou noir ou dur, si que li malaides ne lou sent, si n’i touchier point, car c’est chancre; et s’il est declinans a blenchor, et il i a moistor, si i giete l’oncine, et lou fent d’un spatumile subtil, et lou delivre d’une part et d’autre; et se li sans te vaint a ton ovraige, si met sus vitriole broiet tant qu’il soit estainchiez, puis revien a ton ovraige tant que tu traies tout fuer; puis leve lou leu d’aisil et de seil, et le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	If you see it (the wound) of pale color or black or hard, so that the patient does not feel it, do not touch it, for it is a cancer; and if it is declining towards a blister and there is moisture, pour unguent onto it, and loosen it from both sides with a thin spatula; and if the wound weeps at your work, apply vitriol powder until it is drained, then return to your work until you drain all of it; then lift fresh lambskin or silk and treat it with other remedies until it heals.
des apostemes de la gorge	abscesses of the throat
Aucune fois vient dedens la gorge boces qui sont apelees «godath», et les apele on proprement les .ij. amandres, et quant tu les cures, si com nos avons dit en la division, et elles ne sont sanees, si pren garde: se c’est apostemes dur de petit sens et de fusse color, si ne lou touchier mie de fer. Et s’il est rouges et li racine est grosse, si ne lou touchier mie de fer, ausi por lou decorrement de sanc; mais lou laisse tant qu’il soit meur, et adonques tu lou partiras, ou il rompirait par soi; et s’il est de blainche color reont, et li racine est subtilz, si aies apareilliet l’estrument por coper, mais regarde premierement se li apostemes chalz repose et est apaisiez. Adonques fai seoir lou malaide devant lou soleil, et ses chiés soit en ton sain, et li oevre la bouche et lou preigne li serjans entre ses mains, et presse la lengue desoz a tout l’estrument, de coi ci est li forme; et soit d’argent ou d’arain subtil ausi com uns coutelz:	Sometimes boils called 'godath' appear within the throat, which are properly called the two mandibles. And when you treat them, as we have said in the division, and they are not healed, take care: if it is a hard abscess with small sense and pale color, do not touch it with iron. And if it is red and the root is large, do not touch it with iron, for fear of blood flow; but let it be until it dies, and then you will cut it, or it would burst by itself; and if it is of white color, retracted, and the root is subtle, prepare the instrument to cover. But first check that the abscess is cold and calmed. Then make the patient sit in front of the sun, his chin in your hand, and open his mouth wide, and take hold of the sergeant with the tongs between his hands, and press the whole instrument under it, which is its form; it can be made of silver or subtle brass like a knife:

Et je medicinai une femme d’un aposteme que li estoit neis dedens la gorge, c’est a savoir .i. aposteme de petit sens; et avoit jai bien pres close toute la gorge, si que li femme ne pooit expirer por le conduit qui estoit estoupez, et ne pooit ne mengier ne boivre, et fust morte s’elle demorast ensi .i. jor ou .ij. I treated a woman with an abscess that was inside her throat, specifically one of small size; and I had closed the entire throat, so that the woman could not exhale through the blocked passageway, nor eat or drink, and would have died within a day or two if she had remained in this state. The abscess was so large that it had filled two fingers' width through both openings of the throat. I immediately drained it, and inserted a cannula through one opening, then pulled it out, and extracted a large piece of pus; after which, I closed the other opening of the throat, and opened her mouth and pressed her tongue; afterwards, I inserted the cannula into these abscesses, took some of its contents, and only a little blood came out; and in this way, the blocked passageway of the throat was unblocked for the woman, and she began to drink hot water and then wine, and did not stop cutting away from this abscess for long periods; and the abscess grew back again, filling the space that I had intended to empty, until it became quite large; at that point, I tricked it and cauterized it inside her throat: in this way, it stopped growing; and I left the area, and did not know what happened to her afterwards.
de l’uve	of the eye
Quant reume dessent a l’uve, et elle est enflee et elle est longe, si est apelee «perpendiculaire»; et s’elle est desoz grosse et reonde, si est apelee «uve». And have a hair or a piece of cloth where medicine is placed, like the handle of a spoon, and put the instrument completely over the medicine on the eye; and let the patient lie on his side, so that the saliva and mucus flows from his mouth into the medicine, but does not go down the throat or nose; then hold your hand over the entire medicine and press it on the eye, for about half an hour, until you see the swelling and pain of the medicine subside; and if you see, take cotton and wrap it around some instrument, wet the cotton in the medicine, and insert the instrument into the sheath above, so that the cotton adheres to the eye; and do this frequently, until the cauterization is complete, then let it dry, and wait for four or five days. de la sansue de la gorge	the windpipe of the throat
Aucune fois est medicinee li sansue, si com j’ai dit en la division, par la cure de medicines; et quant ceu ne profite mie, adonques regarde en la gorge dou malaide au soleil, puis que tu li presses la lengue a l’estrument que je t’ai dit. And if you see the windpipe, pull it out with a small pair of scissors or fine pliers suitable for that purpose. If this is not possible, take a thin cable and put it into the patient's throat, then insert or bend the hot part of the cable into the throat several times. And anoint the patient with cold water all day. Then take a full glass of cold water, open his mouth, pour it in without letting him swallow, and move it around in his mouth frequently; and as soon as the windpipe feels the cold water, it will fall.
Et s’elle ne chiet si com nos avons dit, si subfumige lou malaide d’asefetide, a l’estrument que j’ai dit en la fumigation de l’uve; fai ceu maintes fois, car elle cherra sens targier. li chapistres des apostemes	The chapters on abscesses
Mout de semblances d’aposteme sont, selonc ceu que li remembrance vient ci aprés d’un et d’autre en cest livre, et sont diver en perforation et en taille; et c’est en .ij. manieres dont l’une est en sa semblance meisme, et de ceu qu’il tient moistor. Et li seconde maniere si est por les leus ou il sont au cors. car li apostemes dou chief est autres que cil dou fondement, et li apostemes dou leu charnut est autres que cil qui vient en jointures, et chescuns ait son jugement en l’uevre.	Many resemble abscesses, according to what is remembered hereafter from one and another in this book, and they are diverse in penetration and cutting; and it is in .ij. ways that one is like itself, and of those that retain moisture. And the second way is for the joints where they are in the body. For abscesses of the head are other than those of the base, and abscesses of the shoulder blade are other than those which come in joints, and each should have its judgment in the work.
Et si a apostemes c’on ne doit mie percier, tant que li bowe est meure selonc son acomplissement; et si a de telz qu’il covient percier quant il sont crut, et ne meurent mie selonc lor acomplissement, si com aposteme qui sont delez jointures. Car quant apostemes vient delez jointures, et on le laisse tant qu’il est porris entor, par aventure si sont corrumput li liien et li nerf de la jointure, par coi ce est cause de contraction en celui membre. Ou li aposteme est delez lou membre principel, et se tu tardes la perforation tant qu’il soit meurez, si nuira au membre principeil; ou il est delez lou fondement, si le perce on ainsois qu’il soit meurs; et ne covient mie que tu perces aposteme crut sens digestion acomplie, fuers que celui qui est delez lou fondement, qu’il ne porrisse em parfont, et soit alongiez dedens, et i viegne fistule; et ne puisse saner en grant termine.	And if the abscess should not be pierced, until the bowels are ripe according to their completion; and if of those that require piercing when they are hard, and do not die according to their completion, such as abscesses which come from joints. For when abscesses come from joints, and it is left until it is surrounded by pus, perhaps the ligament and nerve of the joint will be corrupted, causing contraction in that member. Or if the abscess is from the main part of the body, and the piercing is delayed until it is ripe, it will damage the main part; or if it is from the base, pierce it thus before it becomes ripe; and do not pierce a hard abscess without complete digestion, except that which is from the base, that it may not be hollowed out and become long within, and a fistula comes forth; and cannot heal in great term.
Et covient que tu saiches l’oure de la perforation de l’aposteme qui est meur selonc l’acomplissement, et c’est quant li dolor est apaisie, et li departemens de la fievre, et l’amenuisement de la dolor et de la roujor, et dou debatement et de l’aguisement dou chief de l’aposteme, et les autres signes; et covient que tu faices seoir la perforation ou plus dependant leu de l’aposteme, et la ou il apert mues; et soit li perforation dou lonc dou cors, et se li apostemes est as mains ou as piez, ou en jointures et au ners et as arteres, et en toz leus igalz ou il n’a point de ploieure.	And you should know the time of piercing the abscess that is ripe according to its completion, and it is when the pain is alleviated, and the departure of the fever, and the decrease of pain and redness, and the swelling and movement of the head of the abscess, and other signs; and you should make the piercing sit where the abscess depends more closely, and where it has opened; and let the piercing be long in the body, and if the abscesses are in the hands or feet, or in joints and nerves and arteries, and in all even places where there is no plaque.
En ces que ploient, par selonc celui membre. Et quant apostemes est en leu charnut, si vaut mues que tu laisses la perforation tant qu’il soit confermez en digestion acomplie, si com nos avons dit. Car se tu lou perces devant ceu, si iert alongiez li cors dou venim de lui, et est plains de mout d’ordure; et par aventure endurcissent les levres et li parfondetez de lui. Et si a aucun aposteme que sont perciet selonc le large dou cors, selonc ceu que li membres en ait mestier. For if you pierce it before this, the body will fill with blood and be full of much pus; and possibly harden the lips and deeply affect them. And for any abscess that are pierced according to the size of the body, according to what the limb needs. Cil qui n’ont point de chief, si com aposteme souef superficial, il covient que tu lou perces plainnement; et covient quant li apostemes est gros, et il a coillit grant bowe, et tu lou perces, si ne traire mie toute la bowe en celle houre, mais en trai une partie; puis estoupe l’aposteme jusc’a l’autre jor, puis en trai aucune chose derechief; fai ceu par maintes fois de greit en greit, tant que li bowe isse toute; meismement se li malaides est de foible vertut, ou femme portans, ou petis enfes, ou viez hons decrepites. If there is no head (abscess), and it is a superficial abscess, you must pierce it completely; and when the abscess is large, and it has collected a lot of pus, you must pierce it, but not drain all the pus in that hour, but some part; stop the abscess until the next day, then drain something incorrectly; do this many times gradually, until the pus goes away; be careful with weak patients, women, children or old people. Et se decorremens de sanc avient a ton ovraige, si amenistre aigue froide et aisil, et moille .i. drapeil, et met sor le leu decorrant par maintes fois. des soros	This means "of sores".
Ou keur dou chief vienent petis apostemes, et sont manieres de nous que sont en toiles, ausi com li josier d’une geline, et mout en i a de semblances. Il en i a de gras et de telz ou il a moistor ausi com poulz; et si a de telz qui sont dur et pierous au taillier, et n’i a point de doutance se li artere n’i fait contraire. Et li ovraiges de la taille si est que tu esprueve a tout .i. estrument qui est apelez «entromissoire», de coi li forme vient ci aprés, quel chose il contient. Car s’il contient moistor, si lou fent par desus dou lonc. Et quant li moistor est vuidie, si escorche sens rien laissier la peil qui contient celle moistor, car il revient adés quant on i laisse rien; puis plonge coton en oignement egiptien, s’il est presens; se ceu non, en aigue et en seil, et en emple la plaie, et la laisse jusc’a l’autre jor; et ceu corront ceu qui est demorez dou nit. Et pues rencomence lou coton, si com devant, le second jor, et lou tier, tant que tu saiches bien qu’il ne demoure point dou nit; puis cure la plaie d’oignement a ceu convenauble, tant qu’il soit sanez. Et se li apostemes tient .i. nout gras, si le cope selonc ceste forme, dou lonc; et i giete tes oncines, et l’escorche de toutes pars, et met toute ta cure de traire fuer la cotte ou il gist; et se li artere te fait contraire, si fai ceu que je t’ai dit aprés. Et ausi fai de l’aposteme s’il est pierous, et dou taillier et dou curer si com je t’ai dit.	1. For small abscesses that come on the head, we have ways which are in bandages, as the jeweler of a pearl, and there are many similarities. There are some fat ones with moisture, like pustules; and there are some hard and stony ones where there is no doubt that the arteries do not oppose. And the treatments for the neck are as follows: you prove everything individually with an instrument called "entromissoire," from which the following form comes, what it contains. For if it contains moisture, they should be dealt with above the long side. And when the moisture is drained, scrape skin without leaving any hair that contains that moisture, for it will return immediately if anything is left; then place cotton in Egyptian ointment, if it is available; if not, in oil and linen, and apply it to the wound, and leave it until the next day; and those who are delayed by night will heal. And on the second day, renew the cotton as before, on the third day, as long as you know that it does not remain by night; then treat the wound with ointment as appropriate, until it is healed. And if the abscess contains one hard nut, cut it along this form, lengthwise; and pour your eyes into it, and scrape it from all sides, and apply all your care to draw pus out where it is located; and if the arteries oppose you, do as I have said before. And similarly deal with the abscess if it is stony, and treat and cure as I have told you.
Et li taille sus l’aposteme pierous et le moiste, si est plus legiere, car il sont de poc de sanc. Et si a aucuns de ces apostemes ou chief ou il n’a point de moistor, et de ces fut .i. apostemes que je copai ou chief d’une vielle femme; et trovai l’aposteme ausi com une piere xourde, aspre et blainche, et ne pooit brisier; et s’on en eust ferut aucun, on li eust ausi bien fait plaie com d’une piere. En autres apostemes venans ou chief, fuer que ces qui vienent as chief des enfans et as racines des oreilles, li overture si soit toz jors au plus dependant leu, por mues issir la bowe; et les cure si com il covient.	And the cutting above the stony abscess and the moist one is easier, because they have little blood. And if any of these abscesses or heads have no moisture, and of these there was one abscess that I cut on an old woman's head; and I found the abscess as hard as a quartz stone, harsh and white, and could not be broken; and if any were made with iron in it, it would have made an equal wound as with a stone. In other abscesses coming from the heads, whether they are those that come on children's heads and the roots of the ears, they should be opened every day depending on the location, to let the pus out; and they should be treated as appropriate.
des scrophules	of scrofulas
Maintes fois avienent cist aposteme au col, et desoz les asseles, et ens angres, et aucune fois vienent autre part ou cors, et sont mout, et sont enjanrees l’une avec l’autre. Et chescune scrophule est proprement dedens sa cote, si com li nout et li aposteme dou chief, si com nos avons dit; et les semblances de ces scrophules sont maintes. Il i a de teles que contienent moistor, et si a de malignes qui ne vuellent obeir a santeit. en celle donques que tu vois de bone disposition au tochier, et est semblans a la color dou cors, et muet de chescune part et n’est mie aerse as ners dou col ne a l’artere ne au conduit, et n’est mie parfonde; si covient que tu la copes par desus, et l’escorche de chescune partie, et estent les .ij. levres dou keur as oncines, se tu en as mestier, si com nos avons dit en apostemes dou chief; et la trai poc et poc, et soies seur que tu ne coper lou nerf ne la voine, et ne soit mie li spatumile agus ne trenchans, que li mains n’eschaipe, et ne voise trop avant, que tu ne coper mie ceu que tu ne dois.	There are often these abscesses at the neck, under the jaw, and in the throat, and sometimes they appear elsewhere on the body, and they are many and interconnected. Each scrofula is properly within its own side, as the notch and the abscess of the neck, as we have said; and the similarities of these scrofulas are many. There are some that contain moisture, and there are others that are malignant and do not want to obey health. In such a case where you see it well disposed to be touched, and is like the color of the body, and silent on all sides and not swollen at the throat or artery or duct, and not inflamed; then you must cut it above, and scrape off each part, and hold the two lips of the cautery (if you need them), as we have said in abscesses of the neck; and pull it little by little, and be sure that you do not cut the nerve or the vein, and let the spatula be neither sharp nor cutting, so that the hand does not slip, and look too far ahead, so that you do not cut what you should not.
Et se tu copes la voinne ou l’artere, et ceu ne te laisse ovrer, si met en la plaie vitriole broiet, ou aucunes poudres que restainchent sanc, et estraint la plaie; et la laisse tant que li apostemes soit apaisiez, et soit amollie li plaie, et encomence a porrir. Et quant li sans est estainchiez, si revien a ton ovraige, tant que tu l’acomplisses; puis quier a ton doit indice s’il i demoure nules petites scrophules, si les cope et les munde. Et s’il a en la racine de la scrophule voinne grant, si ne covient mie que tu copes celle scrophule en sa racine, mais la lie d’un fil double fort, et la laisse cheoir par li, sens nuisement; puis emple la plaie de viel coton plongiet en oignement egiptien, puis la cure.	And if you cut the vein or the artery and it does not let you finish, put vitriol powder into the wound, or some powders that stop bleeding, and hold the wound; then let it stay until the abscess is appeased and the wound softened and begins to purify. And when the blood is stopped, return to your work, as long as you complete it; then check your guide if there are any small scrofulas remaining, cut them and clean them. And if there is a large root in the scrofula's wound, do not cut that scrophula at its root, but tie it with a strong double thread and let it hang down, without harm; then use old cotton dipped in Egyptian ointment on the wound, then heal it.
Et se tu copes toute la scrophule, si covient que tu assembles les .ij. levres de la plaie, et les cout maintenant, puis qu’il n’i a point demoreit de superfluiteit por la grandor de la scrophule. si covient que tu entendes a coper la racine de li, et traire fuer, et la cout si com nos avons dit. Celles scrophules que tienent superfluiteit, perce lai ou il apert meure; et la perce ensi com celle devant dite, en dependant, puis i amenistre tentes avec oignement et semblans choses, si qu’elle corrompe ceu qui est demorez de la corruption; et quant li plaie est bien mundee, si la cure d’oignement enjanrant char, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if you excise the entire scrofula (boil), you must gather the two edges of the wound and sew them together since there is no excess to remain due to the size of the scrofula. You must understand how to cover its root and draw out pus, then sew it as we have said. For those scrofulas with excessive tissue, perforate where it has become necrotic; and perforate in the same way as that mentioned before, depending on it; then introduce tweezers with ointment and similar things so that they corrupt what remains of the corruption. Once the wound is well cleaned, apply an ointment of rejuvenating char to it until it heals.
de squinance	And if you lancet a sciatic vein (swelling in the lower limb), you must cauterize the opening with a hot iron and bind it up, then keep the leg raised for seven days without moving it; otherwise there will be excessive bleeding.
Li ancien dirent et parlerent de la tailleure de la gorge; mais je ne vis onques en nostre terre qui la feist, et c’est li escripture de lor parole.	The ancients spoke of the measurement of the throat, but I have never seen anyone do it in our land, and this is their written word.
A ces qui ont squinance, il covient que li fendure de la gorge qui est apelee «epiglote» soit eschuee; et c’on ne faice aide par ceu, por ceu que toutes les voines et li pormon dou malaide sont a ces qui ont aposteme chaut en la bouche, ou en la gorge ou en .ij. amandres.	For those who have squinancy, it is necessary that the throat slit called "epiglote" should be opened; and no aid should be given by these, because all the veins and the pore of the sick person are in those who have an abscess hot in the mouth, or in the throat, or in two tonsils.
Quant li maladie est en la chenal dou pormon, il covient coper l’epiglote por fuir la perdition qui vient de l’estranglement.	When the sickness is in the channel of the pore, it is necessary to cover the epiglote to avoid the destruction that comes from strangulation.
Il covient donques, quant nos volons fendre l’epiglote, que nos le fendons desoz .iij. cercles ou .iiij. une petite fendure dou travers, entre les .ij. cercles ou par la quantiteit de la fendure dou syfac, ne mie en la cartillaige;	Therefore, when we want to cut the epiglote, it is necessary that we make a slit below four circles or two small cuts across the transverse, between the circles or according to the size of the fissure of the fistula, not in the cartilage.
et cil leus si est covenaubles a la section de l’epiglote qu’il n’i a point de char, et li vasseil sont lonc d’enqui.	And if the loosened joint is at the section of the epiglottis where there is no cartilage, and the vessels are long in length.
Et se li maistres est paourous, si covient qu’il estende le cuir de la gorge a tout l’oncine, puis fende lou keur tant qu’il viegne a la cheneil; et eschue les vasselz de sanc, se tu vois aucune chose, et puis cope lou syfac, si com nos avons dit;	And if the master is afraid, then you must stretch the skin of the throat all the way down to the chin, then make an incision in the neck until it reaches the trachea; and cut off the vessels carrying blood, if you see anything, and then sever the windpipe as we have said.
et est demostrez par la section dou fleume de la cheneil ki saut fuer par le leu qui est rompus, et par la defaute de la voix;	And it is proven by the incision of the trachea that flows out due to the broken joint, and by the lack of voice.
et laisse la plaie overte une piece.	And leave the wound open for a while.
Et quant li houre est passee de coi on doute l’estranglement, assemble les .ij. levres de la plaie dou keur, et la cout toute soule sens la cartillaige; puis aministre medicines qui font naistre char, tant qu’il soit sanez.	When the hour has passed in which there is doubt about strangulation, bring together the two edges of the wound with care, and sew it all around the cartilage; then administer medications that cause pus to form, until it heals.
Albucasim dist c’on ne faice ce jusc’a tant que li gorge est toute estoupee, et li malaides est jugiez a mort, et li defaut li alaine.	Albuscasis says that this should not be done until the throat is completely stopped up, and the patient has been judged to be dead, and the bird removed from him.
Adonques cope on l’epiglote por ceu que li malaides ne puet alener, et il respire par la plaie, et ensi est gardez de mort;	Then the epiglottis is seized because the patient cannot swallow, and he breathes through the wound, and in this way he is kept from death.
et por ce commanderent li anciain a laissier la plaie overte tant que li malice de la maladie soit passee, et elle est passee en .iij. jors ou en .iiij.	And for this reason, the ancients commanded to leave the wound open until the evil of the disease has passed, and it has passed in 3 or 4 days.
Et adonques il comanderent a coudre la plaie et curer, tant qu’elle fut curee;	Then they commanded to sew up the wound and heal, until it is healed;
et je vos dirai ceu que je vis.	And I will tell you what I have seen.
Je vis que une damoisele prist .i. coutel, et le ficha en sa gorge, et copa partie des chenelz dou pormon;	I saw a maiden take one knife, and she thrust it into her throat, and cut part of the windpipe.
et je fui apelez por li curer, et la trovai ausi com morte.	And I was called to heal her, and found her thus dead.
Je descovris la plaie, et trovai le sanc qui en estoit issus, et soi bien qu’elle n’avoit mie copeit voine ne conduit fuer que la gorge, et li vens issoit fuer par la plaie.	I found the wound, and saw the blood flowing from it, and knew that she had not coughed or breathed except through the throat, and the wind passed through the wound.
Je me hastai, et cousi la plaie, et la curai tant qu’elle fut sanee;	I hastened to stitch up the wound, and healed it until it was healed;
et n’avint a la damoisele fuer qu’elle fut roge de voix, et revint aprés a sa disposition;	And it happened to the maiden that she became red-faced from shouting, and returned afterwards to her position.
por ceu di je que en la tailleure de l’epiglote n’ait mie paour.	Therefore I say that in this manner of the epiglottis have no fear.
de la grosse gorge	from the thick throat   (in this context, "gorge" refers to the neck)
Cist apostemes est apelez «hernie de gorge», et est uns grans apostemes en color d’une jaisse, et est molt en femmes;	This abscess is called "throat hernia," and it is a large abscess in the color of a bluish-green hue, and it occurs mostly in women.
et est selonc .ij. manieres: naturez, et accidens; ou natureil n’a point d’engien.	And it is according to .ij. (2) ways: nature, and accidents; or natural has no device.
Et li accidens est selonc .ij. manieres, de coi l’une est semblans a gras nous, et li autre maniere est semblans a aposteme qui vient de nous d’artere;	And the accidents are according to .ij. (2) ways: one is similar to fatness in us, and the other way is similar to an abscess that comes from us due to artery;
et il i ait paour, et ne covient mie ovrer de feir fuers que en celi qui est petite, et le prueve et cerche a tout l’intromissoire:	And there should be fear, and it is not appropriate to make strong measures unless in the case of small one, and it proves and seeks through all the intromissory.
se tu le trueves ausi com .i. nout gras, et ne pent a nulle voine, si le cope, si com on cope les nous, et le trai a tout sa coife, s’il en i a point;	If you find it [the dislocation] as hard and firm as a knot, and it does not yield to any force, strike it, as one strikes the nails, and pull it completely, if there is any of it left;
et encerche bien tot, et le cure si com il covient, tant qu’il soit sanez parfaitement.	Then surround [the affected area] entirely, and heal it as necessary, until it is perfectly healed.
des nous	The bones   (the affected area being the bones)
Maintes manieres de nous sont, dont je dirai toutes les semblances;	Many ways of ours are, which I will tell all their similarities;
et or covient que je die toute la difference qui est entre nout et issue.	and it is necessary that I say the entire difference that exists between a dislocation and an ulcer.
Je dis que issue est chalors et fievre tenans, tant que li ebulicions est passee, et est acomplie li porriture; adonques repose li fievre et li chalor.	I say that an ulcer is heat and continuous fever until the eruption has passed, and the purulent matter has been completed; then the fever and heat subside.
Avec lou nout n’a ne chalor ne fievre ne dolor, et contient .i. syfac, qui est ses propres sac et est selonc la color dou cors, et encomence ausi com une jaisse, et devient gros;	With an ulcer there is neither heat nor fever nor pain, and it contains one abscess, which is its own sack and is according to the color of the body, and begins as a boil, and becomes large;
et sont selonc ij semblances, ou grais, ou moiste, et mout de color sont si com j’ai dit en la division.	And there are two kinds, either fat or moist, and they are very much colored as I said in the division.
Il covient, quant tu viens a la cure dou nout, que tu esprueves et l’enquier premierement a tout l’estrument qui est apelez «entromissoire», selonc ce que sa forme venra ou chapistre qui est aprés.	It is necessary, when you come to the treatment of the knot, that you test and inquire first about all the instrument called "entromissoire", according to its form or chapter that follows.
Et li maniere de l’inquisicion des apostemes des nous est que tu preignes ou plus moiste leu que tu trueves en l’aposteme, et torne tes dois poc et poc, tant que tu saiches que li estrumens ait perciet le keur, puis que ce soit selonc la grandor de l’aposteme;	And the method of inquiry for abscesses is that you take or more moist soil than you find within the abscess, and turn your fingers little by little, until you feel that the instrument has pierced through, then according to the size of the abscess.
puis estrai l’entromissoire, et pren garde en ceu que saut fuer.	Then straighten the joint, and take care because it can spring out.
Se moistor corrans cort, queil color elle ait, si le fent si com j’ai dit des autres apostemes;	If moisture runs out of the sore, let it be colored as I have said for other abscesses;
et se aprés l’entromissoire nen vient moistor, saiches qu’il est gras, si le fent donques en croix, et le prent as pinceures, et l’escorche legierement de chescune part et warde la cotte ou il gist que tu la traies saine avec le nout;	And if no moisture comes out after the joint is straightened, know that it is fatty, then make a cross incision, take it with pincers and scrape gently from both sides and watch the cloth or linen where it lies to ensure it remains intact.
et se tu ne la pues traire saine, si la trai par pieces si qu’il n’i demoure rien.	If you cannot draw it whole, then draw it in parts so that nothing remains.
Car s’il i demoure rien, si revient li nous par maintes fois;	For if there is nothing left, it comes back to us many times;
et s’il en demore un poc, et li sans te grieve, si emple la plaie d’aucunes poudres corrosives agues, et estraint la plaie, et met sus choses apaisans aposteme chaut, et le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez;	If a little remains and does not trouble you, use the wound with some corrosive powder, hold the wound closed with something warm, apply soothing things to the abscess, and treat it with other treatments until it is healed.
et se li nous est grans, si cout les .ij. levres de la plaie, et le cure de ceu qui enjanre char.	If the injury is large, make two incisions in the wound and treat it with healing salve.
et se li voine batans t’est contraire ou autre si te haste et emple le leu de vitriole broiet, et lou laisse liiet .ij. jors ou .iij., tant que li plaie porrisse, et repose li ebulicion dou sanc; puis revien au coper ceu que i est demoreit dou nout.	And if the vein beats against you or otherwise is in opposition and you hurry and use vitriol powder, leave it lying for 2 to 4 days, until the wound heals, and let the inflammation of the blood subside; then apply the ointment where it has remained unhealed.
Vez ci les formes des estrumens entromissoires, et sont de .iij. manieres: grans et moien et petit; et s’en i a .iij. quarrez qui sont apelez «albaret», et .i. qui est apelez «breb», et s’en i a de .iij. manieres: grant, moien, et petit, por encerchier les apostemes de fistule;	Here are the forms of the intermediary instruments, and they are of three types: large, medium, and small; and among them there are four squares which are called "albarets", and one which is called "breb", and there are also two types: large, medium, and small, for encircling the abscesses with fistula.
et sont ausi com les aguilles dont on cout les sorceles, et sont d’arain citrin, ou de fer, ou d’argent, et mues valent cil qui sont jaune, et sont plus esprovez de plonc noir por encerchier les corbeures de fistule;	And they are also like the needles with which one sews charms, and they are made of citron wood, iron, or silver, and yellow ones have more value, and black ones are more skilled at encircling the corners of a fistula.
et sont de .iij. manieres: grans, moiens, et petis, selonc la quantiteit de la largesce des pertus.	And there are three kinds: large, medium, and small, according to the size of the wound's extent.
Les formes des oncines sont de mout de semblances, si com tu vois ci: grans, moiens, et petis; et si a oncines qui ont .ij. corbeures de .iij. manieres ausi;	The forms of ulcers are similar in appearance, as you see here: large, medium, and small; and if one has two humps in four ways also.
et si a oncines qui ont .iij. corbeures, et sont ausi de .iij. manieres; et si a oncines qui ont .ij. corbeures, et oncines d’une corbeure soulement, et sont de .iij. manieres; et tuit cist sont necessaire en lor leu.	And if the ulcers have four humps in four ways; and if they have two humps, and ulcers with one hump only, and these are also in four kinds; and all this is necessary for their treatment.
Li chief de ces a coi on fent sont trenchant, et de telz i a qui ne taillent mie fuer que d’une part, dont on escorche les nous, por ceu c’on ne cope la voine ne le nerf;	The head of these animals that are being cut is sharp, and those who do not cut thoroughly from one side are at risk of cutting nerves or veins;
et de ces intromissoires sont les alemeles reponues en mainches, si que li malaide ne s’en persoivent a l’overture des apostemes;	And the instruments used for this are the tourniquets wrapped around the limbs, so that the patient does not feel pain during the opening of abscesses.
et sont de .iij. manieres: grant, petit, et moien, si com tu vois;	They come in three types: large, small, and medium-sized, as you can see;
et n’en use on mie fuer que en leu charnut, si com jambes, et bras, et mameles, et as angres, et en semblans leus;	and one should not use it except for the shoulder joint, such as legs, arms, breasts, and similar joints.
et aucune fois fait on .i. autre estrument petit, semblant a escorces de fistices, selonc ceste forme, a coi on estainche sanc:	And sometimes, another small instrument is made, resembling blades of forceps, in this shape, to draw blood.
et le met on aucune fois au leu qui saine a copement des voines, et as arteres, et aucune fois reont selonc ceste grant forme:	and it is placed at times on the joint that heals from veins, and arteries, and sometimes it returns in this large shape:
Aucune fois enflent les mameles d’aucuns homes quant cil encomencent estre corrumput, tant qu’eles semblent mameles de feme;	And sometimes, a man's breast swells when he begins to decay, until it resembles a woman's breast.
et demorent laides et enflees, et qui les vuet curer, si le covient soier selonc ceste forme des ceste ligne b. jusques a .g.:	And they remain swollen and inflamed, and those who wish to treat them must do so according to this form on the following lines b to g:
puis escorche la graisse, et emple la plaie de medicine enjanrant char, puis assemble les .ij. levres de la plaie a costure, et la cure tant qu’ele soit sanee;	then scrape the fat, apply medicinal ointment to the wound, then close the two lips of the wound with stitches and cure it until it heals.
et se li mamele cline aval, et est amolie por sa grandor si com il avient as femmes, si la fent en .ij. costelz desus, par .ij. semblans fendures;	and if the swelling slopes downward and is large like it happens in women, they should be cut into two pieces horizontally through two similar cuts;
de coi l’une soit tenans a l’autre a la fin de l’une et de l’autre, si que li plus grans ligne conteigne la menor selonc ceste forme, des ceste ligne .b. jusc’a la ligne .g.;	From this, one should hold the other at the end of both, so that the larger line contains the smaller according to this shape, from this line b to line g;
puis escorche le cuir qui est entre les .ij. levres, et oste la graisse, et i amenistre ceu que nos avons dit de costure et de poudres, et ceu qui est necessaire en la cure, tant qu’il soit sanez;	Then scrape the skin between the .ij. lips (of the wound), remove the fat, and apply what has been said about stitching and powders, and whatever is necessary for treatment, until it heals;
et s’il n’est sanez, ou li incision n’est mie toute faite, por ceu que li malaides ne vuet reposer, ou por le decorrement de sanc, si covient que tu emplisses la plaie de coton moilliet en oignement corrosif;	and if it is not healed or the incision is not complete because the patient does not want to rest or due to bleeding, you must fill the wound with cotton soaked in corrosive ointment.
et le laisse tant qu’il menjuce le remenant et la graisse, puis le cure tant qu’il soit saneis.	And let it remain until it consumes the remaining flesh and fat, then cure it until it is healed.
des apostemes des asselles	of abscesses on the buttocks
Cist apostemes que vienent desoz les asseles sont manieres de scrophules dures ou il ait cotes, et s’en i a que contienent moistor.	These abscesses that come beneath the buttocks are handled as hard scrofulas where there is a hardness, and if they contain moisture within them.
Cil donques qui contienent moistor covient qu’il soient copez selonc ceste forme, des la ligne b. jusc’a la ligne .g.:	Therefore, those who contain moisture should be cut according to this form, from line b to line g:
Et quant toute li bowe qui est en l’aposteme est vuidie, si emple la plaie de viel coton, et la laisse jusc’a l’autre jor, puis oste tout le coton, et cure d’oignement avenant a ceu tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when the entire cavity in the abscess is emptied, you should use old cotton on the wound and leave it until the next day; then remove all the cotton, and apply ointment to it until it heals.
Et se li apostemes est de semblances de scrophules, si le fent si com nos avons dit en fendures des scrophules, et se li plaie rent bowe, si amenistre cautere si com nos avons dit devant.	And if the abscess is similar to scrofula, you should treat it as we have said in cutting scrofula, and if the wound forms a cavity, you should apply a fire cautery as we have said before.
de la routure de l’artere	Of the rupture of the artery
Quant li artere est route, et li cuir est soudez qui est sus, si en vient maintes fois apostemes, et tout aussi avient il a la voine enflee et aposteme;	When the artery is ruptured and the skin closed over it, there are often abscesses, and this also occurs with an opened vein and abscess;
et si le conoist on ensi quant c’est por l’artere, si est li apostemes lons em parfont;	And if it is recognized in this way because it is from the artery, then the abscesses are long and deep.
et quant tu le sens a tes dois, si sens .i. estraignement; et quant c’est por la voine, si est reons defuer aparans;	And when you feel it with your hands, if it feels dislocated; and when it is through the vein, it appears rounded.
et c’est folie de coper cest aposteme, et meismement quant il est desoz les asseles et as angres et ou col et em mout d’autres leus, et est mout grans.	It is foolish to cover this abscess, especially when it is under the joints and in angles or the neck and in many other places, and it is very large.
Il covient donques eschuir la cure de fer, et celui qui est a chief covient eschuir ausi, et en celui qui est d’enfleure d’artere fent par desus le cuir dou lonc;	Therefore, the iron cure must be avoided, and so should the one at the head. Likewise, in those swollen with an artery, make a cut through the skin along its length;
puis oevre la taille as oncines, et depart bellement l’artere des toiles, tant qu’ele soit descoverte;	Then open the abdomen in one piece, and carefully cut the artery of the intestines while it is exposed.
puis boute desoz li une aguille, et la fai percier jusc’a l’autre costeit, et estraint l’artere d’un fil double en .ij. leus, selonc ceu que je t’ai ensigniet en l’estraction des .ij. arteres qui sont en temples;	Then insert a needle and pierce it until the other side of the chest, and tie an twice thread around the artery, according to what I have taught you in the extraction of the two arteries that are in the temples.
puis point le leu qui est entre les .ij. liens d’un intromissoire tant que li sans en isse qui i est, et soit deliiez li aposteme;	Then poke the gap between the two ligaments with an instrument until the abscess within it bursts and breaks open.
puis amenistre la cure que enjanre bowe, tant que li liien chient;	Then apply the remedy that will cause a swelling to form on the ligament.
puis cure ceu d’oignement avenant a ceu, tant qu’il soit sanez;	Then treat this one with ointment following this procedure, until it heals.
et se li apostemes est por la taille de la voinne, si covient que tu teignes a ta main ceu que tu pues de l’aposteme a tout le cuir,	and if the abscess is due to the vein size, then you must paint the affected area from the abscess all over the skin.
puis boute l’aguille desoz le leu que tu tiens a ta main, et la fai percier, et i ait .i. fil double, si que tu le trais de l’autre costeit;	then insert the needle under the location you are holding with your hand and pierce it, and have one double thread so that you draw it from the other side.
puis lie l’aposteme, si com je t’ai dit, ou liien de l’une de .ij. pars as .ij. chiés dou fil;	then tie the abscess, as I told you, or tie one of the two parts to each of the two shoulders with thread.
et se tu doutes que li filz n’isse fuer, si i reboute une autre aguille a tout .i. fil desoz tout l’aposteme a l’incision de la premiere aguille, et estraint les filz en .iiij. leus;	And if you doubt that the thread is not inside [the wound], push another needle through one end of the abscess at the incision of the first needle, and hold the threads in four places;
puis cope l’aposteme tant que li superfluitez en isse, puis cope la superfluiteit dou keur et laisse ceu qui est liiez;	Then press the abscess until the excess comes out, then cut off the pus and leave that which is attached.
puis met sus .i. drapeil moilliet en vin et en oile, puis li amenistre cures de tentes et d’oignemens tant qu’il soit sanez.	Then put a damp cloth soaked in wine and oil on top of it, then administer medicines such as tents and ointments until it is healed.
des apostemes des ners	From abscesses of the nerves
Ausi com aposteme vienent en l’artere et en la voine, vienent aposteme as ners quant il sont ferut, ou par trop grant travail, et semblans choses.	As abscesses come in the artery and the vein, so abscesses come to the nerves when they are wounded or from too great work, and similar things.
Et ceu avient plus sovent as adjutoires et as dois et en toz leus ou il ait jointures, et c’est .i. grief apostemes, et sa color semble la color dou cors, et est em plusors dispositions sens dolor;	And this happens more often in the shoulder and the thigh, and in all places where there are joints, which is a grave abscess; its color resembles the color of the body, and it is found in multiple positions with pain.
et quant on l’estraint forment, si sent li malaides dolor, et n’est mie em parfont dou cors, mais desoz lou keur;	And when it is strained (pressed), the patient feels pain, but it is not in all of the body, but under the skin.
et muet bien de toutes pars, et ne va ne avant ne arrier, ne desoz ne desus, et celui qui est en jointures ne covient mie coper par fer: par aventure i vanroit contraction;	And it must be kept quiet from all sides, and neither forward nor backward, neither below nor above, and one who is in the joints should not be covered with iron: by chance, there might be contraction.
et cil qui est ou chief ou ou front, fent le cuir au spatumile.	And the one who has a head or forehead, scrape the skin with a spatula.
Se li apostemes est petis, si le tien a unes tenailles, et le cope en sa racine;	If the abscess is small, take tweezers and press it at its root.
et s’il est grans, si le sospent a l’oncine, et l’escorche, puis l’oste et assemble la plaie a la costure, et lou cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	If it is large, lift it with the onion, peel it, then open and stitch up the wound until it heals.
des grosses boces pendans	Large lumps hanging
Aucune fois avient en ventres et ne mie autre part thelul, et est une maladie qui est apelee «funge» par la semblance d’aus, et est li racine subtilz, et li chiez gros; et en i a de petis et de mout grans;	Sometimes it happens in bellies and nowhere else, and it is a disease called "funge," resembling worms, and it has subtle roots, and large heads; there are small and very large ones.
et je vis .i. home qui en avoit .ij. ou ventre qui estoient plus semblans a funges que ai autre chose, et n’i avoit point de difference, et estoient blanc, et avoient menue racine, et estoient jai fendut, et en corroit adés moistor.	I saw one man who had two bellies that resembled worms more than anything else, and there was no difference between them; they were white, had a thin root, were slit, and continually oozed moisture.
Je les copai et trovai en l’un .xviij. onces pesant, et en l’autre .vj. З., et li ovraiges en l’incision si est que tu regardes se li malaides est moistes, et li color de l’artelul est blainche et moiste et de subtil racine;	I cut them out and found one weighing 16 ounces, and the other 5, and the incision in the operation shows that if the patient is moist, the color of the mass is white and moist, and the root is thin.
si le cope au spatumile large, et soient en ta presence li cautere au feu. Car au taillier vient maintes fois trop grans decorremens de sanc, et se li sans te vaint, si te haste donques dou cauterizer;	If the thigh is severely wounded and the fire cautery is in your presence, for in the wounding of the thigh often comes too much bleeding, and if it overwhelms you, then hasten to apply the cautery.
et se tu vois le malaide espoanteit et paourous de l’incision dou fer, si prent .i. fil de plonc bien fait, et en lie l’artelul si com nos avons dit, et le laisse .ij. jors;	and if you see the patient frightened and fearful of the iron incision, take a good thread made from flax and tie it around the artery as we have said, and leave it for two days;
et puis le restraint, et ne cesser d’estraindre lou fil de plonc tant qu’il cope l’artelul, et chiece par lui sens travail; et se les racines sont grosses, si a paour au coper meismement por le ventre, mais tu em pues bien coper la moitiet,	then he restrains it and does not cease to tighten the flax thread until the artery is stopped, and feel by it whether there is work; and if the roots are large, be careful with it for the belly, but you can certainly stop the bleeding on half of it.
puis le cauterize qu’il ne reviegne; puis cure la plaie, et garde que tu ne coper le thelul qui est de fuxe color et de povre sens et de lait regart.	Then burn (cauterize) so that it does not return; then heal the wound and keep covered the thin skin which is of dark color, weak sensation and watery eye.
Car c’est uns apostemes enchancrez, et je venrai a la cure de chancre ci aprés.	For this abscess has grown large, and I will come to treat this syphilis afterwards.
quant li boude ist fuer	when the boil is mature
Se li apparance de la boude vient par cautere de plaie ou de fendure de syfac, et est sus le ventre et en ist aucuns des bouez, si com il avient en autres routures, ou de sanc qui cort de voines ou d’arteres selonc ceu qui est devant, ou de ventositeit;	If the appearance of the boil comes from cautery of wound or crack of hernia, and it is on the abdomen and among some of the boils, as happens in other cases, or from blood that cuts from veins or arteries according to what is before, or from wind;
et se c’est par la routure dou syfac et par l’issue dou bouel, si est li color de l’aposteme semblans a la color dou cors, et est legiere chose sens dolor, et apert de diverse issue.	And if it is by the break of the thigh and the exit of the bowel, its color of the abscess resembles the color of the body, and it is a light thing without pain, and wide open with various outlets.
Et se c’est por l’issue de l’intestine, adonques est il plus divers, et quant on le presse a ses dois si se repont, et puis revient, et par aventure si est sarrez, et agrandist mout a l’entree dou bain et por fort travail.	And if it is by the exit of the intestine, then it is more diverse, and when pressed with hands, it returns and comes back again, and in some cases may become hardened, and increases greatly at the entrance of the bath and through heavy labor.
Et se c’est por moistor, c’est legiere chose, et apert bien quant tu le presses a ta main, ne ne constraint mie; et se c’est por sanc, si apert par ces signes li apostemes gros et dur, et est fichiez selonc une quantiteit;	And if it is due to moisture, it is light and opens wide when you press with your hand, but does not constrict; and if it is due to blood, the abscesses are large and hard, and are filled according to a certain quantity.
et se c’est por ventositeit, si est souef au tochier, et li ovraiges si est que tu regarde se li apparance est por le sanc de l’artere, ou de la voine, ou ventositeit.	And if it is due to inflammation, it is soft and the work indicates that you look to see whether its appearance is due to blood from an artery or a vein, or inflammation.
Si covient que tu laisses la cure. Car il en a doutance et paor, si com je t’ai dit ou chapistre des apostemes, por l’artere et por la voine.	You must allow the treatment to continue. For there is doubt and fear, as I have told you in the chapter on abscesses, for the artery and vein.
Et se li apparance est por l’intestine ou lou boueil, si covient que tu comandes au malaide qu’il teigne son alaine, et soit estendus tout drois, puis seigne d’enche tout entor la boude;	And if the appearance is due to the intestines or feces, you should command the patient to strain his anus and stretch it out straight, then clean all around the stool.
puis le comande a gesir sovin entre tes mains,	Then command him to rest quietly between your hands,
puis va entor le leu que tu as signiet a tout le spatumile,	then go around the limb that you have signed with a splint.
puis estent la moitiet de l’aposteme au desus a tout le grant uncine;	then spread half of the abscess to the great spoon-shaped knife.
puis le lie entor d’un fil fort, ou d’une corde de fort soie fermement, et soit li nous dou liien assolz;	then tie it around with a strong thread or cord made of sturdy silk, and make sure the knots are secure.
puis oevre la moitiet de l’aposteme estendut sus le liien, et i boute ton doit indice, et quier l’intestine;	Then, open half of the abscess stretched over the ligament, and insert your finger as an indicator, seeking the intestine.
se tu le trueves pris dou liien, si le deslie, et boute l’intestine au defuer dou ventre;	If you find it caught in the ligament, undo it, and push the intestine out of the abdomen.
et se tu trueves le boueil, si le prent a l’oncine, et en cope la superfluiteit;	and if you find the fecal matter, take it to the edge, and cut off any excess.
et se li artere te fait contraire, ou li voine, si vai belement entor, puis revien a ton ovraige et pren .ij. aguilles, et i boute .ij. fors filz, et boute les .ij. aguilles entor ceu que tu as fait en crois que tu feis percier;	and if the arteries or veins are obstructed, go around them carefully, then return to your work and take two needles, and insert two threads, and place the needles around what you have done in a cross shape that you make pierced.
puis estrain l’aposteme en .iiij. leus sus les aguilles, et se tu vues, oste les aguilles, et laisse lou leu tant qu’il porrisse, et chiece li char morte par soi;	Then hold the abscess for four leagues above the needles, and if you see, remove the needles, and leave the place as it is until it can, and kill the dead flesh by itself;
ou tu la cope quant elle iert subtiliie et porrie, puis le cure de ceu qu’il covient, et cheve l’aposteme si com nos avons dit;	Then strike it when it has become subtle and can be, then heal what is necessary, and shave the abscess as we have said;
et estrai le sanc ou la moistor que tu trueves, puis cure le leu de ceu qu’il couvient, et soude le leu.	And extract the blood or moisture that you find, then heal the wound of what is necessary, and seal the wound.
dou chancre	The pustule
Nos avons dit en la division les semblances de chancre, et coment on i doit ovrer par medicines, et coment on doit eschuer la cure de fer; et disons le chancre enjanreit en la marris, et grant cautele a en la cure, et dirent li ancien que quant chancres est en leu ou on le puet raier si com chancre qui est em mameles, et en la cuixe, et en semblans leus, et le doit tout oster quant il est en l’encomencement; et quant il est grans et anciens, si ne covient mie que tu l’aproches, car je n’en poi onques nul saner; ne nulz n’en sana onques devant moi.	We have said in the division the likenesses of pustules, and how one should treat them with medicines, and how one should choose the cure of iron; and we shall say what a pustule is, and great caution must be taken in its cure, and the ancients said that when pustules are in a place where they can be shaved like a pustule on a mamel, and in the thigh, and in similar places, one should remove it completely when it begins; and when it is large and old, it is not good to approach it, for I never knew anyone who could heal it; nor has anyone healed it before me.
Et li ovraiges, quant il est en leu ou on le puet oster, si com nos avons dit, est que tu purge aucune fois le malaide de cole noire; puis le fai sainier s’il ait manifeste repletion, puis afaite le malaide .i. boin leu por faire l’ovraige; puis giete tes oncines ou chancre, et le cheve de toutes pars, et l’oste de toutes pars sens rien laissier; et laisse corre le sanc tout fuer, et espreint bien le leu a ta main ou a aucune chose, et se li decorremens de sanc te fait contraire de l’incision de l’artere ou de la voine, si le cauterize tant que li sans soit estainchiez; puis le cure d’autre cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	And the operations, when it is in a place where it can be removed as we have said, are that you purge the patient once with black bile; then make him purge if there is manifest distention, then shave the patient one good length for the operation; then take your lancet or pustule, and shave off all hair and flesh from all parts, leaving nothing remaining; and allow the blood to flow freely, and anoint the wound well with your hand or something else, and if the discharge of blood makes you hesitate about incision of the artery or vein, cauterize it until the wound is cauterized; then treat it with other medicines until it is healed.
de ydropisie	Of hydropisy
Nos avons jai dit en la division les semblances d’idropisie, et en queil maniere li assemblee de l’aigue est faite, et les signes de chescune semblance, et la cure qui est faite par medicines, et cele qui est curee par fer: si est eclites soulement; et ne doit on touchier de fer en ces .ij. semblances: c’est a savoir, tympanites et yposarche, car c’est mortelz chose; donques quant tu medicines ceste semblance de ydropisie qui est apelee «eclites» de medicines, et li cure ne profite, si regarde se li malaides est foibles, ou s’il ait autre maladie que ydropisie, si com toust et solution de ventre et semblans choses; si n’i touchier de fer, car il i a doutance; et se tu vois le malaide de fort vertut, et il n’a autre maladie que ydropisie soulement, et il n’est mie trop jones ne trop vielz, si dois ensi ovrer:	We have said in the division the resemblances of hydropisy, and in what manner the assembly of water is made, and the signs of each resemblance, and the cure that is made with medicines, and the one that is cured with iron: it is revealed only; and no iron should be used in these two resemblances: namely tympanites and yposarche, for it is a deadly thing; therefore when you treat this resemblance of hydropisy which is called "ecchylma" with medicines, and the cure does not help, look to see if the patient is weak or if he has another disease other than hydropisy, such as dropsey of the belly and similar things; if there is no iron used, for there is doubt; and if you see the patient of strong virtue, and he has only hydropisy itself, and he is not too young nor too old, then do so:
lieve le malaide droit sus tes mains, et li ministres presse le ventre em boutant l’aigue a la plus basse partie dou pis, puis pren le spatumile espinous selonc ceste forme: Et soit trenchans de .ij. pars. a pointe, et toutevoie ne soit mie si entrans qu’il puist venir jusc’a l’intestine quant on le fiche ens, et ne le puist blecier;	Lift the patient upright onto your hands, and the assistant presses the belly towards the lower part of the backside, then take the pointed spatula as shown in this form: It should be slit in two parts with a sharp point, but not so deep that it can reach the intestine when inserted, and not sharp enough to poke through.
puis regarde se li ydropisie est enjanree devers les intestines: si covient que tu fendes ensus de la boude .iij. dois droit desoz sus lou poignil; et se li ydropisie est por la maladie dou foie, si soit ta fendure au senestre de la boude .iij. dois; et se c’est por la miuce, si soit a destre, et ne covient mie que li malaides gise sus la fendure que les superfluitez ne corrent a celui foible leu;	Then look to see if the urinary stone is directed towards the intestines: if so, you must make an incision beneath the navel, three fingers' breadth right above the anus; and if the urinary stone is due to liver disease, it should be cut on the left side of the navel, three fingers; and if it is due to constipation, it should be on the right side, and the patient should not lie on the incision so that excess fluid does not flow into the weak place.
puis perce tout le cuir a l’estrument, et le boute, et lieve ta main a tout le spatumile entre le cuir et le syfac ausi com en escorchant a la quantiteit d’une ungle ou enqui entor; puis perce lou syfac tant que li spatumile viegne au leu vuit, et c’est li leus de l’aigue, puis le trai fuer, et i boute cest estrument de coi ci est li forme: Et est semblans a une caine d’argent subtil, et est d’arain ou d’archaut legier, et a en la partie desoz .i. petit pertus; et ou costeit d’une part, .iij. pertus; et .ij. d’autre part, et .i. d’autre; et est li chiés tailliez si com une penne, et c’est li forme de l’incision dont li escrivains taille la penne:	Then cut through the skin with the instrument and push it out, hold your hand on the spatula between the skin and the bladder to the thickness of a nail or within; then cut the bladder until the spatula comes to the place of the water, which is its base, then pull it out and put this instrument in the shape as shown here: It is similar to a thin silver chain, and is made of light iron or brass, and has one small hole at the bottom; on one side, three holes; on two sides, two holes; and on another side, one hole; and the testicle is cut like a feather, and this is the shape of the incision that scribes make when they cut a feather:
au chief desus est li alemele, si que quant li estrumens vient a l’aigue, si dessent maintenant sus l’estrument; vuide la donques la moitiet ou la tierce part, car se tu en vuides plus qu’il ne covient en celle houre, par aventure si muert li malaides por la resolution de son esperit de l’arme, ou il chiet paumez, ou il aproche a la mort;	At the top above is the abdomen, so that when the instrument reaches the water, now push up on the instrument; then empty it now, for if you empty more than necessary in that hour, perhaps the patient may die due to the resolution of his spirit from the weapon, or he falls unconscious, or approaches death.
mais en vuide selonc la quantiteit de sa vertut, et selonc ceu que les dispositions de la vertut dou malaide signifient, et ses poulz; puis trai l’estrument et retien l’aigue, et elle est retenue maintenant por le keur qui estoupe le pertus qui est sus le syfac, de coi j’ai parleit, que tu perces selonc ceste maniere; puis rencomence l’estrument l’autre jor, se tu vois le malaide soffrant ceu, et trai de l’aigue une petite quantiteit;	But in emptying according to the quantity of its power, and according to what the dispositions of the power mean for the patient and his pulse; then draw the instrument and hold back the fluid, and it is held back now due to the cautery which stops the flow that is on the wound, as I have spoken about, so you pierce in this manner; then use the instrument again the next day, if you see the patient suffering from it, and draw a small amount of fluid.
fai ce aucun jor, et te garde de foloier tant qu’il ni demore mais c’un poc d’aigue. Et se tu doutes sus le malaide, et tu i lais mout d’aigue, si le cure de la sepulture ou sablon chaut, et par mout sueir ou bain et au soleil, et se teigne de boivre; et le cure de medicines desiccatives tant qu’il soit sanez, et cauterize sus l’estomac et sus lou foie et sus l’esplen aprés l’estraction de l’aigue, si com j’ai dit devant.	Do this every day and be careful not to let it remain but a little fluid. And if you doubt about the patient, and you leave much fluid, cure him with burial or warm sand, and with sweating or bathing in warm water and sun, and anoint him with wine; and cure him with drying medicines until he is healthy, and cauterize on the stomach and the liver and the spleen after the extraction of the fluid, as I have said before.
de l’estopement de la verge	of the stopping of the member
Aucune fois naissent enfant qui n’ont point de pertus en la verge, ou li pertus est petis, ou il n’est mie en son leu. Si le covient tantost qu’il n’aist percier a tout .i. spatumile molt subtil selonc ceste forme: puis met ou pertus .i. clo subtil de plonc, et le lie et le tien ensi .iij. jors ou iiij. et quant il vuet faire urine, si soit ostez li clos, et faice urine, et puis li remet; et par aventure nen i couvient point, car li urine qui vient fuer ne lou laisse close.	At times, children are born without foreskin in the penis, or the foreskin is small and not properly positioned. If this happens, it should be pierced immediately with a very thin spatula as follows: first place a thin piece of cloth on the foreskin and hold it in place for 2-4 days until the child wishes to urinate; then remove the cloth, allow the child to urinate, and replace the cloth; and if necessary, this should be repeated because the urine that comes out does not close the opening.
Cil de cui li pertus est petis, si est medicinez dou clo de plonc, si com nos avons dit, si s’eslargera. Cil qui n’ont mie le pertus en lor leu sont bleciet, car aucun naissent qui ont le pertus au chief de la verge, por coi il ne puient pissier avant s’il ne lievent lor verge en haut; et ne pueent enjanrer por ceu que li matiere ne puet venir jusc’a la marris, et c’est une male maladie.	Children who have a small foreskin or one that is not properly positioned are treated with a cloth of linen as previously described, which will stretch it open. Those who lack a foreskin at the tip of their penis are blistered because no child is born with a foreskin on top of the penis; therefore, they cannot urinate before lifting their penis and this prevents the matter from reaching the opening. It is a bad disease.
Et li maniere de l’ovraige si est que li malaides gise sovin sus son dos, puies estent le chief de la verge et le cope ausi com la taille d’une penne, si ke li pertus chiece em mileu, si com il covient; et te garde de decorrement de sanc qui i vient maintes fois, et s’il avient, si l’estainche de ceu qui estainche sanc, et cure la plaie tant qu’il soit sanez.	The method of the work is that the patient lies on their back with the penis and scrotum positioned as the width of a feather, so that the foreskin can be easily drawn back, as necessary; you should also avoid the discharge of blood that often occurs, and if it happens, drain the bleeding area and heal the wound until it is healed.
des pustules de la verge	boils of the penis
Maintes fois vienent cist albathe en la verge, et est une apparance de char laide; et en i a malignes et non malignes; si covient que tu les preignes a .i. oncine subtil, et les cope et munde toutes, puis met sus coton moilliet en oignement egiptien; puis le cure d’oignement diafinicon tant qu’il soit sanez.	Often this boil appears on the penis, it is an ugly appearance of pus; and among them there are both malignant and non-malignant ones; you must pick them once a week with a thin instrument, strike and clean them all, then put damp cotton in Egyptian ointment over them; then heal them with diaphinicon ointment until they are healed.
Et se li albathe est maligne, de pute color et depuant, si covient que tu i amenistres cautere. Quant tu l’as copeit, et se li albathe est en som la verge, et en ait partie dedens la peil et partie defuer, si covient que tu oste l’albathe qui est dedens premier; et quant il est soudez, si le cure defuer. Car quant tu le cures ensamble, si n’est mie asseurez li chiez de la verge qu’il ne soit perciez, et vient noiror et corruption en son la verge et ou coion; si covient chever tout ceu qui est noir et corrumput, puis lie sus l’emplaustre de miel et de farine qui soit fait d’escorce de poumes grenates et de veces, puis le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the boil is malignant, full of pus and decayed, you must bring fire cautery to it. When you have struck it, and if the boil is on the top part of the penis and has both parts inside the skin and outside, you must first remove the boil that is inside; when it is sewed, you cure the outside. For when you heal them together, there is no assurance for the testicles of the penis that they will not be pierced, and blackness and corruption comes in the penis and the area around it; you must clean all that is black and corrupted, then lie over it a plaster made of honey and flour which is made from pomegranate peel and wheat, then heal it with other remedies until it is healed.
Et se decorremens de sanc vient, si amenistre le cautere lunaire selonc ceste forme: Li cauteres si aide as .ij. dispositions ensamble: c’est asavoir, au decorrement de sanc, et a la corruption; et se li chiés de la verge est corrumpus et retrais, si covient que tu boutes ou conduit de la verge une cainne de plonc, et pisse li malaides parmi; et quant li pelz iert aerse au chief de la verge qui avient a ces qui n’ont mie esteit circoncis, ou il avient por plaie ou por aposteme, si covient donques que tu l’escorches a .i. estrument cheveit, tant que li liiens soit desliiez, et soit delivrez li chiez de la verge de toutes pars;	And if bleeding occurs, bring the lunar cautery as follows: The cauteries aid in two ways: for bleeding and for corruption; and if the head of the penis is corrupted and retracted, you must bring or lead a sheath of plank from the penis and make the patient urinate; and when the hairs reach the tip of the penis (which applies to those who have not been circumcised, or it applies for injury or abscess), then you should shave it with one instrument, until the ligaments are loosened, and the head of the penis is released from all sides.
et se c’est grief chose de deviser ceu, si covient que tu l’escorches a .i. spatumile aucun poc dou chief de la verge et de la peil; puis dessevre belement entre .ij., et i met .i. subtil drapeil de lin moilliet an aigue froide, qu’il n’aerse derechief.	Then if it is necessary to talk about this, you should shave with one spatula or thin piece of flax from the tip of the penis and the hair; then carefully separate them, and place a thin linen cloth dampened in cold sharp water between them so they do not stick together immediately.
de la circoncision	circumcision
Circoncision n’est mie desliemens de continuation si com les autres plaies; toutevoie quant nos faison ceste oevre de nostre volenteit, et proprement as enfans, si est mestier que nos faisiens la millor oevre, et la plus legiere a salut.	Circumcision is not a simple continuation like other wounds; however, when we perform this work of our own volition and specifically on children, it is necessary that we do the best and easiest job for their salvation.
Je dis que li ancien ne dirent mie la circoncision de lor enfans, car il n’en usent mie en lor loi, et n’en avons mais que ceu que nos avons aquis par experiment.	I say that the ancients did not speak of circumcising their children, for they did not use it in their law, and we have only what we have acquired through experience.
Car j’ai veut la plus grant partie des maistres et des sainors qui faisoient circumcision entor .i. dal, et as forces, et a tout une novacule; si fuioit li keurs car il i a .ij. toiles, et par aventure si cope on celi desus et demore celle desoz.	For I have wanted the majority of masters and lords who perform circumcision to be around one day old, and to use force if necessary, and always with a new knife; however, the foreskin is twice as thick, and sometimes it cuts the upper part and leaves the lower.
Or la recovient coper, et est li dolor double, et a la mundification qui est dou dal n’est mie asseuree li pointe dou membre; et a la mundification de l’ungle par aventure eschaipe li fer, et corront l’uevre, et maintes fois naissent ensi qu’il n’ont mestier de mundification et je l’ai veut.	Or the dislocation should be covered, and the pain is doubled; at the amputation which is near the joint is not assured the tip of the limb; and at the amputation of the nail by accident escapes the iron, and spoils the work, and many times it happens as if there was no need for amputation and I have seen it.
De la mondification qui est faite as forces a tout le liien de fil ai je troveit la bonteit de l’experiment, car les forces taillent justement ausi bien desus com desoz.	Of the amputation which is made at the joint of thread I have found the goodness of the experiment, for the threads cut equally well above as below.
Car quant tu presses ta main, si tailles igalment en .i. tout soul tens; mais que li filz soit bien estrois entor lou cuir; et soit li maniere dou premier ovraige si est que tu faices penser l’enfant, s’il entent, que tu ne li fais fuer que liier le fil entor la verge tant soulement, et pues le fai esjoir en toutes les manieres que tu pues;	For when you press your hand, you cut equally throughout the entire time; but that the threads are well tightened around the skin; and let the manner of the first work be such that you make the child think that you do not tie it tightly with the thread except around the rod, and then allow it to be loose in all ways that you can.
puis le fai ester entre tes mains tout droit, et repont les forces entre tes mains ou desoz tes piez que li enfes ne les voie, ne aucun des estrumens; puis boute ta main a la verge et souffle ou keur, et la trai en haut tant que li chiés de la verge soit ens; puis la mundifie bien de l’ordure qui i est assemblee, puis lie le leu signiet d’un fil double, puis la lie desoz .i. poc a .i. autre liien; et la tien as .ij. dois par la seconde lieeure au pouchet et au doit indice, et cope entre les .ij. liiens, puis lieve le keur desus hastanment et trai le chief de la verge;	Then make it be between your hands straight, and restore the strength between your hands or beneath your feet so that the child does not see [it], nor any instrument; then press your hand to the vein and blow or cough, and pull it up until the head of the vein is in; then clean it well of the filth that has gathered there, then tie the joint signet with a double thread, then tie one end to another loop; and hold it with the second loop at the thumb and index finger, and break between the loops, then quickly untie the knot and pull the head of the vein.
puis laisse corre le sanc poc et poc, car c’est li muedres; et met poudre sus et sus la poudre .i. drapeil glueit d’un moieuf d’uef cuit destempreit d’aigue rose, confit avec oile roset boin et fres, et lou laisse sus jusc’a l’autre jor, et le cure d’autre cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	Let the blood coagulate drop by drop, for it is the pus; and apply powder on top and on top of the powder one cloth glued with a mixture of cooked egg white steeped in rose water, mixed with fresh rose oil, and leave it on until the next day, and treat it with another treatment until it heals.
Li forme des forces a la mundification si est ceste: li dui chiés soient tenves et soient trenchans, et soient li chiés ausi grant com li mainche igalment:	The shape of the forces for cleansing is as follows: the two heads should be tender and sharp, and they should also be as large as the middle finger equally:
li error de la mundification si est quant li keurs dedens fuit a l’incision; donques il covient que tu l’estendes a ton ungle, ainsois que li leus faice aposteme; et le cope igalment, et se tu ne lou pues tenir a ton ungle, si le tien as tenailles, et puis le cope.	The error in the amputation occurs when the cartilage within is incised; therefore, it should be extended to your fingernail so that the bone protrudes equally; and strike it evenly. If you cannot hold it with your fingernail, grasp it with pliers, and then strike it.
