Et s’il trespassent .iij. jors, et ceu qui est desoz la verge est enflez, si le laisse tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez, et l’escorche legierement; si le cope si com tu pues mues, et te garde de la partie de la verge, ce ne li nuira niant.	And if it lasts more than three days and the area below the verge swells, let it be until the abscess has calmed down and the scab has formed; then gently scrape it off; strike it as much as you can move it, but avoid hitting the part of the verge, this will not harm it.
Cure donques le leu de choses soudans plaie de poudre, que nos avons dit ou traitier des poudres, et s’on cope dou keur outre mesure, et il va au desus, si ne nuira point; cure le donques, si com nos avons dit, tant qu’il soit sanez.	Therefore, treat the bone of things submerged in a wound with powder, as we have said or treated powders, and if it is struck too harshly and goes above, it will not harm; therefore, treat it as we have said until it is healed.
dou retenement de l’urine	The retention of urine
Li retenue de l’urine si est d’opilation de piere, ou de sanc congeleit, ou de bowe, ou de char nee, ou de semblans choses, que nos avons dit en la division;	The retention of urine is due to the obstruction of a stone, or frozen blood, or pus, or charneal, or similar things, as we have said in the division;
et se li urine n’est desliie, et tu vois estre la retenue por la piere qui est jai ou col de la vessie, si covient que li malaides soit corbés sus ses genoulz; et li soient mis li piez sor le dos, et estende son ventre de la partie desus lou dos, et restraigne li malaides s’alainne tant com il puet; et adonques est constrains li colz de la vessie a l’expression de la piere au desus, por coi li urine est desliie e;	and if the urine is not relieved, and you see that it is retained due to a stone lodged in or neck of the bladder, then the patient must be placed on all fours; his feet should be put on the back, and he should extend his abdomen from the upper part above the lower back, and hold the patient firmly until he can bear it; then the necks of the bladder are constricted towards the expression of the stone above, so that the urine is relieved.
et s’elle ne vient, si com nos avons dit, et li malaides sent grant dolor, si covient que tu i aministres extraction a tout l’estrument qui est apelez «siringue», de coi ci est li forme: et soit d’argent subtilz legiere chevee, si com li penne d’un oiseil; et soit li caine d’une palme de lonc et demie, et soit subtilz au chief.	and if it does not come out as we have said, and the patient feels great pain, you must administer extraction using all the instruments called "syringe," of which this is the form: it should be made of thin delicate silver tube, like a bird's feather; and its length should be a palm and half, and it should be thin at the top.
Et li maniere de l’issue de l’urine si est que tu pren .i. fil double, et lie au chief .i. poc de laine ou de couton, et boute le chief dou fil dedens la siringue; et cope la superfluiteit de la lainne et le boute jusc’au chief de la siringue, puis oint la siringue d’oile ou de burre et d’aubin d’uef, et fai seoir le malaide sus .i. siege, et li arose la vessie et la verge d’oile moiste et d’oile d’olive et d’aigue tede;	And the method of urine discharge is that you take one double thread, tie one end to the patient's chin with a piece of linen or cotton, and push the other end of the thread inside the syringe; then tie the excess linen and push it up to the tip of the syringe, then oil or butter the syringe and insert egg white or olive oil and water into the bladder and urethra; and make the patient sit on one seat, and irrigate the bladder and urethra with moist oil and olive oil and warm water.
puis met legierement la siringue en la verge, tant qu’elle viegne a la racine de la verge, puis double la verge desus devers la boude; puis boute la siringue avant jusc’a la vessie, et la sente li malaides venir jusc’a la chose vuide, et ceu n’est mie fait selonc cest ordre fuer que por ceu que li conduis ou elle vait est tors; puis estent le fil a tout la laine poc et poc, et li urine en suit la laine, puis l’estrai fuer, et fai corre l’urine;	Then gently insert the syringe into the urethra until it reaches the root of the urethra, then bend the urethra upwards towards the bladder; then push the syringe forward up to the bladder, and make the patient feel it reach the empty place, and this is not done incorrectly because the guide is twisted; then tie the thread to all the linen piece by piece, and the urine follows the linen, then remove the thread, and correct the urine.
et rencomence la siringue tant que li vessie soit vuidie, et soit aligiez li malaides.	And continue the syringe until the bladder is emptied and the patient is relieved.
des maladies de la vessie	diseases of the bladder
Quant escorcheures ou sanc vient en la vessie, ou porriture i est assemblee, et tu i vues distiller aigues et medicines, si fai a tout l’estrument qui est apellé «clepsedre», et c’est li forme:	When scorching or blood comes to the bladder, or pus is assembled there and you see it exuding acids and medications, then do with all the apparatus that is called "clepsydra," and this is its shape:
Elle est close, et si a .iij. pertus: .ij. d’une part, et .i. d’autre, si com tu vois; et li leus chevez par coi li medicine cort soit telz qu’il estoupe bien la verge sens adition, si c’on em puisse traire la moistor, et bouter quant mestier est;	It is closed at three openings: two on one side and one on the other, as you can see; and the necks are shaped so that the medicine comes out easily through the opening without addition, if it is possible to drain the moisture, and insert when necessary.
et quant tu vues giter tes medicines en la vessie, met le chief dou keusteur en la moistor, et trai au traiant qui est ens; si trairas la moistor au kesteur, et puis reboute fort le traiant ens; si entrera li moistors ens, et venra a la vessie maintenant, si que li malaides la sentira;	and when you see that your medicines enter the bladder, put the head of the syringe in the moisture, and pull out the string that is inside; if you draw out the moisture through the syringe, and then push the string forcefully in; the moisture will enter the syringe, and come to the bladder now, so the patient will feel it.
et c’est li forme dou clistere subtil dont on clisterize la vessie: si est ci:	And this is the form of the subtle suppository with which to suppositarium the bladder: it is as follows:
Et est d’argent ou d’archaut, et est li chiés plus haut; et desoz a .i. sein ou li liiens chiet; puis pren une vessie de mouton et i met la moistor dont tu vues clisterizer la vessie, puis la lie entre les .ij. seins forment d’un boin fil double, et chaufe .i. poc celle moistor sus le feu; puis boute le chief dou clistere en la verge, puis estrain ta main sus la vessie a tout la moistor avenanment, tant que li malaides sente que celle moistor est jai venue a la vessie;	And it is made of silver or alum, and the head is raised higher; below that, there should be one knuckle or finger joint; then take a bladder from a sheep and fill it with the moisture intended for suppositories to treat the bladder, then place it between two fingers tied with a good thread, and heat one end of the moisture on fire; then insert the head of the suppository into the penis, then hold your hand above the bladder against all the moisture until the patient feels that the moisture has reached the bladder.
et se tu n’as la vessie, si pren une piece de parchemin, et en fai .i. cercle, et le perce rondement entor; puis boute .i. fil fort en ces pertus, puis assemble le cercle si com on assemble .i. dal, et met dedens ceu que tu vues d’oile et de moistor et d’aigue, et le lie en l’estrument; et fai si com tu as fait de la vessie, de presser a ta main tant que li moistor veigne a la vessie.	If you do not have the bladder, then take a piece of parchment, make one circle, and perforate it roundly; then insert a strong thread into these holes, close the circle like a purse, put inside oil, moisture, and water, and place it in the instrument; and proceed as you did with the bladder, pressing your hand until the moisture reaches the bladder.
de la piere	of stone (in modern English)
Nos avons jai dit en la division les manieres de piere, et l’estraction ensamble medicines; et ai dit la difference entre la piere enjanree as rains, et toz les signes, et en queil piere on doit ovrer de taille; et en la vessie, et en la verge; et je le vos dirai apertement et briément.	We have told in the division the ways of stone, and extraction along with medicines; and I have said the difference between the stone embedded in the flesh, and all the signs, and in which stone one should operate by cutting; and in the bladder, and in the penis; and I will tell it openly and briefly.
Je dis que li piere qui est enjanree en la vessie si avient plus sovent as enfans, et c’est signe que li aigue saut de la vessie semblans a aigue en sa subtiliteit; et i apert harene, et graite li malaides sa verge, et li pent maintes fois, et puis enroidist; et a mout de ces saut li fondemens; et est legiere li sanation des enfans jusqu’il ont .iiij. ans, et est mout grief en viellars, et est as jones moiene, a ces qui sont entre jonesce et viellece; et est li cure plus legiere de ces qui ont la piere grans, que de ces qui l’ont petite.	I say that the stone which is embedded in the bladder occurs more often in children, and this is a sign that the urine jumps from the bladder like water in its subtlety; it opens a small hole, and the patient's penis swells, and it pains him many times, and then wraps itself up again; and often the foundation of these jumps causes the stone to move downwards; and the healing of children is quick until they reach four years old, and it is very difficult in the elderly, and it is among the middle-aged, for those who are between youth and old age; and the cure is easier for those who have large stones, than for those who have small ones.
Et quant nos venons a la cure, si couvient premier mundifier le malaide per clistere, por traire tout le fiens qui est as intestines. Car il encombre aucune fois a querir la piere.	And when we come to the treatment, it is first necessary to cleanse the patient by enema, to draw out all the filth that is in the intestines. For it sometimes obstructs seeking the stone.
Puis prenez le malaide par les piez, et lou deboutez et movez au desoz, si que li piere dessende au parfont de la vessie, et saille aucune fois dou leu haut; puis le fai seoir entre tes mains appareilliet, et ses mains soient desoz ses cuisses, si que li vessie soit toute declinans aval; puis la quier et la touche ded ens;	Then take the patient by the feet, bend and move them downwards so that the stone descends to the bottom of the bladder and sometimes rises up; then make him sit between your prepared hands, and his hands should be beneath his thighs, so that the bladder is completely declining towards below; then press and touch it with your hand.
se tu sens la piere en l’espaice, si te haste maintenant de taillier sus la piere. Et s’elle ne chiet au touchier dou tout, si moille ton doi indice d’oile de la main senestre, se li malaides est enfes, ou ton doi moien, se li malaides est jovencelz acomplis; et le boute en son fondement, et quier la piere, et quant tu la sens a ton doi, si l’amoine au col de la vessie; puis presse sus a ton doi, et la boute au defuer lai ou tu vues taillier.	if you feel the stone in the space, hurry now to cut above the stone. And if it does not fall with the touch, moisten your right index finger with oil, if the patient is an infant, or thumb, if the patient is a mature person; and push it into its foundation, press the stone, and when you feel it with your finger, push it to the neck of the bladder; then press up with your finger, and push it towards where you will cut.
Et comande au ministre qu’il presse la vessie a sa main, et li comande qu’il estende a sa main destre les coions en haut, et a sa main senestre oste le cuir qui est desoz les coions en la partie ou on fait la taille; puis i boute le spatumile copant, de coi ce est li forme:	And instruct the assistant to press the bladder with his hand, and command him to extend his right hand above the testicles, and with his left hand push aside the skin that is below the testicles in the area where they make the incision; then insert the spatula, which is shaped like this:
Et fent entre ceu qui est entre les coions et le fondement, ne mie em mileu mais au costeit de la naige senestre; et soit drois sus la piere, et tes dois soit adés ou fondement, et soit li taille dou traver si qu’ele soit large par defuer, et dedens estroite, selonc la quantiteit de la piere, ne mie trop grans;	And between the place of the testicles and the bottom, not in the middle but to the left side of the navel; let it be straight above the bone, and your fingers should be close to or at the bottom, and the incision should be wide open at the top and narrow inside according to the size of the stone, not too large;
par aventure la presse si li dois qui est ou fondement, qu’elle saut fuer sens travail; et saiches qu’il i a teil piere ou il a angles, et marges: si est griés a issir; et si a teil qui est souez, semblans a une glant, et reonde, dont li issue est legiere.	In case the pressure does not work on the fingers that are at or near the bottom, he presses it firmly until it pops out with effort; and know that there is a stone or an angle there, and edges: it must be removed; and if there is one that is soft, like a plum and round, the release will be easy.
A celi donques ou il a angles et marge, fai la taille plus grant; et s’elle ne saut, si covient que tu estraignes sus as tenailles qui sont ausi com une lime au chief, por mues estraindre la piere si qu’elle n’eschaipe; ou tu boute desoz li .i. estrument subtil corbé au chief; et se tu ne la pues engignier ensi, si eslarge .i. poc lou pertus, et se li sans decort, si l’estrainche de vitriole;	For the person with angles and a border, make the cut larger; and if it does not spring, you must stretch up with tongs like a limed tip, to push the stone so that it does not escape; or you push something subtle curved under the tip; and if you cannot force it thus, expand one small hole, and if it is not pierced, stretch with vitriol.
et s’il i a plus d’une piere, si boute premier la plus grant au col de la vessie, puis cope sus, puis le trai fuer, et les petites aprés s’il en i a plusors. Et s’elle est mout grans, si la covient soier, et faire plus grant plaie. Car .ij. choses avienent au malaide: ou il muert, ou li urine vient adés par lai que li leus ne puet souder; mais toutevoie t’efforce dou traire, ou dou debrisier as tenailles, tant que tu la traies par pieces;	And if there is more than one stone, you must push the largest one at the bladder's neck first, then strike it, then pull hard, and the smaller ones afterward. And if it is very large, it should be, and make a larger wound. For two things happen to the patient: either he dies or urine comes out immediately when the lees cannot seal; but nevertheless, try to draw or break with tongs, as long as you draw it by pieces.
et quant tu as acomplit ton oevre, si emple la plaie d’encens et d’aloe et de sanc de dragon, et l’estraint, et met par sus .i. drapeil moilliet en oile et en vin, ou en oile et en aigue rose et aigue froide, por apaisier l’aposteme chaut; puis resovine le malaide sus son col, et ne desliier lou lien jusc’au tier jor.	and when you have completed your work, apply the wound with incense and aloe and dragon's blood, and hold it in place, and put on top one damp cloth in oil and wine, or in oil and rose water and cold water, to cool the abscess; then make the patient lie on his neck, and do not loosen the rope until the third day.
Et quant tu le desliies, si arose mout bien lou leu d’oile et d’aigue, puis le cure d’oignement dyafinicon et d’oignement basilicon, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when you dislocate [the limb], anoint it very well with oil and water, then treat it with ointment of dyafinicon and ointment of basilicon until it heals.
Et se apostemes chaus vient en la plaie et corrosions, et congelemens de sanc en la vessie, et soit par ceu retenue li urine, qui est conue en teil maniere que sans saut avec l’urine: boutes donques ton doi en la plaie, et estrai celui sanc, car s’il i remaint, si corront la vessie, et la porrit;	If an abscess or ulcer comes in the wound and congealing of blood in the bladder occurs and thus retains urine, which is known to be harmful without delay: therefore, press down on your bladder in the wound, and extract that blood, for if it remains, the bladder will rot and rupture.
puis leve la plaie d’aigue et d’aisil et de seil, et li aide en toutes les manieres que tu seis, tant qu’il soit sanez; et covient que toutes les oures que tu le cures, que tu li lie les .ij. cuisses, et assemble les medicines sus le leu.	Then raise the wound with water and linen and silk, help it in every way you know, until it heals; and all the wounds that you treat, bind them together with bandages and assemble the medications on top of the area.
Et se li piere est petite, et ele est ou conduit de la verge, et fichie ens, et li urine ne puet issir; si le cure de ceu que je dis ainsois, que tu lou tailles maintes fois, est on escusez de la taille per ceste cure. Je ai ja ce proveit ensi.	And if the stone is small and led into the member by a rod, pierced, and urine cannot pass; in this case, you should cut it many times, as I am saying, until excused of the cutting due to this treatment. I have already proven this so.
Pren .i. foret de fer selonc ceste forme et soit a .iij. angles fichiees en .i. tison:	Take a piece of iron in this shape with four corners pierced into one thong:
puis pren .i. fil et lou lie entor la verge desoz la piere, si qu’ele ne puist venir arrier en la vessie; puis boute le foret en la verge legierement, tant qu’il viegne a la piere; et torne le foret a ta main en la piere poc et poc, tant que tu puisses percier la piere d’autre part; si venra tantost li urine, puis presse ta main sus ceu qui est demorez de la piere qui est dedens la verge. Si est tantost brisie, et saut fuer avec l’urine, et est garis li malaides;	then take a thread and wind it around the rod under the stone, so that it cannot return into the bladder; then gently push the iron piece in the rod until it reaches the stone; and turn the iron piece slowly in the stone bit by bit, until you can pierce the stone from the other side; soon the urine will come, then press your hand on the part that is remaining inside the rod which is within the stone. It will soon be broken and expelled with the urine, and the patient will be healed;
et se tu ne pues ce faire por aucune chose qui le deffent, si lie .i. fil desoz la piere et .i. autre desus, puis fent la verge endroit la piere entre les .ij. liiens, puis l’estrai fuer, et deslie lou liien, et mundifie lou sanc congeleit qui est en la plaie; et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if you cannot do that for any reason that prevents it, tie one thread below the stone and another above, then insert a rod towards the stone between the two ligatures, then pull it out, and detach the ligament, and clean the congealed blood in the wound; and heal it until it is healed.
de la piere des femmes	from the stone of women
Poc avient que piere soit enjanree en femmes, et s’il avient aucune fois, si est li cure grief, et est deffendut por .iij. choses: l’une est que per aventure li femme est vierge; et li seconde est c’on ne puet trover femme bien saichant qui se descuevre as mires, meismement quant elle est caste.	It happens that stones appear in women, and if it ever occurs, it is a serious matter, and it is forbidden for four reasons: one is that by chance the woman may be a virgin; and the second is because one cannot find a wise woman who reveals herself to mirrors, especially when she is chaste.
Et li tierce maniere si est que par aventure on ne puet trover femme bien saichant en cest art de mains; et li quarte maniere si est que li piere de la femme si est plus em parfont que li piere de l’ome, por coi il i couvient faire plus parfonde taille, et grant paour i a.	And the third way is that by chance one cannot find a woman skilled in this art of hands; and the fourth way is that the stone (arrow) of the woman is deeper than that of the man, for which it requires a more profound incision, causing great fear there.
Et se necessitez semont a ceu, si covient que tu preignes une mieresse bien sachant, et a poines la trueve on, et se tu n’en trueves, point si quier .i. caste mire subtil; et li presente une baile bien saige en la vie des femmes, ou une femme qui saiche une partie de l’art, et li comande qu’ele faice ceu que tu li comandes de l’inquisicion de la piere;	If you must do this (incision), it is necessary that you take a midwife who knows the art of hands and if she cannot be found, not even one cast-iron midwife; and present a wise woman in the life of women or a woman who knows a part of the art, and command her to do what you command for the incision of the stone.
et regarde mout bien se li femme est vierge: adonques li covient bouter son doit ou fondement et querir la piere; et s’ele la trueve, si la constraigne desoz son doit, et li recomande qu’elle boute son doit ou con la malaide, et quiere et presse sa main senestre sus la vessie forment.	And carefully observe if the woman is a virgin: then she must thrust her pelvis and seek the stone; and if she finds it, she should hold it under her pelvis and command the patient to bear down with her left hand on the bladder in the manner of pushing.
S’elle la trueve, si covient qu’elle la mueve de greit en greit des l’entree de la vessie jusque desoz, tant qu’elle viegne a la racine de la cuisse; puis cope sus la piere en la racine de la cuisse encontre le mileu dou con, lai ou il est mues apparilliet, et sent la piere en celle partie; et ne mueve son doi desus la piere ou desoz, et soit li taille au premier petite;	If it is found (the dislocation), then it must be moved forcefully from the entrance of the bladder to below, until it reaches the root of the thigh; then strike above the pelvis in the root of the thigh near the middle of the bone, where it is joined together, and feel the bone in that area; and do not move your finger above or below the bone, and cut (the bone) first at a small size.
puis boute lou rait en la taille, se tu sens la piere si acroi la plaie tant que li piere puisse issir fuer, et saiches que maintes manieres de pieres sont: c’est a savoir, petites et grans et aspres et souez, longes et reondes, et qui ont rains. si saiches les semblances por savoir l’issue.	Then push the thighbone (femur) towards the pelvis, if you feel the bone protruding, cut open the wound so that the bone can come out, and know that there are many types of bones: for example, small and large, sharp and smooth, long and round, and curved. Recognize their shapes to know the course (of action).
Et se li sans te vaint, si met au leu vitriole broiet, et li tien une houre tant que li sans soit estainchiez; puis revien a ton ovraige, tant que li piere soit fuer, et aies des estrumens que je t’ai dit en l’estraction de la piere as homes por toi aidier en ton oevre;	And if the bone does not come out by itself, place vitriol powder on it and keep it for an hour until the bone is stained; then return to your work, when the bone has protruded, have tools that I told you about in the extraction of the bone for men to help you with your task.
et se li sans te vaint, et c’est de l’artere qui est copee, si met la poudre sus le leu et l’estrain de tentes et de bendelz, et ne rencomencier plus ceu, et laisse la piere et ne la traire mie, que par aventure morroit li malaide; puis cure la plaie.	And if it (the limb) moves without restraint, and it is the artery that has been struck, place powder on the spot and hold it with straps and bands, and do not touch it again, and leave the arrowhead and do not draw it out, lest the patient dies; then treat the wound.
Et quant li chalor dou sanc est apaisie, et li leus porrist, si revien a ton ovraige, tant que li piere soit fuer.	When the heat of the blood has subsided and the limb can be moved, if the arrowhead is still in, return to your work until the arrowhead comes out by itself.
de hernie carnouse	Of carnous hernia
Ramice aquouse n’est autre chose que assemblee de moistor ou blanc syfac, qui est desoz lou keur des coions, que contient l’uef; et est apelez «syfac», et aucune fois est proprement en la toile de l’uef, si c’on cuide que ce soit .i. autre oef; et c’est li cuir dou coion entre lou blanc syfac que nos avons dit; et ceu n’avient se poc non.	The first sentence to translate:
Et li generation de cest ramice si est de foibleteit que vient as coions, et est espandue celle matiere.	And the production of this ramice is due to weakness that comes from the kidneys, and the matter spreads out.
Et aucune fois si vient de percussion sus les coions, et ceste moistor si a maintes colors: ou c’est color declinans a jaunice, ou c’est sans rouge, ou noir, ou aquous blans, et ce avient plus;	Sometimes it comes from trauma to the kidneys, and this moisture appears in various forms: either with a declining yellow color, or without redness, or black, or white watery, and this occurs more often.
et ce sont li signe de conoistre ceste assemblee, car s’elle est ou blanc syfac que nos avons dit, si est li apostemes reons, .i. poc lonc si com li figure d’un oef, et n’apert mie li coions, car il a moistor tout entor.	And these are the signs to recognize this assembly, for if it is white as we have said, it is an abscess, that is, a long thin shape like an egg, and it does not open the joints, because it has moisture all around.
Et s’il a moistor en la propre toile, si est li apostemes reons avec une partie de l’uef, et por ceu pense on que c’est uns autres oef;	If there is moisture in the very fabric (of the abscess), it is an abscess with a part of the egg-like shape, and for this reason, people think it is another egg.
et se li moistor est entre le cuir des coions et le blanc syfac, si le sent om bien; donques quant tu vues savoir la color de la moistor, si esprueve a tout l’intromissoire quarreit, de coi li forme est ci devant.	If the moisture is between the skin and white matter (of the abscess), it can be felt; therefore, when you want to know the color of the moisture, you should probe the entire cavity, from which the shape is described above.
Selonc ceu donques qui vient aprés l’intromissoire, juge de ceu qui est dedens.	According to what follows after the incision, judge what is within.
Et quant nos la curons par fer, si covient que li malaides soit sainiez selonc som pooir et la repletion de son cors; puis le sovine sus son dos, sus une chose un poc haute, et met desoz lui mout de drapelz;	And when we cure it with iron, the patient should be bled as much as our power allows and his body can bear; then put him on his back, on something slightly raised, and place many cloths beneath him.
puis sié sus sa senestre, et comande au ministre qu’il sié a destre, et estende la verge a l’un des .ij. costelz dou keur des coions;	then lie him on his left side, and command the minister to sit on the right, and extend the rod to one of the two breasts from the shoulders.
puis pren le spatumile leit, et cope le cuir des coions parmi leu dou lonc jusque delez lou poignil, et soit ta fendure toute droite en devisant le cuir des coions jusc’a syfac blanc, et l’escorche subtilment selonc tom pooir;	then take the spatula and cut the skin of the shoulders along their length to the tip of the thumb, ensuring the incision is straight from cutting the skin of the shoulders up to white fat, and peel off the skin delicately as much as our power allows.
puis perce lou syfac plain d’aigue a .i. large pertus, et estrai toute l’aigue, et puis met tes oncines, et estent lou syfac amont; et ne touchier le keur des coions, mais que le syfac soulement; cope tout ou par pieces meismement le costeit de lui subtil, que se tu ne le copes bien saigement, si revenra li aigue;	Then pierce the sore completely full of water about one inch deep, drain all the water, then place your fingers, and close the sore from above; do not touch the core of the bones, but only the sore; cut all around or in pieces the edge of it carefully, otherwise the water will return.
et se l’uef saut fuer a ton oevre, si le ramoinne en son leu quant tu avras acomplit l’uevre dou syfac; puis assemble les .ij. leivres dou keur des coions a une costure, puis le cure si com les autres plaies, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the egg (abscess) jumps out of your work, reset it in its place when you have completed the job with the sore; then bring together the two sides of the bones to a suture, and treat it as other wounds, until it heals.
Et se tu trueves l’uef corromput d’autre maladie, si covient que tu lies les vasselz que sont suspensoire, en doutant le decorrement de sanc; puis cope le coion a tout le suspensoire, et estrai l’uef, et le cure si com nos avons dit.	And if you find the egg corrupted by another disease, it is necessary to tie the vessels that are suspended, being careful not to release the flow of blood; then cut the bone all around the suspension, and drain the egg, and treat it as we have said.
Et se aigue est assemblee en .ij. parties ensamble, saiches que ce sont .ij. ramices; si cope l’autre partie si com tu as fait la premiere igalment, puis essue lou sanc, et met en la plaie lainne moillie en oile roset;	And if a wound is assembled into two parts together, know that these are two branches; if you cut the other part in the same way as you did the first one, then draw out the blood, and put wet linen soaked in rose oil in the wound.
et met defuer autre laine moillie en vin et en oile, et met sus les .ij. coions, et met desus drapelz doublés, et le lie sus a tout le liien qui est selonc ceste forme:	and place another linen soaked in wine and oil on it, and put two poultices on top of it, and cover with double cloths, and tie it all up with the lacing as follows:
Puis pren .ij. drapelz, et les emple de laine charpie selonc ceste semblance et soient assemblez par cousture en la gorle des braies, et li uns des chiés preigne sus le fondement jusc’au dos, et li autres a la partie dou poignil; et li autre dui chief sus les .ij. angres, et soit toute assemblee li restreinture en la boucle dou braier;	Then take two cloths, and use hemp lining according to this appearance and assemble them by sewing into the belt of the braces, and one of the heads takes hold at the base up to the back, and the other at the handle part; and the other head on the two angles, and let the rest be gathered in the brace loop.
et aucune fois est medicinee ceste ramice de cautere en leu de taille de fer, et est que tu preignes .i. cautere cultellaire subtil, et cope le cuir des coions, et soit eschaufez si com nos avons dit, si que li syfac blanc que contient l’aigue est descovers;	And sometimes this ramice of cautery medicine is used in the place of iron cutting, and it is that you take one subtle cautery cutter, and strike the hide of the boil, and let it be heated as we have said, so that the white pus containing the water becomes exposed;
si pren lou cautere selonc ceste forme, et perce celui syfac as oncines, et l’escorche a cest subtil cautere chaut:	if you take the cautery in this form and pierce that pus at once, and strip it with this subtle heated cauterizer:
Et lou cope en toutes les manieres que tu pues, tant que tu esraiches tout; et garde que li feus ne touche l’uef; et saiches que ceste oevre est plus salve; et mues gardans de decorrement de sanc, et muedres que li ovraiges de taille;	and hit it in all ways that you can, until it is burned through completely; and be careful that the fire does not touch the egg; and know that this work is more saving; and beware of the discharge of blood, and make sure the incision is straight.
et se nulle chose te fait contraire, ou aposteme chaus ou decorremens de sanc ou autre chose, si cure ce qui te fait contraire, selonc ceu qui est devant dit.	And if no thing happens contrary to you, or abscesses boil or bleeding or something else, then heal what is contrary to you, according to what was said before.
Et se li malaides est paourous, et ne vuet atendre cest ovraige por son horribleteit, si amenistre perforation, si com je te di, et est que quant tu es bien certains par les significations que nos avons dit que ramice aquouse est lai,	If the patient is afraid and does not wish to endure this work due to its horrible nature, then perform a perforation as I tell you, and it will be that when you are sure by the signs we have said that the bladder is located there.
si fai seoir le malaide sus .i. siege leveit; puis perce l’aposteme an la partie desoz a tout le spatumile large, et met la perforation dou lonc dou cors; et soit larges li pertus, si que toute li aigue corre fuer;	Make the patient sit on a raised seat; then pierce the abscess in the lower part with a lancet of broad blade and make the perforation long along the body; let the openings be wide, so that all the pus can flow out.
puis met coton sus le leu, et le lie, et laisse por corre le remenant de l’aigue, puis le cure tant que li plaie soit sanee;	Then place cotton on the place, bind it, and leave to drain the remaining moisture, then heal it until the wound is healed.
et se li blainche toile ne laisse issir l’aigue en la bouche de la plaie, si covient que tu i boutes une penne ou l’estrument dont on trait l’aigue des ydropiques, de coi li forme est ci devant; et eslarge .i. poc la plaie, et saiches que li aigue revient, et est assemblee aprés .vj. mois ou enqui entor, et quant elle est assemblee si com devant, et ensi passera li malaides ses jors.	and if the white cloth does not allow the moisture to come out from the wound's mouth, then you must put a reed or instrument for draining the moisture of edema in its place, as described earlier; widen .i. inch of the wound, check that the moisture returns, and is collected after 5-7 months, and when it is collected as described earlier, then the patient will pass their days.
de l’aposteme des coions	from the abscess of the eyes
Saiches que en la section de ceste ramice a paor em plusors dispositions, por coi il me semble que mues vaut c’on la laisse;	Know that in the treatment of this disease [ramice], many fear various positions, therefore it seems to me that one should leave [it].
et je vos dirai l’ovraige et les semblances de l’aposteme.	and I will tell you the work and similarities of the abscess.
Je dis donques que maint aposteme vienent ou cors, et meismement as coions; et c’est par mout de cas.	Therefore, I say that many abscesses come from the body or from the kidneys; and this is often so.
C’est a savoir par superfluiteit aigre et ague, qui est espandue as coions, ou de percussion;	This is due to an excess of sour and damp humors, which is spread through the kidneys or by trauma.
et est li color de l’aposteme selonc la color dou cors; et ne trueve point de dolor, et est aposteme grief;	And the color of the abscess is according to the color of the body; and it does not cause pain, and it is a severe abscess.
et par aventure est uns apostemes griés paourous et pierous, et de fuxe color, et aucune fois vient de nout d’artere, ou d’enfleure de voine.	And sometimes an abscess is hard and tough, of the same color, and at times comes from an artery, or the inflammation of a vein.
Quant c’est par nout d’artere, si est conus par la disposition d’aposteme chaut, quant tu la presses a tes dois;	When it is due to an artery, it can be recognized by the hot abscess pustule formation when you press on it with your fingers.
et ne covient mie que tu i touches.	And one should not touch it.
Cil qui est fais d’enfleure de voine est conus par sa disposition a l’expression dou touchement des dois,	The one who is made of swelling of the vein is known by his disposition at the expression of the touch of the fingers,
et puet om bien faire la taille sus ceste semblance, et sus les autres chars;	and can well make the cut on this appearance, and on the others.
et est que tu cope lou keur des coions, puis estent l’uef en haut, et le trai fuer dou blanc syfac, et delivre lou suspensoire de toutes pars de l’uef.	and it is that you cut the core of the kidneys, then the yolk is above, and the thread far from the white yolk, and deliver the suspensioner of all parts of the yolk.

et s’il est aers au syfac, ou en ceu qui est dedens les vasselz, si covient que tu delivre toute celle tenve, et la cope reondement.	And if it is affected by the sores within the body, you must release all that pus and crush it thoroughly.
Et se li naissance de la char est ou leu derrier, si covient que tu la copes toute, et estrai l’uef, si com nous avons dit.	If the birth of the boil is on the backside, you must cut it all off and extract the egg, as we have said.

de l’aposteme des coions	of the abscess on the cheeks
Cis est uns apostemes envoloupez d’un envoloupement semblant a .i. borjon, avec le mollifiement des coions,	This is an abscess enclosed by a swelling resembling a boil, with the softening of the cheeks,

de la routure dou syfac	of the breaking of the saffron
Li avenemens de ceste ramice si est par la section que vient ou syfac, ou l’estension sus le ventre en la partie des angres, por coi li intestine dessendent de celle routure a l’un des coions;	The effects of this herb (ramice) are by the section that comes or saffron, or the extension on the stomach in the part of the flanks, because the intestines descend from that cut to one of the kidneys.
et ceste routure est ou dou syfac, ou de l’estension de li, et vienent ces .ij. manieres de mout de causes: ou de percussion, ou de saut, ou de braire, ou de levement de grief faix, et par semblans choses;	and this dislocation is either simple or extended, and these two types of movement come from several causes: either from impact, or jumping, or pushing, or lifting heavy weights, and similar things;
et li signes quant c’est de l’estension dou syfac, si est qu’il avient poc et poc, en lonc tens, et ne vient mie soudainnement;	and the signs when it is of the extension of simple dislocation are that they occur gradually over a long time, and do not happen suddenly.
