de hernie carnouse	of a hernia carnivorous
En ceste ramice ne vis je onques nul qui osast faire la cure par fer.	In this case, I never saw anyone who dared to heal with iron.
Et li ancien dirent qu’ele est faite si com li ramice qui est ensamble la vis, en teil maniere que tu lie les vasselz, aprés la taille sus ous legierement au desoz;	And the ancients said that it is made in a similar way to the treatment of hernia, by binding the vessels together lightly on top of each other after the incision.
puis cope em mi, et cure l’aposteme de ceu qui oevre, tant que li vasselz chient; et le cure si com nos avons dit, tant qu’il soit sanez.	Then, press it [the abscess] in the middle and treat the abscess of those who work, until they burst; and treat it as we have said, until it is healed.
Aucune fois vient routure ens angres, si com nos avons dit, et apert li leus; et ne dessent nulz des intestines as coions, et s’il en i dessent, c’est poc, et repaire toutes houres;	Sometimes rupture comes in the entrails, as we have said, and open the belly; and do not remove any of the intestines from the anus, and if it is done, it is bad, and repair them every hour.
et toutevoie s’il demoure trop en cest point, si croit li plaie ou syphac, tant que li intestine dessent;	And even if it remains too long in this place, the wound or syphac grows, as long as the intestines are coming out.
et ceu avient par l’estension dou syfac qui est as angres, si com nos avons dit, car il est estendus, puis est mollifiez et enflez li leus et apert;	And this happens due to the extension of the siphac, which is in the anguish, as we have said, because it is extended, then the joints are softened and opened.
et li cure si est par cautere, si com nos avons devant dit; et aucune fois est curee par fer en ceste maniere:	And the cure is by cautery, as we have said before; sometimes it is cured by iron in this way:
et est que li malaides gise sovin sus son dos entre tes mains, puis cope le leu de la routure enfleit dou large selonc la quantiteit de .iij. dois;	and it is that the patient lies down on his back between your hands, then strike the swollen joint of the rupture with a large iron rod according to the size of three fingers.
et puis estrai le syfac qui est desoz le cuir que l’ensuet, puis pren lou rait et lou met sor le leu apparant dou syfac;	and then extract the siphac that is beneath the skin, then take the wire and place it on the swollen joint of the siphac.
et lou presse au parfont dou ventre, puis cout les .ij. leus apparans dou syfac sus lou chief dou rait, et cout l’un et l’autre;	And press the entire belly deeply, then cut the two apparent ribs above the right side of the breast, and cut one and the other;
puis estrai le chief dou rait, et ne coper point dou syfac ne n’estendre l’uef n’autre chose, si com je t’ai fait savoir en la cure de la ramice des intestines;	then remove the right side of the breast, and do not cover the rib nor extend or any other thing, as I have told you in the treatment of removing the entrails;
puis le cure par la cure des plaies. Et quant tu copes les filz, si le mundefie et cure la plaie, tant qu’elle soit sanee.	then treat it by wound care. And when you cut the threads, if they are putrefied and the wound is healed, let it be until it is healed;
Li syfac est constrains, et n’a point d’apparance en la routure, et li cauteres est muedres en cest leu, et plus prochiens a salut.	The ribs are constricted and have no appearance in the wound, and the cauterizations are made in this place, and closer to salvation.
de l’amollissement dou cuir des coions	Of the softening of the skin around the eyes
Maintes fois est amollis li cuirs des coions en aucuns homes, por ceu que les chars que sont dedens sont mollifiees, et est lait a veoir; et est mestier, quant on le vuet curer, c’on faice gesir lou malaide sus son dos, et li cope le cuir qui est mollifiez sus le cuir natureil; puis assemble les .ij. levres a une costure, et se tu vues, cout premier la superfluiteit dou cuir mollifiiez a .iij. costures ou .iiij. fermement; puis cope entre les costures, et lou cure si com les autres plaies, tant qu’il soit sanez, et chient li fil.	Many times the skin around the eyes becomes soft in some men due to the moistening of the glands that are inside, and it can be seen; and it is necessary when you see this, to cure it, to make the patient lie on his back, and strike the softened skin on the natural skin; then join together the two lips at a suture, and if you see, sew first the superfluous skin that has been moistened with four or five stitches firmly; then strike between the sutures, and the cure is done as for other wounds, until it heals, and bind the thread.
dou chastrement	of the lancing
Saiches que chastremens est escomeniez en nostre loi, et por ceu il me plairoit que je n’en parlasse mie en cest livre; et n’est necessaires fuer que por .ij. manieres: dont l’une est que li mires en saiche respondre quant on li demandera, et en saiche la cure; et li autre, por ceu que nos avons sovent mestier de chastrement d’aucunes bestes por nos aidier, si com de bouc et de mouton et de chait et d’autres bestes. Je dis donques que chastremens est fais selonc .ij. manieres: ou par atraction, ou par fendure.  En celle que nos faisons par attraction, faisons nos seoir la beste en aigue chaude, tant que li coion soient mollifiez et pendant; puis les preing a ta main, tant qu’il soient remis et que tu ne les sentes plus.  Du chastrement de taille: covient que tu teignes la beste, et li presse le cuir des coions a ta main senestre, puis lie le suspensoire, et cope sus chescun oef a .i. cop, quant tu les avras bien escorchiez; et i laisse aucun poc dou syfac et lou subtil syfac qui est sor les vasselz; et ceste maniere de chastrement est muedre que cele qui est faite par attraction, por ceu que a l’atraction demoure par aventure aucune chose des coions, par coi li beste desire luxure; puis cure la plaie tant qu’ele soit sanee.	1. Know that castration is mentioned in our law, and I would prefer not to speak of it in this book; and it is only necessary for two reasons: the first being that the mirrors in castration respond when asked about it and its cure, and the second, because we often have need for castration of certain animals to help us, such as a bull or sheep or cat or other animals. I say therefore that castration is done in two ways: either by attraction or by cutting. In the way we do it by attraction, let us sit the animal in hot water until its genitals are softened and relaxed; then seize them with your hand, keeping them pressed down until they are reset and you no longer feel them.
des hermofrodites	Hermaphrodites
Hermofrodie est selonc .ij. manieres as homes: l’une si est que entre les .ij. coions apert ausi com li figure de la nature d’une femme, ou il ait poil, et aucunes fois en cort li urine.  Et li autre maniere si est en femmes, et ait sus lou poignil ausi com une verge et .ij. coions.  Et li cure de l’ome et de la fame si est que tu copes les chars ajostees toutes, et les cure si com autres plaies; en la seconde maniere, des homes dont li urine saut par lou cuir des coions, si n’a point de cure.	Hermaphrodites are of two kinds, namely males who have an opening between the two testicles as a woman does, with hair and sometimes urinate in court. The second kind is in women who have something above the clitoris like a penis and two testicles. The cure for both male and female hermaphrodites is to cut the surrounding skin (scrotum) and treat it like other wounds; however, there is no cure for males whose urine shoots through the skin of their genitals.
de la tentigene	Of the tension
Tentigene est une chars ajostee sus la partie natureil, tant qu’elle est trop laide a veoir; et aucunes femmes l’ont ausi grant com une main, et c’est li cure. Il covient que tu teignes la superfluiteit de la tentigene a ta main ou as oncines, et la cope legierement; et n’aler mie trop em parfont, que decorremens de sanc n’i viegne, puis le cure d’autre cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et a une autre char que naist a la bouche de la marris, et l’emple, et par aventure saut fuer, et est selonc la semblance d’une kowe, et por ceu l’apelerent li ancien «maladie kowee». Si covient que tu la copes, si com nos avons dit la tentigene, et la cure tant qu’elle soit sanee.	The superfluous tension (tentigene) that is too unsightly should be removed from the natural part; and some women have it as large as a hand, and it is a disease. You should dye the excess of the tentigene with your hand or onions, and lightly cut it; do not go too deep so that no bleeding occurs, and cure it with another remedy until it is healed; and in another case where a growth arises from the mouth of the vagina, and it swells, and possibly jumps, and resembles a cow, for which they will call it "the disease of cows" among the ancients. If so, you should cut it as we have said with the tentigene, and cure it until it is healed.
de erratique	Of the erratic growth
Erratique si est quant li nature de la femme n’est mie percie, ou li pertus est petis; et est naturez par naissance, ou accidens par maladie que venue i est; ou c’est par char ajostee, ou dou syfac subtil ou espés, et est fais em parfont en la marris, ou en costez, ou desoz, ou que soit; et deffent le concevoir, et l’enfantement, et par aventure les flors a avoir; et li connoissance de ceu si est par le regart de la baile. Se li estoupemens est prochiens apparans, si quier a tes dois ou au rait. S’il est dou syfac subtil, et il est prochiens as .ij. leivres, si te haste, et la ront ensi: met tes .ij. dois indices ensamble, et li femme soit sus son dos, espandues ses jambes; puis estent les .ij. leivres forment, tant que li subtilz syfac soit rons, et soit overs li estoupemens; puis pren laine, et la moille en oile, et la met sus le leu, et gise li femme a home chescun jor, si qu’il ne puist souder. Et se li syfac est dur et espés, si covient que tu lou copes au spatumile semblant a foille de mirte. Se li estoupemens est de char nee, si la sospent a l’oncine et la cope; et aies les medicines estainchans sanc, si com acaice, sanc de dragon, encens, ensamble abun d’uef; puis amenistre une caine de plonc large, si que li plaie ne puisse souder; et ensi soit longement, et li amenistre une tente de lin sec; puis soit curez d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.  Et quant en la marris vient char nee, si la covient coper selonc ceste maniere, se ce n’est apostemes enchancrez. Car a l’aposteme enchancreit qui est en la marris, ne doit on touchier de feir.	1. If the nature of a woman is not perceived or small; it may be natural at birth, or an accident due to illness that comes upon her; or it may be due to discharge, whether subtle or thick, and this occurs in the marriage bed, or on the side, or underneath, wherever it may be; they should be aware of it, and know when to conceive and give birth and possibly have flowers; and knowledge of these things is by the observation of the midwife. If the discharge is approaching, whether at your hand or at the head, if it is subtle, move quickly and follow these steps: put both hands together, and the woman should be on her back, with her legs spread apart; then the subtle discharge will form, as long as the thick discharge subsides; then take wool, moisten it in oil, and place it on the area, and have the woman lie down each day so that it does not heal. If the discharge is hard and thick, you should cut it with a spatula resembling a myrtle leaf. If the discharge is of blood, suspend it at the navel and cut; and apply medicines to stop the bleeding, such as acacia, dragon's blood, incense, together with much egg; then place a large bandage around the wound so that it does not heal; and in this way it should be kept open for a long time, and you should also apply a linen tent; then cure her of other ailments until she is healthy. And when there is blood in the marriage bed, if necessary, cover it in this manner, unless it is an abscess that has grown. For an abscess that has grown in the marriage bed, one should not touch to treat.
des emorroides	If the nature of a woman is not perceived or small; it may be natural at birth, or an accident due to illness that comes upon her; or it may be due to discharge, whether subtle or thick, and this occurs in the rectum, or on the side, or underneath, wherever it may be; they should be aware of it, and know when to treat and cure it; and knowledge of these things is by the observation of the physician. If the discharge is approaching, whether at your hand or in the rectum, if it is subtle, move quickly and follow these steps: put both hands together, and the woman should be on her back, with her legs spread apart; then the subtle discharge will form, as long as the thick discharge subsides; then take wool, moisten it in oil, and place it on the rectum, and have the woman lie down each day so that it does not heal. If the discharge is hard and thick, you should cut it with a spatula resembling a myrtle leaf. If the discharge is of blood, suspend it at the anus and cut; and apply medicines to stop the bleeding, such as acacia, dragon's blood, incense, together with much egg; then place a large bandage around the wound so that it does not heal; and in this way it should be kept open for a long time, and you should also apply a linen tent; then treat her of other ailments until she is healthy. And when there is blood in the rectum, if necessary, cover it in this manner, unless it is an abscess that has grown. For an abscess that has grown in the rectum, one should not touch to treat.
Emorroydes sont overtures de voines dont sans cort acostumeement, et quant les emorroydes sont vielles si devienent thelul; et nos avons jai dit en la division les semblances d’aus, et les signes, et je dirai ci celles qui resoivent curation. Je di que les emorroides et li thelul, quant il sont em parfont en la marris, et il n’aperent au sentir, si n’est mie li cure par fer. Cil qui sont a la bouche de la marris, c’on puet sentir, sont cil c’on puet curer. Il covient donques que tu mettes la femme en une maison froide, puis estent l’altelul as tenailles, et le cope en ses racines, puis poudre sus medicines restraignans sanc, si com acaice et sanc de dragon et encens, et semblans choses; puis boute ses piez a la paroit une houre, puis la met en aigue froide; et se decorremens de sanc i vient, si la fai seoir en une decoction de sumac et d’escorce de pomes grenates et de gales et de semblans choses, et puis pren farine d’orge, et la confis avec miel et aisil, et en fai .i. emplaustre sus son dos. Et se il estainche, c’est boin. Se ceu non, se li fai aerdre ventouses au dos et as mameles sens ferir; puis pren lainne, et la moille en jus de plantain ou en jus d’aglentier avec vin viel, et fai aerdre au leu.  Et quant li aposteme repose, si cure lou leu d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez; et celle qui est apelee «albathir» est rouge, et est semblans a .i. chief aspre, si le covient coper si com j’ai dit le thelul; et puis lou cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	1. Emorroydes are openings of veins which, without care, often become inflamed; and when emorroydes are old, they become hardened; and we have said in the division, their resemblances, and signs, and I will say here those which receive treatment. I say that the emorroides and the hardened ones, when they are fully within the anus, cannot be felt, unless they are cured by iron. Those which are at the opening of the anus, can be felt, and these can be treated. It is therefore necessary that you place the woman in a cold house, then press the inflamed area with tweezers at its roots, then sprinkle medicines that stop bleeding such as cinnamon and dragon's blood and incense, and similar things; then hold her feet to the air for an hour, then immerse it in cold water; and if blood comes out, let her sit in a decoction of sumac and grenade bark and gall, and similar things, and then take barley flour, mix it with honey and oil, and make one poultice on her back. If it bleeds, that is good. If not, make bladders inflate on the back and at the breasts without piercing them; then take linen, wet it in juice of plantain or marshmallow with old wine, and apply to the area. And when the abscess subsides, cure the area with ointment until it is healed; and that which is called "albathir" is red, and resembles a hard knot, it must be covered as I have said for the inflamed one; and then heal it until it is healed.
des apostemes de la marris	openings of the anus
Maintes manieres d’aposteme vienent en la marris, si com chancre et aposteme pierous et herpes et estiomenes et fistules et emorroides et aposteme chaut, et plusors autres maladies que j’ai dit en la division. Il covient donques que je die en cest traitier l’aposteme chaut qui vient en la marris, qui n’est mie des apostemes que coillent bowe; et se tu vues savoir l’ovraige de fer, si regarde se li apostemes est agus en l’encomencement de sa venue, et plain de chalor et de fievre, et s’il devient rouge se tu le pues veoir.  Adonques ne te haster mie de percier, mais lou fais meurer tant que li dolor soit apaisie; et puis fai seoir lou malaide sus .i. siege, et ait .ij. petis sieges ou il se cline, et apoie sus son dos et assemble ses piez as parties defuer la jambe; et soient ses cuixes espandues, et mette ses braz desoz ses genous, et les lie bien d’un boin liien; puis succe li baille devers lou destre costeit, et i amenistre l’estrument dont on oevre la bouche de la marris, de coi ci aprés vient li forme; et covient que quant tu i vues amenistrer cest estrument, que tu fiches le rait premier ens por savoir la parfondeté de la marris, si que ceu qui entre ens de l’estrument n’i viegne plus em parfont qu’il ne doit, et qu’il ne blece la malaide; et se li estrumens est plus grans, si covient covrir la parfondesce de la marris de drapelz, si que li estrumens ne li grieve; et covient qu’il mette le cornet de l’estrument au desus, et qu’il teigne l’estrument. Et quant li apostemes apert, et on lou fent a la main mol, si le covient coper au chief, au spatumile leit; et quant li bowe est vuidie, si covient que tu mettes en la plaie tentes moillies en oile roset, ou en oile vert sec; et met la tente fuer de la plaie au parfont de la marris, et met par defuer sus la marris et sus le poignil lainne nette moillie en aigue ou malves soient cuites; puis le cure aprés .ij. jors d’oignement avenant a ceu, tant qu’il soit sanez; et aucune fois leve on la marris et la plaie par clistere d’aigue et de miel, et puis d’aigue ou racines de lis et aristologe longe soient cuites; puis reveigne a l’oignement.  Et se li plaie est reponue en la marris, si covient que tu te gardes de cuire de fer, mais cure la si com nos avons dit en la division.	Many types of abscess come in the anus, such as canker sores, pustular abscesses, herpes, fistulas, emorroides, and other diseases that I have mentioned earlier. It is therefore necessary for me to describe in this treatise the hot abscess that comes in the anus, which is not the same as hemorrhoids; and if you wish to know about iron treatment, look to see if the abscess is acute at the beginning of its occurrence, and full of heat and fever, and becomes red when touched. In this case, do not hurry to lance it, but let it ripen until the pain subsides; then make the patient sit on one seat, or two small seats where he can lean, and support his back and feet at the parts away from the leg; and spread his thighs, and put his arms under his knees, and tie them well with a good ligature; then squeeze the rectum towards the right side, and bring the instrument used to open the anus into position, as follows: when you wish to introduce this instrument, make sure that what enters does not go further than necessary, and does not hurt the patient; and if the instrument is large, cover the depth of the anus with cloths, so that the instrument does not cause pain; and put the handle of the instrument on top, and mark the instrument. And when the abscess opens, and is softened by hand, it should be covered with a sponge dipped in rose oil, or dry green oil; and place the sponge inside the wound, and over the anus and over the handle linen that has been washed and rinsed. Then apply ointment for two days, following this procedure until it is healed; occasionally lift the anus and the wound using enemas of water and honey, then of boiled lentils or long-cooked aristolochia root; then return to the ointment. And if the wound has healed in the anus, you should be careful not to burn with iron, but treat it as we have described earlier.
de l’enfantement	Of childbirth
Mestier est premier a la baile qu’elle conoisse la figure de l’enfantement natureil, et li signes si est quant tu vois la femme apresser aval, et desire odorer l’ar: adonques se haste li enfes de fuer issir; adonc saiches que cil enfantemens est selonc la figure natureil, et est li issue soz son chief, et li secondine avec lui; et quant tu vois ces signes, si covient presser legierement son ventre, si que li enfes isse tost; car quant il dessent sus son chief, si ist li secondine avec lui, et est mondee li marris de ses superfluitez par bone mundification; et cist qui vient autrement ne vient mie naturelment. Car il vient aucune fois sus ses piez, et vient fuer li cors ou li chiés, et les mains, ou il vient sus son ventre, ou sovin, et est convertis par aventure sor son col, et par autres figures malvaises; si est mestier a la baile qu’elle soit saige et subtilz en ces choses, et se warse d’error et de decevement, et je vos mostrerai toutes les figures coment on li doit aidier.	The midwife must first recognize the figure of natural childbirth and the signs when she sees the woman in labor and desires to defecate; then hasten the birth of the infant; afterwards know that this childbirth is according to nature, and it comes out through its head, followed by another part with it; and when you see these signs, gently press on the woman's abdomen so that the infant is born quickly; for when it descends towards its head, it follows it, and the husband sheds his superfluidities through good purification; and this which comes otherwise does not come naturally. For sometimes it comes over the feet, or the body or the shoulders, or the hands, or over the abdomen, or the backside, and it may be turned by chance on its neck, and in other evil figures; therefore, the midwife must be wise and subtle in these matters and beware of error and deception, and I will show you all the figures as to how one should help.
Se li enfes vient sus son chief par issue natureil, et li femme enfante griement, et li vertus de li est foible, si la fai seoir sus une selle, ou les femmes la tienent; et arose sa nature d’oile ou fenugreic soit cuit, et puis boute li baile entre ses dois le petit spatumile dont ci est li forme:	If the infant comes out through its head naturally and the woman is laboring intensely with weak vitality, let her sit on a saddle or have women hold her; then apply oil or fenugreek that has been cooked to her nature. Then insert the small spatula-shaped instrument shown here between her fingers.
et fende la secondine, et cope a son ungle tant que li moistors qui est ens corre fuers; et preint lou ventre de la femme tant que li enfes dessende, et s’il ne dessent, si covient clisterizer la femme de muscillaige de fenugrec avec oile de sisament; puis la fai preindre et esternuer de condisi, et tien sa bouche et son neis une houre: si istra maintenant l’enfes.Et se les .ij. mains issent fuer, si covient que tu les ramoinne legierement poc et poc; et s’elles n’i puent entrer, si met la femme sus .i. siege, et li lieve les piés en haut; puis deboute le siege sus terre, et teigne on la femme, qu’elle ne chiece au deboutement; et se li mains n’i puet entrer, et li enfes muert, si li cope les mains au couteil qui est ci devant mis, et estrai l’enfant, et ramoine igalment.	And cut the second bone [or birth canal], and strike its nail [or fetus] until the moisture that is within it goes out; and press the woman's belly until the child comes out, and if it does not come out, then you must oint her with mustard seed oil of sesame; then make her take a position and vomit with emetics, and hold her mouth and nose for an hour: this is now when the child will come.
de l’issue de l’enfant sus ses piez	Of the birth of the child onto its feet.
Quant li enfes vient sus ses piez, si lou covient bouter en haut;	When the child comes onto its feet, then you must push it upwards;
et puis le torne poc et poc, tant qu’il soit igalz;	And then turn (the shoulder) to and fro, until it is even.
puis preigne .i. des piez et l’estende poc et poc.	Then take one piece of wood and stretch it back and forth.
Cant il saut jusc’as cuixes, si la comande a preindre, et la fai esternuer de condisi;	Can it jump up to the hips (or groin), if commanded, and make it vomit by squeezing?
si saut fuer, se Deus vuet.	If it should jump forward, as God wills.
Et s’il n’ist fuer si com nos avons dit, si le torne poc et poc, tant qu’il soit selonc la figure natureil.	And if it is not as we have said, it should be turned bit by bit, until it is according to the natural shape.
Car adonques ist il legierement.	And therefore it should be done gently.
Et s’il ne vient fuer si com nos avons dit, si pren muscillaige de altee, et oile de sisament, et gomme fondue, et broie tout en .i. mortier;	And if it does not come as we have said, take musk oil of altar, and oil from roses, and melted resin, and grind all together in one mortar.
et met sus la nature de la femme dedens et defuer cest oignement,	and apply it to the woman's nature within and cover this ointment,
puis la fai seoir en aigue tede jusque desoz les costelz;	Then make him sit upright with high fever below his ribs;
et quant elle est moillifie desoz, se li fai .i. coliere de mirre, et li met desoz, et li laisse une houre;	and when it becomes soft beneath, make one myrrh cataplasm, place it beneath, and leave it for an hour;
puis la fai seoir sus .i. siege, puis la fai esternuer et estraint sa bouche et son neis, et li preint le ventre legierement, car li enfes saut maintenant.	Then make him sit on a chair, then make him vomit and hold his mouth and nose, and gently press his stomach, for the infant now jumps.
de l’issue de l’enfant sus ses genous	Of the birth of the child upon its knees
Quant li enfes vient en ceste forme, si i mette li baile ses mains poc et poc;	When a child comes in this manner, place the birthing blocks, hand over hand;
puis soit sovinee sus son col, et li pendent li piez aval, et soit gisans sor .i. lit;	then be supported on its neck and let its feet hang downwards, and lie upon one bed.
et plie ses mains poc et poc, et puis li preint les mains sus lou ventre, et li oste les cussins desoz, tant qu’elle soit appareillie aval;	fold its hands over each other, and then take hold of its hands above, and remove the pillows underneath until it is prepared below.
et se li enfes ne saut, si pren ses piez et li muef forment, puis li muef lou ventre amont, puis i boute tes mains;	And if the child does not jump, take its feet and turn it upside down, then turn it over belly upward, then put your hands on it;
et ewe l’enfant poc et poc; et comande a la femme qu’elle se preigne tant que li enfes isse.	And shake the child gently; and command the woman to hold herself until the child excretes.
de l’issue de l’enfant qui vient dou large une main pendant	The issue of the child coming through one hand wide;
I covient engignier a ramener la main:	It is necessary to devise a way to set the hand:
s’on ne la puet ramener, si fai lever la femme, et aler;	If it cannot be set, have the woman lift it and walk:
s’elle ne puet aler, si la fai gesir sus .i. lit, et li deboute les jambes forment;	If she cannot walk, make her lie on a bed with her legs spread apart:
puis amenistre lou muscillaige que j’ai conteit;	then bring the belladonna that I mentioned:
et s’elle n’enfante, si la fai seoir sus .i. siege, puis estudie au rameneir la main;	And if it does not give birth [to anything], make her sit on a seat or chair, then study how to reposition the hand;
et ewe l’enfant selonc la figure natureil, et la fai esternuer, et li comande qu’elle se preigne tant que li enfes isse fuer.	And if it gives birth according to its natural shape, make her vomit, and command her to grasp it as long as the child comes out;
de l’issue de l’enfant sus son col, et ait espandues ses mains, et sa faice tornee devers lou dos sa mere	Hold the issue of the child by its neck, and spread your hands wide apart, turning your body towards the back of its mother;
I covient que li baile teigne sa main, puis le torne poc et poc, et l’ewe legierement;	You must hold the child's hand first, then turn it gently and draw it out lightly;
et quant il est igalz, si met sus la nature muscillaige de altee et oile, si com nos avons dit, puis li comande qu’elle se mueve poc et poc;	And when it is equal, place upon it a salve of muscle relaxant and oil, as we have said, then instruct it to move little by little.
et quant tu avras ce fait, si la fai seoir sus .i. siege, et li comande k’elle se preigne; et la fai esternuer.	When you have done this, make her sit on a chair, and instruct her to catch it. Then make her vomit.
de ceste meisme maniere a tout la secondine	In the same manner, apply the remedy to all the others.
Quant il vient fuer en ceste maniere a tout la secondine, si cope la secondine a ton ungle, tant que li moistors soit vuidie;	When it comes on in this manner for all the others, grasp the sore with your nail, until the moisture is removed.
et se li enfes pent sus sa faice et sus son col, si la cope des la boude, qu’elle ne soit retenue, et muere li enfes;	And if the child presses upon its face and neck, the head of the bone should not be held back, and the child dies.
puis boute l’enfant dedens, tant que tu l’aies mis si com il covient, et comande a la femme qu’elle se preigne aucune fois:	Then push the child inwards until you have put it correctly, and command the woman to take herself once.
adonques si istra legierement.	then carefully.
de l’issue des gemelz	of twin births
Saiches que gemeil naissent maintes fois, et aucune fois en naissent .iij. ou .iiij.; et ceu n’est mie estrainge chose, et poc avient.	Know that twins are born many times, and sometimes three or four; and this is not strange and rarely happens.
Dui sont estrainge chose, et ne vivent mie, se poc nom;	Twins are rare and do not often live, unless they are named.
je sai ceu, qu’il soient multipliiet, et sont desevrez par lou syfac qui les devise, qui est liiez a la boude;	I know that they multiply, and are conceived by the seed which is tied to the cowd.
et aucune fois issent ausi naturelment com uns tous sous, si com nos avons dit.	Sometimes they are born naturally like any other child, as we have said.
Et s’il issent griement, si la cure si com nos avons dit, et soit li baile subtilz, et faice tost et legierement ceu qu’elle fait;	And if it issues loudly, treat it as we have said, and let the balm be subtle, and do quickly and lightly what it does.
et faice ensi com il vaut mues a salut.	and make it such that it brings salvation.
de plusors enfans	of many children.
Aucune fois sont formez en la marris .i. ou .ij. ou .iij. ou .iiij. ou .v. ou .vj. ou .vij., ou plusors jusc’a .xv., et sont tout formeit en forme d’enfant par le mesurement dou saige glorious,	Sometimes they are formed in marriage. One, two, three, four, five or six, seven, or more up to fifteen; and they are all formed in the shape of a child according to the measurement of sacred glory,
et couvient que li baile saiche tout ceu, car par aventure semblans chose li avient;	And it is necessary that the bailiff knows all this, for similar things often happen.
si faice selonc ceu qu’il covient.	Follow according to what is necessary.
de l’enfant mort	of a dead child.
Quant tu cures la femme de l’enfant mort ou ventre, si com j’ai dit en la division, et il ne vient fuers, et tu es constrains d’ovraige de mains;	When you cure the woman of a dead or unborn child, as I have said in the division, and it does not come out by itself, and you are compelled to perform an operation by hand.
si covient que tu saiches se li femme est de saine vertut, et n’ait accident ou elle ait paor de mort;	If you need to know if the woman is of sound virtue and not experiencing any accident or fear of death;
si covient que li femme soit sovinee sus son dos, et soit ses chiés enclins aval, et les jambes levees;	If you need to know if she is pregnant, lay her on her back with her head down and raise her legs.
et li ministre la teigne de .ij. pars, ou elle soit liie au lit si qu’elle ne soit traite au dessendement de l’enfant;	and the minister should examine her in the lower abdominal area, or bind her to the bed so that she is not treated for childbirth.
puis frotez la bouche de la marris d’oiles moistes avec muscillaige de altee et de fenugrec et semence de lin, puis oigne li baile ses mains de ces oiles et de ces muscillaiges;	Then anoint the mouth of the woman with moist oil mixed with musk, aloe, and fenugreek seeds, and then anoint the minister's hands with these oils and mixtures.
puis les boute en la marris legierement, puis quiere .i. leu ou elle boute les oncines que soient covenaubles a ceu,	Then push it gently into the socket, then seek one side where it pushes out, that is suitable for this.
et pren warde se li enfes est apparilliez qu’il dessende sus son chief;	and take care if the tendons are exposed so they do not slip back up on the head;
si fiche les oncines en ses eulz ou en son col ou en sa bouche ou en som palais ou desoz la barbe ou en la forcele ou pres des costez,	if you push the tendons into his eyes or neck or mouth or throat or under the beard or in the hollow of the jaw or near the sides,
et se li dessendemens est sus piez, se li fiche ou poignil et as costes moienes;	and if the dislocation is on limbs, it is pierced or pressed and the ribs are broken.
et covient qu’il teigne l’oncine a sa main destre, et mette la corbeure entre ses dois de la senestre main, et li boute a tout sa main legierement, et fiche l’oncine en aucun de ces leus que nos avons dit, tant qu’il viegne a la chose vuide;	and it must be held with the right hand, and the curvature placed between its two left hands, and it should be pushed with all its left hand lightly, and the oncine is pierced in any of the places mentioned above, until it comes to an empty place.
et c’est li forme de l’oncine:	This is the shape of the oncine:
puis fiche encontre .i. autre oncine, ou le tier se tu en as mestier, si que li estractions soit igalz;	then pierce towards one other oncine, where necessary, so that the extraction is equal.
et puis l’estent igalment en movant d’une part et d’autre, por mues issir, et soit li oncines dentez por mues tenir, si com ci est li forme:	And then it should be kept equal by moving from one side to the other, so that movement can occur, and the bones should be brought together for movement, as shown in this figure:
Et s’il en demoure une partie, si oigne li baile aucuns de ses dois d’oile, et les boute en celle partie, et traie l’autre partie;	And if any part remains, then open one of the joints with oil and press it into that part, and pull the other part.
et s’il en i demoure point, si met cest oncine ou plus haut leu, et fai ceu tant qu’il s’en isse tout fuers.	And if no part remains, then put the bone in a higher position and do this until it comes out completely.
Et se l’une mains vient devant l’autre, et il ne puet ramener por l’estreignement,	And if one hand comes before the other and cannot be returned due to strain.
si covient que tu envoloupes sus .i. drapeil, tant qu’il isse tote;	and you must wrap it up in a cloth until it subsides;
puis la cope en la jointure de la plante ou au coute, et ensi covient que tu faices en l’autre main, et as .ij. piés.	then the wound in the joint of the palm or fingers, and you should do the same for the other hand, and to both feet.
Et se li chiés de l’enfant est gros et il est estrois en l’issue, ou il ait ou chief aigue assemblee,	And if the child's hips are large and the birth canal is narrow or there is a sharp assembly of the head:
si covient que tu boute le spatumile espinous entre tes dois, et fent le chief et estrai l’aigue;	It is necessary for you to insert the pointed spatula between your teeth, and bend it and draw out the pus.
ou tu la ront a l’estrument qui est apelez «almidach», de coi li forme vient avec les estrumens ou chapistre qui est aprés cestui;	you turn to the instrument called "almidach", from which the form comes with the tools or chapter that follows this;
et ensi meisme faice se li enfes a grant chief naturelment;	and in the same manner, make the opening naturally large for him.
et puis traie fuer les osses as tenailles,	and then remove the bones with the pliers.
et se li chiés saut fuer et il estraint a la forcele, si soit fendus, tant que li moistors qui est ou pis issue fuer;	And if the head of the shoulder leaps out and is held with force, it should be cut, as far as the moisture that is further out;
et s’elle ne puet issir, si le cope par pieces au mues que tu pues;	If it cannot come out, strike it into pieces as far as you can;
et s’il est enflez au ventre ou desoz les costez, si covient que tu lou perces tant que li moistors corre.	And if it is swollen in the belly or under the ribs, it must be pierced until the moisture subsides.
Et se li enfes est sus ses piez, si est li attraction legiere, et li adrecemens a la bouche de la marris est legier.	And if the swelling is on the feet, the treatment is light and the reduction to the mouth of the bladder is easy.
Et s’il est estrois au ventre ou au pis, si couvient que tu l’estraies a .i. drapeil envoloupeit sus la main;	And if it is narrowed in the stomach or thigh, you must straighten it with one gauze rolled up on the hand;
et fent le ventre ou le pis, tant que li moistors qui i est corre;	and if it is narrowed in the stomach or thigh, until the moisture that is there is corrected;
et se li autre membre sont osteit, et li chiez demoure,	and if other limbs are dislocated, and the head remains,
si boute li baile sa main em parfont de la marris, et le traie jusc’a la bouche de la marris;	push the ball of the thumb into deep within the anus and pull until it reaches the mouth of the anus;
puis i boute .i. oncine ou ij., et le trai fuer;	Then push one or two times, and pull it through.
et se li bouche de la marris est retrecie por aposteme chaut qui i est venus, si n’i covient mie travillier,	and if the mouth of the sore is narrowed by the hot abscess that has come, do not try to force it.
ains covient amenistrer choses moistes et grasses;	Instead, administer moist and fatty substances.
et li amenistre emplaustres, et siece en aigue mollifians et amoistans.	Apply poultices, and soak in warm water to soften and moisten them.
Et se li enfes est sus son costeit, et tu le pues mettre igal, si amenistre ceu que nos avons dit en l’enfant vif;	And if the infant is on its chest side, and you can place it straight, bring the head downwards as we have said in the living child.
et s’on nen ait pooir, si lou trai fuer par pieces, et n’i laissier rien de la secondine.	And if one cannot do it, pull it apart piece by piece and leave nothing of the afterbirth.
Et quant tu avras ce fait, se li amenistre ceu que nos avons dit ens apostemes chaus que vienent en la marris;	Then bring the head downwards as we have said in abscesses that come during childbirth;
et se decorremens de sanc vient, si soit mise en aigue restraignant, et li amenistre autres cures.	And if bleeding comes out, it should be put in tight constriction and other treatments applied.
Et je vis une femme en cui ventre uns enfes avoit esteit mors, puis consut .i. autre sus celui, et refut mors li autres.	And I saw a woman whose womb had a child die, then consulted another on it, and revived the other.
Aprés lonc tens li vint uns apostemes en la boude, et enfla tant qu’il ovrit, et comensa a grant porreture.	After a long time, an abscess came in the armpit, and swelled so much that it opened and began to rot.
je fui apelez a la cure, et i pensai lonc tens, et ne pot soder li plaie.	I was summoned for treatment, and for a long time I thought about the wound, but could not heal it.
Je mis sus emplaustre de fort attraction, et en issit uns os, et aprés aucuns jors uns autres.	I applied powerful astringent, and an bone came out, then after several days another one did.
Je me mervillai mout, por ceu c’ou ventre n’a point d’os.	I marvel greatly, because the belly has no bones.
Si pensai que c’estoit des os d’un enfant mort.	I thought it was the bones of a dead child.
Je quis la plaie, et en traï mains os, tant que li femme fut em miglior point;	I wanted to treat the wound, and took out many bones until the woman was in better condition;    Je me mervillai mout, por ceu c’ou ventre n’a point d’os.
et vesquit li femme lonc tens ensi, et issoit adés un poc de bowe dou leu;	and the woman recovered for a long time in this manner, and after a short while she had some swelling in the place.
et je n’ai recordeit cest chapistre fuer que por ceu que, quant li maistres trueve une estrainge chose, qu’il i saiche mettre aide.	And I have not recorded this chapter except for the reason that, when masters find an unusual thing, they know how to help it.
dou ramener la marris a son leu	To remedy a dislocated joint to its place
Ci aprés vient li forme dou pressor, a coi on ewe les livres; et a .ij. tornans as .ij. chiés des .ij. liiens.	Here follows the form of the pressor, which we use in books; and to the two joints of the two chains at each turn.
Toutevoie, li cornes soit plus subtilz dou restrictoire, et soit fais de ebene ou de bux;	Nevertheless, the horns should be thinner than the retractor, and made of ebony or boxwood;
et soit li bouche dou fust .i. doi de large, et li marge des arbres .i. doit, et de lonc une palme et demi;	And let the mouth of the furnace be 1 finger wide (about 0.6 cm), and the edge of the trees (anvils) 1 dactyl (approx. 2.4 cm), and length of half a palm (about 7.5 cm).
et enmi les .ij. liemens soient dui ajostemens de cest meisme fust, qui soient fermeit en l’un et en l’autre, de demi palme de lonc ou un poc plus;	And within two leagues (about 10 km) should be two anvils (stones) aligned with the same furnace, which are joined together in one and the other, half a palm long (about 3.75 cm) or slightly more;
et cist dui ajostement sont bouteit en la bouche de la marris por ovrir quant on torne les .ij. cornes.	And these two alignments are placed in the mouth of the hammer to open when turning the two horns (anvils).
Une autre forme, a sa semblance plus subtilz et plus legiere, soit faite de fust de ebene ou de bux, selonc la semblance des tenailles;	Another form, similar but more subtle and lighter, should be made of ebony or boxwood, in the shape of pliers.
et ait as .ij. chiés .ij. ajostemens, si com tu vois, d’une palme de lonc, et .ij. dois de large;	and have two heads, two pliers, as you see, one palm length, and two fingers wide;
et quant tu vues ovrir la marris a tout l’estrument, si fai seoir la femme sor .i. lit, les piez pendant et les jambes overtes,	and when you see opening the matrix (of childbirth), make the woman sit on one bed, legs apart and knees opened,
puis boute les .ij. ajostemens ajostez ensamble en la marris, et tien le chief de l’estrument desoz entre ses cuixes;	Then push the two jaws together, close them together in the mouth, and hold the head of the instrument beneath between the thighs;
puis oevre ta main a tout l’estrument, si com tu as fait as tenailles igalment, selonc la quantiteit que tu vues ovrir la bouche de la marris, tant que li baile faice ceu qu’elle vuet.	Then work your hand on the whole instrument, as you have done with the pliers equally, according to the quantity that you see to open the mouth of the jaws, until the patient does what he wants.
Cist estrument sont tuit sormontez, et sont multiplies lor semblances; et quant li mires les ait apareilliez, tant est plus hastans li oevre, et plus haute as homes por lor quantiteit.	This instrument is completely covered, and they are multiplied in their resemblances; and when the patient has arranged them, he works more quickly, and higher for men according to their size.
Si ne despire mie l’estrument que tu ne l’aies apparelliet, car lor necessitez n’est mie escusauble.	Do not unnecessarily discard the instrument you have prepared, for there is no excuse for its necessity.
Quant li secondine est retenue a l’enfantement, si covient que tu comandes a la malaide qu’ele reteigne son alaine, et puis la fai esternuer de condisi, et li estraint tes mains a la bouche et au neis;	When the afterbirth is retained during childbirth, you should instruct the woman to hold her breath and then make her vomit with a blow to the abdomen; next, hold her hands to the mouth and nose.
et s’elle saut per ceu, bien est.	if she jumps because of this, it is well.
Se ceu non, si prent .i. pot, et fai .i. pertus ou cuvercle, et i met herbes que puissent ovrir la bouche de la marris, si com calament, rue, anis, camomille, cassialigne et centoire;	If this does not work, take a pot and make a perforator or spoon, and put herbs that can open the mouth of the woman, such as calamint, rue, anise, camomile, chamomile, and centaurium;
toutes ces herbes, ou aucunes d’eles, soient cuites ou pot en aigue sus le feu; puis met une caine ou pertus dou pot, et l’autre chief en la bouche de la marris,	All these herbs, or some of them, should be cooked or boiled in water over fire; then put a tube or punctured pot at one end and the other end into the mouth of the patient.
et la teigne tant que li vapors viegne dedens la marris; puis la fai esternuer, si com nos avons dit.	And let the steam rise within the patient until the vapors arrive, then make them vomit as we have said.
Si saut li secondine hastanment.	If the second one (the patient) jumps up quickly.
Et s’elle remaint aprés ceste cure, et n’ist mie fuer, si comande a la baile qu’ele moille sa main senestre en oile de sesement ou en muscillaige de altee, et puis la boute en la nature,	And if the patient remains after this treatment and does not recover as commanded by the nurse, tell her to wet her left hand in oil of savin or in musk-essence of ambergris, and then apply it to the affected area.
et quiere la secondine; et quant elle l’avra trovee, si la preigne et l’estende poc et poc droitement, si que li marris ne chiece a l’estraction;	And who desires the seconding; and when he has found it, take it and extend it slowly straight, so that the male does not resist at the extraction;
mais la covient movoir legierement a destre et a senestre, et puis traie; si venra et se desaerdra.	But you must move it gently to left and right, then pull; it will come and will dislocate.
Et se li bouche de la marris est jai estrecie, nos avons dit la cure d’esternuer, et de fumigation des herbes;	If the male's orifice is strangled, we have said the cure for purging, and of fumigating with herbs;
et s’elle n’ist de tout ceu que nos avons dit, si garde que tu ne foloies au traire;	if it does not have any of that which we have said, then make sure you do not pull;
mais il couvient que ceu qui est a la bouche de la marris, que tu le lies a la cuixe de la femme, puis la clisterize d’oignement tetrafarmaçon;	But it is necessary that he who is at the mouth of the woman's womb, you tie him to the woman's thigh, then you clisterize with a four-medicine ointment.
si la porrira et remettra, et venra fuer; mais toutevoie, quant elle porrist si en vient male odor au stomac et au chief, et blece la malaide.	If it will pass through and be expelled, it will come out; but nevertheless, when she has passed it, if a bad smell comes to the stomach and head, and burns the patient.
Si covient donques fumigations covenaubles a ceu: aucun des anciens ont esproveit fumigation de cresson et de figues seches.	Therefore it is necessary that appropriate fumigation is provided for this: no one of the ancients has tested fumigation with dill and dried figs.
Li forme de l’estrument a coi on fumige la femme a la retenue des flors et de la secondine si est ceste:	The shape of the instrument with which one fumigates a woman to retain flowers and her afterbirth is as follows:
Et est de voirre semblant a une caine, et met on le chief subtil en la nature, et les chiés larges sus le feu;	And it resembles glass in shape, with a narrow neck in its nature and wide lips over the fire.
et soit li fumigations sus les charbons, et la teigne tant qu’elle soit gastee, et rencomence une autre.	and let the fumigation be over the embers, and let the tinder burn until it is consumed, and start another.
de percier lou fondement	of piercing the foundation
Maint enfant naissent qui n’ont mie le fondement perciet, ains l’ait estoupeit uns subtilz syfac:	Many children are born who do not have the foundation pierced, but rather it has been stopped up by a subtle obstruction.
si covient donques a la baile qu’ele perce celui syfac a son doit, et ne lou perce mie de spatumile agut, et garse le lacement qu’elle ne le touche;	Therefore it is necessary to give birth by piercing that obstruction at the appropriate time, and not with a sharp spatiule, and ensure that it does not touch the membrane.
puis met sus lainne moillie en vin et en oile, puis la cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez.	Then put moistened linen in wine and oil on it, then cure with an ointment until it is healed.
Et se tu doutes qu’il ne restoupe, si met ou pertus une caine de plonc, et li laisse mains jors, et soit ostee quant li enfes vuet aler en chambres.	And if you doubt that it will reopen, put a plug of wood in it and leave it for several days, and let it be removed when the child wants to go to bed.
Et aucune fois vient cist estoupemens de soudement de plaie ou d’aposteme; si covient coper celui soudement: si soit curez, si com nos avons dit de la caine de plonc.	And sometimes this sudden swelling of wound or abscess occurs; it should be covered: whether it is to be cauterized, as we have said about the lime of lead.
de la fistule dou fondement	of the fistula from the bottom
Fistules qui vienent desoz le fondement sont nodation, et groissor que vienent delez lou fondement defuer, ou en l’espaice des .ij. parties,	Fistulas that come from below the foundation are nodules, and those that come out above the foundation or in between two parts,
si a une fistule ou plusors; et quant celle nodation est anciene, si aoeuvre, et encort moistor awouse blainche ou subtilz bowe,	If it has a fistula or more than one; and when the swelling is old, if it is opened, and moisture awakens pus or thin pustules,
et aucune fois sont ces fistule persans; et sont conues par ceu qu’il en ist ou egestion ou ventositeit quant li malaide fait egestion, et par aventure en saut uns vers.	And sometimes these fistulas are persistent; and they are recognized by those who are familiar with either the discharge or wind when the patient has discharge, and by chance it jumps one direction or another.
Et si a fistules que percent jusc’a la vessie, et jusc’a la moitiet de la verge; et parvienent jusc’a la jointure de la cuixe, et jusc’a nout de la kowe.	And if there are fistulas that penetrate to the bladder, and halfway down the penis; they reach the joint of the thigh, and to the knee of the cow.
Et ensi conoist on la fistule persant au fondement, et ne mie persant:	And so one recognizes the fistula persistent at its base, but not non-persistent:
et est que tu boutes ton doi indice ou fondement, et boute une aguille subtil d’arain ou de fer en la fistule quant il n’i a tortuositeit.	and it is that you bite your thumb joint or base, and insert a fine awl of iron or steel into the fistula when there is no twist to it.
Et s’il ait tortuositeit, si i boute une tente de plonc subtil, ou .i. poil de cheval, tant que tu sentes la tente ou le poil a ton doit;	If it has a twist, then insert a thin splint or horsehair until you feel the splint or hair at your thumb.
et se tu ne le sens, et il ne vient dou pertus egestion ne ventositeit ne ver, si com nos avons dit:	and if you do not feel it, and it does not bring forth pus, wind, or worms, as we have said:
saiches qu’elle ne perce mie; si te haste dou curer.	Know that it does not pierce at all; hasten to cure it.
Et quant li fistule est persans jusc’a la vessie ou jusc’a conduit de l’urine, si en saut li urine, et ne puet soudeir par medicines.	And when the fistula extends to the bladder or the channel of urine, if it bursts and cannot be healed by medicines.
S’elle est percie jusc’a la jointure de la cuixe, si est li tente venans jusc’au leu;	If it is pierced at the junction of the calf, then the tendons come to the surface.
s’il n’i a tortuositeit et li invention de la dolor entor, si est qu’il en ist adés bowe, et n’i vaut medicine ne soudement par oignement;	If it is not twisted and the pain is around it, then it is always bent, and no medicine nor poultice helps.
et en ces fistules persans n’a point de cure fuer que labor, et vaniteit des folz mires qui s’en entremettent.	And in these Persian blisters, there is no cure but labor, and the empty vanity of foolish physicians who meddle with them.
En celle qui n’est mie persans et n’est mie anciene, a esperance de saniteit par fer, si com j’ai esproveit,	In those which are neither Persian nor ancient, hoping for health by iron, as I have experienced,    \*Note: The term "ancien" can mean "old", but in this context it may refer to an open wound or sore rather than the age of the patient.
et est que li malaides gise entre tes mains sus son dos; et li lieve les jambes jusque sus ses cuixes, et ait ses cuixes enclinees a son ventre;	and it is that the patient lies between your hands on his back; and lift his legs up to his thighs, and have his thighs inclined towards his stomach;  \*Note: The terms "ventre" can mean "stomach" but in this context it likely refers to the abdomen or belly.
puis boute une tente d’arain, ou de plonc s’il i a tortuositeit, tant que tu saiches ou li tente vient.	Then push a tent of reed, or plank if there is curvature, as long as you know where the tent comes from.
Se li malaides la sent entor le fondement, si covient que tu i boutes ton doi indice,	If the patient feels it around the foundation, then you must push your finger into it,
se sens adonques que li tente l’ait perciet; et soit descoverte ou tu sens entre ton doit le syfac ou la char, adonques saiches qu’elle est persans;	If you feel that the tent has been pierced; and it is exposed where you feel a hole or flesh, then you know it is pierced.
si n’i travillier mie c’on ne la puet saner.	If one does not work on it, it cannot be healed.
On dist toutevoie c’on em puet bien saner aucuns, mais ce avient poc;	It is said that one can heal some, but this happens rarely;
et li aide c’on i fait, si est c’on eschaufe le cautere subtil selonc la largesce de la fistule, si com il est devant dit;	and the help that is given, if it is done, is to heat the cautery subtle according to the width of the fistula, as mentioned before;
et le boute tout chaut en la fistule, tant qu’il viegne delez le fondement; et faice ceu .ij. fois ou .iij., tant que tu saiches que ces chars fautrees soient arses, qui sont semblant a une penne d’oiseil;	and put the heated cautery completely in the fistula until it reaches its foundation; and do this two or three times until you know that these small fibrous growths are burned, which resemble a bird's feather;
et puis le cure de tentes moillies em burre, tant que celle chars isse fuer, puis le cure d’oignement enjanrant char et soudant.	And then treat the wound with softened tents moistened in butter, until the inflammation subsides, then treat it with an ointment soothing and healing.
S’il est ensi sanez, c’est bien. Se ceu, nom autrement ne puet estre sanez;	If it is thus healed, that is good. But if it cannot be healed otherwise;
et se li tente entre, et ne perce jusc’au doit qui est ou fondement, et a entre ton doi et la tente une coverture espesse de char ou de syfac, et tu vois la fistule a ceu qui enseut la coverture dou keur;	and if it breaks open, not all the way to the underlying foundation, and cover between your finger and the wound with a thick layer of fat or silk, and you see the fistula where the covering is damaged.
si le cope des l’encomencement de la fistule, et boute adés avant la tente, et pues le cautere aprés, tant qu’il viegne au chief de la tente;	If the head of the fistula at its beginning, presses forward towards the tent and then apply the fire cautery afterwards until it reaches the tip of the tent.
et sera delivré li tente, et cherra; puis mondefie celles chars fautrees que semblent une penne d’oisel, et n’en remaigne niant.	and the tent will be released, and burnt; then remove those charred pieces that seem like a feather of a bird, and nothing remains.
Et si li sans te vaint, et cort entre toi et l’uevre, si le cauterize de feu ou de medicine ague.	And if the sinew swells and splits apart, cauterize it with fire or medicine.
Car li cauteres de feu assemble .ij. bones choses: c’est a savoir, l’arsure de ces chars ajostees, et l’esteinchement de sanc et la sechor de la moistor;	The fire cautery gathers two good things: namely, the burning of these charred joints and the stopping of blood flow and the drying out of moisture.
puis le cure de tentes moillies em burre ou en choz broiez, tant que li leus giete bowe, et isse fuer li chars arse en la bowe;	then the treatment for damp tents with butter or crushed cheese, until the limbs become hard, and the charred joints are burned in the fire.
puis cure la plaie des oignemens soudans enjanrans dure char, et sont les medicines seches.	then treat the wound of onion juice boiled hard char, and these medicines are dry.
Car quant il est restoree, si est sanee et ne revient mie.	When it is treated, it heals and does not return.
Et se fistule vient jusc’a parfont dou fondement, et est esloigniez dou cors, se li boute ton doi ou fondement, et enquier ceu.	And if a fistula reaches down to the bottom of its foundation and is separated from the body, push your finger into it or its foundation, and examine it.
Se tu sens la tente, et entre .ij. est li toile ou li syfac ou chars, ou il est pres a percier, si n’i ait fuers que voie de fiance et d’esperance, par l’aministrement de l’une des .iii. manieres:	If you feel a swelling and enter between 2 layers or the skin or flesh where it is about to pierce, but there is no way out except for a path of faith and hope, through one of the three methods of administration:
ou tu le cauterizes si com nos avons dit, ou tu le cope jusc’a fons, ou se tu pues si i met tentes et cure si com premier;	or you can cauterize it as we have said, or cut it open to the bottom, or if it is a boil, treat it and heal it as we have described in the beginning.
et n’aler mie trop em parfont, que tu ne coper le tenement qui tient le fondement, et viegne li egestions par lai sens volenteit;	And do not go too deep that you do not cover the foundation's support, and let the evacuation come through the body by natural desire;
puis le cure, si com nos avons dit;	then heal, as we have said;
par aventure si sera sanez, ou tu esloigne celle coverture et la munde puis qu’elle est copee delez lou fondement, ou par tente ou par autre estrument apointé;	In case it becomes healthy, then remove the cover and clean it after it is cut away from the foundation, either by force or another instrument pointed;
puis mondefie cele char fautree qui est en la plaie, tant com tu pues;	Then clean the charred material that is in the wound, as much as you can;
puis estudie a restorer la plaie, et a demorer la fistule en la partie defuers le fondement: si iert plus legiere chose au malaide.	Then study to heal the wound, and keep the fistula in the part distant from the foundation; this will be easier for the patient.
Et aucune fois sont fistules selonc ceste maniere: et est quant tu boutes la tente en la fistule, et elle est ou costeit dou fondement delez lou cuir desus,	And sometimes there are fistulas in this manner: and it is when you insert the probe into the fistula, and it is where it touches the foundation of the skin above,
si pren une tente percie au chief selonc ceste forme:	If you take a probe pierced at the head in this manner:
Et i boute .i. fil tort en .ij., et boute la tente a tout le fil en la fistule tant qu’il soit au chief.	And insert one threaded wire in two, and insert the sheath to the entire length of the wire into the fistula until it reaches its end.
S’elle est persans en la marge dou fondement dedens, adonc estrai lou fil de celui pertus, ensi que tu boutes ton doi ou fondement;	If it is perforated at the edge of the foundation within, then pull out the thread from that one, thus insert your hand or foundation;
et trai le chief dou fil, et assemble les .ij. chiés ensamble, et estraint l’un a l’autre, et le laisse .i. jor ou .ij.;	Pull the head out with the wire, and join the two heads together, and pull one against the other, and leave it for one day or two;
et le restraint aucune fois, tant que li filz cope ces chars que sont entre dous, et chiecent;	And it holds any movement, until the children squeeze those things that are between them, and they burst.
puis cure la plaie tant qu’elle soit soudee et sanee.	Then heal the wound until it is healed and healthy.
Se li fistule ne perce, si la fai percier en toutes les manieres que tu pues, s’ele n’est trop em parfont.	If the fistula does not pierce itself, make it pierce in all possible ways, if it is not too full.
Car il ne covient mie faire por le lacement coper si em parfont, et puis le cure, si com nos avons dit, tant qu’il soit sanez.	Because it should not be covered too full for the ligation, and then healed as we have said, until it is healthy.
Li forme dou spatumile espinous dont on fent la fistule si est mout agus d’une, part et trenchans;	The shape of a spurlike spine from which a fistula is made is very sharp at one end and cutting.
et d’autre part non, por ceu c’on ne cope mie ceu c’on ne doit mie copeir, si com tu vois ci:	and not the other end, because you should not strike where you should not, as you can see here:
des emorroydes	piles of hemorrhoids
Emorrydes sont selonc ij. manieres: ou elles sont dedens le fondement, ausi com grain de resin, et s’en i a petites et grans, et en cort adés sanc,	Hemorrhoids come in two forms: either they are located inside the foundation, like a piece of resin, and there are small and large ones, and on the outside there is blood.
et s’en i a une ou plusors, et sont defuer le fondement et au chief dou fondement; mais celles qui sont defuer si ont poc de moistor,	And if there is one or more [dislocations], and they are dislodged from their foundation and the base of the foundation; but those that are dislodged have little moisture,
et encort adés ou un poc d’aigue citrine ou un poc de sanc, et ont la color dou cors;	and there is always a little amount of citron juice or blood, and they [the affected limbs] have the color of the body;
et li cure de ces qui les ont dedens le fondement, si est que tu comandes au malaide qu’il s’espreigne por aleir en chambres, tant que li fondemens li isse fuer, et c’aperent li filz;	and the cure for those with dislocations within the foundation, is that you instruct the patient to lie down on their bed, until the foundation recovers, and this can be observed by the son.
si te haste, et le pent as tenailles, ou tu le tien a ton ungle, puis le cope en ses racines;	hurry, and hold it with pliers or your fingernail, then strike at its roots;
et se li uncine ne les pueent tenir por ses moistors, si les prent a .i. drapeil, ou a couton, ou d’une piece de chamelot;	And if the joint cannot be held by moisture, take either linen cloth or cotton, or a piece of gauze;
et les estrai a tes dois, puis les cope, et poudre desus aucunes chaudes poudres que soient en leu de cautere;	and straighten it with your hands, then press and powder some hot powders that are used instead of fire cautery;
ou tu les cauterize si com il est dit ou chapistre de cautere, puis les cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez;	or cauterize them as the cautery chapter says, then cure them with other treatments until they heal.
et se li fondemens ne puet issir, si clisterize le malaide de clistere mordant et aspre por laver ceu qui est ou fondement, si qu’il puist issir apertement;	and if the foundation cannot come out, cleanse the patient with biting and sharp clisterium to wash the area where the foundation is, so that it comes out openly.
cant li malaides se preint, et se li fil sont fuer dou fondement, si est li cure legiere;	The patient must take care, and if his veins are too deeply pierced, the treatment is easy.
et est que tu les preignes a ton ungle ou as tenailles, et les cope, puis les cure si com nos avons dit, tant qu’il soit sanez, et qu’il redoute l’incision par fer.	And you grasp them with your fingernail or tweezers and crush them, then treat them as we have said, until they are healed and fear the incision with iron.
Si covient que tu amenistre la costure selonc ceste maniere: pren .i. fil tort, et le boute en une aguille, et puis trai le fil au desus et fai percier l’aguille d’autre part, et torne les .ij. chiez dou fil desoz l’aguille,	You must apply the stitching in this manner: take a twisted thread and insert it into a needle, then pull the thread above and pierce the needle from the other side, and twist the two threads below the needle.
et si soit dou large; et estraint le fil forment, puis noe le fil, et estrai l’aguille, et fai ensi de toz les autres, et en laisse .i. por corre la superfluiteit dou sanc;	and make it wide; then bind the thread tightly, knot the thread, draw out the needle, and do the same with all the others, leaving one to tie off excess blood.
puis met sus le fondement .i. drapeil moilliet en oile roset ou en cerote, et met sus le fondement, et comande au malaide k’il repose;	Then place a soft cloth soaked in rose oil or cerote on the foundation, and place it there, and instruct the patient to rest.
et puis le laisse tant qu’il chiecent, et quant il seront cheut, si les cure d’oignement et d’autre cure, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And then leave it until it drips, and when it stops, if he cures it with ointment and other remedies, until it is healed.
dou sechement dou fiens ou fondement	the drying of the fire or foundation.
Maintes fois avient sechement de fiens en l’intestine, et par constrignement de nature, et quant li maladie est vielle et medicine n’i vaut.	Often, there is drying in the intestines due to fire and by the nature of constraint, and when the disease is old and medication does not work.
Si covient que tu reses a la point d’un spatumile ou a ton ungle l’escorce desus, qui ne le laisse a moistir;	It is necessary that you pierce with a splint or your nail the bark above, so as not to let it moisten.
puis le cure tant qu’il soit sodez si com il covient;	then heal it until it dries as required;
et s’il ne puet soder, si rencomence la rasure plus fort que devant, tant qu’il saine mout, et soit escorchiez;	and if it cannot dry, renew the shaving more forcefully than before, until it heals well, and be barked;
puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	then heal it until it is healed.
dou fremit	The trembling (or shuddering)
Formice est une petite apparance fautree antor le cors, et va mout em parfont;	Louse is a small growth that comes before the body and goes deep in;
et aucune fois la trueve li frois, et le sent on ausi comme mort de fremit, et vient en tout le cors, et plus as mains que autre part.	And sometimes the trout (or eel) bites, and it is felt as if one were dying from trembling, and it comes over the entire body, but more on the hands than other parts.
Et li cure si est que tu pren une cainne d’une penne d’oie, ou une penne de vultul fort, et met celle caine sus le fremit, tant que li cercles porpreigne le fremit tot entor;	And the cure is that you take a cane of an owl's feather or a strong eagle's feather and place it on the trembling part, until the purple circles encompass the trembling part entirely;
puis torne ta main a tout la cainne tant que tu copes tout entor le fremit, et le met em parfont, et esraiche le fremit de ses racines.	Then turn your hand along the entire cane until you cover the trembling part entirely, and press it deeply, and dry up the trembling part from its roots.
Et se tu vues, si fai ceu d’une caine d’arain ou de fer selonc ceste forme, et soit subtilz desoz et traians desus:	If you wish, do it with a cane of iron or steel in this form and be subtle underneath and traverse above:   In the medieval context, "subtle underneath" probably means intricate or delicate, while "traverse above" likely refers to applying pressure from above. ne mie perciet, por mues tenir au doi, et mues presser Et se tu vues, si cauterize lou fremit, si com il est devant ou chapistre de cautere.	Do not pierce, instead hold it tight and press. And if you wish, cauterize the quivering, as described in the chapter on cauterization.
de la forme dou clistere	The form of the cluster.
Aucune fois fait on clistere d’argent ou d’archaut, ou d’arain fondut ou mailliet; et aucune fois fait on de ces estrumens petis et grans, selonc ces a cui il sont amenistrez.	Sometimes one makes the cluster of silver or iron, or melted tin or wax; and sometimes makes these tools small and large, according to those for whom they are prepared.
Cil donques c’on amenistre en la cure des enfans et qui sont foible et dolorous, sont petis.	Therefore, the ones that are brought in the treatment of infants and those who are weak and suffering, are small.
Li forme dou clistere petit et grant si est desus large, ou li ventres est liiez selonc ceste maniere:	The form of a clister (small or large) is above wide, where the bellies are tied in this manner:
et i ait une desevrance ou li ventres soit liiez, si com tu vois, et li chiez soit dedens perciez; et ait a l’un des costez .ij. pertus, et en l’autre .i.;	and there should be an opening where the bellies are tied, as you see, and the cheeks should be pierced from within; and on one side there should be two holes, and in the other one;
et soit li ventres ou om met les medicines d’une vessie de beste ou de parchemin, et soit perciez tout entor de menus pertus,	and let the belly or ointment for the medicines of a beast's bladder or parchment be placed within, and it should be pierced all around with small holes,
et ait entre chescun pertus .i. doit d’espaice, puis boute en ces pertus .i. fil fort de fil crut tort en .x. ou enqui entor, et assemble le ventre si com est une chievre;	And fill in each wound, that is to say, it should have some space between them, then push into these wounds, that is, a strong thread made of twisted thread in ten or twelve [stitches] around, and bind the belly as if it were a goat's pouch.
et quant li medicine est dedens, si la lie a l’estrument devant d’un fil fort, puis clisterize; et c’est li forme dou cercle:	And when the medicine is inside, tie it with a strong thread to the instrument in front, then apply a plaster; and this is the shape of a circle.
Et soit li medicine ne trop chaude ne trop froide, et oint le chief dou clistere d’oile ou d’aubun d’uef, ou de semblant chose, puis le boute ens legierement;	Let the medicine neither be too hot nor too cold, and oil or egg yolk should be applied to the head of the plaster, or something similar, then gently insert it.
puis l’espreigne li ministres a ses .ij. mains ensamble, tant qu’il soit toz vuis, puis estrai lou clistere, et lieve li malaides ses jambes a la paroit,	Then the ministers should grasp the patient's two hands together until they are fully visible, then pull out the plaster, and wash the patient's legs at the opening.
et se li medicine vuet issir, si la teigne tant com il puet; et s’il dort une nuit atot, si est plus grans aide.	And if the medicine appears to come out, pull it as much as possible; and if it does not move for an entire night, it is more beneficial.
Et se tu le clisterizes em maladie de decorrement de ventre, et li medicine se haste d’issir, si le rencomence tant qu’il soit sanez.	If you plaster the patient with belly distention caused by intestinal blockage and the medicine starts to come out, renew it until it becomes healthy.
Et se li emorroide sont ou fondement, ou aposteme, si soit li clistere ausi subtilz com por .i. enfant;	And if the hemorrhoids are founded or abscessed, or even the rectum [cleansing], let it be as subtle as for a child;
et c’est li forme dou clistere subtil sus coi li cuir soit estraint:	and this is the shape of the subtle enema where the skin should be stretched:
des plaies	wounds (plural)
Nos avons jai dit en la division la cure des plaies; or vos dirons les cures de mains et de medicine, selonc l’acomplissement.	We have said in the division the treatment of wounds; and we shall tell you about the treatments of hands and medicines, according to their completion.
Je dis que les plaies sont diverses selonc ceu qu’elles sont faites, et selonc les leus ou les plaies sont faites, et de coi elles sont faites.	I say that wounds are various according to what they are made, and according to the places where the wounds are made, and of how they are made.
Les choses par coi plaies sont faites sont par gitement de piere, et taille d’espee et de couteil, ou de lance ou de fust ou de siette, ou de semblans choses;	The things by which wounds are made are by piercing with a spear, cutting with a sword or knife, or a lance or mace or similar objects;
ou que sont faites selonc les leus dou cors, si com plaie que chiet sus le col, ou sus le chief, ou le peis, ou le ventre, ou le foie, et semblans membres;	or according to the parts of the body, such as a wound that falls on the neck, or the head, or the side, or the belly, or the liver, and similar limbs;
et je vos dirai la cure de chescune plaie, et encomencerai as plaies dou chief simples, car li remenbrance venra en son chapistre.	And I will tell you the treatment for each wound, starting with wounds of the head, as the remembrance will come in its chapter.
Je dis que quant simple plaie vient ou chief, et li os n’est brisiez, si pren garde se c’est de gitement de piere ou de semblans choses, et li cuir est toutevoie rompus et est li plaie grans,	If the wound is simple in the head and the bone is not broken, beware if it comes from an arrow or similar things, and the skin is completely torn and the wound is large.
et tu doutes levement d’aposteme chaut: si le fai tantost sainier de la cephalique meismement s’il vient poc de sanc de la plaie, et soit li sainie au contraire de la partie navree;	And if you have doubt about the abscess, let it rise: if it is filled with pus from the wound itself, cleanse it immediately from the head side of the wound. If on the contrary, it fills with pus from the injured part, cleanse it in the opposite direction of the injury;
et eschuisse li malaides repletion de vin et de viandes grosses.	And let the patient empty himself of wine and heavy foods.
Et s’il ne vuet sainier, si soit amenuisie sa viande, et ne boive point de vin, ne ne menjuce point de char;	If he does not want to urinate, his food should be reduced, and he should neither drink wine nor eat meat.
et met sor la plaie, se apostemes chaus i vient, coton moilliet en oile roset soulement, ou en vin stiptice;	Place cotton soaked only in rose oil or vinegar steeped on the abscess if it comes.
et s’il n’i a aposteme chaut, si met sus la plaie, s’elle est fresche a tout son sanc, et elle n’est muee par l’air, poudre, que je dirai un poc ci aprés;	And if there is no abscess formed yet, place it [the substance] on the wound, if it is fresh with all its blood, and it is not affected by air or powder, I shall say a little more about it shortly.
et se li ars l’ait muee, si met sus aucuns oignemens, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the worms have moved it [the substance], place some ointments upon it until it is healed.
Et se li plaie est grans si com de tailleure d’espee et de semblans, et les levres ne se pueent assembler par tentes, si les assemble par cousture, si com je dirai as plaies dou ventre, de la costure.	If the wound is large like a sword and similar, and the lips cannot be brought together by pressing, bring them together by stitching, as I shall say about abdominal wounds, in stitching.
Se li plaie est descoverte de l’os, et pent, et ne tient mais que a un poc, si le cope; puis cure la plaie de medicine, et restoure char dure en leu de cuir,	If the wound is exposed of the bone, and it gapes, and does not hold but only slightly, then press [it]; afterwards, treat the wound with medicine, and restore hard flesh in place of skin.
et comande au malaide a mengier grosses viandes, si com testes et froment cuit, ausi com poulz, et semblans choses.	Instruct the patient to eat thick meats, such as cooked heads [of animals] and bread, also pulses, and similar things.
Et se tu trueves ou cuir porriture, et il n’aert a l’os, si cope lou porrit tot, et giete fuer, puis le cure;	And if you find or suspect putrid flesh, not touching the bone, press it completely, and pour boiling water over it, then treat [it].
et se il ait artere en la plaie ou voine, dont sans cort, et il ne puet estainchier par medicines, si quier l’artere, et se tu la trueves desloie, si la lie d’un fil;	And if there is an artery in the wound or vein, which without stitching cannot be stopped, you may need to tie it off; and if you find it dislocated, tie it with a thread.
et se ceu ne profite mie, si la cauterize.	And if that does not help, cauterize it.
Et se ces plaies sont petites et simples, si est li cure legiere: et est que tu mettes ens ceste poudre qui soude ainsois que li ars l’ait muee.	And if these wounds are small and simple, the cure is light; place this powder on it as soon as the arsenic has made it harden.
Et li maniere de la poudre si est: pren encens une partie; sanc de dragon .ij. parties; chalz vive .iij. parties, et le poudre subtilment,	And the method of the powder is as follows: take an equal part of incense; two parts of dragon's blood; four parts of quicklime and grind them finely together.   ~= And the manner of making the powder is as follows: take one part of incense; two parts of dragon's blood; four parts of quicklime, and grind them finely together.
et emple la plaie, et l’estraint forment, tant qu’elle s’aerse bien et se joigne a tout son sanc;	And apply the wound, and hold it open shaped, until it heals well and joins with all its blood.
et puis la lie bien, et la laisse sens desliier, s’elle n’enfle; car on n’oste la madicine tant qu’ele soit sanee.	Then bind it well, and let it heal by itself if it does not swell; for medicine is not removed while it is healed.
Et aucune fois fait on ceu de chalz soulement, quant on n’ait l’encens ne lou sanc de dragon, mais que li ars n’ait muee la plaie.	And sometimes they do this with only calcined substances, when they do not have incense or the blood of a dragon, but the wound has not healed.
Et se li ars ait mueit la plaie, meismement en esteit, si n’i met om mie ceste poudre;	If the wound has already healed, in any case do not put this powder on it.
