Je fui apelez a une femme malaide, et me descovrit som bras, et vis une petite enfleure en la voinne dou brais;	I was called to a sick woman, and she revealed her arm to me, and I saw a small swelling in the vein of the arm;
et .i. poc aprés, li vis monter ausi com un ver a l’espaule,	and later, it rose like a worm towards the shoulder,
plus tost que nulle chose, ausi com vif argent quant il cort de leu a autre;	sooner than anything else, just as living silver cuts from its source;
li dolor se departit de celui leu, et se ficha en l’espaule,	The pain spreads from that place and pierces the shoulder.
et puis un poc aprés corrut par tout le cors, tant qu’ele vint en l’autre brais;	And a little later it runs through the entire body, until it comes to the other arm;
puis me contait qu’elle tornioit adés entor le cors, si com je la vis.	And then he told me that it returned again around the body, as I saw.
Je me mervillai mout coment elle se movoit ensi de membre em membre, car je n’avoie onques veut ceste maladie selonc ceste maniere.	I wondered greatly how it moved thus from limb to limb, for I have never seen this sickness in such a manner.
Toutevoie, je avoie veut maint que bien avoient veut movoir dolor de leu a autre,	Nevertheless, I had often heard that pain moved from place to another,
mais je ne l’avoie mie veut, si com je le vis en la femme;	but I had never seen it happen, as I did in the woman;
et je me pensai que c’estoit por ceu que li femme avoit sec cors, et les voinnes descovertes,	And I thought it was because the woman had a dry body and exposed veins.
et por ceu apparoit celle ventositez constrainte;	and for this reason that condition appears constricted.
et n’aperent mie selonc ceste raison a ces qui sont delicious, et qui ont moistes cors et voinnes reponues.	and it does not appear according to this reason to those who are luxurious, and who have moist bodies and covered veins.
Et quant tu vues curer ceste maladie, et li malaides sent celle dolor, s’elle t’apert si com nos avons dit,	And when you see treating this disease, and the patient feels that pain, if it opens as we have said,
si la lie desus et desoz hastanment, et puis cope sus tant que cele ventositez constrainte au leu isse fuer;	If the ligament above and below presses together tightly, and then push up until the windpipe is compressed to its proper place.
et cauterize le leu; et se tu ne la vois a tes eulz,	And cauterize the site; and if you do not see it with your eyes,
si le cure de ceu qui deboute les ventositez, si com pilules fetides, et pilules de serapin, et semblans autres.	use medicines that help to move the windpipe, such as pills made from poppy seeds, and serapin pills, and similar others.
Des saiettes	Arrows
Les saiettes sont diverses, selonc lor semblances et selonc les leus dou cors ou elles chient.	Arrows are varied according to their appearance and the parts of the body where they strike.
Li diversitez de lor si est qu’il i a de celles qui ont grans pointes, et petites, et chevees, et soudees;	The differences among them are that some have large points, small ones, pointed or flat-headed, and those that are bound.
et de celles qui ont .ij. angles, et de celz qui ont lengues, et de celles ou il a pieces;	and of those with two prongs, and of those with tongues, and of those with splinters.
et celle qui chiet en aucun membre si chiet selonc .ij. manieres: ou en membre principeil cheveit,	and an arrow that strikes any member does so in two ways: either it strikes the principal member with its head,
si com cerveil, cuer, foie, pormon, rains, intestine, vessie, et semblans membres.	As marrow, heart, liver, spleen, kidneys, intestines, bladder, and similar organs.
Quant elle chiet donques en aucun leu de ces membres, et li signe de mort, que je te dirai ci aprés, t’aperent:	When it falls from any position of these organs, and the signs of death which I will tell you below will show you:
si covient que tu te warses de l’estraction de ceste saiette, car li mors vient aprés en plusors dispositions;	It is necessary that you beware of the extraction of this arrowhead, for death comes in many ways afterward.
et quant cist mal signe ne t’aperent mie, et li saiette n’est mie em parfont, si la trai, et cure la plaie.	and if this sign is not clear to you, and the arrowhead is not fully inserted, pull it out and treat the wound.
Et li signe dou cerveil quant li saiette i chiet et perce l’os, et saut li syfac fuer qui est sus le cerveil,	And the sign of the skull when the arrow pierces the bone, and the brain flees upwards which is above the skull,
est quant scotomie et sode et esvertin et roujor ens eulz, et enflammation et roujor de lengue, et spasme et permixtion d’entendement, et vomissemens de cole;	is when there is a hollowing out and softening and swelling of the eyes, and inflammation and redness of the tongue, and spasm and confusion of understanding, and vomiting of bile;
et per aventure ist sans fuer des narines, ou des oreilles; et par aventure pert la parole et la voix;	and possibly without sweat from the nostrils or ears; and possibly losing speech and voice;
et saut de la plaie moistor blanche semblant a poulz, et en saut ausi com bruee de char;	And from the wound leaps white moisture resembling pus, and it jumps also like boiling oil;
et se cist signe t’aperent, si te tien de la cure, et trai la saiette s’elle n’est ens.	If this sign appears, beware of the treatment, and draw out the arrow if it is not in [the wound].
Li signe de la siette quant elle chiet ou cuer, sont qu’elle est pres de la mamele senestre, et sent ausi com s’elle estoit fichie en chose dure, ne mie vuide;	The sign of the arrow when it falls or pierces [the flesh] is that it is near the left nipple, and feels as if it has been driven into a hard thing, not empty.
et par aventure li siette se muet ausi com li poulz, et en cort noir sanc, et vient froidor et suor froide, et sincope:	And by chance the arrow may become soft like pus, and it will bleed black blood, and bring coldness and cold sweat, and fainting.
saiches adonc sens doute ke li mors dessent.	Therefore, one must know without doubt that death is near.
Et li signe de la saiette que nevre lou pormon est que sans plains d’escume saut de la plaie, et li gorge enfle, et li malaides mue color, et sospire haut et quiert le froit ar.	The sign of an arrowhead that has pierced the flesh is when there is no bubbling of pus from the wound, and the throat inflates, and the patient turns pale and sighs deeply and seeks cold air.
Et se li saiette chiet en la coverture dou pis, si est delez les petites costes; et giete grant alainne et grant dolor et sospire; et li muevent tuit li membre des espaules.	If the arrowhead falls into the bedclothes of the patient, it has passed through the ribs; and it causes great pain and sighing, and moves all the limbs of the shoulders.
Et se li saiette chiet ou stomac, par aventure si saut de la plaie aucune chose de la viande indigeste.	If the arrowhead falls into the stomach, it may cause something undigested to escape from the wound.
Et se li saiette chiet ou ventre, et en saut point de fien par l’intestine rout, si n’a point d’esperance en la cure, ne en l’estraction de la saiette.	And if the arrow strikes or pierces the belly, and it does not jump out through the intestine hole, there is no hope in the cure, nor in the extraction of the arrow.
Et se li saiette chiet en la vessie, et li urine en saut et vient defuer, et li malaides sent fort dolor: saiches que li plaie est mortelz.	If the arrow strikes into the bladder and the urine jumps out and runs away, and the patient feels strong pain: know that the wound is deadly.
Li autre membre, si com li faice et li colz et li gorge et li espaule et li adjutoire et li espinee dou dos et li forcele et li cuixe et les jambes, et li membre semblant, sont sauf selonc plusors dispositions.	The other member, such as the hand and arm, neck, shoulder, armpit, spine of the back, wrist, hip, legs, and similar parts, are safe according to various conditions.
Quant li saiette est en lou nerf ou l’artere, et elle n’est venimouse, si com je vos dirai qu’il m’avint, por ceu que vos faciez autretel.	When the arrow is in the nerve or the artery, and it is not venomous, as I will tell you what happened to me, do this instead.
Il avint a .i. home c’une saiette li chut ou larmier en la racine dou neis:	Once there was a man whose arrow hit or wounded the root of the nose:
je la tentai, et la traï d’autre part desoz la graisse de l’oreille, et fut sanez sens nusement.	I pulled it out from the other side below the ear fat and it came out senselessly.
Et traï a un jeu une saiette que li chut en la graisse de l’oil desoz la papiere desoz,	I took out a game arrow that hit in the fat under the oil below the paper (?).
et li saiette estoit reponue, et n’en poi ataindre que la pointe devers lou fust,	And the arrow was withdrawn, but could not reach beyond its shaft point.
et estoit li saiette grans d’un arc turcois, a tout .i. fer legier sens oreilles; li jeus fut sanez, et ne li vint nulz mavais accidens.	And the arrow was large, of a Turkish bow, with a sharp point suitable for ears; it pierced through, and no ill accident came upon it.
Et traï une saiette de la gorge a un crestien, et estoit li saiette arabique a oreilles:	And the arrow passed from the throat of a Christian, and the arrow was Arabic with pointed ears.
je soiai les barbions, et subtiliai tant que je la traï, et fut sanez li crestiens.	I was barbered, and skillfully extracted it, and the Christian survived.
Et traï une saiette a .i. home, que li estoit cheue ou ventre, et pensai qu’il moroit;	And take an arrow out of a man who was shot or stabbed, and I thought he would die;
et puis qu’il ot passez .xxx. jors, si ne mua point sa disposition;	and after thirty days, his condition did not change;
je taillai sus la saiette, et l’engignai, et la traï fuer, et n’ot point de mavais accident.	I cut above the arrow, bent it, extracted it, and had no adverse effects.
Et si vis .i. home cui une saiette chut ou dos, et fut li plaie soudee sus;	If a man has an arrow lodged in his back, and the wound is sutured above;
et demora li saiette dedens li, et ne chainja point ses dispositions naturez,	And the arrow remained inside [the body], and did not change its position naturally.
ne ne trova nuisement en aucune de ses oevres naturelz.	It does not find any harm in any of its natural functions.
Et vis .i. autre homme, cui il chut une saiette en sa faice, et fut soudee li plaie;	And a man, to whom an arrow struck in his body, and the wound was sutured.
et demora ensi sens soffrir grant dolor; et mout d’autres semblans.	And remained thus without suffering great pain; and many other similar things happened.
Et traï une saiette a .i. home des princes le roi, que li estoit cheue enmi lou neiz,	And draw an arrow from a knight of the king who was stuck in the snow.
et estoit un poc declinans a la destre partie; et estoit li saiette toute reponue	and it was slightly tilted to the right side; and the arrow was completely reversed.
Je fui apelez a la cure aprés ceu qu’elle fut cheue .iij. jors. Si trovai la plaie mult estroite.	I was called for treatment after it had been stuck for three days. I found the wound to be very narrow.
Je la quis a tout une subtil tente, et ne la sentis mie;	I probed it all with a thin probe, and felt nothing.
et il sentoit pointure et dolor desoz sa destre oreille.	And he feels sharp pain beneath his right ear.
Je pensai que c’estoit de la pointe de la saiette	I thought it was the tip of the arrowhead.
Je mis sus lou leu emplaustre atratifet digestif, por ceu que li leus n’enflast;	I placed him on a soft cushion, as he did not swell.
et m’aparut li leus de la saiette.	And the arrow appeared to be protruding from the wound.
Je i mis l’emplaustre mains jors, et resouda li plaie derechief, et demora ensi li malaides lonc tens,	I place the plaster on the wound daily, and heal the wound directly, and keep the patient for a long time.
tant qu’il sentit la saiette .i. jor dedens son neis; et il le me dist.	until he feels the arrowhead inside his body for a day; then tell him this.
Je mis sus la plaie medicine ague corrosive par mains jors, tant qu’elle fut overte,	I apply the wound with corrosive medicine for several days, until it is healed.
et la tentai, et sentis le chief de la saiette qui s’aerdoit au leu;	And I pulled, and felt the head of the arrow sticking at its place;
puis ajostai en l’overture de la plaie par celle medicine ague, tant que li chiés de la saiette m’aparut visablement;	then inserted into the wound opening with that medicine powder, until the head of the arrow became visible to me;
et trespassa bien li termines entor .iiij. mois,	and he passed well beyond the four-month limit.
et puis eslarja si li plaie que je i boutai les tenailles, et le meus d’une part et d’autre, et ne pot issir;	And then I spread open the wound that I had stitched, and stretched it from one side to another, but it could not heal.
adonques ne cessai de subtiliier et d’engignier de manieres d’estrumens, tant que je la pris .i. jor as tenailles bien faites,	Then I did not cease to refine and devise methods for tools, until I took a day to make the pliers well.
selonc ceu que sa forme venra en la fin de cest chapistre, tant que je la traï, et restourai la plaie.	According to its shape in the end of this chapter, while it heals, and I return the wound.
Et li mire jugent que li cartillaige dou nez ne puet restorer:	And they judge that the nose cartilage cannot be restored:
je la restourai adonques, et fut soudee li plaie, et fut sanez li malaides entierement.	I restored it then, and the wound was healed, and the patient was completely healthy.
Or t’ai dit la qualiteit de l’estraction d’aucunes saiettes,	And I have told you the quality of extracting some arrows,
si que tu mettes ta cure sus ceu que je ne dis mie, car li livres ne puet mie tout porprendre;	so that you may apply your remedy to this, for books cannot fully grasp everything.
mais li saiges maistres compere sus bien poc grant chose, et sus ceu que li est present et defaillant,	but wise masters can easily understand a little thing and what is present and failing.
trueve nueve oevre, et nuef estrument, au dessendement des choses estrainges qui avienent en cest art.	True, nine works and new instruments are required for this craft, especially in dealing with foreign things that may occur in this art.
Je dis que les saiettes n’issent des membres ou elles sont fichies fuer que selonc .ij. manieres:	I say that arrows do not come out of limbs where they are inserted except by two ways:
ou par lou leu ou elles entrent, ou par d’autre part;	or through the place where they entered, or from another side.
et celle que saut fuer par lai ou elle entre, c’est saiette entrans en leus charnus, et saut fuer aucune fois maintenant.	and that which goes out by the same place it entered is an arrow entering flesh, and occasionally comes out sometimes.
Et s’elle ne saut maintenant, si la laisse tant que li chars soit porrie entor, et soit alegie li issue;	And if it does not come out, leave it until the flesh is swollen around it, and make the opening even;
et ausi s’elle est fichie en l’os, et elle ne puet issir, si la laisse ensi aucuns jors, et la muef chescun jor;	And likewise if it [the dislocation] is embedded in the bone and cannot move out, leave it for some days and try to move it each day;
et adonques elle saut, et s’elle ne saut, si perce entor a tout .i. foret subtil, tant que li leus entor soit eslargiez, et puis la trai.	Then it jumps and if it does not jump, pierce around it all the way through with a sharp needle, only when the opening is widened, then pull it out.
Et se li saiette est fichie en l’os dou chief, et vait jusc’a l’un des ventres dou cerveil,	And if the arrow is lodged in the bone of the head and goes to one of the cavities of the brain,
et aucuns des accidens que j’ai dit apert au malaide: si ne la traire mie, mais la laisse tant qu’elle soit igalz aprés aucuns jors,	And some of the accidents that I have mentioned to the patient: do not draw it out at all, but let it remain even after several days.
car se li saiette vient jusc’a syfac, c’est li mors.	for if the arrow comes up to the shaft, it is death.
Et se li saiette n’est fichie fuer qu’en l’os soulement, et ne vient jusc’a syfac,	And if the arrow is not inserted in flesh but only in bone and does not come up to the shaft,
et demoure li malaides aucuns jors sens mavais accident, si l’engigne dou traire.	And the patient remains for some days with a bad accident, if he wants to draw it out.
Et s’elle est mout fichie ensi et ne puet issir fuer, si i aministre tareres entor, si com je t’ai dit; puis cure le leu tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if it is very deeply inserted and cannot come out by itself, then you administer emolients around it, as I told you; afterwards, heal the wound when it is healed.
Et se li saiette est reponue en leu dou cors si c’on ne la puisse veoir, si la quier a tout la tente;	And if the arrow is lodged in the body so that it cannot be seen, search for it thoroughly.
et se tu la sens, si la trai a aucun estrument covenauble;	And if you feel it (the dislocation), pull it with any suitable instrument.
et se tu ne pues por l’estrecement de la plaie, et por la parfondesce de la saiette,	and if you cannot due to the narrowness of the wound and the depth of the arrowhead,
et il n’i a os ne nerf ne voine, si la fens tant que li plaie soit grans;	and there is no bone, nerve, or vein, so make the wound large.
et trai la saiette se tu pues, et s’il ait en la saiette oreilles a coi elle tient,	pull out the arrow if you can, and if it has ears (the broad part of an arrowhead) attached to it like this.
si oste la char qui est ens fichie de .ij. pars au mues que tu pues,	If the bone which is fixed through two parts at the end where you can pierce it,
et puis brise ou ploie les oreilles de la saiette, tant que tu la puisses traire;	and then break or bend the arrows' ears (points), so that you can draw them out.
et subtilie bien que tu ne brisier la saiette, que tu la trairoies plus griement.	and be careful not to break the arrow but rather to draw it more gently.
Et se tu ne pues a une fois, si la lai jusque li leus entor soit porris, puis la trai, car li estraction iert alegie.	And if you cannot do it at once, press down the flesh around it, then draw it, as extraction will be easier.
Et se li decorremens de sanc te fait contraire, si amenistre ceu que nos avons dit de la cure en son chapistre;	And if bleeding obstructs its progress, bring forth what we have said about its treatment in its chapter.
et te warde de l’incision dou nerf et de la voinne, et met engien coment tu pues mues traire la saiette sens peril,	and guard against cutting the nerve and vein, and place devices to draw out the arrow safely.
ou tost ou tart, ou fermement ou belement; et met le malaide selonc la forme qu’il estoit quant li saiette li chut ens,	quickly or slowly, firmly or gently; put the patient in the same form as they were when the arrow struck them.
car c’est li plus grans aide que i soit, et se tu ne pues, si lou met selonc ceu que li signe lou te mostrent.	because this is the greatest help that can be, and if you cannot, put it according to what the signs show you.
Li saiette que vient fuer d’autre part, ou il apert aucune chose de li, ou li cuir est enflez endroit si c’on le voit ou sent aparamment:	The arrow that comes from another place, if it opens anything of it, or the skin is swollen in one place as can be seen or felt.
taille donques sus, tant que les tenailles i puissent prendre, et puis l’estrai: si saut fuer maintenant.	Cut then on top, as long as the tweezers can take hold of it, and then pull it out; if it leaps away now.
Et s’elle est retenue en l’os, si tornoie ta main rondement, tant qu’elle entre en l’os, et eslarge l’os, puis la trai.	And if it is held in the bone, turn your hand round and round until it enters the bone, and widen the bone, then pull it out.
Et s’elle ne puet issir, si la laisse encor, et puis rencomence l’estraction tant qu’elle isse fuer;	And if it cannot come out, leave it for a while, and then continue with the extraction until it comes out.
et se li fust de la saiette i est, se le boute a tout le fust;	And if it were of an arrow in it, push it all out;
et se li fust chiet, et tu vues aministrer boutement, si i aministre .i. estrument cheveit,	and if it were a dislocation, and you wish to administer binding, then administer one instrument of hair,
si que li pointe de la saiette entre en la cheveure de l’estrument; et puis boute fuer,	so that the point of the arrow enters into the hair of the instrument; and then push it with force.
et se li saiette est chevee, se i boute .i. estrument a pointe entrant ens, por alegier l’estraction.	And if the arrow is hairy, push one instrument into the point entering in; to make easier the extraction.
Et se li saiette est entouchie, si covient que tu copes toute la char entor ou li venins est, se tu pues,	And if the arrowhead is touched, it is necessary that you cut all the flesh around where the poison is, if you can.
puis cure la plaie si com il couvient.	Then heal the wound as necessary.
Et se li saiette chiet ou peis ou au ventre ou a la vessie ou au costeit, et elle est prochiene, et tu pues coper sus, se i cope;	And if the arrowhead falls into the abdomen or bladder or side and is close, and you can cover it, then do so.
et te garde de coper la voinne et lou nerf, et puis l’estrai, et puis cout la plaie, se mestier est;	and beware of cutting the vein and the nerve, and then extract it, and then sew up the wound if necessary.
et la cure tant qu’elle soit sanee.	And let the treatment continue until it is healed.
Li forme des tenailles dont on trait les saiettes sont semblans au bec d’oiseil, et vez ci la forme:	The shape of the tweezers used for arrow extraction resembles an owl's beak, and here is its form:
Et en sont mout de manieres: grans, moienes, et petites, selonc la quantitei de la saiette.	And they come in many shapes: large, medium, and small, according to the size of the arrow.
Li forme dou boutant cheveit est ausi com li penne d’un oisel,	The shape of the handle is also similar to an owl's quill.
por bouter a la pointe de la saiette, si com ci est li forme:	To drive the arrow to its tip, as follows:
li forme des tenailles por bouter et por sachier si est ci:	The form of pliers for pushing and pulling is as follows:
des voinnes dou cors communes	handles with common bodies (i.e., pincers)
Des voinnes dont on se saine sont .xxxi., de coi il a ou chef xvi.,	Pliers for healing are 31 in number, of which the head is 16.
c’est a savoir: .ij. batans qui sont aprés les oreilles, qui sont apelees les dous «herbech»;	This is to know: 2 bands that are after the ears, which are called the double "herbech";
et les .ij. arteres qui sont en .ij. temples apparans;	and the 2 arteries that are in the 2 temples apparent;
et .ij. voines que sont en .ij. larmiers des .ij. eulz, que sont apelees «aspires»;	and the 2 veins that are in the 2 inner corners of the 2 eyes, which are called "aspirers";
et li voine que est emmi le front; et li voinne que est au chief dou neis;	and the vein that is on the forehead; and the vein that is at the head of the nose;
et les .ij. guindeges qui sont ou col;	And the two glands that are at the neck;
et les .ij. voinnes que sont en levres desus de la bouche, et ce sont les voines que sont apelees «augeherich»;	And the two veins which are above the mouth, and these are called "augeherich";
et .ij. voinnes que sont desoz la lengue.	And the two veins that are beneath the tongue.
Les voinnes dont on saine communement sont .v. en chescun bras:	The veins which are commonly known to be five in each arm:
l’une est li cephalique, et est dou senestre costeit, et l’apelent li laie gens «voinne dou chief»;	The first one is the cervical, and it is on the left side of the neck, and the common people call it "vein of the head".
et li moiene est apelee «faste», et est composte de la cephalique et de la basilique,	And the middle one is called "fast" and is composed of the cervical and basilar.
et l’apelent li laie gens «voinne dou cuer»; et li basilique si est ou destre costeit,	And the common people call it "vein of the heart"; and the basilar is on the right side,
et l’apelent li laie gent «voinne dou ventre», et est sus le foscile,	And the common people call it "vein of the belly"; and it is above the abdomen,
et est celle dont on saine, qui apert manifestement sus le pouchet.	And this is the one whose wound clearly opens above the pocket.
Et li salvatelle est li voine qui est entre l’auriculaire et l’anulaire, et si a .ij. rains;	The veinlet is located between the auriculary and anularia, and has two fingers' breadth.
et en la jambe et ou piet sont .iij. voinnes: l’une si est desoz la corbeure dou pochet dou senestre costeit,	and in the leg and foot there are four veins: one is beneath the hollow of the pocket on the left side,
et li seconde sophene qui est a la cheville dou destre costeit; et li voine qui est apelee «nesse», que est en la cheville de l’autre costei;	and the second saphenous vein that is on the wrist of the right side; and the vein called "nesse", which is on the other side's wrist.
et en l’autre jambe sont .iij. voinnes desoz celles.	And in the other leg there are three veins beneath those.
Li sainie des voinnes que sont aprés les oreilles si aide as catharres anciens, et a emigraine;	The vein that is behind the ears helps with ancient catarrhs and migraines.
et li qualiteis dou sainier, si com je te dis, et est que tu reises lou chief dou malaide,	And the qualities of the bloodletter, as I tell you, are that you grasp the patient's head,
et frote lou leu ou les voinnes sont d’un drap aspre; puis estrigne li malaides son col a une vis,	And rub the joint or veins with a rough cloth; then tighten the patient's neck with a screw.
tant que les .ij. voinnes aperent derrier les oreilles en .ij. leus dependens dou chief:	until the two veins appear behind the ears in two places depending on the head:
quier les donques a ton doi, et ou tu sens lou poulz desoz ton doi, si seigne d’enche;	then find the place where you feel the pulse below your neck, and press firmly there:
puis pren la lancette, et la boute par desoz la voine jusc’a l’os, puis lieve ta main a tout la voinne amont,	then take the lance, and push it through the vein up to the bone, then lift your hand all along the vein:
et cope et lou cuir et la voinne bien .ij. dois dou traver, et fai issir dou sanc tant que tu vues;	And cut (the area) with a sharp knife and skin (it) well, making two incisions with the tips of the thumb, and make blood flow out until you see (it).
puis l’estrain et lie, tant qu’ele soit sanee;	then strain and bind it, until it heals;
et j’ai ja dit l’incision et le cautere ou premier livre.	And I have already said the incision and the cautery in the first book.
Li sainie des .ij. arteres que sont en .ij. temples, si vaut a emigrainne anciene,	The healing of the two arteries that are in the two temples, is worth ancient emigration.
et sode, et obtalmie acostumee, et au cors des larmes agues as eulz;	And sores, eye diseases, and tears of blood from the eyes;
et li qualitez dou sainier si est si com je dis:	and the qualities of a healer are as I say:
et est que li malaides estraigne son col, tant que les .ij. voinnes aperent apertement;	and it is that the patient extends his neck, until two veins appear openly;
et sent lou polz desoz ton doi, et puis seigne d’enche;	And the pole is beneath your throat, then swallow it.
puis lieve lou keur sus la voinne en haut a ton doi indice, et boute la lancette desoz,	Then lift the cure on top of the vein at the throat indicator and push the lance underneath.
et lieve la voine en haut, et la cope, si com tu as fait en .ij. autres voinnes, et fai corre dou sanc selonc ta necessiteit;	lift up the vein and strike it, just as you have done in the two other veins, and let the blood flow according to your need.
puis deslie lou malaide, et met ton doi sus la voine une houre, puis met sus coton;	then release the patient, and place your hand on the vein for an hour, then put a cotton cloth over it.
et puis la lie forment, et la laisse tant qu’elle soit sanee; et nos en avons jai parleit et de lor copement et de lor estraction, ou comencement dou livre.	And then form the wound, and leave it until it heals; and we have spoken of its covering and extraction, or the beginning of the book.
Li sainie de la voine dou front si vaut autant com li sainie de la cephalique as maladies de la faice ancienes, et a emigraine, et a roujor;	The healing of the vein in the forehead is as effective as the healing of the skull in ancient facial diseases that have spread and turned red.
et li qualitez si est que li malaides estraigne son col en tordant, tant que li voine apere;	And the qualities are such that the patient strangles his neck until the vein appears;
puis pren l’estrument qui est apelez «fosseur», dont ci est li forme:	Then take the instrument called "fosseur", here is its shape:
Et met la pointe sus la voinne, et fier sus de ta main, ou d’autre chose, et laisse dou sanc issir selonc la quantiteit que tu vues;	Place the point on the vein, and strike with your hand or something else, and let the blood flow according to the amount that you see;
puis delie au malaide le col, et lie la voine tant qu’elle soit saneel et aucune fois l’uevre on d’un flaime large.	Then cut the patient's neck and tie the vein until it is healthy, and never use a wide flame.
Toutevoie, il ne covient mie que li flaimes soit trop agus; et le saine de travers, car li os est pres, et par aventure brise li flaimes quant il est subtilz.	Moreover, the flames should not be too sharp, and the vein should be cut obliquely because the bone is near, and by chance the flames may break when they are thin.
Li sainie des .ij. voines que sont en .ij. larmiers si aide as eulz, et a la tigne, et a la roujor, et a l’oriuel en l’oil, et as maladies de la faice;	The sinuses of the two veins that are in the two arms aid the eyes, and in the throat, and the tongue, and the ear in oil, and in facial diseases;
et li qualitez de lor sainie si est que li malaides estraigne son col en tordant d’aucun liien, si com devant;	and the qualities of their sinuses are that the patient stretches his neck by twisting a certain rope, as before.
puis le saine, et soit li sainie dou traver, un poc dou lonc dou flaime un poc large, car il n’i a point de char.	then put the hot iron, and let the sinus be the size of a finger length and a little wider, because there is no need for heat.
Et se li flaimes est subtilz, par aventure si brise; puis fai corre dou sanc, tant com tu en as mestier, et puis lie sus couton, et le lie bien.	And if the flames are subtle, perhaps they break; then correct the blood flow, as much as you need, and then cover it with linen, and bind it well.
Li sainie de la voine dou neis si vaut a ague, et a sode forsenee, et a maladies de faice,	The vein of the nose is beneficial for cough, scrod fever, and fevers of the face.
si com emigraine et roujor que vient en la faice, et meimement quant elle est anciene;	as migraines and redness that comes in the face, and especially when it is old;
et li qualitez de la sainie si est que li malaides estrigne son col, puis estrain son neis a ta main senestre,	and the quality of the vein is that the patient presses his neck, then grasps his nose with his left hand,
et pren lou flaime subtil lonc, et le fiche emmi la levre en l’espaice qui est entre les .ij. narines,	And take the subtle flame long, and thrust it into the mouth between the two nostrils,
car li voinne n’apert mie bien enqui, et li sans comencera maintenant a corre;	for the vein does not open well thus, and the blood will start to flow now.
et n’aler mie trop em parfont, et fai corre dou sanc selonc ta necessiteit, puis la lie une nuit, car elle est mout tost restoree;	do not go too far inward, and let the blood flow according to your necessity, then bind it for a night, as it is quickly restored.
et c’est li forme dou flaime:	this is the form of the flame:
Li sainie des .ij. guindeges si aide a l’estrecement de l’alainne, et a l’encomencement de meselerie, et a mout de maladies, et a empetigine, et a corrodens, et a herpes, et estiomenes;	The first joint of the two fingers helps in the straightening of the thumb and at the beginning of swelling, and in many diseases, abscesses, corrosion, sores, and ulcers.
et li qualitez de la sainie si est que li malaides estraigne son col desoz l’une et l’autre, si com nos avons dit;	And the qualities of the joint are such that the patient straightens his neck under one and the other, as we have said;
et soit li maistres estans sus lou chief dou malaide, et li malaides siece sus .i. siege,	and let the master be standing over the head of the patient, and the patient lies on one seat,
puis saine la voine dou lonc un poc largement, puis trai dou sanc tempreement, ou tant com mestier est;	Then open the vein along its length with a slight width, then draw out the blood moderately, as needed.
puis refai autreteil en l’autre voinne, puis deslie lou liien, et estraint andous les voines moienement,	Then repair the other side of the vein, then untie the ligature, and hold the veins evenly in the middle.
que li malaides n’estrangle; et le laisse jusc’au matin, que li plaie soit sanee.	let the patient not strangle; and leave it until morning, so that the wound heals.
De la sainie des leivres	On the treatment of boils.
Li sainie des voinnes des levres desus si aident a cole en la bouche, et a corruption de gencives, et fendures de levres, et dou neis et entor.	The sinews of veins in the mouth above help in swallowing and contribute to gum corruption, lip fissures, and teeth and surrounding issues.
Et li qualitez de la sainie si est de faire seoir lou malaide devant toi, et estraint son col si com j’ai dit;	And the qualities of the sinew are to make the patient sit in front of you and hold his neck as I have said.
puis torne la levre, et regarde as .ij. voinnes, dont l’une est a la destre levre et li autre a la senestre,	Then turn the lip, and look at the two veins, one on the right lip and the other on the left.
et les conoist on par ceu qu’elles sont noires, et par ceu que entor elles a voines menues noires:	And one recognizes them by the fact that they are black, and by the fact that around them there are small black veins:
cope donques l’une et l’autre, et se tu ne les conois, et tu en es en doutance,	Touch both of them, and if you do not recognize them, and you are in doubt,
si cope la plus grosse de chescune part, et tout ausi fai des .ij. voinnes que sont desus et desoz, car c’est une meisme maniere.	If you touch the largest one from each side, and likewise do with the two veins that are above and below, because it is the same way.
De la sainie desoz la lengue	From beneath the tongue
Li sainie des voinnes que sont desoz la lengue si aide aprés la sainie de la cephalique, et c’est a l’estrecement de la gorge, et as maladies de l’uve, et as maladies de la bouche;	The evacuation of blood from the veins located below the tongue assists after the head incision, and this is when the throat is cut and the diseases of the eye and mouth occur.
et li qualitez dou sainier si est que li malaides siece entre tes mains devant lou soleil, et li lieve la lengue, et regarde desoz en chescun costeit une voinne noire:	And the quality of bleeding is that the patient swallows between your hands in front of the sun, lifts the tongue, and looks below on each side to find a black vein:
saine donques l’une et l’autre, et n’aler mie trop em parfont, car desoz sont les arteres.	Therefore, one and the other, but do not go too deep, for beneath are the arteries.
Les voinnes dou coute dont on saine communement sont sainies selonc .ij. manieres:	The veins from which one commonly drains are usually drained according to two methods:
ou em poignant a tout .i. flaime mirtin large, ou olivaire subtil si com coutez trenchans, et est apelez «anesil»;	Or in pricking with all fire, either the large myrtle mordants or subtle olive oil as you know sharpening is called "anesil";
et sont large et subtil selonc la largesce et l’estrecement des voinnes.	and are wide and thin according to the width and narrowness of the veins.
Li forme dou flaime mirtin si est mout renommee, et est large si com tu vois:	The form of the flame mirrin is very renowned, and it is wide as you see:
Et ait mestier por ovrir les voinnes chevees plaines de gros sanc apparent, et que contienent gros sanc et trouble;	It is necessary to open the large veins with bald heads that contain much blood and are disturbed.
et c’est li forme dou flaime olivaire:	and this is the form of the olive oil flame:
et est plus subtilz apointé, et est por sainier les voinnes subtilz, ou il a subtil sanc citrin.	and it is pointed more finely, and it is for thinning out the subtle veins that have a yellowish thin blood.
Li sainie de la basilique, qui est une de ces voinnes, si aide as maladies que sont desoz la gorge, et ou col, et ou peis, et ou ventre;	The sanctuary vein, which is one of these veins, helps with the diseases that are under the throat, neck, chest, and belly;
et covient au sainor qu’il saine saigement, et qu’il se warse de l’artere qui est desoz.	and it is necessary for the lord to bleed profusely and let go of the artery that is below.
Et s’il cope l’arterre, et decorremens de sanc vient, si le covient estainchier, si com j’ai dit;	And if the artery is touched, and bleeding occurs, it must be stopped, as I said earlier;
et ne doit mie estre poignans li flaime, mais taillans si com anesil.	And the flame should not be pricked, but cut as an anvil.
Et se li basilique n’apert manifestement, si covient que tu l’estrainges, et chainge une autre;	If the cataract does not open naturally, then you must break it and change another one.
ou tu quieres aucun rain de li, ou tu saine en leu de li la voinne emmi le bras: elle apert manifestement;	or you want to get rid of it, or clean the vein in its place with the arm: it opens naturally.
et la cope au flaime anesil, si com nos avons dit.	and strike the flame as an anvil, as we have said.
Et se tu vues conoistre le leu de la sainie, si covient ainsois que tu estraignes lou bras, que tu touches le leu tant que tu conoisses le poulz;	And if you wish to know the location of the wound, it is also necessary that you dislocate the arm, touch the place where the pulse is;
puis signe le leu d’enche, et puis lie lou bras, et cope la voine dou flaime anesil;	then mark the location with a sign, and then tie the arm and burn the vein with fire.
et warde que tu ne ferir en l’artere quant tu vois le leu enfleit, car c’est de l’artere: eschui la donques.	and be careful not to wound an artery when you see it swelling, for it is the artery: avoid it then.
Et se tu vois saillir en haut ausi com l’urine d’un enfant, et li sans est rouges et subtilz, saiches que c’est sans de l’artere:	And if you see it rise high like the urine of a child and it is red and thin, know that it is not from the artery:
haste toi donques, et met ton doi sus longement, puis oste ton doi se li sans estainche, que maintes fois avient;	Hurry up then, and place your hand on it for a long time, afterwards cut your hand off without stopping, for this often happens.
se lie lou bras, et laisse ensi, et ne lou mueve li malaides; et soit sus paour, et ne lou mueve tant qu’il soit sanez.	Tie the arm and leave it like that, do not move it by the patient; let him be afraid, and do not move it until it is healed.
Et se li sans n’est estainchiez, et il te vaint, et li medicine ne t’est presens, si cope l’artere s’elle apert, car li chief de li retraient; et estainche li sans.	And if the wound is not stopped and it bleeds, and no medication is present for you, strike the artery if it is open, because the head will retreat; stop the bleeding.
Et pren une escorce de fistice, et la fent, et pren l’une des moitiez et lie sus bien jusc’a l’autre jor;	And take a piece of willow bark, and cut it in half, and tie one of the halves above the other for one day.
se li sans estainche, c’est bien; se ce non, si le cure, si com nos avons dit, des poudres qui estainchent sanc;	If it (the wound) stops bleeding, that's good; if not, treat it as we have said, with powders that stop bleeding.
et li estainchemens n’est mie griés em plusors dispositions por le petit leu de la plaie, et la possance dou liien dou bras.	And the stopping of bleeding is not always necessary in various positions due to the small size of the wound and the slender nature of the vein in the arm.
Li sainie de la voinne em mileu si aide qu’elle trait sanc dou chief desus, et dou cors desoz,	The opening of the vein in the middle helps to treat blood from the head above and the body below,
por ceu qu’elle est composte de la basilique et de la cephalique, si com nos avons dit;	Because it is composed of the basilica and the cephalica, as we have said.
et covient au sainor qu’il se warse por lou nerf qui est desoz, et s’il point trop em parfont, et il trueve lou nerf,	and it is necessary for the lord to pierce through the nerve that is underneath, and if it pierces too deep, and it finds the nerve,
et il enfle et li santez soit griés, et par aventure ne puet saner;	and it swells and the patient becomes ill or injured, and in case it cannot heal.
et cist nerf apert mult de fois, et s’il n’apert en aucuns homes por sa subtiliteit, si covient que tu lou saines de l’estrument anesil; et eschui lou nerf a ton pooir.	and this nerve opens up many times, and if it does not open in any man due to its subtlety, then you must heal it with the instrument anesthetic; and cut the nerve to your power.
Et se il a voinne entre les .ij. ners, si la fent dou lonc.	And if there is a vein between the two nerves, make it long.
Li sainie de la cephalique si aide, qu’ele atrait sanc dou chief, et aide as eulz;	The incision of the head should aid, so that blood from the head and eyes is drawn out.
et covient sainier em poignant au flaime olivaire ou au flaime mirtin, car c’est li plus sauve de toutes les voinnes, car il n’a desoz li ne nerf ne artere.	And it is necessary to make an incision in the point of olive oil or myrtle fire, for this is the safest of all veins, as there is no nerve or artery beneath it.
Toutevoie, covient querir lou plus legier leu, et ne grieve rien s’on faut la premiere fois, et on rencomence;	Therefore, one must seek the lighter joint, and not worry if it is necessary for the first time, and one may begin again.
et par aventure enfle li leus a aucuns homes, cant on faut la premiere fois, mais il ne grieve rien.	And sometimes the joints swell in some men, when it is necessary for the first time, but do not worry about it.
La qualitez de la sainie si est selonc ta pensee.	The quality of the urine is according to your opinion.
Li premiere chose que tu dois savoir de sainier, si est que sainie n’est amenistree fuer que por garder santeit,	The first thing you should know about urination, is that it is brought forth only for preserving health,
et por eschuir les maladies a venir;	And to avoid future illnesses;
et soit li sainie faite en l’une des .iij. voinnes que sont ou coute: c’est a savoir, cephalique, faste, et basilique;	and let the bloodletting be performed in one of the four veins that are near: namely, cephalic, femoral, or basilic.
et se doit on sainier en l’encomencement de prientens a geun, et en autompne et en yver aprés mengier, quant li signe de repletion aperent;	and it should be done at the beginning of spring, in autumn, and in winter after eating, when the signs of fullness appear;
et se doit on sainier le premier jor ou le tier, aprés .ij. houres ou .iij. dou jor.	and it should be done on the first or third day, after 2 or 4 hours.
Li sainie qui est aministree as maladies n’a point d’oure determinee, mais que quant besoing est de jor ou de nut, en toutes houres et en toz tens;	The salve given for diseases has no fixed hour determined, but it is administered whenever necessary, day or night, at all hours and in every moment.
et ne covient mie sainier les enfans jusc’a .xiiij. ans, ne femme portant fuer que des lou quart mois jusc’a septime.	And it is not necessary to salve children until they are 12 years old, nor women in childbirth except during the fourth, fifth and sixth months.
Ne ne se doient mie sainier li viel qui ont passez .lx. ans.	Nor should the elderly who have passed 60 years be salved.
Et quant aucuns se vuet sainier, en quel maniere que ce soit, si covient k’il mondefie les intestines d’un clistere legier,	And when anyone wishes to be salved, in whatever manner that may be, it is necessary that their intestines be emptied with a light clyster.
s’il a mout de fiens retenut, si que les voines n’atraient des intestines les superfluitez porries nuisans as membres principelz;	If there is much bile retained, so that veins do not expel the superfluidities from the principal members.
ne ne se saine mie cil qui est trop saolez de viandes, ne qui est yvres, tant k’il en soit fuer, ne ydropiques;	That one who is excessively salted with foods, or drunk, to such an extent that he sweats and is watery.
et se warse on de sainier aprés colique passion, et vomissement, et decorrement de ventre, et multipliement d’abiter a femme, et de traval, de veiller et de juner, et ceu que tot la vertu, ou par chose de l’arme ou dou cors;	and if he is purged after a colic passion, vomiting, stomach disorder, excessive ejaculation with women, labor, staying awake, and fasting, or from the strength of weapons or from the body.
puis subtilie les humors, se li sans est gros, par viandes et par bevraiges et par medicines, se tu en as lou poir;	Then thin out the fluids, if it is fatty, with foods and drinks and medicines, if you have the power to do so.
puis entre ou bain, s’aucune chose ne lou deffent, por subtiliier lou sanc,	then immerse [it] in a bath, if nothing prevents it, to thin out the blood.
et te saine de la voinne dou pis entor la tierce, si com nos avons dit;	and heal the vein with the pus surrounding it, as we have said.
et te garde celui jor de travail, et de poinne, et de luxure, et de semblans choses;	and keep that day from work, from pain, and from lust, and similar things.
et soies liez et joians, et soit li sainieres plus haut que cil cui on saine, et li frote lou bras .ij. fois ou .iij.,	And you should bind and squeeze, and let the bandages be higher than those who are bled, and rub the arm two or three times.
puis estraigne lou liien desus moienement, car quant il est trop estrois ou poc, si ne puet corre li sans;	Then gradually pull out the ligature above, for if it is too tight or narrow, it cannot heal without.
et puis le frote le leu as mains, tant que les voines enflent, et les sente on;	and then rub the wound with your hands until the veins swell, and feel them.
puis moille li sainieres le flaime d’un poc d’oile viel, puis mette son doit de sa main senestre sus celle voinne desoz lou leu un poc ou il vuet sainier,	then wet the bandages with a little oil from an old bottle, then put your left hand's fingertip on that vein under the wound where you want to bleed.
que li voinne ne fue et faille au ferir.	That the vein does not open and fail when cutting.
Car il i a voinnes que fuient ausi com cordes au sainier, et si a de telz que sont plainnes de ventositeit,	For there are veins which run like cords to be bled, and some which are full of venosity.
si que quant on met sus le flaime, si retrait a flaime, et ne puet ovrir li voinne, et ensi est on de ceus;	for when you put the fire to it, if it takes flame, and cannot open the vein, then that is one of these.
et s’il aoevre la voinne, si est li plaie trop estroite, por ceu si covient que li sainieres soit avisez en ces choses.	And if it opens a vein, then the wound is too narrow; therefore, the surgeons should be aware of this matter.
Et se li voine oevre la premiere fois, c’est boin; se ceu non, si rencomence ancor un poc desoz celui leu ou sus hastanment, se li leus n’est enflez.	And if it opens the vein again for a second time, that is good; but if not, then start anew under that place or cut more quickly if the wound is not inflamed.
Et se li leus est enflez, et li malaides s’espoante, se li laisse .i. jor ou .ij., et ne liier mie le bras:	And if the wound is inflamed, and the patient becomes afraid, he should wait one or two days and not bind the arm:
par aventure i venra apostemes chaus; ne n’entre ou bain, puis rencomence la sainie s’elle li plait;	In case abscesses appear, do not enter into water before starting anew with the surgery if it pleases him.
et se li pertuis est petis, ou li sans cort subtilment et tu doutes qu’il n’isse mie tant de sanc com tu vues, si fier en celui pertuis meisme a tout le flaime droitement;	And if the piercings are small, or the veins thinly and subtly, and you doubt that much blood will flow as you see, put all the flame directly into the piercing itself.
et l’uevre un poc hastanment, ainsois que li leus soit enflez; car ceu avient maintes fois, quant li plaie est petite.	And work it a little hastily, so that the flesh is inflamed; for this happens often when the wound is small.
Se tu vois le leu enfleit, si ne rencomencier mie la sainie, et met sus un poc de lie d’oile, car elle alige lou cors dou sanc, et est muedre en cest leu li lie que li oile;	If you see the flesh inflamed, do not start the bleeding again, and put a little bit of oil on it, for the oil alleviates the pain of the blood and is moistened in this place by the oil.
et ensi aministre la lie de oile en chescune sainie que tu saines les voines, por estanchier lou cours dou sanc;	And thus administer the oil poultice on each wound that you open the veins, to stop the flow of blood;
et ceu meisme fait triaicle et bowe d’eus, quant on le met sus le leu; si subtilie li sans et s’espart quant il est trop gros.	And similarly, use a three-pronged instrument and forceps for removing arrows when placing it on the spot; make sure it is thin and split if it is too thick.
Et s’il i vient uns apostemes gros, qui avient maintes fois, meismement quant il n’est sainiez fuer que a celi fois ou li overture de la voinne est petite,	And if there comes a large abscess, which often happens when the wound is not cleaned before that time or when opening the vein is small,
si te haste, et met sus le leu esponge moillie en aigue et en seil un poc chaut, et l’estraint une houre;	If you hurry, place a moist sponge in warm water and salt for an hour, and then strain it.
et covient que tu faices ceu aprés l’issue dou sanc de la voinne, et s’il demoure au leu aprés aucuns jors aucune noiror ou verdor, si ne li nuist mie;	and you must do this after the evacuation of blood from the vein, and if it stays in place for several days without any black or green discoloration, that is not harmful.
et se tu vues, met sus aucune chose de aloes ou de mirre remise en jus de calament, monstastre, ou semblant.	and if you find (something), place some balm of aloes or myrrh in it, anointed with cooled oil or something similar.
Et maintes fois avient aposteme et aparance a la sainie de la basilique: met donques ta main sus, et se tu trueves le leu mol a la compression de la main, si est celle aparance male.	And there are often abscesses and appearances at the sanctuary (hospital): put your hand on it then, and if you find it soft to the pressure of your hand, that is a bad sign.
Eschui donques que tu ne mettes sus aucune chose de ceu que nos avons dit, car par aventure en cort sans de l’artere; mais li fai .i. emplaustre sec por endurcir le leu, puis le cure d’autre cure, tant qu’il soit sanez.	Therefore, you should not put anything on any of the things we have mentioned, for by chance without the artery; but he should be given one dry plaster to harden it, then cured with another treatment until it is healed.
Et trai a chescun dou sanc selonc la quantiteit de sa vertu, et de la color dou sanc.	And draw blood from each according to the quantity of its virtue, and from the color of the blood.
Car se li sans est noir, si en laisse issir tant qu’il soit rouges; et se tu lou vois gros, si lou laisse tant qu’il soit subtiliiez; et s’il est trop chaus, si le laisse refroidier.	For if the wound is black, let it drain until it turns red; and if you see it thick, let it drain until it becomes thin; and if it is too hot, let it cool.
Et covient a celui qui est plains et fors, et ait mestier d’estraction de sanc, c’on li faice plus large plaie, et soit li flaimes larges;	And it is necessary for the one who is wounded and needs bloodletting, to make a larger wound, and let the veins be wider.
et a celui qui est foibles, fai le contraire, et le covient sainier poc et sovent, et le doit on sainier en taillant de travers, ne mie en poignant;	And for the weak one, do the opposite, and it is necessary to let him bleed little by little, and it should be done by cutting across, not by pricking.
et ceste maniere de sainie est sauve de decorrement de sanc et de copement de nerf, et vaut mues que li sainie dou lonc ne dou large.	And this method of bleeding is safe from contamination of blood and nerve damage, and it is more beneficial than long bleeding or wide bleeding.
Et a celui cui li cors faut a la sainie, covient doner pain moilliet en jus de pomes grenates; s’il est eschaufez, si trai dou sanc .iij. fois ou .iiij.	And for the one whose body needs to be purified, it is necessary to give soft bread below pomegranate peels; if he is scorched, draw blood three or four times or more.
Et s’il est de froide complexion, si menjuce devant la sainie pain moilliet en sirop muzé, ou en sirop de miel aromatique avec espices, si com poivre, canelle, gingibre, et chiches, et sirop bien odorant.	And if he is of cold constitution, eat soft bread in syrup before the purification, or in aromatic honey syrup with spices such as pepper, cinnamon, ginger, and anise, and a pleasant-smelling syrup.
Et s’il paume a la sainie, aprés l’issue de mout de sanc, si covient qu’il hume brouet de char, et sirop odorant subtil,	If he has diarrhea during the purification, after the passage of blood, it is necessary that he drink broth of meat and subtle scented syrup.
et use des autres choses que nos avons dit en la division ou chapistre de sincope, por l’evacuation de voinne.	And apply other things as we have said in the division or chapter of fainting, for the evacuation of blood.
Et s’il vuet esventer som bras, et sainier autre fois, si covient, quant il est afoiblis par grant sainie, k’il se saine poc et poc, selonc la quantiteit de sa vertu continueement.	If you want to burst open an arm, or draw blood another time, if it has been weakened by excessive bleeding, let it bleed drop by drop according to the amount of its strength continuously.
Et qui vuet esventer som bras aprés la premiere sainie, et il a cors fort, si se saine .vij. houres aprés la premiere sainie, ou aprés la nuevime houre.	And whoever wants to burst open the arm after the first bleeding, and has a strong constitution, should let it bleed for 6 hours after the first bleeding, or after the ninth hour.
Et qui se vuet sainier d’autre part, si se doit sainier lou secont jor ou le tier.	And whoever wants to draw blood from another part, should draw it on the second day or the third.
Car il a mout de sanc dedens le cors qui est ja eschaufez, et fait venir fievre; si en covient traire grant quantiteit, et eslargir le pertus tant qu’il chiece em pameson;	Since there is much blood within the body which has already been heated and produces fever, it is necessary to draw out a large quantity of it and widen the opening until it comes through in a cloth.
puis que tu rewardes toutes les conditions de sainie, et met ta main sus som poulz quant il saine, que li mors ne viegne en leu de pameson,	then you must observe all the signs of healing, and place your hand on top of the pulses to prevent death from coming through cloth.
et ceu avient maintes fois, quant li sainieres est negligens;	this happens many times when healers are negligent.
et ne covient mie quant tu vues desliier lou bras, et faire issir sanc la seconde fois, et li pertus est clos, que tu presses forment sus;	and it is not appropriate when you dislocate the arm, and make blood come out the second time, and the opening is closed, that you press firmly.
ne s’il est corbes, qu’il estende lou bras hastanment, car ce seroit malz;	If it is curved, let him stretch out the arm as much as possible, for this would be bad.
mais le laisse tant qu’il saine la seconde fois; ou tu i point a la pointe dou flaime, tant que li sans qui est congelez a pertus de la voinne isse fuer,	but leave it until it heals the second time; or you prick it with the tip of the flame, until the wound that has congealed opens again.
et met sus .i. poc de seil remis en aigue, et presse sus legierement.	and put on it one piece of clean linen wet with vinegar and press lightly.
Et se li voine est enflee, si la laisse et ne l’estreindre mie, tant que li aposteme soit apaisiez.	And if the vein is swollen, do not bind it at all until the abscess has been calmed.
Et se necessitez est dou traire dou sanc la seconde fois, si le saine en celui leu meisme, ou en un autre voinne, ou en l’autre bras.	And if it is necessary to draw blood again, do so in the same vein, or another one, or in the other arm.
Li voinne emmi le bras est sainie en leu de la voine dou chief por ceu qu’elle est composte.	The vein in the arm is similar to the vein in the head because they are composed of the same thing.
Et li maniere de la sainie si est que li malaides boute sa main en aigue chaude, tant que li foscile soit rouges;	And the method of bloodletting is that the patient should insert their hand into hot water until the vein becomes red.
puis soit liiéz moienement, si que li voinne apere bien, puis le saine maintenant dou travers, ne mie dou large ne dou lonc;	Then he should be tied gently so that the vein can be seen clearly, then draw blood carefully, neither too wide nor too long.
et soit li pertus larges, et soit sainiez bien pres de la jointe de la main, et se sans n’en puet issir, si remet la main en aigue chaude, et laisse corre lou sanc en l’aigue, tant que tu en aies assez;	And let the wounds be wide open, and let them be well cleaned close to the joint of the hand; if it cannot be removed from there, put the hand in hot water and let the blood come out in the hot water until you have enough.
et se c’est en esteit, si ne rebouter mie la main en aigue chaude, car on l’i met plus en yver que en esteit;	if it is cold, do not push the hand into hot water, for you put it more in winter than in summer.
et li sainie de ceste voine est plus sauve de toutes autres voinnes, qu’il n’i a ne artere ne nerf.	and the cleaning of this vein is safer than all other veins, for there are neither arteries nor nerves.
Li sainie de la salvatele de la main destre si vaut a toutes les maladies dou foie, et c’est li maniere:	The salve for the sore on the right hand is beneficial for all diseases of the liver, and this is how it is done:
estrain la main, et boute en aigue chaude, tant que li voinne soit enflee, si c’on la voie;	hold the hand and apply hot vinegar until the vein is opened, if possible to see.
et se la saine de travers, et se tu la copes dou tout en tout, si ne grieve rien;	and if the wound is transverse, and you cover it with something entirely, it will cause no pain;
et n’aler mie trop em parfont, car li nerf sont desoz toz desnuez de char,	and do not go too deep because nerves are exposed bare under all the skin,
et puis remet la main en aigue chaude, se li sans est congelez en la plaie, et n’en puet issir.	And then place the hand in hot water, unless it freezes at the wound, and cannot come out.
Et quant tu avras trait dou sanc tant com mestier t’est, si met sus la voinne oile et seil por souder hastanment, et ensi fai de chescun rain.	And when you have treated the blood as needed, put oil and silk on the wound to heal it quickly, and do this for each wound.
Li sainie de li en la main senestre si vaut a la maladie de la mice, et fai tout ausi com je t’ai dit devers destre.	The salve of the left hand is good for the disease of the mice, and do it just as I told you on the right side.
Li sainie de la sophene si vaut a toutes les maladies que sont desoz le cors,	The salve of sulphur is beneficial for all diseases that are beneath the chest.
si com maladies de la marris, et retenement de flors, et maladie des rains, et des cuixes et des jambes ancienes, et semblans maladies.	as marsh fever, retention of fluids, rain disease, thigh and leg ailments, and similar diseases.
Et li qualitez de sa sainie si est que li malaides boute som piet en aigue chaude, et frote sus la voinne tant qu’elle pere,	And the properties of its salve are that the patient must dip their foot in hot water and rub it over the vein until it burns.
et lie desus la jointure dou piet; et li voinne si est a la cheville, et par desus lou piet en vont mout de rains;	and place it on the joint of the foot; and the vein is at the ankle, and there are many rivers flowing over the foot.
saine la donques ou plus large rain, ou a la cheville, que mues vaut.	Keep a clean bandage or cloth, wide enough or at the ankle, as it is useful.
Et se tu la saines sus lou piet, si te warde des ners qui sont desoz, et la saine de traver ausi com en copant; et soit li flaimes anesil.	And if you have a wound on the foot, be careful of the veins that are below it, and keep it clean in the same way as you would when wrapping; let the flames not touch it.
Et se li sans n’en puet issir, si remet lou piet en l’aigue, et laisse bien vuidier la voine.	And if the wound cannot be removed, immerse the foot in water and let the vein drain well.
Et se li sainieres faut la premiere fois, si rencomence la seconde au desus un poc, car li leus est salz;	And if the saline is needed for the first time, start with the second one a little higher up because the wound is salted.
ne ne douter de nerf, si com nos avons dit, et ensi fai de la sophene de l’autre piet igalment.	Do not doubt about the nerve, as we have said, and do the same with the tendon of the other leg equally.
Li leus de la voinne sciatique est a la cheville de fuer, et sa sainie vaut a la dolor de la hainche, quant c’est por sanc chaut.	The saline for the sciatic vein is at the ankle of the foot, and its application alleviates the pain of the haunch when it is used for hot blood.
Et li qualitez de sa sainie si est que li malaides entre ou bain, et estraigne desus la cheville .iiij. dois en tordant,	And the quality of its saline is that the patient immerses himself in it and stretches above the ankle four fingers width,
car autrement n’apert li voinne; et s’elle apert, si le saine en toutes les manieres que tu pues, et en traversant;	For otherwise the vein will not open; and if it opens, bleed in all possible ways that you can, and across.
et vaut mues que tu la copes, car li leus est saus, et elle est mout reponue a mains homes.	And it is better that you strike it, for the shoulder is dislocated, and it is much restored by human hands.
Et se tu ne la trueves, si saine aucun rain de li qui apert ou dos dou piet, et vers lou petit doi, et te warde des ners;	And if you don't pierce it, no blood will flow from it that opens or its back, and toward the little hole, and beware of nerves.
et fai tant corre dou sanc que tu vues, et puis deslie lou lien, et met sus coton et l’estraint; ele est maintenant sanee.	Make as much incision in the blood as you see fit, then untie the ligature, and put cotton on it and bind it; it is now healed.
Des sainies de ventouse	From blisters of the bladder (or boil)
Ventouses sont fait de cornes, ou d’arain, ou de voirre; et ventosation si est faite selonc .ij. manieres: ou par ferir et atraire sanc, ou sens ferir.	Blisters of the bladder (or boil) are made of horns, or hairs, or glass; and blistering is done in two ways: either by cutting and drawing blood, or without cutting.
Et ceste ventosation qui est sens ferir si est selonc .ij. manieres: ou elle est a tout feu, ou sens feu;	This blistering done without cutting also has two ways: either it is to be applied to any heat source, or it is heated with fire.
et ventosation qui est faite par ferir et par estraction de sanc si est faite en .xiiij. leus dou cors,	And ventosation (a term used for certain medical procedures), which is done by wounding and extraction of blood, is made in 12 places in the body,
de coi li uns est tout en som le chief; et li autres est emmi le col;	because one is completely in the head; and the others are in the neck;
et .ij. autres en .ij. costeis dou col; et li ventouse desoz lou menton;	and two others in the two sides of the neck; and the vents (probably a typo, should be ventosation) under the chin;
et li ventouse des .ij. espaules; et li ventouse sus les crupies;	and the vents (probably a typo, should be ventosation) on the two shoulders; and the vents (again probably a typo for ventosation) above the ankles;
et les ventouses emmi les .ij. bras; et les ventouses des .ij. jambes;	And blisters on both arms; and blisters on both legs;
et les ventouses des .ij. chevilles; et li ventosation ne trait point de sanc, fuer que des menues voinnes que sont esparses en la char,	and the swellings of the ankles; and blistering does not treat blood, except for small veins that are scattered in the flesh.
et por ceu n’en afoiblist om mie, si com on fait de sainie de voinne;	and because it is not to be drained at all, as one does with blood from a vein;
et ne covient mie qu’elle soit aministree, ne a tout feu ne sens feu, en aucune maladie qui vient de repletion, tant que toz li cors soit vuidiez.	and it should not be given, neither by fire nor burning, in any disease that comes from repletion, until the entire body is emptied.
Et se par necessiteit de maladies covient ventoser, ou por acostumances, si l’amenistrons chescune houre en l’encomencement dou mois, ou en la fin, et emmi et en chescun tens;	And if, due to necessity or habit, it is required to administer cupping, we shall do so every hour at the beginning or end of the month, or in between and at every opportunity.
car il i a de telz qui, quant il ont mestier de ventoser, si ont pesant chief;	for there are some who, when they need to administer cupping, have a heavy head.
et si a telz qui truevent repletion et roujor en lor faice, et en lor chief, et au col, et tenebrour as eulz;	and if those who find swelling and redness in their face, head, and neck become blind.
et telz qui truevent une goute de sanc en lor bouche, et ont enflee la lengue, et raichent sanc;	and those who have a drop of blood in their mouth and swell the tongue and bleed.
et si i a de telz qui songent, et voient par nut sanc et navrez et mors et semblans choses.	And if there are such [cases], who think, see by no blood, swell and die, and similar things.
Et quant nos voions ces signes, et meismement quant c’est emmi lou mois, nos lou commandons a ventoser aprés .iij. houres dou jor.	And when we observe these signs, especially during the month, we order to bleed after three hours of the day.
Li sainie de la muze si aide a la grieteit dou chief … que vient as eulz, et ne covient mie que ce soit aprés l’evacuation de tout lou cors;	The bleeding from the mouth helps with the headache that comes to the eyes, and it is not advisable that this be done after evacuating the entire body.
et ceste ventosation si est en leu de la sainie de la cephalique,	And this bloodletting is in place of the bleeding of the skull,
et ne covient mie que cil qui est de froide complexion en use, ou qui ait chatharre, car ce lor fait mout grant nuisement;	And it is not appropriate for someone who has a cold constitution or who has scabies to use [this treatment], because it causes them much harm.
et por ceu ne covient mie que li veillart en usent, ne qui ont ou chief froides maladies.	And therefore it is not appropriate for the elderly to use [this treatment], nor those with cold diseases.
Et cil qui s’en saine sovent, si devient oblious, et por ce covient mettre la ventouse un poc plus aval par la doutance d’obliance.	And those who often heal themselves become indolent, and therefore it is necessary to place the cupping glass a little lower due to the fear of indolence.
Li ventosation emmi le col est en leu de la sainie dou chief et de la basilique, et por ceu vaut elle a l’estrecement dou pis,	Cupping at the neck is in the area of the brain and base of the skull, and for this reason it is effective in treating the lower parts of the body.
et a fendure de la chenal dou pormon, et a toust, et a repletion;	And to cut the channel of the penis, and entirely, and to fill [it].
et la covient poc bouter, car s’elle tient trop fermement, si enjanre obliance ou stomac et ou cuer.	Then it must be pressed gently, for if it holds too tightly, it may cause obstruction or injury to the stomach and heart.
Li ventosations as .ij. costelz dou col si vaut as dolors dou chief, et obtalmie et emigrainne, et a l’estranglement, et a la dolor as racines des dens,	The ventosations at the two costels of the neck are equal to the pain in the head, and obstruction and migraine, and strangulation, and pain in the roots of the teeth,
et est en leu de la sainie de la basilique; et covient que tu comandes au sainor qu’il espresse sa main au mettre, qu’il ne cope l’artere, et ne veigne decorremens de sanc.	And it is in the place of the basilica's safety; and you must instruct the lord to extend his hand to insert, not to touch the artery, and no bleeding should come forth.
Li ventosations desoz lou menton si vaut a maladie de bouche, et a corruption de gencives, et semblans maladies qui sont en la bouche; et est en leu des sainies des .ij. levres.	Ventilations under the chin are good for mouth diseases and tooth decay, as well as similar diseases in the mouth; and they are located near the safety of the lips.
Li ventosations des espaules vaut a maladie que vient de chalor et de remplissement.	Ventilations under the shoulders are good for diseases that come from heat and swelling.
Li ventosations des coutes si vaut autant com des .iij. voinnes dou bras,	The ventosations of the flanks are as much as three veins from the arms.
car elle atrait sanc de ces grosses voinnes;	for it draws blood from these large veins.
et comande au sainor qu’il ne fiere mie trop em parfont, car li leus est nus de char, et sait desoz ners et arteres.	and instruct the lord not to pierce too deep, for the flesh is bare of skin, and it knows beneath black and arteries.
Li ventouse qui est sus la croupe si vaut as emoroydes dou fondement, et as maladies desoz, et covient que li ventouse soit grans, et soit d’arain, qu’elle a mestier de bien traire; et par aventure, s’elle estoit subtilz, si briseroit; et i fai grans plaies.	The ventouse located on the rump is as much as for the emorroid from its foundation and diseases underneath, and the ventouse should be large and made of lead, as it needs to drain well; and in case it is fine, it would burst, causing great wounds.
Les ventouses des jambes si sainent apertement, car elles atraient sanc de tout le cors, et valent as dolors ancienes des rains, et de la marris, et de la vessie, et ramoinnent les flors; et sont en leu des .ij. sophenes, et des .ij. chevilles, et toutevoie elles afoiblissent lou cors aprés lonc us, et font venir paumison em plusors dispositions.	The swellings of the legs open widely because they draw blood from all over the body, and are like the old pains of the kidneys, and bladder, and vagina, and diminish the flowers; and are in the position of the two shins, and the two ankles, and yet they weaken the body after a long time, and bring pus in various dispositions.
Li maniere de mettre la ventouse si est que tu la mettes premier vuide, et succe tempreement, et la met hastanment, et remue igalment, et ne cesser de ceu faire, tant que tu voies lou leu rouge et enfleit, et apere li roujor dou sanc; puis fier, et remet les ventouses, et pren warde en la disposition des cors, car il i a telz qui ont tanre char, et clers porez: si covient ferir une fois soulement, et covient faire larges plaies, et un poc parfondes; et suce legierement.	The way to put the swelling is that you empty it first, suck it promptly, apply pressure immediately and move it evenly, and do not stop doing so until you see the place become red and swollen, and the color of blood appears; then stop, and put the swellings, and take care in the disposition of the body, for there are some who have loose skin and clear pores: it is necessary to cut only once, and it is necessary to make wide wounds, and a little deeper; and suck gently.
Et se li sans est gros, si couvient ferir .ij. fois: la premiere fois por subtiliier la voie dou sanc gros.	And if the wound is large, it is necessary to cut twice: the first time to refine the path of the thick blood.
Et se li sans est tres espés, si covient ferir la tierce fois; et quant nos volons traire dou sanc poc et poc, si nos soffist soulement une fois.	And if the bone is very thick, it must be struck three times; and when we wish to draw blood drop by drop, we should prick only once.
Et se nos volons mout de sanc, si rencomensons sovent; et se li sans est espés, si fier em parfont, et li termines si est que li keurs soit perciez soudement,	And if we wish to have much blood, let us often do it; and if the bone is thick, we should strike it through and through, and make sure that the arteries are pierced suddenly.
et couvient a celui qui a gros cuir et dur, et qui ont estrois porelz, que tu oignes les leus des ventouses d’oile aperitif et dissolutif:	And for those with thick and hard skin, and narrow pores, you should anoint the joints of the shoulders with sharp and dissolving oil:
se c’est en esteit, d’oile violet, ou d’oile d’amandres douces, ou d’oile de semence de cucurbite;	if it is summer, use violet oil, or sweet almond oil, or seed oil of cucumber:
et se c’est en yveir, d’oile de cresson, ou de lis, ou de camomille, ou autre semblant.	And if it is in ivy, oil of watercress, or lilies, or chamomile, or something similar.
Et se li superfluitez est grosse et froide, si pren oile amaratin, ou de balsamite, ou oile d’anet, et les semblans.	And if the excess is thick and cold, take bitter almond oil, or balm of Gilead oil, anise oil, and similar.
Et se cil cui on saine a tendre char et larges porelz, se n’i covient mettre point d’oile,	And if the person you are treating has thin and narrow pores, do not put any oil.
mais le covient laver aprés la ventosation d’aigue rose, ou d’aigue froide, ou d’aigue de morelle, ou d’aigue de cucurbite, ou d’aigue de porcelainne, ou autre semblant.	But it should be washed after ventosation with rose water, cold water, blackberry water, cucumber water, or pearl-water, or something similar.
Et cil qui a mout de moistor, si se leve d’aisil, ou d’aigue de mirte, et de sumac, et de semblans choses.	And he who has much moisture should rise from asafetida or myrtle water, and sumac, and similar things.
Et cil qui ont grosses superfluitez se levent de vin viel, ou d’aigue de seuc, ou de decoction d’anet ou de camomile, ou d’autres semblans;	And he who has large excesses should rise from old wine, or sour water of vinegar, or a decoction of anise or chamomile, or others similar.
et ne se covient mie sainier de ventouse devant le bain ne em bain, mais aprés lou bain une houre ou .ij.; et ne dorme mie aprés la ventosacion,	and it is not good to bleed from a blister before the bath or during the bath, but after the bath for an hour or two; and he should not sleep after venesection.
et covient k’il se warse, quant il se doit ventoser et quant il est ventosez.	and it is necessary that he washes himself when he must bleed and after bleeding.
Et warde se cil qui se saine est coleriques, et se li sans est trop agus et enflamez;	And guard that he who is recovering (or healing) is colicky, and that he is not too sharp (agitated) and inflamed;
si covient qu’il preigne choses froides, si com pomes grenates et endives et laitues a l’aisil, et semblans choses;	it is necessary that he takes cold things, such as pomegranates, endives, lettuces and similar things;
et menjuce pucins, et char de chastron, et viandes moistes.	and eats pulses (legumes) and mutton meat, and moist foods.
Et cil qui a froide complexion, si preigne syrop de miel, et vin odorant moien, qui est entre viel et noveil, et menjuce poc, et menjuce pucins et petis oiselz et pijons;	and he who has cold constitution should take honey syrup and mild scented wine, which is between old and new, and eat barley, pulses (legumes), small birds and birds such as pigeons;
et lou jor qu’il se ventousera, si doit plus boivre que mengier;	And on the day when it turns sour, he should drink more than eat;
et covient doner a aucuns homes aucune fois triaicle ou muscate devant la ventosacion, ou aprés, por conforter les membres principalz;	And it is necessary to give some men sometimes treacle or muscat before or after, for comforting the main members;
et soit subtiliiez li sans, mais il ne covient mie que cil qui sont chaut le boivent.	and let the thin ones be purged, but it should not be drunk by those who are hot.
Les ventouses que sont mises sens ferir sont celles que sont mises sus lou foie, et sus la mice, et podagre, et sus lou ventre et la boude et les rains et la hainche, car cil membre ne soffrent mie ferir sus oulz,	The wounds that are made for injury are those made on the liver, spleen, gout, belly, buttocks, loins and kidneys, as these members cannot bear to be injured under them;
et ne le fait on fuer que por atraire sanc de membre em membre,	And one does not make him fever except to draw blood from one member to another.
si com nos mettons sus les mameles quant li neis sainne; por oster la viscositeit qui est au membre, si com nos metons ventouses sus lou ventre et sus la boude por amenuisier le membre;	as we put on the limbs when the nails are swollen; to remove the viscosity that is in the limb, such as putting leeches on the belly and on the buttocks to reduce the limb.
et oste la dolor, quant il i a opilation ou piere, si oste par sa vertu atractive par aventure l’opilation, ou desaert la piere de son leu;	remove the pain when there is an abscess or stone, remove it by its attractive virtue in case of abscess, or dislodge the stone from its place.
et ensi fait ele quant on le met sus lou foie et sus la mice quant il i a ventositeit retenue,	and thus one does when he puts it on the liver and spleen when there is retained windiness,
et ces ventouses sont aministrees vuides por sucier tant soulement; et aucune fois sont aministrees ensamble feu, et aucunes fois plainnes d’aigue tede,	And these blisters are administered empty to be sucked only; and sometimes they are administered with fire, and sometimes filled with cold liquid.
si com em maladies dou pleuresin, et en tel maniere c’on emplisse la ventouse d’aigue chaude soule, ou d’aigue ou il ait cuit herbes covenaubles a ceu.	as in diseases of the lungs, and thus the blister is filled with hot water or water in which cooked herbs suitable for this purpose have been steeped.
