Li forme de la ventouse aministré a feu si est ci:	The shape of the blister administered with fire is as follows:
Et ait .ij. dois de large et demi palme de parfont, et ait ou costeit entor lou mileu .i. petit pertus, ausi com por bouter une aguille,	And it should be two fingers' width and half a palm in length, and have one small hole at its center, like pushing an awl through.
et soit d’arain, souef devant si qu’ele ne blece lou malaide au mettre sus lou membre;	and let it be of iron, soft enough that it does not scald the patient when placed on the limb;
et ait em mileu une verge de travers d’arain ou de fer, por mettre une chandoile emprise,	have in the middle a rod of iron or steel to insert a handle;
et en soient et grans et petites selonc les maladies et l’eaige de ces qui les prenent;	and be large or small according to the diseases and age of those who take them.
car les ventouses des enfans sont autres que des vielz, et des maigres que des gras.	For the ulcers of children are different than those of adults, and thin ones from fat ones.
Et doit on ensi mettre ceste ventouse sus lou membre:	And this ulcer should be placed thus upon the member:
empren la chandoile de cire ou .i. linement, et le met emmi la ventouse au traver de la verge qui est emmi la ventouse,	Apply the plaster of wax or linen thread and place it across the rod that is within the ulcer.
si que li clartez soit au fons de la ventouse qu’elle ne brule le malaide;	So that the light is at the bottom of the bladder so as not to burn the patient
et puis la met sus lou membre, et tes dois soit sus lou pertus que nos avons dit, si que quant on vuet, si en va li vapor, et oste on la ventouse;	and place it on the member, and your fingers should be on the opening as we have said, so that when one looks, if steam comes out, then remove the bladder;
et emprent on le linement si com devant, et le rencomence sovent, se tu as mestier.	and wrap it with the linen thread as before, and repeat it often if needed.
En la ventouse donques qui est aministree em maladie de pleuresin, a tout aigue, n’a point de verge ne de pertus, et n’est amenistree fuer que quant ele est plaine d’aigue, et est mise sus lou membre tant soulement;	In the blister administered for disease of pleurisy, there is no thorn or prick, and it is not applied unless when it is full of water, and it is placed only on the member.
et c’est li forme:	and this is the form:
Sansues ne sont amenistrees fuer que en membres ou on ne puet mettre ventouses por lour petitece, si com levres et gencives, et semblans leus;	Blisters are not applied unless to members where blisters cannot be placed due to their small size, such as lips and gums, and similar places.
et en leus desnuez de char, si com doi ou neis, et autres semblans;	and in bare areas of skin, such as palms or soles, and other similar places.
et li qualitez de l’user si est que quant tu trueves sansues que sont en aigues douces nettes sens porreture, si les pren;	And the qualities of the user are such that when you find wounds that are in sweet, clean waters clear to the touch, take them;
et les met une nut en aigue douce, tant qu’elles soient famillouses, et n’aient rien en ventres;	and place them in a fresh water bath until they become familiar with it, and have nothing inside of them;
et puis soit sainiez de voinne et de ventouse, puis frote le membre tant k’il soit rouges, et met sus les sansues;	then let it be purged by bleeding and leeching, then rub the limb until it turns red, and place the wounds back on it;
et quant elles seront plainnes, et cherront, se c’est leu ou on puisse mettre ventouse, se li met, car ce vaut mout aprés.	and when they are full and hot, if there is a place where leeches can be applied, do so, for it is very beneficial.
Se ceu non, si leve le leu d’aisil, et puis d’aigue, mout bien, et puis l’espreint;	If not, lift the shoulder blade gently, then press firmly afterwards.
et se li leus saine trop aprés lou cors des sansues, si moille .i. drapel de lin en aigue froide, et met sus, tant que li sans soit estenchiés;	and if the shoulders are too close to the body along the back, moisten a linen cloth in cold water, and place it there until the pain subsides;
et se li sans est multipliez, si met sus vitriole broié, ou gales, et semblans choses, tant qu’il soit estenchiez;	And if the pain multiplies, place broken glass, or similar things on it to reduce the swelling.
ou tu met sor le leu moitiez de feves pelees, et les laisse tant qu’elles s’aerdent au leu, si estanchera maintenant;	or place half of the boiled and peeled beans on the spot, and leave them there until they harden at the spot, it will now stop bleeding.
et se tu en as de plus mestier, si pren autres sansues.	and if you have more need of it, take other snares.
Et se les sansues ne se vuellent prendre, si frote le leu de sanc fres, ou tu i fiche une aguille tant que li sans en isse,	And if the snares do not want to be taken, rub the spot of fresh blood, or you poke an awl through it so that the snares come out.
et puis les met sus, et tantost com elles sentent lou sanc, si s’aerdent;	and then place them on top, and as soon as they feel the blood, they harden.
et quant tu vues qu’elles chieent, si poudre sus un poc d’aloen et de seil broiet, ou de cendre, si cherront maintenant.	And when you see them falling (the joints), sprinkle a little powder of aloe and crushed seeds or ashes, they will stay in place now.
Ci comence li livre des brisures	Here begins the book of fractures
Cist chapistres est maintes fois necessaires en l’art de medicine, et est restorement de brisure et de desaluement.	This chapter is frequently necessary in the art of medicine, and it is for the restoration of fractures and dislocations.
Saichiez, chier fil, que li fol mire se gietent de cest chapistre, qu’il ne virent onques nul des anciens livres, ne lettre n’en lurent;	Know, dear child, that the foolish fools who read this chapter will never see any of the ancient books or read letters about it;
et por ceste cause est estraingie li science en nostre terre, car je n’en trovai onques nul boin;	And for this reason, knowledge of this kind is introduced into our land, since I have never found anyone skilled in it.
et n’en sai nient, fuer que par la science des anciens livres, ou j’ai tant estudiiet que je en ai traite la science, et par experiment, et par l’acostumance de ma vie;	And I do not know it, except through the knowledge of ancient books, where I have studied the subject, and by experience, and by the practice of my life.
et je vos ai jai descrit en cest chapistre ceu qui est contenut, et l’ai abregié en la fin, et ai mostreit clerement les formes des estrumens que sont amenistrez, si com j’ai fait en ces .ij. chapistres ci devant.	And I have described it in this chapter what is contained, and summarized it at the end, and clearly shown the forms of the instruments that are used, as I have done in these two chapters before.
Il covient donques que nos disons ou prologue de cest livre les sommes de la parole et les chapistres ou li saiges met son entendement, et demore sus la verteit, si que cil qui sont esproveit saichent et aprenent cest art noble, et l’aprenent a autrui.	Therefore, it is necessary that we say the prologue of this book and the subjects where wise men put their understanding, and dwell on truth, so that those who are experienced know and learn this noble art, and teach it to others.
Je dis que quant brisure ou dislocation ou torsions ou quasseure vient a aucun, si covient que tu te hastes de sainier lou malaide d’une part et d’autre, s’aucune chose ne lou te tot, si com foiblece de cors, ou enfes, ou viellars;	I say that when fracture or dislocation or twisting or disfiguring comes to anyone, it is necessary for you to clean the patient from both sides, if anything does not stop you, such as weakness of body, or infants, or old people;
ou se li tens n’est tres chaus, ou trop frois; et menjuce cholz frois, c’est a savoir froides joutes, et char d’oiseil et de chevril, et ne boive point de vin, ne menjuce nules grasses chars, et ne s’emplisse mie trop de viandes qui remplissent les voinnes de sanc, tant que tu n’aies doute d’aposteme chaut, ne d’espandement de matiere au membre; si reviegne li malaides a som premerain governement k’il a useit.	or if the time is not very warm or too cold; and avoid cold joints, that is to say cold meats, meat of chicken and shrimp, and do not drink wine, nor eat any fatty meats, and do not overfill yourself with meats that fill the veins with blood, until you have doubt about abscess heating or spreading matter in the member; if the patient returns to his first government as he used it.
Et quant li os brisiés comence a restourer, si covient que on norrisse le malaide de viandes que font gros norrissement, ou il ait viscositeit, si com froment cuit en aigue, et ris, et testes, et piez, et pance de vaiche, et oefz, et poissons fres, et gros vin, et semblans chose.	And when the broken bones begin to heal, it is necessary to nourish the patient with meats that make thick nourishment or have viscosity, such as cooked wheat in water and rice, meat pie, beef, mutton, fish eggs, fresh fish, strong wine, and similar things.
Car a teil norrissement se reprent mues et plus tost li brisure.	For prolonged nursing leads more often to fractures.
Et saichiez que li os brisiez des vielz et des decrepites ne se pueent mie bien reprendre ne souder selonc lor nature por la sechor des membres, ne cil ausi qui sont trop tendre, si com os de petis enfans;	And know that the bones of the old and decayed cannot be properly restored or mended according to their nature due to the relaxation of the limbs, nor those that are too soft, such as a child's bones.
mais n’a cure, ramoinne sus l’os brisiet .i. gros tenrons qui s’aert et joint le membre ensamble, tant qu’il enforce si com il fut devant; et ne li tot point de son oevre, et por ceu le covient norrir de grosses viandes, si com nos avons dit.	but there is no cure, reset the broken bone with large splints that are held tightly and join the limb together, until it heals as it was before; and not to put any weight on it, and for this reason, you must nourish it with large meats, as we have said.
Et saiches que les briseures sont diverses em maintes manieres.	And know that fractures are diverse in many ways.
Car li brisure dou chief est autre que li brisure dou pis, ou de la jambe, et je vos dirai en cest chapistre toutes manieres de brisure.	For the break of the neck is different from the break of the leg or foot; and I will tell you in this chapter all ways of breaks.
Car il i a brisure que vait a arvol, et autre en aguisant, si com li taille d’une penne por escrire.	There are breaks that heal by themselves, and others that grow worse if not treated, like the tip of a feather for writing.
Et si a brisure avec plaie, et brisure a tout une petite fendure.	And if there is a break with a wound, and a break with a small crack.
Et a chescune maniere ait son engien, et son estrument propre en la restauration, selonc ceu que li remembrance vient en son leu;	And each type has its own tool and proper instrument for restoration, according to what memory comes in its place.
et est conue li brisure de l’os par ceu que li leus est tors, et apert bien par defuer, et sone au presseir de la main;	And it is recognized as the fracture of the bone when the joint is twisted, and it opens widely by displacement, and it sounds at the pressure of the hand;
et quant il n’i a tortuositeit ne son au tochier, et li malaides ne sent mie grant dolor, se n’i a point de brisure;	And if there is no twisting or touching, and the patient feels no great pain, then there is no fracture.
mais il puet bien avoir tortuositeit, ou fendure, ou petite brisure.	But it may have twisting, or a split, or a small fracture.
Si ne covient mie que tu lou mueves a la main, mais met sus medicines que vienent ci aprés, et puis l’estraint maintenant subtilment.	Do not move the hand but put medicines that come after this on it, and then hold it gently now.
Et saiches que li brisure que vait en arvol, et sont les .ij. parties desjointes, il les covient maintenant mettre a point igalment, ainsois que apostemes chaus i viegne;	And know that the breaks which go towards the tree, and are the two parts disjoined, it is necessary to set them evenly now, so that abscesses grow not there.
et se apostemes chaulz i vient, si lou laisse aucun jor, tant que li apostemes soit apaisiez;	and if abscesses come near, let it stay for some days until the abscess is soothed;
puis le met igal au mues que tu pues legierement et saigement, et saiches que li restauration de li est plus legiere que li restaurations de celi ou il ait pieces; puis l’estraint, si com il covient ci aprés.	then set it equal to the muscle that you can easily and wisely move, and know that the restoration of it is easier than the restoration of where there are pieces; then tighten, as necessary hereafter.
Et se en l’os a piéces brisies, si l’estent de .ij. pars, se c’est mains ou piet, ou a ta main se c’est uns petis membres, ou a .ij. cordes, ou a une corde et a ta main;	And if the bone is broken into pieces and it breaks in two, whether it is hand or foot, or at your hand if it's a small member, or if there are two strings, or one string and at your hand;
et met le membre selonc sa figure natureil, si que quant les parties dou membre brisiet sont desevrees, si ramoinne par toz engiens les additions en lor leus au mues que tu pues, et garde que par ton ovraige ne viegne au malaide lesion ne doulor;	then place the limb according to its natural shape, so that when the parts of the broken limb are separated, you align them using all means possible in their places and ensure that through your work no damage or pain comes to the patient.
et ajoste bien les .ij. chiés des os selonc les millors formes.	then align well the two bones according to the best shapes.
Et le sent bien a la main s’il te semble k’il ne soit mie bien: si la dresce bellement, et ne l’estraindre mie trop, ne presser si com font cil qui i font venir par lor ovraige aposteme chaut et contraction au membre, si com nos avons veut maintes fois.	And it feels well to the touch if it seems not quite right to you: straighten it properly, and do not strain it too much, nor force it as those who bring it by their work, abscess hot and contraction to the member, as we have seen many times.
Et quant li membres est a point, si chastie bien lou malaide qu’il ne lou mueve, ne en veillant ne en dormant, ne en tornant, ne en autre maniere;	And when the limb is healed, correct the patient so that he does not move it, neither while awake nor sleeping, or turning, or in any other way.
et warde bien que li membres soit si asseurez qu’il ne sente nule dolor.	and watch carefully that the limb is so secure that it feels no pain at all.
Car quant il sent nulle dolor, si n’est mie a point, et le covient mettre en teil disposition qu’il ne sent nule dolor;	For when it feels no pain, it is not broken, and it should be placed in such a position that it feels no pain;
et te garde k’il soit mis droitement, que tortuositez n’i veigne quant il iert restorez;	and keep it straight, so twisting does not come when it is restored.
et li qualitez dou membre brisiet est selonc ceu que je te dis.	and the qualities of the broken limb are as I tell you.
Saiches que li membre brisiet sont divers em petitece et en grandor et en forme.	Know that the broken limbs can be various in smallness and size and shape.
Car il i a petis membres, si com brais et dois et semblans: si covient envoloupeir drapelz de lin molz et subtilz;	Because there are small members, such as arms and fingers, etc. It is necessary to wrap them in linen cloth, soft and fine.
et cil qui sont gros, si com cuixe et jambe: si covient envoloupeir d’un liien large et dur, car li larges liiens embraice tout le grant membre, et l’estraint de toutes pars igalment, si qu’il n’i a nule taiche;	and those that are thick, such as thighs and legs: It is necessary to wrap them in a large and hard bandage, for the broad bandages bind the whole large member evenly on all sides so that there is no swelling.
puis lie entor estoupes legieres, .iij. tours ou iiij. selonc lou membre, et estraint ta main un poc a tout le liien, puis vai au desus de la brisure et l’estraint moins, que la brisure puis esloigne un poc la brisure;	then tie light bandages around it, 3 or 4 times depending on the member, and hold your hand slightly on the bandage, then go above the fracture and bind less than the fracture, then move away from the fracture.
et mollifie lou liien poc et poc, tant que tu preignes grant partie dou leu sain, puis repren .i. autre liien, et torne entor derechief sus lou leu brisiet;	And soften the ligament little by little, until you take a great part of the healthy flesh, then take another ligament, and turn it around reversely on the broken joint.
puis revai a la partie desoz de la brisure, et l’estraint moienement, ne mie trop fort ne trop molement, si com nos avons dit en la premiere lieure desus;	Then return to the part beneath the fracture, and hold it moderately, neither too strongly nor too gently, as we have said in the first lesson above.
puis met entre les liiens estoupes de lin ou drapelz, tant qu’il soit toz igalz, puis lie tout par desus .i. bendeil, et puis met tes esteles bien faites sus, s’il n’i a aposteme ou enfleure.	Then place stuffed linen or woolen ligaments between the ligaments, until they are all even, then tie it all with one bandage, and then put your well-made splints on top, if there is no abscess or swelling.
Et s’il i a enfleure ou aposteme, si met sus chose apaisant aposteme chaut, et qui oste l’enfleure, et le laisse ensi aucuns jors;	And if there is swelling or an abscess, put something soothing for the abscess on it, and let him who removes the swelling leave it alone for some days.
puis estrain sus tes esteles, et soient de moitiet d’une large cainne rese saigement, ou de fust dont on fait les clives, ou de rains de palme, et soient selonc ceste figure:	Then hold your arms steady, and they should be half the width of a thick cane, or of a beam used for splitting logs, or of palm branches, and shaped as follows:
mais il covient que li estele que om met sus la brisure soit un poc plus grosse et plus large que les autres;	but the arm that one places over the fracture should be a little larger and wider than the others;
et soit ausi longe com il covient au membre de petitece ou de grandor;	And let it be as long as is necessary for the small or large member.
puis estraint sus les esteles ausi com tu as fait a la premiere lieure, puis lie desus un fil avenanment, si com en la premiere lieure sus la briseure;	Then tie it up with the pegs in the same way you did at the first joint, then bind over it with thread coming together, as in the first joint for the break.
plus estroit est ensus, adés moins; et covient que li fil soient moien, ne trop gros ne trop menus, et soient de lin mol;	The cord is narrower now, and it must be medium-sized, neither too thick nor too thin, and made of flax thread.
car se li fil sont gros, si com j’ai veut des oevres des folz qui font lor lieures des cordes de linement tort, et c’est grant error, car li lieure ne puet estre igal s’il est trop subtilz, et ne covient mie qu’il ait entre chescune estele moins dou doi d’espaice.	because if the cord is thick, as I have seen from the work of fools who make their joints using twisted flax thread, and this is a great error, for the joint cannot be equal if it is too thin, and it should not have less than two fingers' width between each peg.
Et se li malaides est navrez par les chiés des esteles aprés l’estrignement en leus sains, si met desoz elles estoupes de lin, ou lainne charpie, si qu’il ne se blece.	And if the patient is wounded by the heads of the ribs after the resetting in healthy places, place linseed poultices or cotton wool over them to prevent bleeding.
Quant li plaie est avec la briseure, et li keurs est rompus, je en dirai la cure ci aprés.	When the wound is with fracture and the bones are broken, I shall tell the remedy afterwards.
Et saiches qu’il ne covient mie estraindre d’esteles toz les membres brisiez le premier jor.	Know that it is not necessary to reset all the fractured limbs on the first day.
Car quant li membres est grans, se n’i covient mie mettre esteles fuer que aprés .v. jors ou .vij., ou plus selonc ta seurteit d’aposteme chaut sorvenant;	For when the limbs are large, it is not necessary to set them with force except after 5 or 7 days, or more according to your certainty of the abscess healing.
et vez ci la maniere des emplaustres anciiens por restorer brisure, dislocation, et torsion: et est que tu pren de la farine que se tient as parois dou molin, et la confis avec abun d’uef, et met ceste confection, ne trop clere ne trop espesse, et en use, et c’est li commune maniere de l’emplaustre restorant la brisure a plusors dispositions, et meismement as femmes et as petis enfans, car il n’est mie ne trop chas ne trop frois.	And here is the method of ancient plasters for healing fractures, dislocations, and twists: it is that you take flour that remains in the mill's walls, mix it with plenty of egg, and apply this mixture, neither too thin nor too thick, and use it; this is the common method of restoring a plaster for healing various fractures, and especially for women and small children, because it is not too hot or too cold.
Autre maniere d’emplastre restorans la brisure et la dislocation et la torsion: pren З abareis et ladani et enule et asefetide et gomme arabique et mugat, ana .x. З.; mirre et aloes, ana .v. З.; alechil .viiij. З.; et en fai poudre, et les melle avec aubun d’uef; se li complexion de l’ome est chaude, si use de cest emplaustre, car il est de bone composition, et restoure les os brisiés hastanment, et vaut a plusors homes.	Here is another method for plasters that heal fractures, dislocations, and twists: take barley meal, salt, vinegar, asafetida, and Arabic gum, in amounts of ten; myrrh and aloes, in amounts of five; alchil, eight; grind these ingredients into powder and mix with plenty of egg. If the patient's complexion is hot, use this plaster, because it has a good composition and quickly heals broken bones for many men.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre que vaut a torsion: pren mugat et vismalve, ana .x. З.; mirre et aloes, ana .viiij. З.; acaice vi. З.; bolic armenic .x. З., et broie bien, et confit avec aigue ou abun d’uef, et l’aministre.	Another method of plaster for twisting: take mugat and vismalve in amounts of ten; myrrh and aloes in amounts of eight; acacia wood in six; Armenian bolus in ten; grind it well, mix with water or plenty of egg, and administer it.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre a jointes et as os desevrez de lor leus, et apaise la dolor sorvenant, et le taille usent de l’os, et la briseure: pren lainne novele, et la moille en aisil et en oile cuit, et met sus lou leu. Cist emplastres ne restoure mie, mais il est boins por apaisier d’aposteme chaut, et oste proprement les dolors.	Another method of plaster for joints and bones displaced from their places, and to relieve the pain occurring, and it is applied with cutting the bone and breaking: take new linen, wet it in water and oil, and put it on the place. This plaster does not restore [the condition], but it is good for relieving abscess heat and proper bones pain.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre qui restoure les os brisiez: pren foilles de figuier seches, et foilles de pavol terrestre, et broie ensamble, et fai emplaustre.	Another method of plaster to restore broken bones: take dried fig leaves and ground ivy leaves, grind them together, and make a plaster.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre a la restoration de la brisure de l’os et por amenusier lou remenant de l’aposteme. Pren racine de vismalve, camomille, flors de violettes, farine de veces, de chescune une partie; et broie, et confis avec vin, et se li membres est eschaufez, se le confis avec aigue de coriandre moiste, ou d’aigue, et en use.	Another method of plaster for the restoration of broken bones and to hasten the healing of an abscess: take root of mallow, chamomile, violet flowers, flour of oats, from each one a part; grind them together, infuse with wine, and if the limb is scalded, use it with coriander water moistened or plain water.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre plus fors que li premier, quant aposteme dur vient a la restauration dou membre. Pren racines de vismalve, et semence de lin, balauste, mellilote, et sansuce, et flors de violetes et de camomille, de toutes ana une partie; et broie, et confit avec aigue de salz, ou aigue douce, ou avec vin, selonc la chalor du membre, et son repos.	Another method of poultice stronger than the first, when an abscess hard comes to the restoration of the member. Take roots of mallow, and flax, balm, clover, and wormwood, and flowers of violets and chamomile, all in equal parts; and grind and cook with salt water, or sweet water, or with wine, according to the heat of the member, and its rest.
Ypocras dist en son livre c’on ne mette sus lou membre brisiet por restorer fuer que cerote fait de cire et d’oile, et nulle autre chose plus, et dist qu’il soit entre dous ne trop molz ne trop durs.	Hippocrates wrote in his book that nothing should be placed on a broken member for restoration except a plaster made of wax and oil, and no other thing more, and he said it should be between soft and hard but not too much of either.
Et il semble galien c’on doit mettre sus lou membre brisiet, por restoreir, choses seches un poc chaudes, si com mirre et aloes et encens et semblans choses, si com nos avons dit.	It seems Galen said that for restoring a broken member, dry and slightly warm things should be placed on it, such as myrrh, aloes, incense, and similar things, as we have stated.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre que vaut a lesion et a dolor: pren mugath et chevolz d’omes decopez, ou pennes d’oiseil, et vismalve, et seil igalment, et les broie, et en fai emplaustre et lou lie.	Another method of plaster that is good for injuries and pain: take mugath (possibly a kind of flour) and crushed bones from men or feathers of birds, also mallow, and mix it equally; grind them into a paste and apply the mixture.
Et puis lou deslie un poc aprés, et pren garde se li malaides ne sent nule dolor, ne ne s’est meus li os de son leu; si ne lou deslie par mains jors	Then loosen it a little afterwards, and take care that the patient feels no pain, nor has the bone moved from its place; do not dislocate it for many days.
Et se dolor vient au leu, ou prurite, sens repos ou enfleure, si te haste, et le deslie, et oste l’emplaustre maintenant; et pren drapeil legier, et esponge de mer moiste, et plonge en aigue, et en leve lou leu, tant que li prurite cesse, et soit apaisie li dolor;	And if pain or itching comes to the place, with no relief or swelling, hasten, dislocate it, and remove the plaster immediately; take light cloth, sea sponge moistened, dip in water, and apply to the place until the itching stops and the pain is soothed.
puis laisse reposer lou membre une houre, puis met sus lainne seche, moillie en aigue ou en oile roset, et lie sus une nut, tant que tu soies seur d’aposteme chaut;	Then let the member rest for an hour, then put dry linen on it, wet in vinegar or rose oil, and tie it with a nut until you are sure of the abscess heating up.
et repose li enflammation dou membre, et soit ostee li dolor, puis rencomence la lieure subtil, et un poc d’emplaustre, et ne l’estraindre mie si fort com devant; et subtilie tant qu’il soit sanez.	And let the inflammation of the member rest, and let the pain disappear, then resume tying it gently, a little plaster, and do not strain it too much as before; tie it delicately until it heals.
Et se tu vois que aposteme chaus et roujor et dolor et enfleure sont jai osteit dou tout, et tu as mestier d’emplaustre et de liien, si le rencomence, si com tu a fait premier igalment.	And if you see that the abscess has healed and turned red, swollen, and pain has disappeared, and you need plaster and linen, then resume tying it as you did before equally.
Et s’il ne vient au membre nient de ceu que nos avons dit, si ne le desliier fuer que aprés .iij. jors ou .iiij. ou .v. ou .vij.; et aucune fois le laisse .xx. jors, selonc ce c’on voit, tant que li briseure s’aert, et aproche li ajostement de la char sus;	And if no injury comes to the limb as we have said, do not dislocate it unless after 3, 4, 5 or 7 days; and sometimes leave it for 20 days, as one sees, until the break heals and the joint approaches the flesh above.
adonques lou restraint plus que premier, et li engroisse sa viande, si com j’ai dit devant; et se tu vois lou leu sechier plus que mestier n’est, saiches que norrissemens n’i puet venir;	Then bind it more tightly than before and fatten the flesh, as I have said before; and if you see the joint dry out too much, know that nourishment cannot enter.
arose lou donques d’aigue chaude tede, toutes les fois que tu lou deslies, et ce soit chescun tier jor, et eslaiche un poc la lieure;	Then apply warm moist heat to the joint, every time you dislocate it, and do so three times a day, and loosen the binding slightly.
par cest ovraige donques cort li norrissemens au membre, et esmende hastanment ceu que font li fol mire, que restourent le membre tortement: c’est malvais, et si est ovraiges paourous, et je n’i voi autre chose que dou lassier et de l’ovrer droitement.	Through this work, therefore, cut the nerves of the limb and repair as much as possible what the foolish physician leaves dislocated: it is wrong, and it is a fearful task, and I see nothing else but to ease and to work directly.
des diverses manieres de brisure	Of various ways of breaking
Maintes manieres de brisures sont, et diverses figures, et les causes sont destintees;	There are various ways of breaking and different shapes, and their causes have specific purposes;
car il a brisures que sont faites de percussion d’espee, et li colz oste tout l’os jusc’a syfac qui est desoz l’os, si com fait haiche ou fust; et por ceu est apelee ceste maniere de briseure «haichure».	For there are breakages made by the impact of swords, and the collarbone breaks the whole bone up to the shaft which is beneath the bone, as a haw or club does; and for this reason, such a breakage is called "haw-breaking".
Ou li espee cope l’os par desus sens percier, et est apelee ceste maniere de brisure «absolue»; et est li plaie de ces .ij. brisures grans ou petite.	For the sword strikes the bone from above causing it to be broken completely, and such a breakage is called "complete break"; and these are the wounds caused by either great or small complete breaks.
Et s’il i a percussion emboee, ou fendure ou de colz de piere, ou de cheoir sus piere, ou d’autres semblans.	And if there is a thrust-through injury, a fracture or falling on stone, or other similar injuries.
Et s’il a brisure persant, qui aproiche jusc’a la toile qui est desoz l’os, ou elle est sus l’os, et est ceste plaie ou grans ou petite.	And if there is a persistent fracture, which reaches up to the membrane that is beneath the bone, or it is on the bone, and this wound is either large or small.
Et si a plaie qui est reponue en l’os ausi subtil com uns chevous, et est li fendure petite, et por ceu est apelee ceste brisure «capillaire»;	And if the wound is healed in the bone as fine as a hair, and the fracture is small, and for this reason it is called this fracture "capillary".
et si la plaie qui est faite ou par ferir de piere, ou par cheoir, ou par semblant chose, et fait entrer la piece de l’os aval, et est li leus chevez si com font li chaudelier quant il fierent sus les chaudieres; si entre li piere dedens.	and if the wound is made either by piercing with a stone, falling, or in similar ways, and drives a piece of the bone inside, and the limbs are closed as a cook does on top of pots; if the stone enters within.
Et ceu avient plus a sous qui ont ou chief moistes os, si com chief d’enfant;	And this happens more often in those who have or a moist skull bone, such as a child's head.
et avient a toutes ces manieres de brisure que pieces menues en sont desevrees si com esteles; et je em parlerai en son leu.	And it happens in all these ways of fracture that small parts are displaced as pieces, and I will speak about it in its place.
Et conoissons toutes manieres de briseures par la detraction sus elles, et l’inquisition a tentes, et par la char corrumpue qui est sus.	We know all ways of fracture by the distraction on them, and the examination with probing, and by the rotten flesh that is above.
Li semblance capillaire est conue par ceu que quant on a descovert l’os, et on frote enche sus, si apert li brisure noire.	The similarity of hair-like appearance is known by those who, when the bone is discovered and scraped over it, an opening appears black at the fracture.
En la cure de la brisure, pren garde as accidens dou malaide, et se tu vois nul malvais accident, si com vomissement de cole, et amission d’entendement, et estension, et paumeson, et fievre ague, et les eulz issir fuer et rougir, et autres semblans em plusors dispositions, si ne puet saner sens doute.	In the treatment of a fracture, beware of the sick person's condition, and if you see any harmful symptoms such as vomiting of blood, loss of consciousness, swelling, numbness, fever, pallor, and other signs in various conditions, it cannot heal without doubt.
Et se tu ne vois accident espoantauble, et tu esperes salut, si comence la cure.	And if you do not see any doubtful symptoms and expect a healing, then start the treatment.
Et quant li navrez vient premier a toi, et c’est en yver, si covient oster l’os devant lou quatorzime jor au mues que tu pues.	And when the wound first comes to you, and it is in winter, then remove the bone before the fourteenth day if possible.
Et se c’est en esteit, si te haste d’oster l’os devant lou septime jor, ainsois que li toile desoz l’os soit corrumpue, et vienent li accident que nos avons dit.	And if this is the case, hasten to remove the bone before the seventh day, so that the tissue underneath the bone is not corrupted, and the incidents mentioned will occur.
Et se li brisure de l’os vient jusc’a la toile que cuevre lou cerveil, si covient que tu fendes la partie fendue ensi: et est que tu preignes lou chief dou malaide navreit, et descuevre sus l’os en toutes les manieres que tu pues, et sus la figure de la plaie plus souef que tu pues,	And if the bone fracture reaches to the tissue that covers the brain, you must cut the broken part as follows: and it is necessary that you take hold of the patient's head, and expose above the bone in all ways possible, and on the figure of the wound more gently than possible.
et se decorrement de sanc vient au descovrir l’os, ou aposteme chaus, se li aide de ceu qu’il covient, et est que tu emplisses lou leu de drapelz moilliez en oile roset;	and if blood corrosion occurs when the bone is exposed or an abscess forms, help with what is necessary, and it is that you fill the wound with linen soaked in rose oil.
et fai reposer la plaie tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez, et soies asseurez de decorrement de sanc; puis comence entor l’os a oster, et c’est fait selonc .ij. manieres d’ovraige: l’une manieres si est que tu copes au taillement estroit devant, et c’est li forme:	And make the wound rest until the abscess is calmed and you are assured of the flow of blood; then begin around the bone to remove it, and this is done according to two ways of work: one way is that you cut narrowly in front, and this is the shape:
Et puis i boute .i. autre taillement plus grant que lou premier.	And then make another incision larger than the first.
Et li seconde maniere si est que tu aies nombre de taillemens divers, les uns estrois et les autres larges, et soient a pointe, et soient de fer inde; et en oevre legierement, que tu ne bleces le chief.	And the second way is that you have various incisions, some narrow and others wide, pointed and made with an iron blade; and work lightly, so as not to cut the tendons.
Et se li os est fors et durs, si covient que tu lou perces entor, ainsois que tu i aministres taillemens avec tareres, ne mie parfont qu’il ne percent outre l’os dou test, et doit avoir desus la pointe une marge ou .i. cercle, que ne laisse passer la pointe outre l’os; et t’en covient avoir plusors, si que chescuns viegne en son leu de l’espés de l’os, si que tu aies tareres por toz test; et c’est li forme des .iij. manieres de tareres:	And if the bone is out of place and hard, it is necessary that you pierce around it, in such a way as you administer incisions with trephines, but not so much that they cut through the bone to the other side, and there must be a margin or circle above the point to prevent the tip from passing beyond the bone; and you must have more than one, so that each comes into its place along the width of the bone, so that you have trephines for all sides; and this is the form of the four kinds of trephines.
Li qualitez por percier entor l’os brisiet est que tu mettes .i. tarere sus l’os, et torne a tes dois tant que tu saiches que li os est perciez; puis remet lou tarere autre part un poc aprés, et ensi fai tout entor, puis cope as incisoires l’espaice de l’os qui est entre les pertu, et fai ceu plus subtilment que tu pues, et legierement, si com nos avons dit, tant que tu en traies l’os a ta main, ou a aucun des estrumens que tu as si com tenailles, pinceures; et garde que tu ne touchier au cerveil ne au syfac.	The qualities for piercing around the broken bone are that you put one trephine on the bone, and turn it with your hands until you feel that the bone is pierced; then move the trephine a little farther away, and do this all around, then cut the space of the bone between the perforations as subtly and gently as possible, following what has been said, until you draw out the bone or any of the tools you have such as pliers or tweezers; and be careful not to touch the brain or the sinus.
Et quant tu avras l’os perciet, et trait, si couvient que tu reses l’apreteit qui est demoree de l’os a tout .i. autre estrument semblant a un incisoire, mais il covient qu’il soit plus tenves et plus subtilz que li autre incisoire;	And when you have pierced and treated the bone, it is necessary that you reset the tightness remaining between the bone and any other tool resembling an incisor, but it must be thinner and more subtle than the other incisors.
et s’il demore rien des petis os, ne nulles escailles, si les oste legierement a .i. des estrumens; puis cure la plaie de tentes et d’oignemens que nos avons dit.	And if any small bones or no scales remain, gently remove them with instruments; then treat the wound with bandages and salves as we have said.
Et li autre maniere d’ovraige si est cil que Galiiens dist, qui est plus saus; et le loa molt fort, et c’est sa parole.	And the other method of work is that which Galen describes, who was very skilled; and he holds it in high esteem, and this is his saying.
Il covient premier que tu descuevres une partie de l’os, lai ou li brisure apert mues, si que quant tu avras descovert celle partie, si metras desoz lou chief de cest incisoire lenticulaire, de coi ci est li forme:	First, you should expose a part of the bone where the break is open, so that when you have exposed that part, place the lenticular anvil on top of it as shown by its form:
Et ne trenche mie d’une part, et est li partie ague en .ij. costez, si que li trenchans est devers l’os; puis fier d’un petit maillet sus, si que tu copes legierement l’os tout entor, et te done bien en garde de la toile que est desoz;	And do not cut it from one side, and the parts are sharp in two edges, so that the cutting is towards the bone; then hit with a small hammer on top, so that you lightly chip away at the bone all around, and take care of the cloth that is underneath.
s’elle est aerse a l’os, si l’oste legierement, car on l’oste bien sens nuisement, et sens paor.	If it is near the bone, chip away lightly at the bone, for one chisels well with harm and with fear.
Et se li brisure de l’os ne perce jusc’a la toile, et li os est copez tant soulement par desus, et il i a petites pieces, si couvient rere celle asperiteit, et oster les escailles au raseur subtil dont tu dois avoir diverses quantitez, por amenistrer en chescun leu le plus covenauble, selonc l’ovraige et la figure de la brisure.	If the bone breaks through to the cloth, and the bone is chipped only from above, and there are small fragments, then it is necessary to smooth over the roughness, and remove the scales with a sharp scraper of different sizes, in order to bring the most suitable one for each place, according to the work and shape of the fracture.
Si reis devant de grant raseurs, et aprés de plus subtilz, et ne cesser de ceu faire tant k’il soit bien.	The patient should shave himself with great razors, then with more subtle ones afterwards, and should not cease until it is well done.
En chescune des autres tailleures capillaires et brisure subtil, covient que tu amenistres cause selonc son adrecement; et c’est chose que n’est mie reponue a celui qui a mis son estude en cest art.	In each other kind of hair cut and subtle breakage, it is necessary that you bring the cause according to his guidance; this is not a matter for anyone who has put his study into this art.
Et se li syfac est descovers, si covient que tu preignes .i. drapeil de lin, selonc la quantiteit de la plaie, et le moille en oile roset, et le mete sus la plaie;	If the wound is exposed, you must take one linen cloth, according to the size of the wound, and moisten it in rose oil, and place it on the wound.
puis pren .i. autre drapeil doublé en .ij. ou en .iij., et le moille en vin et en oile roset, et le met sus le premier drapeil; et fai ceu plus legierement que tu pues, que tu ne grever lou syfac, puis aministre par desus .i. autre liien, et ne l’estraindre mie fuer que tant k’il teigne la plaie soulement;	Then take another cloth doubled either in 2 or 4 layers, moisten it in wine and rose oil, and place it on top of the first cloth; do this more gently so as not to burden the wound, then administer another string over it but do not tighten it any further than covering the wound.
et le laisse ensi .i. jor ou .ij., tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez, puis le deslie, et i aministre medicines si com racines de lis, et farine de veces, et poudre d’encens, et aristologe, et semblans choses; et de ces choses fai poudre, et met sus la plaie, et i aministre adés medicines mondefians sens mordication;	And let it remain for one or two days until the abscesses calm down, then release it, and administer medications such as marshmallow roots, barley flour, incense powder, arum, and similar things; and from these things make a powder, and apply it to the wound, and immediately administer trustworthy medications without harm.
et warde que li plaie soit adés nette, que tu n’i laissier mie l’oignement, ne n’i laissier mie assembler bowe, car quant bowe s’asemble sus la toile dou cerveil, si la corront et porrist, et avient au malaide grans malice; car quant on met sus lou syfac chose mordant, si nercist par desus.	And ensure the wound remains always clean, do not leave any ointment on it, nor allow pus to accumulate, for when pus accumulates on the brain tissue, it corrupts and rots, causing great harm to the patient; for when something bitter is applied to it, it burns through from above.
Pren warde donques, se nulz mavais accidens vient au malaide, si com nos avons dit, si est doutable sens doute.	Therefore, take care that no bad accident happens to the patient as we have said, for it is doubtful with a doubt.
Et se noiror n’i vient fuers que por la medicine c’on a mise sus, que teil vertu ait, si covient que tu preignes une partie de miel, et .iij. parties d’oile roset et en glue .i. drapel, et lou met sus lou syfac;	And if blackness does not come violently except through medicine that we have placed there, which has this property, you should take a part of honey, and 3 parts of rose oil and one piece of cloth and mix them together;
puis lou cure de manieres de cures qu’il couvient, tant qu’il soit sanez.	then heal it in the manner of treatments that are needed, until it is healed.
Saiches que aucune fois sont brisies les .ij. parties dou neis desus, ou li une par li soulement, car ce sont .ij. os; et cil desoz est cartillaginous, et ne brise mie, si ne fait fuer k’enbower ou tordre, et puis saine.	Know that sometimes the two parts of the nose above are broken, or just one of them because they are two bones; and the one below is cartilage, and does not break but only bows or twists, and then heals.
Et se l’une des .ij. parties est brisie, si covient que tu boutes ton petit doi ou pertus dou neis, et met igal cele brisure dedens a ton doi indice, et au pouchet par defuer, tant que li neis reveigne selonc sa figure natureil;	And if one of the two parts is broken, you must put your little finger or thumb into the nostril, and insert the breakage into the index finger of the same hand, and into the hollow part facing outward, until the nose regains its natural shape.
et fai ce legierement, et warde que li malaides ne sente dolor par ton ovraige.	and do it gently, and be careful that the patient does not feel pain due to your work.
Et se li brisure est en la partie desus lou neis, et ne puet venir li dois au leu, si couvient que tu lou mettes igal au chief d’un rait un poc gros.	If the breakage is in the upper part of the nose and the finger cannot reach it, then you must insert a small splint into the nostril.
Et se li brisure est de .ij. pars, si refai autretel, et te haste de restorer lou premier jor, se tu pues;	And if the break is in two parts, then you should set it again, and hurry to restore it as soon as possible, if you can;
se ce non, aprés lou septime ou le disime, quant li apostemes chaus est apaisiez, puis bouthe au chief dou neis tentes de drapelz de lin, se li brisure est en une partie.	If not, after the seventh or tenth day, when the abscess has subsided, then apply the dressing of linen to the head of the needle if the break is in one part.
Ou tu boutes .i. autre d’autre part, se li brisure i est; et soient les tentes si grosses qu’eles emplissent les pertus dou neis.	Or you apply another to the other side, if the break is there; and let the dressings be as thick as they fill the openings of the needle.
Et dirent aucun restorour c’on doit moillier les tentes em burre, et muer chescun jor. Il ne me semble mie que ce soit bien, mais covient qu’elles soient moillies en confection d’aubun d’uef, et de poudre de molin; puis laisse la tente, tant que li os soit fers, et li cartilaiges endurcis.	And they said that any remedy should moist the dressings with butter and change them every day. It does not seem good to me, but it is necessary that they be moistened in a mixture of egg yolk and flour powder; then leave the dressing until the bone is hard and the cartilages harden.
Et aucune fois boute on ou neis pennes d’oie en leu de tentes, et si a .i. souef drapeil entor, et se tient la briseure, et soffle li malaides parmi; or fai lou kel ke tu vues.	And sometimes feathers of goose are inserted in place of tendons, and if one side is wrapped with a thin cloth, and the breakage is held, breath is blown through it; do as you see fit.
Et se apostemes chaus vient au neis tandis com tu i oevres, si i met cerote ou coton moilliet en oile roset, ou en .i. poc de dyaquilon.	If abscesses come up while you are working, put either wax or cotton soaked in rose oil, or a little bit of quicklsilver.
Et se apostemes chaus n’i vient, si met emplastre par defuer, de farine de sisament, et de poudre d’encens, confites avec aubun d’uef, puis met sus estoupes legieres, et ne liier mie lou neis;	If abscesses do not come up, put an ointment on the outside made of sizemant flour and incense powder mixed with egg yolk, then place light poultices on top, but do not tie the wound shut.
et se li brisure dou neis est petite, et il est brisiés em menues pieces, si l’estrai as estrumens covenables a ceu, puis cout la fendure, et la cure de choses enjanrans char, et soudant, si com emplastres et oignemens covenables a ceu;	And if the fracture of the neck is small, and it is broken into small pieces, extract them with appropriate instruments, then make an incision, and treat the wound with suitable charms, plasters, and ointments.
et s’il n’a dedens lou neis nule plaie, si lou cure de tentes, et i met cainnes de plonc, tant qu’il soit sanez.	If there is no wound within the neck, treat it with bandages and place planks until it is healed.
de la routure de la mandibule	of the fracture of the jawbone
Quant li mandibule est route desoz, et il n’i a point de plaie defuer, et li brisure est defuer tant soulement, et n’est mie brisiez en dous, fuer que corbelz dedens, si le conoist on legierement.	When the lower jaw is dislocated and there is no wound outside, and the break is only outside but not broken through, if one knows it easily, it means there is a curvature within.
Il covient, se li brisure est en la destre partie, que tu boutes ton doi indice en la bouche dou malaide; et se li brisure est en la mandibule senestre, si boute ton doi indice de la main destre, et boute la brisure dedens legierement, et l’afaite a l’autre main par defuer, et met igal.	If the break is on the right side, you must insert your index finger into the patient's mouth; if the break is in the left lower jaw, insert your index finger of the right hand, and gently push it inside, then adjust it from outside using the other hand, and make it even.
Et se li brisure de la mandibule est desevree en .ij., si covient que tu aministres extension de .ij. pars, tant qu’il soit igalz.	And if the break in the lower jaw is dislocated by .2 (two fingers), you must administer an extension of .2 parts to make it equal.
Et se commovemens des dens avient, ou routure, si les estrain d’un fil d’or ou d’argent ou de soie, puis met sus la mandibule brisie cerote, et met sus .i. drapel double; et met sus lou drapel une grant estele bien faite, ou une piece de cuir igal, longe et large selonc la mandibule, et la lie sus au mues que tu pues, et comande a malaide qu’il se repose, et menjuce viandes legieres.	And if there is movement of the teeth or fracture, hold them with a thread of gold, silver, or silk, then place a broken bit gag on the mandible and put one double cloth on top; put a large, well-made splint or equal piece of leather on top, long and wide according to the mandible, and attach it where you can, and instruct the patient to rest and eat light food.
Et se tu vois que li figure se chainge, si le deslie au tier jor, et puis remet a point ceu que c’est chaingiet; et met emplaustre sus, de la poudre dou moulin avec abun d’uef ou farine de sisament, aprés ceu que tu as osteit lou cerote; et met sus l’emplaustre lainne legiere, et se li emplaustres s’aert, et li disposition dou malaide ne se chainge, laisse le tant k’il soit sanez; maintes fois est sanez en .iij. semainnes.	If you see the figure changing, dislocate it after a day, then reset it to its original position; put a plaster on top, with flour from the mill mixed with egg or oatmeal after removing the gag; put a light linen bandage on top, and if the plaster sets, and the dislocation does not change, leave it until it is healed; many times it is healed in four weeks.
Et se apostemes chaus vient, si amenistre ceu que nos avons dit maintes fois.	And if an abscess appears, apply what we have said many times before.
Et s’il i a brisure et plaie ensamble, rewarde se nule piece de l’os en est ostee; si subtilie de l’oster as estrumens covenaubles a ceu.	And if there is a fracture and wound together, make sure no piece of the bone has been removed; if necessary, remove the splinter with suitable tools.
Et se li plaie est estroite, si l’eslarge a flaime selonc ta necessiteit.	And if the wound is narrowed, stretch it with fire according to your need.
Et quant tu avras ostees toutes ces pieces, et il n’i demore nule, si cout la plaie, s’ele est large, et met sus .i. des emplaustres covenaubles a ceu, por enjanrer char, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when you have removed all the pieces and none remain, if necessary, close the wound if it is wide and apply one dressing suitable for that purpose to promote healing until it is healed.
de la forcele	of the forceps (instrument)
Li forcele brise plusors fois devant, devers l’espaule, et li brisure si est selonc .iij. manieres: ou elle est brisie et desevree en .ij., et i a pieces, et est li plus legiere a restorer; ou il i a brisure avec plaie.	The forceps break multiple times towards the shoulder, and the fracture is in four ways: either it is broken and dislocated in two parts, split into pieces, and is the easiest to restore; or there is a fracture with a wound.
Et li ovraiges si est quant li brisure est sens plaie, que tu aies .ij. ministres, si que li uns teigne l’ajutoire que sent la forcele brisie; et li autres estende lou col vers la partie; puis met igal la brisure a tes dois, si que li forme soit si com il covient, et n’i ait ne apparance ne chevement.	And the work is when the fracture has a wound, you should have two assistants, one of whom holds the shoulder that feels the forceps broken; and the other stretches the neck towards the affected area; then align the fracture in your hands so that the form is as it should be, and there is no appearance or deformation.
Et se tu a mestier de plus estendre, si met desoz l’espaule au malaide une spere reonde de drap, ou de lainne, et soit grosse selonc ta necessiteit; et estent et lieve la forcele, et estraint le spere a ta main, si que tu mettes igal la brisure, si com il covient.	And if you need to stretch more, put a round cushion of cloth or linen on the patient's shoulder, and make it as large as necessary; then extend and raise the forceps, and press the cushion with your hand so that the fracture is aligned as it should be.
Et se tu ne pues traire le chief de la forcele au defuer, por ceu qu’elle vient em parfont, si covient que li malaides gise sovin sus son hatereil, et met desoz l’espaule .i. oreillier moien, et boute li ministres l’espaule aval, tant que li os de la forcele soit levez.	And if you cannot pull the head of the shoulder out by force because it comes in fully, then the patient must lie on his affected side, and place one pillow under the shoulder, and push the ministers to move the shoulder downwards until the bone of the socket is raised.
Et puis adrece la brisure a tes dois, et se tu lou trueves debrisiet, si covient que tu fendes sus; et trai fuer les pieces legierement, et se li os ne puet joindre por aucun sormontement, si le cope a l’un des incisoires que tu as; mais que tu mettes desoz la forcele cest estrument, por warder lou syfac:	Then direct the fracture to your fingers, and if you see debris, then it is necessary that you cut across; and separate the pieces gently, and if the bone cannot join due to any obstruction, hit it in one of the incisions you have made; but place this instrument under the socket to prevent dislocation.
et semble une cuiller, et n’est mie chevez, et soit ausi large com il lou covient, selonc la grandor de l’os et la possance de l’uevre; et ait .ij. chiés, si com tu vois, et soit li uns larges, et li autres estrois, si com est li routure de la plaie que tu as fait quant tu as trait les os;	and resemble a spoon, but not concave, and be of such size as necessary, according to the size of the bone and the power of the work; and have two prongs, as you see, and let one be wide, and the other narrow, as is the groove of the wound that you made when you treated the bones.
et quant tu es asseurez d’aposteme chaut, si cout la plaie, et se li routure est petite, ou tu doutes aposteme chaut, si emple la plaie de drapelz et de tentes, selonc sa quantiteit.	And when you are certain of the abscess being heated, if it opens, and if the hole is small, or you doubt the abscess has opened, then use cloths and bandages on the wound, according to its size.
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si moille .i. drapel en oile roset et en aisil et en vin, et met sus.	And if hot irons come for it, moisten a cloth with rose oil, asafetida, and wine, and place it on top.
Li estrignement de l’os, quant il est sens plaies et sens tailleure, est que tu mettes sus l’os l’enplaustre de la poudre dou molin et d’aubun d’uef, et met estoupes legieres sus, et met une spere desoz l’assele, se tu en as mestier;	The tightening of the bone, when it feels sore and swollen, is to place a plaster made from flour of mill and egg white on the bone, put light packs on top, and insert a splint beneath if needed.
puis pren une tres grant bende d’une palme de large, puis met .i. drapeil double sus estoupes, et l’emplaustre; puis pren une estele subtil de .iij. dois de large et de lonc, et l’envoloupe entor celui bendeil, si que li chief dou bendeil soient pendant;	Then take a very thick bandage of one palm's width, then put a double cloth dampened on top of it and roll it up; then take a thin needle three fingers wide and long, and wrap it around the bandage so that the edge of the bandage is hanging.
et met l’estele sus la briseure, et torne le bendeil sus lou col, et desoz l’asselle sainne, et desoz l’asselle malaide; et la ramoinne de chescune partie, et quant tu vois ke li lieure tient la briseure avenanment, et tu vois clerement que li estele ne se muet desus l’os brisiet, si le rewarde chescun jor, et quant li liiens eslaiche, si lou restraint;	and place the needle on the fracture, then turn the bandage around the neck, and below the patient's jawbone, and below the patient's cheekbone; and roll it from each side, and when you see that the bandage is in alignment with the fracture, and you clearly see that the needle does not move over the broken bone, then hold it every day, and when the threads slip, restrain it.
et fai gesir lou malaide sus son dos, et li met quant il dort .i. petit orillier desoz l’assele, por lever l’ajutoire en haut; si aligera li brisure de la forcele par l’aligement de l’espaule, ou tu li lie lou bras au col, et ne lou desliier se malvais accidens n’i vient, jusc’a .xx. jors;	and make the patient lie on his back, and put a small pillow under his jaw, to raise the shoulder; if the fracture aligns due to the alignment of the shoulder, or you bind the arm to the neck, and do not unbind it except for a bad accident occurs, until twenty days.
puis rencomence l’emplaustre, se tu vois qu’il en ait mestier, et l’estraint et le laisse ensi, tant qu’il soit restorez; et elle est restoree au plus en .xxviij. jors, et en moins a aucuns homes.	Then repeat the treatment, if it is needed, and hold it in place until it is restored; and it is restored within 28 days at most, and less for some men.
de la brisure de l’espaule	on the fracture of the shoulder
Poc avient que li espaule brise ou large leu ne em mileu, et ne lou seit on fuers que par lou touchement; si l’apareille selonc la figure de la brisure, et la ramoinne selonc sa forme natureil, en toutes les manieres que tu pues; puis met sor le leu poudre dou molin avec abun d’uef, et estoupes legieres, et met sus .i. drapeil double; puis met sus une estele large et subtil, un poc plus large de l’espaule, et se desoz l’estele est chevemens en aucun leu de l’espaule, si emple celle cheveure d’estoupes de lin, si que li estele siece igalment; et puis l’estraint a tout une grant bende fermement, si que li estele ne se mueve de son leu, et regarde le liien chescun jor; et toutes les fois k’il amolist, si l’estraint, et met igal l’estele s’elle est fuer de son leu, et gise li malaides sus son costeit; et li espaule est restouree en .xx. jors ou en xxv,  Et quant cist nombres est acomplis, si le deslie, et soies seur, car ce n’est mie os qui se mette fuer legierement.	If the shoulder is broken or dislocated, it will not heal on its own, and one should only try to put it back in place through touch; if it is aligned according to the shape of the fracture or dislocation, and reset according to its natural form in all ways possible; then apply powder from a mill with plenty of egg whites and light ointments, and cover with two layers of cloth; then apply a broad and thin splint, about one finger wider than the shoulder, and if there is any gap between the splint and the shoulder, fill it with linen ointment so that the splint fits evenly; then tighten it firmly to keep the splint in place and observe the ligament every day; whenever it loosens, re-tighten it and adjust the splint if it is off its place, and let the patient rest on their side; and the shoulder will be restored within 20 or 30 days, and when this number is completed, remove the splint carefully, as it is not bone that moves easily.
Et se une piece de l’os tent avant, et point desoz lou keur, si fent sus, et l’oste, et fai ceu que nos avons dit en la brisure de la forcele d’apaisier aposteme chaut.	And if a bone fragment protrudes in front and not beneath the skin, lift it up, remove it, and follow what was said earlier to heal an abscess with hot cautery.
de la brisure dou pis	of the fracture with fish
Li peis est aucune fois brisiez em mileu, mais ce avient poc; mais il brise sovent au defuer. Et quant il est brisiez emmi, si decline au desoz, et sent li malaides grant dolor, et faute d’alainne, et toust, et par aventure vomist sanc, et apert li chevemens en l’os brisiés, et lou sent om bien.	The limbs are sometimes broken in the middle, but this is rare; however, they often break at the joint. And when it is broken inside, it slips downwards, causing the patient great pain, and lack of strength, and immediately vomits blood, and the wound opens in the broken bone, and it feels badly.
Et li restoracion si est que li malaides gise sovin sus son dos, et li met .i. cussin entre les espaules, puis presse les espaules, et li assemble les costes des .ij. costelz a tes mains, et subtilie dou mettre igal a toutes les manieres que tu pues, tant que li figure de l’os soit si com il covient; puis met sus emplaustres et estoupes desus l’estele subtil de salz, ou d’autre fust legier, et l’envoloupe en .i. drapeil, et la lie sus l’os brisiet, si qu’elle ne se mueve; et torne le liien reondement au dos, et l’estraint avenanment, et rewarde chescune houre la liure, et s’elle ramolist, si l’estraint; et s’il lou covient desliier, por corrosion ou por prurite que vient au leu, ou dolor ou aposteme, si te haste, et lou deslie, et raie l’emplaustre, et adresce ceu qui i est venus de manieres de cures; puis ramoinne l’emplaustre, et l’estraint tant qu’il soit sanez.	And the restoration is that the patient lies on his back with one cushion between the shoulders, then presses the shoulders, and assembles the ribs of both sides to your hands, and subtly puts it all in equal alignment in every way possible until the bone figure is as required; then put a plaster and bandages over the broken bone, or a lighter splint, and wrap it in one cloth, and tie it on the bone so that it does not move; then turn the limb round and round, and tighten it gradually, and check each hour whether it heals, and if it swells, tighten it; and if it needs to be dislocated due to corrosion or pruritus at the joint, or pain or abscess, hurry up and dislocate it, remove the plaster, and direct the one who has come there in ways of treatment; then reset the plaster, and tighten it until it is healed.
de la brisure des costes	of the broken ribs
Saiches que li briseure des costes ne vient fuer que en leus gros aprés le dos, et au chief dedens, et ne ploient fuer que por ceu qu’eles sont glairouses; et le sent om bien a l’inquisition as dois.	Know that the fracture of ribs does not occur except in large ones behind the back and near the neck, and they do not break unless they are slippery; and it hurts greatly upon examination at the joints.
Et li restoremens si est que tu met igal la brisure, si com il covient. Et puis met l’emplaustre, et l’estraint d’une estele, se tu en as mestier.	And the restoration is that you set it even again, as required. Then put the splint and hold it with a stick, if needed.
Et se li brisure des costes est declinans au dedens, si sent li malaides tres grant dolor, et pointure, ausi com de pleuresin, car li os point la toile; et alaine a poinnes, et toust et vomist grant planteit de sanc, et c’est de grief santeit, et li ancien i ont mis grant engien.	If the fracture of the rib is slanted within, the patient feels great pain and swelling, as if from pleurisy, for the bone points to the skin; and the fingers become hardened, and immediately vomits a large amount of blood, which is a grave illness, and the ancients have made great effort to treat it.
Et si a de ces qui dient qu’il le covient aministrer viandes qui enflent le ventre, por bouter la briseure au defuer.	And if among those who say that it is necessary to administer foods that swell the abdomen, to push the fracture outward.
Nos ne faisons mie ceu, que apostemes chaulz n’i viegne, s’il n’i est venus.	We do not bring hot irons unless they have come (to be used).
Et s’il i est venus, si le saine.	And if they have come, then let them be heated.
Et dirent aucun d’ous c’on met ventouses sor le leu, por sucier forment, et c’est semblant a raison; toutevoie, doutance i a que li ventouse n’atraie les superfluitez au leu por la disposition de foiblece.	And they said that one puts vents on the side to suck out pus, which seems reasonable; however, there is doubt whether the vents do not attract the superfluidities to the side due to weakness in position.
Et dirent aucun d’ous c’on doit covrir le leu de lainne moillie en oile chaut, et met on tentes entre les costes por metre igal la lieure entor, puis soit curez de la cure de pleurisin, de viande et de medicine.	And they said that one should cover the side with damp linen dipped in hot oil and place bands between the ribs to make the wound equal on all sides, then it should be cured with the cure of pleurosy (inflammation of the pleura), meat and medicine.
Et se li malaides sent grant dolor qu’il ne puet soffrir par l’os qui point la toile, et doutance est au malaide, si covient fendre sus lou leu de la coste brisie, et covient mettre desoz .i. estrument por warder lou syfac; et adonques doit on trenchier l’os, et traire legierement, et puis coudre les .ij. levres de la plaie, s’elle est grans, et le curez d’emplaustres, tant qu’il soit sanez. Et se apostemes chaus vient, si met sus drapelz moilliez en oile roset, et met sus lou leu; et cure tandis le leu de ceu qu’il covient a aposteme, et soit gisans sovins sus lou costeit ou il doit, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the patient feels great pain that he cannot endure through the bone which does not penetrate the skin, and there is doubt in the patient, then it is necessary to make an incision over the broken rib, and it is necessary to put an instrument underneath for support; and then you must cut the bone, draw it gently, and then sew up the two edges of the wound if it is large, and dress with plasters until it heals. And if pus comes, place moistened linen soaked in rose oil on top, and cover the area; cure the area as necessary for the abscess, and lie still on the side where it should be, until it heals.
de la brisure dou col	of the broken collarbone
Aucune fois vient briseure as os dou col, et poc avient k’il ploie; et ausi a l’espinee dou dos.	Never does a break occur in the bones of the collarbone, and it never bends; and similarly in the spine of the back.
Et quant ce avient a aucun, et tu vues savoir s’il sera sanez ou non, si pren warde se tu vois ses mains mollifiies et enflees et mortes, et ne les puet movoir ne estendre, et quant tu les poins d’une aguille, si ne lou sent. Saiches qu’il est mortelz em plusors dispositions, et s’il les muet et sent bien quant on les estraint et point, saiches que li jointure de l’os est sauve, et que li malaides iert curez, s’on i met cure.	And when this happens to someone, and you wish to know if they will recover or not, take notice if their hands are softened, swollen, and dead, and they cannot move or stretch them, and when you prick them with a needle, they feel nothing. Know that they are mortally ill in many positions, and if they do not speak and feel well when you squeeze and prick them, know that the joint of the bone is saved, and that the patient will be healed if care is given to it.
Et se semblans chose vient a l’espinee dou dos, et tu vues savoir s’il iert sanez ou non, si pren warde se li piez sont amollis, et se li accident i sont qui sont em mains, et sus lou dos saut ventositeit et egestion sens volonteit; et quant on l’a sovineit sus son ventre, si saut egestion sens volonteit. Et quant il est sovinez sus son dos et il vuet asseller, si ne puet. Saiches qu’il est mortelz: si ne laboreir mie en sa cure.	If similar things happen to the spine of the back, and you wish to know if it will recover or not, take notice if the feet are softened, and if there is an injury that is in the hands, and the back arches involuntarily and emits a sound; and when it is placed on its stomach, it arches involuntarily. And when it is placed on its back and wishes to straighten, it cannot. Know that it is mortally ill: do not labor at its healing.
Et se cist accident ne li vienent, si est li chose plus legiere.	If this event does not occur to them, then the situation is easier.
Et li cure si est que tu rewardes s’il i a aposteme chaut, si met sus l’espinee oile roset ou oile de moieuf d’uef, tant qu’il soit apaisiez; puis met sus un des emplaustres confortans et sechans, et le lie d’un liien, et comande au malaide a reposer; et ne dorme mie sus celle partie ou il sent la dolor, tant k’il soit sanez.	And the cure is that you soothe if there is an abscess that burns hot, put on top of it rose oil or egg yolk oil until it calms down; then put on top one of the soothing and drying plasters, and tie it with a string, and command the patient to rest; and do not let him sleep on that part where he feels pain, until he is healed.
Et se aucuns os se dessevre, si covient coper sus lou keur; et oste l’os, puis assemble les .ij. levres de la plaie, s’elle est grans, a une costure, puis le cure d’oignement enjanrant char, tant qu’il soit sanez; et se li chiés de l’os est brisiez, ki est apelez li «chiés de la kowe», se i boute ton pouchet de ta main senestre, et le met igal a l’autre main a ton pooir, puis met l’emplaustre et l’estele sus, se tu en a mestier; puis l’estraint, et s’il i a os desevreit, si fent sus, et l’oste, et cure la plaie tant qu’elle soit sanee.	If any bone dislocates, it is necessary to cover it with a cloth; then remove the bone, next join the two edges of the wound together with stitches if it is large, and heal it with soothing ointment for as long as it heals; and if the head of the bone is broken (which is called "the head of the cow"), push your left hand's pocket into it and hold it equal to your right hand strength, then put on an plaster and a dressing, if you have them; then tie it, and if there is bone dislocating, make it go back, and remove it, and heal the wound until it heals.
de la brisure de l’os de la hainche	of the break of the shinbone
Poc avient que li os de la hainche soit brisiez, et s’il avient, si n’avient fuer c’un poc d’amenuisement au chief; et fent dou lonc, et decline au pardedens, et vient au malaide dolor au leu, et pointure, et enfle ceu que brise.	It happens that the bone of the thigh is broken, and if it happens, there is only a slight reduction in mobility at the hip; it becomes long, bends toward the outside, and causes pain at the site where it is broken.
Et li restoration si est que tu estendes ta main sus, tant que tu soies sus la briseure; et saiches quelz est li brisure et li figure de li; et se li brisure est au chief soulement, si met igal cele brisure, tant qu’ele soit a figure natureil.	And the restoration is that you extend your hand above [the break], until you are above the broken area; and recognize which [bones] are broken and their shape; and if the break is only at the hip, set the break straight, until it is in its natural shape.
Et se li brisure est dou lonc, ou elle decline au dedens, si fai gesir le malaide sus son ventre, tant que li restauration de cele brisure te soit aparillie.	And if the break is long or bends inward, place the patient on his back, so that the restoration of the break can be seen.
Et quant tu l’avras mise igal, si met sus l’emplaustre, puis met sus une estele de fust ou de keur, et estraint la briseure, si qu’ele ne se mueve; et emple le leu desoz les costes, tant que li lieure soit igalz.	And when you have set it straight, place the plaster on top, then put a stick or a splint on top, and hold the fracture in place so that it does not move; apply the [medical] solution under the ribs until the fracture is healed.
Et comande au malaide k’il dorme sus son costeit sain, ou sus son dos.	Instruct the patient to sleep on his healthy side or on his back.
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si n’i tochier, tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez, et met sus ceu que nos avons devant dit; et puis revien a la restauration, et l’estraint si com il covient, s’il n’i a nul mavais accident; et c’est li maniere.	And if an abscess appears, do not touch it until the abscess has calmed down, and apply what we have previously mentioned; then return to the treatment, and hold it as necessary, if there is no bad incident; and this is the manner.
de la brisure de l’ajutoire	Of the shoulder breakage
Li adjutoires est ceu qui est entre lou coute et lou chief de l’espaule, et s’il est brisiez, si le doit on restorer selonc l’une des .ij. manieres: dont l’une est que tu pren .i. fust plain de moiene groissor, selonc ceste forme:	The shoulder joint is between the neck and the chest of the shoulder, and if it is broken, it should be restored according to one of the two methods: one of which is that you take a large splint made of wood or bone, in this shape:
Et lie as .ij. chiés .ij. liens, et les pent en haut, et siece li malaide sus .i. siege; puis li giete som bras brisiet sus le fust, tant qu’il viegne a l’aissele, et ait em mi une corbeure de fust, puis pent sus aucune pesant chose ou li ministres l’estende aval; puis mette li mires la briseure igal a ses mains ensamble, tant que li briseure retorne si com il covient.	And tie the two shoulders with two ropes, and place them high up, and make the patient lie on one seat; then lower the broken arm onto the splint, so it comes to rest, and have a slight curve of the splint in the middle; then place a heavy object or the assistant holds it down below; then have the assistant hold the breakage equal with his hands until the breakage returns as it should.
Et li autre maniere si est que on sovine le malaide sus son hatereil, et li lie la main a son col, puis comande a .ij. ministres que li uns teigne ceu qui est sus la briseure a ses mains, et li autres teigne desoz a tout .i. liien, et estende chescuns a sa partie.	And the other method is that you lay the patient on his back and tie his hand to his neck, then command two assistants that one holds above the breakage with both hands, and the other holds below with all the ropes, extending each rope to its side.
Et se tu vues que li estraction soit plus fors, si estraint .i. liien desoz la briseure, et sus la briseure, et estende chescuns des ministres a sa part. Et se li briseure est prochiene au chief de l’espaule, si covient que tu mettes .i. liien moien desoz l’assele, et .i. autre vers lou coute, desoz la briseure; et ausi se li briseure est devers lou coute, si i covient mettre .i. liien legierement, sens labor, tant que li briseure soit igalz sus lou leu, et sus lou coute; puis met igal la brisure, si com il covient, et l’estraint, se apostemes chaus n’i vient.	And if you see that the extraction is forceful, hold one ligament beneath the break and another on top, and extend each of the attendants to their part. And if the break is close to the shoulder head, you must place one ligament in the middle beneath the fracture and another towards the skin, beneath the break; and similarly if the break is towards the skin, you should place one light ligament without labor, as long as the break is level with the surface, and with the skin; then make it level, as required, and hold, unless an abscess does not come.
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si ne l’estraindre mie jusc’a .vij. jors, et met sus lainne moillie en aisil et en oile roset, tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez; puis l’estraint, et li maniere de l’estraindre si est que tu mettes l’emplaustre sus la briseure, puis assemble le bras sus l’ajutoire, et met ta main sus l’espaule ou sus lou sein; et met le drapeil, et estraint sus l’ajutoire, et sus lou bras, si que li bras soit en leu d’esteles, s’aucune chose ne le te deffent, ou se li os n’est muez.	If an abscess does come, do not hold it for more than seven days, and place a soft cloth in oil on top of the abscess to soothe it; then you can hold it, and the method of holding is that you put the clamp on the fracture, then bring the arm towards the shoulder, and place your hand on the shoulder or chest; place the bandage, and hold towards the shoulder and towards the arm, such that the arm remains in a straight position, unless something prevents it, or if the bone is not moved.
Et se tu doutes que li os ne se mueve, si use d’esteles, et met sus la brisure une estele plus large et plus fort des autres, et ait entre chescune estele .i. doi d’espaice, et soit chescune estele si grans qu’elle passe la briseure .iij. dois de chescune part; puis estrain sus les esteles, ensi com j’ai dit au comencement dou chapistre sus la briseure, plus fort et moins en aloignant.	If you doubt that the bone does not move, use splints and place a larger and stronger splint than the others on the fracture, and let there be one inch of space between each splint, and let each splint be so large that it passes the break two inches from each side; then hold on the splints, as I said at the beginning of the chapter on the fracture, stronger and less in alignment.
Et se tu vois l’assise des esteles, et l’estrignement, si com nos avons dit, en l’oure que tu restoures le membre brisiet, et tu doutes l’aposteme chaut, si le laisse a liier jusc’a septime jor, si com nos avons dit; puis regarde chescuns .iij. jors lou lien, que prurite ne enfleure n’i viegne au leu, ou li norrissemens ne puist venir au membre por ceu k’il est trop estrois. Si l’adrece, si com nos avons dit.	And if you see the abscess of the wound and the constriction, as we have said, during the time you are restoring the broken limb, and you doubt about the suppuration heating up, leave it to heal for seven days, as we have said; then look every three days at the suture, so that inflammation does not swell or come to the place where the new flesh cannot come to the limb because it is too tight. If it becomes infected, do as we have said.
