Et se nulz telz accidens n’i vient, si ne lou desliier fuer que aprés .iij. jors ou plus, et dorme li malaides sus son dos, et ait ses mains sus son stomac; et met desoz l’ajutoire .i. cussin plain de laine igalment, et regarde chescune houre dou jor ou de la nut, que li figure dou membre brisiet ne se mueve, ou ne soit amollis li liiens; si l’adrece par la vertu de medicine, et li done la viande que nos avons devant mis, en teil maniere que li viande soit au premier subtilz; et quant il comance a reprendre, si soit grosse. Et est costume que li ajutoire et li jambe doient estre repris en .xl. jors dou tout; et adonques lou doit on desliier et aministrer bain et medicines d’oignemens por le leu adrecier.  Et se li estricture est laide et emboee, si demore a desliier .l. jors ou .ij. mois.	If no such accidents happen, do not undress it for more than two days or less, let the patient lie down on his back and put his hands on his stomach; place a linen cloth of equal thickness underneath the wound and observe every hour of the day or night that the figure of the broken limb does not move or is not softened; treat with medicine to help it heal and give the food as previously mentioned, in such a way that the food is initially subtle; when it starts to recover, it should become thick. It is customary for the wound and the leg to be redressed every forty days; and then undress it and administer baths and ointments to aid healing. If the constriction is ugly and swollen, wait one day or two months before undressing it.
de la brisure du bras	of the break in the arm
Li bras est compos de .ij. os, qui sont apelez li dui «foscile», de coi li uns est petis, et est cil qui enseut le pouchet; et li autres est grans, et est cil qui est desoz, devers lou petit doi; par aventure brise li grans foscile soulement, ou li petis, et par aventure andui ensamble.	The arm is made of two bones, which are called the "two shinbones". One is small and it forms the elbow joint; and the other one is large, and it is located below, near the little finger. Sometimes, only the large shinbone breaks, or sometimes both break together.
Quant li petis fosciles est brisiez, li restaurations est legiere, et li sanations; et quant li grans est brisiez, si est li sanation male, et plus griés que quant il sont brisiez andui ensamble. Se c’est li petis foscile qui est brisiez soulement, si le covient poc estendre legierement, et mettre igal.	When the small shinbone is broken, the restoration and healing are easy; but when the large one is broken, the healing is bad, and more difficult than when both break together. If it's only the small shinbone that breaks, you should gently extend it slightly and align it properly.
Et se c’est li grans foscile, si le covient estraindre plus fort; et l’estende sus .i. cussin, et teigne le pouchet de la main plus haut des autres, et li petis dois plus bas des autres dois, et soit li malaides croisiez sus lui meisme, et .i. cussin devant lui plus haut, que li malaides ne soffre nule labor; puis estende li ministres som bras a la partie desoz a sa main, ou a .i. liien, et uns autres ministres a .i. autre au desus. Et puis le mette li mires igal, selonc sa millor forme.	If it's the large shinbone that breaks, it must be pulled harder; and extend it by one cubit, raise the elbow of the hand higher than the others, and the smaller finger lower than the others, and cross the patient over himself, and place a cubit in front of him higher, so that the patient does not suffer any pain; then stretch the assistants' arms to the area below his arm or one link, and have another assistant at the top. And then align the limb as best as possible according to its best form.
Et se en la brisure a pieces, si met chescune en son leu, et s’il en i a nule desevree ke poigne lou keur, et tu ne la pues restorer en son leu, si fent sus et l’oste, si com nos avons dit devant.	And if it is broken into pieces, place each one back in its place, and if any of them cannot be held straight and you cannot restore it to its place, make a bone splint, as we have said before.
Et se avec la briseure a plaie, je en ai parleit au chapistre singuler; si pren la cure.	If with the break into a wound (i.e., fractured open), I have spoken of it in the specific chapter; take care.
Et se en l’encomencement dou restorement sorvient apostemes chaus, si glue .i. drapeil de cerote fait d’oile roset et de cire blainche, que ne soit mie ne trop durs ne trop molz; et lie .i. drapeil par sus subtilment, tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez. Et puis oste lou cerote, et i met l’emplaustre de la poudre dou molin avec abun d’uef, pues met les esteles, et soit li estele de la briseure adés plus fors, et un poc plus large que les autres; et saiches que il doit avoir vj. esteles ou bras em plusors dispositions: soit que li briseure soit en l’un des os, soit en .ij.; et estraint plus sus la briseure que autre part, et toz jors moins en aloignant, si com j’ai dit au comencement dou chapistre; et soient li drapelz que sont sus la briseure molz et moistes, et ne soient mie dur ne aspres; et soit li filz, dont il est estrains, de lin, ne trop gros ne trop menus, si com nos avons dit. Et rewarde lou membre et lou liien aprés aucuns jors.	If in the beginning of the setting (i.e., during the healing process), abscesses arise, apply one cloth made from lard oil and white beeswax, neither too hard nor too soft; and stick one cloth subtly on top, until the abscesses subside. Then remove the wax, and put on the dressing of powder from the mill with plenty of egg, then place the sticks, and let the sticks for the fracture be more prominent, and slightly larger than the others; and know that it should have 7 sticks or more depending on the position of the fracture: whether in one bone or two. Pull up more on the fracture than elsewhere, and always less in aligning, as I have said at the beginning of the chapter; and let the cloths above the fracture be soft and moist, not hard nor harsh; and let the thread, which holds it, be of linen, not too thick nor too thin, as we have said. And observe the member and the ligament afterwards after some days.
Et se aucuns mavais accidens vient au membre, si com prurite ki vient au membre, si covient que tu aroses lou membre d’aigue chaude, tant que cil prurites soit apaisiez; et laisse le membre ne mie estroit reposer. Et puis rencomence l’estrignement, et se li liiens est amolis et li os desevrez, et semblant chose, si l’adresce.	And if any bad accidents happen to the limb, such as prurit that happens to the limb, you must irrigate the limb with hot water until the itching is alleviated; and do not let the limb rest. Then begin the setting again, and if the ligaments are weakened and the bones dislocated, as well as similar things, give advice accordingly.
Et se pren warde se li norrissemens ne puet venir au membre, por ceu qu’il est trop estrois, si covient que tu l’amollisses .i. poc, et laisse ensi aucuns jors, tant que li norrissemens i corre, et puis l’estraint.	If the narrowing of the anus cannot come to the limb because it is too tight, then you must soften it for a little while, and leave it for some days until the narrowing passes, and then set it.
Et se nules de ces choses que nos avons dit ne vient au malaide, si ne lou desliier jusc’a .xx. jors. ou enqui entor, puis li pent les mains a son col, et soit ses cols igalz, et se warde de movement et de degitement, et dorme sus son dos; et saiches que ceste briseure est restoree en .xxx. jors ou en .xxxv., et par aventure en .xx. jors, selonc les compositions et les complexions des vertus.	If none of these things we have mentioned come to the patient, do not loosen him for up to twenty days. Or around that time, he should put his hands on his neck and make his necks even, and guard against movement and displacement, and sleep on his back; know that this fracture will be restored in thirty or forty days, and by chance in twenty days, according to the compositions and complexions of the virtues.
de la brisure de la main	Of the break of the hand
Saiches que au dos de la main et as nous des dois avient poc de briseures, et n’i vient mais que ploieure maintes fois.	The back of the hand and fingers rarely suffer breaks, but it often bends multiple times.
Et quant li plante de la main est brisie ou ploie, si covient que li malaides siece croisiet, et siet droitement devant lui igalement; puis met sa main sus la toie estendue, et estende li ministres les os brisiez, et les mete igalz li mires, tant qu’il soient bien joint; et met l’emplastre et les estoupes, se apostemes n’i vient, puis i met une estele selonc la quantiteit dou leu; et soit envoloupee en .i. drapeil de lin.	And when the palm of the hand is broken or bent, the patient should lie down crosswise, straight in front of him equally; then place his hand on a cloth spread out, and extend the broken bones, and align them with mirrors, until they are well joined; and apply a poultice and lint, if an abscess does not develop, then apply a splint according to the size of the limb; and it should be wrapped in one linen cloth.
Et se li briseure est au pardedens entor lou ventre de la plante, si fai une spere de drapelz, et comande au malaide qu’il l’estrigne a sa plante brisie; et puis l’estrain d’un lonc drapeil, et soit li estele de keur souef ausi grans com li plante de la main, et l’estraint, si com il covient.	And if the fracture occurs at the front near the abdomen of the foot, make a bandage from rags, and instruct the patient to bind it to their broken foot; then bind it with a long strip of cloth, and ensure the wound is covered as well as the hand's palm, and bind it as needed.
Et se li brisure est au defuer, si covient que tu mettes une estele sus, et une autre desoz en la plante, si que li mains soit overte et droite, puis le lie tot entor la main, et estanche lou liien entre les dois.	If the fracture is at the back, it is necessary that you place a bandage on top and another under the foot to keep the hand straight, then bind it all around the hand, and tighten the lace between the fingers.
Et se li briseure vient a aucun des nous des dois, se c’est li pouchés, si le met igal, si com il covient; et l’estraint avec la plante, et se tu vues si met une estele droite petite por lever la briseure, et ne se mueve; et se li brisure est as autres dois, si com en l’indice ou l’un des autres, si le met igal, et lou lie avec lou doi sain qui est aprés; ou tu les lie toz en .i. tenant, que mues vaut, ou tu met sus une estele, si com ou pouchet; et pren warde en la restauration et en la disposition d’aposteme chaut, et secor ceu qui i vient, si com j’ai dit.	If the fracture comes in any of the fingers (such as the thumb), make it straight as needed and bind with the palm; if you see that a splint is needed to lift the fracture and keep it from moving, place a small straight splint there; if the fracture is in other fingers, such as the index or another finger, make it straight and bind with the healthy finger that is next to it; or bind them all together in one place, as you would for a thumb; take care in restoring its position and proper healing of the abscess, and watch for any signs of infection, as I have said.
de la cuixe brisie	of the broken leg
Li os de la cuixe est maintes fois brisiez, et bien le voit on quant elle torne devant et derrier; et li restauration si est c’on lie .i. liien desus la briseure, et .i. autre desoz.	The bones of the leg are often broken, and one can see it when it twists in front and behind; and the restoration is such that one tie is placed above the break, and another below.
Et li malaides gise sus sa faice, puis estende chescuns ministres son lien a sa part igalment; et c’est quant li brisure est emmi l’os.	And the patient lies on his face, then extends each minister evenly to their respective positions; and this is when the break has been set in the bone.
Et se li brisure est prochiene a la racine de la cuixe, si soit li uns des liiens devers lou poignil, et li autres liiens desoz la briseure. Et ausi s’elle est prochiene au genoil, et adonques soit li liens delez lou genoil, et soit li extension aval; puis mette li mires l’os igal a ses .ij. mains, tant qu’il soit selonc sa figure natureil, et puis met l’emplaustre, et lou lie, se apostemes chaz n’i vient.	And if the break is near the root of the leg, one tie should be towards the ankle and the other ties below the break. And similarly, when it is near the knee, then the ties should be on the side of the knee and the extension below; then the surgeon should align the bone with both hands according to its natural figure, and then apply the splint, and tie, but do not use an arrow if there is no abscess present.
Et s’il i a aposteme chaut, si le laisse apaisier puis revien a ton ovraige et a ta cure; li lieure est faite en teil maniere.	And if there is an abscess boiling, let it calm down before returning to your work and care; the treatment is made in this manner.
Il covient que tu envoloupes sus la briseure .i. bendeil dur doublé en .ij. ou .iij., et en demoure li superfluitez, puis torne la jambe tant que li talons veigne a la racine de la naige, et boute .i. fil lonc entre la cuixe et la jambe, delez lou genoil desoz, et veignent li chief dou fil au desus; puis torne sus la jambe et sus la cuixe le bendeil, puis met sus la briseure esteles, et met une estele sus l’os de la jambe; puis emple le leu vuit entre la jambe et la cuixe de drapelz souef por mettre igal l’estrignement, puis comence a liier forment .iij. tors ou iiij. sus la briseure; et quant plus vas en sus de la briseure, et moins l’estraint; puis enten as .ij. chiés dou fil que tu as bouteit entre la jambe et la cuixe, et en lie .iij. esteles que sont desus, puis revai au desoz au chief dou fil, tant que tu veignes delez le piet; et l’estraint, si qu’il ne se mueve de son leu, puis le laisse ensi, puis k’il n’i vient ne aposteme ne enfleure n’autre semblant.	You must place a bandage, thick and doubled in two or three layers, and let the excess remain, then turn the leg until the heels come to the root of the calf, and insert one long thread between the thigh and the leg, below the knee, and bring the end of the thread above; then turn the leg and the thigh over the bandage, then put two bands across the break, and place a band on the bone of the leg; then use soft cloth between the leg and the thigh to keep the straining equal, then begin to tie four or five turns around the bandage; and as you go higher on the bandage, loosen it; then hold the two ends of the thread that you inserted between the leg and the thigh, and tie four bands that are above, then return to below the head of the thread, until you come down to the foot; tighten it so that it does not move from its place, then leave it like this, so that neither abscess nor swelling nor any similar thing appears.
Et s’il i avient, si le deslie, et adresce ceu que i vient, si com nos avons dit maintes fois; et se il i a pieces de l’os que poigne, si le covient ewer, s’om puet; et s’on ne puet, si covient fendre le leu, et traire fuer; et le cure si com nos avons dit, tant k’il soit sanez.	And if there is a fracture, dislocate it and treat the part that is injured, as we have said many times; and if there are pieces of bone protruding, they must be cut off, if possible; and if not, the limb must be broken and marrow extracted; and cure it as we have said until it heals.
Et aucune fois est brisie li cuixe ensi c’on i met esteles, si com en l’ajutoire et ou bras; toutevoie, en la restauration ensi faite ne cloche mie li malaides.	And sometimes the thighbone is broken in such a way that pegs are inserted, as in the shoulder or arm; however, in restoration of this kind, the patient does not experience any pain.
Et saiches que li cuixe est restoree en .l. jors, ou poc moins ou poc plus, selonc les diversitez des complexions.	Know that the thighbone is restored in one or two days, depending on the different complexions [of patients].
de la ruelle dou genoil	of the groin [area]
Saiches que en la ruelle dou genoil avient poc brisure, mais elle ploie maintes fois. Et s’elle brise, si n’est mais c’une fendure, ou .i. pertus, et avient a tout plaie, et sens plaie, et ce sent om bien.	Know that in the knee joint there is little damage, but it bends many times. And if it breaks, it is not just a fracture, or a wound, but all injury, and there is pain everywhere.
Et li restauration si est c’on mette igal ceu qui est rons a ses dois, tant qu’il soit assemblez mues c’on puet; puis met l’emplaustre, et i met une estele reonde, se tu en as mestier, et l’estraint si com il covient, puis rewarde toutes les dispositions que nos avons dit ens autres briseures, si com aposteme chaut et autre semblant; si met a chescun accident ceu k’il li covient, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And the restoration is that one puts equal traction on what is round at its ends, as long as it can be assembled; then place the splint, and put a round bandage, if necessary, and tighten it as required, then check all the dispositions as we have said in other fractures, such as abscess or other similar things; place whatever is needed for each accident until it heals.
de la brisure de la jambe	of the fracture of the leg
Saiches que en la jambe ait .ij. os, de coi li uns est apelez par droit non «mustelz», et li autres est apelez «foscile»; et avient tout auteil briseure com il vient au bras, et por ceu est li restauracion si com celle dou bras igalment, et li ovraiges est tout i.	Know that in the leg there are two bones, one of which is called correctly "shinbone" (tibia), and the other is called "fibula"; and it breaks just like the arm does, and for this reason, the restoration is similar to that of the arm, and the treatment is all the same.
Et se li dui os sont brisiet ensamble, si torne li jambe de toutes pars.	If both bones are broken together, the leg turns in every direction.
Et se li os subtilz est brisiez, si torne devant.	And if the thin bone is broken, it bends forward.
Et se li gros os est brisiez, si sent on grant dolor, et le voit on bien; et torne desoz. Adonques amenistre extension, et le met igal, et lie les esteles igalement; mais toutevoie, il covient se li brisure est laide, et il i a plusors pieces, que li extension soit menor et plus legiere; et l’alige selonc ta vertu.	And if the large bone is broken, one feels great pain and sees it clearly; then turn it back. Then apply extension, make it even, and tie the limbs equally; however, if the fracture is misaligned and there are more pieces, then the extension should be smaller and lighter; align according to your judgment.
Et quant tu as tout acomplit ton ovraige, si pren .ij. faixes de fust chevees que porpreignent la jambe d’une part et d’autre, et soient dou lonc de la jambe des le genoil jusque desoz; puis envoloupe en .ij. leus .i. bendeil desus et desoz, et le lie em mileu ausi, et a ceste lieure ne pora li jambe decliner a destre ne a senestre, et ensi est bien; et aucun i aministrent .i. bers dou lonc de la jambe, et s’est de fust, et i met on la jambe por warder de movement, et proprement fait on ceu en la brisure ou il a plaie; et remue chescun jor la jambe, por veoir s’il i a aposteme chaut n’autre accident; si le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	When you have completed your task, take two fists full of straw that will bind the leg from one side and the other, and be as long as the leg from the knee down to its end; then wrap it in two layers, one above and one below, and tie it in the middle so that the leg cannot decline to either the right or left, and thus it is good; and no one should bind one arrow-length of the leg, and it should be made of straw, and put the leg for protection from movement, and properly apply it at the fracture where there is a wound; move the leg every day, to see if there is an abscess or any other accident; cure it until it is healed.
de la brisure des os dou piet	of the bone fractures of the foot
A la cheville ne vient point de brisure, mais as os dou piet vient aucune fois brisure et as dois poc, et n’i avient fuer que quassure em plusor dispositions.	At the ankle there comes no break, but the bones of the foot sometimes suffer a break and also the toes; no fire is needed except in various positions.
Et s’il avient as os dou piet brisure, et tu vois ces os sormonter l’un l’autre, si mette si malaides som piet sus la terre, ausi com s’il voloit aler, et puis met maintenant ton piet sus lou sien, lai ou li os sont levez, puis le presse tant k’il reveignent en lor leus; puis met l’emplaustre et estoupes sus, et met desoz lou ventre dou piet une petite tauble a .ij. chiés plains, puis l’estraint au piet avenanment, puis que tu as envoloupez drapelz entor, et autres choses dont tu as mestier.	If the bones of the foot suffer a break and you see them overlapping each other, then place the patient's foot on the ground, as if he wants to walk, and now place your foot on his, where the bones are raised, then press it until they align again; then put a splint and padding on, and put a small table under the foot with two flat cushions, then tighten the splint towards the affected foot, then when you have wrapped cloth around it, and other things that you may need.
Et quant .iij. jors ou .iiij. seront passez, si deslie lou liien, car tu troveras les os igalz, soient brisiez, soient desaluez.	And when three or four days have passed, loosen the splint, for you will find the bones aligned, whether they are broken or dislocated.
Et s’il i a aucuns des dois brisiez, si les restoure, si com nos avons dit as dois de la main; puis met au doi brisiet une estele selonc la longesce dou doi, et soit un poc plus large, puis met desoz le piet celle tauble que j’ai dit, et l’estrain avenanment; et s’il en i a .ij. ou .iij., ou plus, brisiez, si met sus chescun doi une estele selonc sa quantiteit, envoloupee en .i. drapeil de lin, et estraint la tauble desoz lou piet; et soit estans sus lou chief de la tauble defuer lou ventre dou piet, si qu’il le teigne bien.	And if any of the two [bones] is broken, restore them as we have said for the bones of the hand; then place a splint on the broken bone according to its length, and let it be slightly larger, then put a small board underneath the injured one that I mentioned, and tighten it accordingly; and if there are 2 or 3 [broken bones], or more, break each bone separately, place a splint on top of each bone wrapped in one linen cloth, and tighten the board beneath the foot; and let the protrusion be facing the abdomen of the foot so it covers it well.
Et covient que tu n’oblier mie les autres choses que j’ai dit as autres briseures, des que nos avons dit; et secor chescun accident si com il covient.	Also do not neglect the other things I said about other fractures, after what we have said; and treat each accident according to its needs.
de la brisure de l’os dou poignil	of the bone of the thumb
Quant li os de la nature la femme est brisiez, si la fai seoir enlargie, puis l’encline a la partie dou dos, et soit tenue par derrier; puis emplisse li baile la nature de couton, et en i mette ausi gros com .i. sto; puis deboute la femme, et lieve lou dos poc et poc, et adonques saut li coton, tant qu’il vient a l’entree de la nature, et revient li os avec lou sto; et quant elle vuet pissier, si oste lou coton, et quant elle a pissiet, se li remette, et ensi faice .vij. jors ou entor: si sera restoree li brisure, et se tu vues, pren une vessie de berbis, et lie au pertus une cainne, et boute toute la vessie en la nature; puis soffle en la cainne forment, tant que li vessie soit enflee dedens: la nature si revenra li brisure; puis soit emplie de coton, et le laisse ensi aucuns jors, tant qu’il soit sanez.	When the bone of the female's womb is broken, make her sit upright, then incline her towards the lower back and hold her from behind; fill the belly with cotton and put as big a wad as a fist inside it; then turn her, lift the buttocks little by little, and let the cotton protrude until it reaches the entrance of the womb, and the bone returns with the wad; and when she wants to urinate, remove the cotton, and when she has urinated, replace it, and do this for 7 days: the break will be healed, and if you see, take a bladder of straw, tie one end to the wound, and push the entire bladder into the womb; then inflate the bladder with force until it swells inside: the break will return to its place; then fill it with cotton and leave it for some days until it is healed.
Et quant li os dou poignil de l’ome est brisiez, ou de la femme, si le restoure ensi com nos avons dit en l’os de la hainche; et ne sont mie occultees ces briseures prochienes a celui qui i met son estude et son us, et entent mon livre. Car li brisure li signifie em plusors dispositions la droite voie de la restauration: enten le donques.	And when the bone of the hand (or female) is broken, restore it as we have said in the case of a fracture of the thigh; and these breaks should not be concealed from those who study and practice this art and read my book. For the break signifies several ways to restore it: therefore follow them below.
En la verge, quant elle est brisie, pren une gorge d’oie et i boute la verge; puis envoloupe drapelz entor, et le laisse .iij. jors ou enqui entor, et il sera sanez hastanment.	In the shaft (long bone), when it is broken, put a goose's gullet around it; then wrap cloths around it and leave for 3 or 4 days, and it will heal quickly.
de brisure avec plaie	Of breakage with wound
Il covient a celui qui a brisure avec plaie, meismement s’elle est grans, si com li os de la cuixe ou de l’ajutoire ou semblant, qu’il soit sainiez maintenant, si que les sainies que nos avons dit le tesmoignent.	To the one who has a breakage with wound, especially if it is large, such as the bone of the shin or shoulder or similar, it must be set immediately, so that the settings we have mentioned take place.
Et se li plaie saine, si la restainche de vitriole, se tu n’as autre chose, puis rencomence a restorer la briseure en cele meisme houre, ou celui jor, se apostemes chaus n’i vient.	And if the wound is healthy, clean it with vitriol, if you have nothing else, then continue to restore the breakage in that same hour or day, unless an abscess comes.
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si laisse la restauration jusc’a nuevime jor, tant que li apostemes soit apaisiez, et n’i touchier ne au tier jor ne au quart, car tu i feroies venir malvais accident.	If an abscess comes, leave the restoration until the ninth day, until the abscess is calmed, and do not touch it for three days or four, because you would bring a bad outcome.
Et se li os brisiez est aparans sus lou keur descovert, si covient que tu lou mettes a point legierement a tes mains, a extension petite.	And if the bone breaks through, it must be set lightly by your hands, in a small extension.
Et se li extensions ne t’est apareillie por mettre igal a tes mains, si le ramoine a cest estrument qui est de fer, qui a .vij. dois ou .viij. de lonc, et li largesce est selonc la quantiteit de la plaie; et por ceu est mestier au mire qu’il empreigne .iii. ou iiij., selonc ceu qu’il en ait mestier en chescune cure de briseure; et soit rons et un poc gros, k’il ne ploie mie a la compression sus lou membre a ton ovraige, et soit agus devant, et gros des le mileu en avant, ensi:	If the extension is not provided for setting equal to your hands, it should be made with this tool that is made of iron, which has 7 or 8 inches long, and the width is according to the size of the wound; and therefore, the mirror must grasp 3 or 4 depending on what is needed in each cure of breaking; and be round and slightly large, so that it does not bend during the compression on the member during your work, and be sharp before, and thick from the middle forward, like this:
Et est apelez «palainche», por coi il covient que li chiés corbes soit mis sus lou chief de l’os apparent; et le boute a une fois, tant k’il reviegne, et soit igalz l’un encontre l’autre. Et se li brisure est subtilz, et li estrumens ne puet bien prendre l’os, si covient que tu copes lou chief de l’os, tant que li estrumens en ait possance.	And it is called "palainche," therefore the curved shoulders should be placed on top of the apparent bone; and push it once until it returns to its original position, making sure both are even against each other. If the break is subtle and the tool cannot properly grasp the bone, you must cut the top of the bone so that the tool has enough grip.
Et se tu ne pues ramener l’os, si com nos avons dit, si lou cope d’un estrument covenable a ceu, ou incisoire ou soieure, a ton pooir; puis reis ceu qui est demorez en l’os d’aspreteit et de menues escorces.	And if you cannot reset the bone as we have said, then strike it with an appropriate instrument, either chisel or saw, to your power; then remove that which is stuck in the bone with sharpness and small shavings.
Et quant li os est ramenez, et li malaides sent grant dolor aprés, saiches qu’il n’est mie en son leu natureil. Si fai tant qu’il soit en son leu, puis moille .i. drapeil en vin stiptique noir, et proprement se c’est en esteit; et ne mettre mie sus la plaie cerote ne autre chose ou il ait oile, qu’il n’i faice venir porriture et corruption; puis aministre esteles quant tu as restoreit l’os, et laisse la plaie descoverte, et cope la coverture tout entor, selonc la quantiteit de la plaie, et te done bien en garde que li plaie ne soit estrainte avec la brisure; et maintes fois ont ce fait li fol mire, et ont fait venir sus le malaide ou mort ou corrodent aucune fois; et soit li estrignemens plus molz et plus souef des autres brisures.	When the bone has been reset and the patient feels great pain afterwards, know that it is not in its natural place. Make it so that it is in its natural position, then moisten one linen cloth with black sticky wine, and carefully if it is summer; do not put any ointment or other thing over the wound where there is oil, as this will bring pus and corruption; then administer ointments when you have restored the bone, leave the wound uncovered, and cover the surrounding area, according to the size of the wound, and take good care that the wound is not bound with a splint; and many times have fools made this mistake, causing infection or death or sometimes rotting; and let the bindings be softer and more pliable than other splints.
Et se li plaie est male ou grans, et tu doutes que mavais accidens n’i veigne, si com nos avons dit, et tu trueves dolor au leu, si n’i covient mie mettre sus esteles; mais envoloupe entor, en leu d’esteles, drapelz durs, et les lie. Et quant tu vois aprés .i. jor ou .ij. enjanrer bowe a la plaie, si oste ceu que tu as mis sus a tout vin, et i met oignement sanant plaies, si com oignement tetrafarmaçon et semblans.	And if the wound is bad or large and you fear that some accident may occur, as we have said, and you feel pain at the place, do not apply ointments; instead wrap it with dry cloths in place of ointments and bind it. And when you see after one or two days that the wound begins to swell at the place, remove what you have put on it and apply healing ointment for wounds such as tetrafarmaçon and similar ones.
Et covient que tu deslies lou membre .ij. fois le jor, lou matin et au vespre, tant qu’il soit soudez et sanez.	And you must release the member twice a day, in the morning and at evening, until it is healed and sound.
Et covient que li membres soit aparilliez en teil maniere que li bowe corre aval legierement.	The limbs should be set in such a manner that the bone moves downward lightly.
Et se maint jor trespassent, et il ne puet souder mais rent adés bowe, saiches k’il i a petites pieces d’os, por coi il covient que tu quieres la plaie avec tente, et oste toutes ces pieces desevrees que font venir celle dolor.	If it passes for several days without healing but the bone continues to break, knowing that there are small bone fragments; therefore, you must treat the wound with care and remove all those dislocated bone fragments that cause pain.
Et se fistule vient au leu, ou autre maniere de corruption, si covient que tu le cures, selonc ceu qu’il dist en son chapistre ci devant. Et quant li os est brisiez, et apert sus lou membre, si com li os de la cuixe ou de l’ajutoire, et autres semblans des grans membres, si ne le traire mie, car maintes fois en vient li mors, mais le laisse tant qu’il porrisse; par aventure cherra par lui aprés .xx. jors ou .xxx., puis cure la plaie, se tu pues; et se tu ne pues, si la laisse.	If there is a fistula or any other form of corruption, you must treat it according to what was previously written in this chapter. When the bone is broken and opened on the member, such as the bone of the thigh or shoulder, and similar major limbs; do not drain it as many times death may come; but leave it until it can heal by itself. After 20 or 30 days, if healing occurs, cure the wound if possible; otherwise, leave it alone.
des brus qui vienent sor la sodure	The arriving bruises upon the sore
Nous vienent maintes fois aprés la santeit de la briseure, meismement quant c’est pres de la jointure, et laide chose est a veoir li figure dou membre; et par aventure ne puet faire li membres ses ovraiges naturelz.	We often see it following the breaking of health, particularly near the joint, and it is displeasing to see the appearance of the limb's figure; and unfortunately, the limbs cannot perform their natural functions.
Pren warde donques se li nous est fres: si li aministre medicines stiptiques, si com aloes, encens, et mirre, et sarcocolle, acaice, et semblans autres, ensi que tu preignes aucune de ces choses, ou toutes ensamble, et les confit avec vin stiptique ou avec abun d’uef ou avec aisil; et les met sus le nout en estoupes, et l’estraint bien, et ne la desliier en mains jors; et puis la desloie, et rencomence une autre, tant que li nodations soit ostee; ou tu estrain sus une piece de plonc bien faite; car li proprietez dou plonc si est qu’il oste toutes les enfleures desus les membres; et se li nodation est ja convertie en durteit ausi com piere, et il est besoing de l’oster, si la cope desus, et fent la superfluiteit apparent; ou tu la reis a aucun raseur, tant qu’ele soit ostee, et la cure tant qu’ele soit sanee.	Therefore, be cautious: if it is fresh, administer medicines such as aloes, incense, myrrh, and gum arabic, and similar things, so that you take one of these substances or all together, and mix them with a strong wine or with egg white or oil, and put them in poultices, and keep them on for a long time without removing them; and then loosen it, and start another, until the nodulation is removed; or you hold above a well-made piece of wood because the properties of wood are to remove all swellings from the limbs; and if the nodulation has already hardened like stone, it must be removed by cutting off the top, making the excess appear; or you shave it with any razor until it is removed, and cure it until it is healed.
dou membre qui est foibles aprés la garison	The weak member after being treated or healed
Quant li brisure de l’os est restoree, et demoure aprés li membres foibles et subtilz, si avient por mout de causes: de coi l’une est por ceu qu’il fut liiez trop estroit, et ne fut mie liiez si com il covenoit; ou por ceu qu’il i ot trop de liiens, et ne pooit venir li norrissemens au membre; ou por multitude d’arosement; ou por trop grans movements, ne mie en son houre; ou por ceu qu’il a poc de sanc en son cors, si est foibles.	When the bone fracture is restored and remains weak and subtle afterwards, this occurs for many reasons: one of them being that it was tied too tightly, but not properly bound as required; or because there were too many bandages, preventing blood supply to the limb; or due to excessive bleeding; or due to excessive movements, not at the right time; or because there is little blood in the body, making it weak.
Et li cure si est que tu faices mengier le malaide, et faire le cors tendre, tant que li sans soit multipliiez en lui; et li aministre bain, et li done joie et liesce; puis met poix sus le membre, si que li poix atraie a li grant norrissement, et l’arose sovent d’aigue tede, tant que li norrissement corre au membre; et reviegne a sa figure natureil.	And the cure is that you make the patient eat, make the body lean, until the blood multiplies in him; administer baths, and give joy and peace to him; then apply wax over the limb so that the wax attracts strong blood supply to the limb; frequently drain off the pus with warm water, until the blood flow returns to the member; and return it to its natural shape.
dou membre tort aprés la santeit	twisted limb after health
Quant li membres est tors aprés la restauration, et li os brisiez apert, et li forme dou membre est laide, toutevoie ne pert mie son ovraige natureil: si ne croire mie les folz qui dient c’on doit brisier lou membre tout de noveil, et maint fol mire ont ce fait en nostre terre; et cist ovraiges est blamez, et en vient grans malz, et par aventure li mors; toutevoie, se li nodations et li torture sont fres, si covient k’il soient arosez d’aigue chaude, ou herbes mollifians soient cuites, si com foilles de vismalve, et racines, et mellilote, et semblans choses; et li fai .i. emplaustre mollificatif, si com dyaquilon bien fait, et tu pren le muscillaige de vismalve, et la confit avec graisse de geline ou oile de sisament, et fai emplaustre sus; ou tu pren figues graisses, et les broie avec fien de colon, et semblans medicines que amenuisent le soudement.	When a limb is twisted after restoration and the bones are broken open, and the shape of the limb is deformed, yet it does not lose its natural function; do not believe in the foolish who say that one must break a limb anew, and many foolish men have done this in our land; this practice is condemned, and great harm comes from it, and perhaps death; however, if the swelling and torment are fresh, you should apply hot water or softening herbs such as mallow leaves, root, medicinal trefoil, and similar things; and make a soothing emplaster, like dittany well made, and take the myrrh of mallow, mix it with ginger oil or sesame oil, and make an emplaster; or use figs greased, grind them with wheat bran, and similar medicines that alleviate pain.
Et aucune fois est ostee li nodacion por froter continuelment et longement a mains moistes. Et soit amenistrez movement au membre chescune houre.	And sometimes the swelling is removed by rubbing continuously and for a long time with wet hands. Movement should be brought to the limb every hour.
Et se li tortuositez est enveillie et endurcie, ausi com piere, et besoins est de l’oster au fer, si la covient coper jusc’a l’os, a l’incisoire subtil legierement; et mettre cusenson et estude en la cure.	And if the tortuosity is growing hard like stone, it needs to be cut with iron, it must be covered up to the bone, with a subtle and gentle incision; and put dressing and study in the treatment.
Ci encomence li livres des dislocations	Here begins the book of dislocations
Dislocations est issue d’aucune jointe de son leu, por coi il ne se puet muevre, et est li membres mal figurez, et sent li malaides grant dolor et grant lesion.	Dislocation occurs when a joint moves out of its place, which prevents it from moving, and the limb is misaligned, causing the patient great pain and injury.
Quant dislocation vient a aucun, si le covient maintenant ramener sens targier.	When dislocation occurs to anyone, it must now be reset carefully.
Car s’on tarde, si enfle li leus, et par aventure si le remet on a poines au leu; por ceu ne covient mie c’on le mueve a l’oure k’il est enflez: maintes fois fait venir spame et autres dolors;	If one waits, the joint swells, and if it is set again at the same time, it should not be moved until it has subsided: many times this causes pus and other pain.
toutevoie, quant ce avenra, si fai sainier lou malaide, puis le laisse, tant que li apostemes chas soit apaisiez; puis arose le membre d’aigue chaude et d’oile, puis le ramoinne legierement, et cure chescun membre si com li cure venra en son leu.	Furthermore, when this happens, let the patient cleanse himself, then let him rest until all the abscesses have subsided; then immerse the affected limb in hot water and oil, then gently move it, and heal each member according to where the healing will occur.
Et j’ai ordenez les chapistres des dislocations des lou chief jusc’a piez.	And I have organized the chapters on shoulder dislocations from head to feet.
des mandibules	jaws
Poc avient que les mandibules soient desaluees andous, et li dislocations d’ambedous est selonc .ij. manieres: ou elles sont un poc ostees de lor leus, et mollifies un poc; ou elles sont desaluees entierement, et pendent vers lou pis, et cort li salive de la bouche qu’il ne la puet tenir, ne ne puet clore sa bouche, et envoloupe sa langue avec la parole.	It often happens that the jaws are dislocated in two ways: either they are somewhat disjointed from their places and softened; or they are completely dislocated, hanging towards the lower part, and saliva flows out of the mouth which it cannot hold, nor can close its mouth, and wraps its tongue with the speech.
Quant li dislocations est petite, si revient par li em plusors disposicions.	When a small dislocation returns, it often does so in multiple ways.
Et s’elle est entiere et acomplie, si covient que tu la ramoinne hastanment, et ne targier mie;	And if it is complete and has reached its full extent, you must reset it quickly and not delay.
et en tel maniere que li ministres teigne le chief dou malaide, et boute li mires som pochet de l’une de ses mains en la racine de la dislocation de la mandibule dedens la bouche, se li dislocations est de .ij. pars; et li autre doi des mains soient defuer, por mettre igal; et comande au malaide qu’il les amollisse, ses mandibules, et les mueve de toutes pars.	And in such a way that the minister holds the head of the patient and pushes one of his thumbs into the root of the dislocation of the jaw within the mouth, if the dislocation is at two points; and the other hand should be spread apart, to straighten; and instruct the patient to soften, their jaws, and move them in all directions.
Et li mires la mete igal, tant qu’elle reveigne en son leu.	And the thumb is placed evenly, until it returns to its place.
Et se li ramener est griés, meismement se ce sont les .ij. mandibules ensamble, si les arose d’aigue chaude et d’oile, tant que les ramoinnes legierement; ne ne targier mie dou ramener, si com nos avons dit.	And if it is difficult to set it, just as if it were two jaws together, warm them with hot water and oil, until they are easy to move back into place; do not force it to return, as we have said.
Et quant elles sont ramenees igalment, et li bouche dou malaide clot bien sens mollifiier, si met sus drapelz moilliez en cerote fait d’oile roset et de cire, puis le lie legierement de molz liiens;	And when they [the dislocated limbs] are reset equally, the patient should close the mouth with mildly softened linens soaked in a mixture made of rose oil and wax, then tie it lightly with many threads.
et dorme li malaides sus son dos, et ses chiés soit estans entre .ij. cussins, si qu’il ne lou mueve ne a destre ne a senestre, ne ne s’efforce mie de maixier, mais preigne legiere viande, tant que les dolors soient ostees, et soient noees les mandibules;	The patient should sleep on his back, with his arms between two pillows, so that they [the dislocated limbs] do not move to the right or left, nor force themselves in any way, but take light food until the pain is gone and the jaw bones are knitted.
et puis menjuce ce qu’il vuet legierement, et ne se travaille mie d’ovrir la bouche au mengier et au boivre, tant que li mandibule soit bien noee et sanee.	then eat as desired lightly, and do not make an effort to open the mouth for eating and drinking, until the jaw bone is healed and well knitted.
Et se les .ij. mandibules ne pueent estre remises a point a une houre, et ne sont mie converties a lor leus, si en vient fievres et sode acostumees, et par aventure solution de ventre, et par aventure vomist cole pure.	And if the two mandibles cannot be set right within an hour and are not returned to their places, fevers and usual sickness follow, and perhaps abdominal distention, and perhaps vomiting of clear bile.
Et quant tu verras ceu, adonc saiches que c’est perdicions; et maintes fois muert cil cui il avient, en .viiij. jors.	And when you see this, know that it is destruction; and many times the person who experiences it dies within eight days.
de la forcelle	of the noose (traditional English translation: neck)
Li forcele ne puet desaluer dou costeit dedens la continuation de li et dou pis, et est desaluee aucune fois au defuer, et bien le sent on.	The forceful cannot dislocate from the inside along with the ribs and it is dislocated once at the back, and this is felt.
Et li restauration si est que li malaides gise sovin sor son dos, et estende ses bras; et puis presse le leu forment a ta palme, et elle revenra; puis met sus l’emplaustre et lou bendeil, et l’estraint;	And the restoration is that the patient lies supine on his back and extends his arms; then presses the area firmly with your palm, and it will return; then place the splint and bandage on top and hold it.
et li chiez qui est devers lou coute ne puet desaluer; se poc non, et se il desalue aucune fois, si le ramoinne a son leu, si com nos avons dit; puis met sus l’emplaustre et le bendeil, et l’estraint, et coumande au malaide qu’il se repose tant qu’il soit sanez;	And the head that is towards the side cannot dislocate; if it does, and if it dislocates once, reset it to its place as we have said; then place the splint and bandage on top and hold it, and instruct the patient to rest until he is well.
et ensi meisme est ramenez li chiés de l’espale, quant il est desevrez de son leu.	And similarly, the head of the shoulder is brought back when it is dislocated from its place.
de la dislocation de l’espaule	When the shoulder is dislocated, it must be reduced first.
Saiches que li espaule n’est desaluee fuer que selonc .iij. manieres: de coi l’une est qu’ele desalue a la partie de l’assele au desoz; et li seconde est a la partie dou pis; et par aventure desalue a la partie desus, et ceu avient poc;	The shoulder can only be dislocated in four ways: the first way is when it dislocates to the hollow below the armpit; the second way is at the side of the hip; and sometimes it can dislocate above as well, but this rarely happens.
et ne desalue mie derrier por l’espaule, et ne desalue mie dedens por les ners; et plusors fois desalue desoz vers l’assele, meismement a ces qui ont poc de char, car a ces saut ele fuer hastanment; a ces qui ont assez char, saut ele a poines, et rentre a poines.	The shoulder does not dislocate behind or within the nerves, and it rarely dislocates inward towards the back, especially in people with little fat, because it jumps out quickly; however, in people with enough fat, it jumps out slowly and returns slowly.
Et par aventure avient a aucuns homes percussion ou casseure, et enfle li espaule d’un aposteme chaut, et cuide qu’elle est desaluee par ceu.	And sometimes it happens to some men that they get struck or broken, and the shoulder swells with a hot abscess, and they think it is dislocated by this.
Il covient donques que tu l’esprueves, tant que tu en soies certains; et adonques encomence la cure.	Therefore, you should verify it, as long as you are certain; and then begin the treatment.
Et est conue li dislocations quant il est aval vers l’assele, et met difference entre l’espaule malade et la saine, et tu troveras entre lor diversiteit manifeste;	And it is known that dislocation occurs when it moves towards the inner part of the shoulder, and you should distinguish between the sick shoulder and the healthy one, and you will find a clear difference between them.
et troveras au chief de l’espaule une fosse, et desoz l’assele au tochier le chief de l’espaule, ausi com se ce soit uns oes; et ne puet li malaides ramener sa main a son neis, ne movoir de nulz movemens;	You will find a hollow at the top of the shoulder and under the inner side of the shoulder near its top, like an eye socket; and the sick person cannot return their hand to their body, nor can they make any movement.
et ausi, s’elle est desaluee en haut, si n’est mie occultee, car tu le trueves manifestement au tochier;	And likewise, if it is dislocated upwards, it should not be hidden, for you will find it clearly on the surface;
et ceste maniere de dislocation n’est mie fors a ramener, quant elle est novele, ou se li enfes est malaides.	This method of dislocation is not only to reset when it is new, but also when the child is ill.
Et li maniere est que li ministres lieve la main dou malaide en haut, puis met tes peuchas desoz l’assele, et lieve la jointure a force en haut au leu; et li ministres lieve la main, et l’estende en haut, pues le mette desoz; si venra hastanment.	The method is that the minister lifts the patient's hand upwards, then places their thumbs under the dislocated joint and pulls it upwards forcefully to its place; and the minister lifts the hand, extending it upward, then places it back in; it will come quickly.
Et s’elle ne vient si com nos avons dit em mains jors aprés, si covient ke li malaides soit baigniez en aigue chaude; et li amenistre arosement mollifiant et assouajant, si com decoction de altee et de fenugrec et de mellilote en aigue, et soit amenistree;	And if it does not come as we have said in the hand within a few days, then the patient should be bathed in hot water; and bring a soothing and calming ointment made from decotion of althea, fenugreek and melilot in hot water, and apply it.
puis soit sovinez li malaides sus son dos, et mette on desoz l’assele un sto de lainne igal, ne trop mol ne trop dur, puis mette li mires son talon sus le sto, et lieve le chief de l’espaule vertuousement, et traie la main dou malaide;	Then let the patient lean forward on his back, and place a strip of linen equal in length underneath the affected shoulder, neither too soft nor too hard, then put the hand of the healer under the linen and carefully lift the head of the shoulder, pulling the patient's arm gently.
et uns autres ministres teigne lou chief dou malaide, si qu’il ne se mueve aval; celle espaule revient tout maintenant, et se tu vues si le ramoinne selonc ceste maniere:	And another servant ties the patient's head so that it does not move downwards; this shoulder will return immediately, and if you see that it dislocates again in this way:
et est que tu faices estre present .i. home qui soit plus grans que li malaides; et soit drois devers lou costeit, et boute s’espaule desoz l’assele dou malaide, et lieve l’assele en haut, si que li malaides pende en l’ar;	and it is that you have a man who is larger than the patient present; he should be straight towards the affected side, and push the shoulder of the patient down under the affected shoulder and lift the affected shoulder upwards so that the patient hangs in the air.
et uns autres ministres traie la main dou malaide aval devers lou ventre. Et se li malaides est trop legiers, si pent avec lui aucune chose pesant, et li dislocation revient maintenant.	And another assistant draws the hand of the patient towards the stomach. If the patient is too light, he can hold something heavy with him so that the dislocation returns immediately.
Et le ramoinne on ausi en autre maniere: et est c’on fiche .i. lonc tison en terre, dont li chiés soit ausi reons com .i. pistal, et ne soit ne trop gros ne trop graile;	And one resets it in another way: and this is done by inserting a long thorn into the ground so that the head is as round as a pea, neither too big nor too small;
puis soit mis desoz lou malaide, mais k’il ait drapelz souef sus, et li malaides soit estans dou lonc dou fust; puis soit estendue sa main aval d’autre part forment, et li jointure revenra en son leu hastanment;	Then it should be placed under the patient, but with soft cloth underneath, and the patient should be standing tall; then his hand should be stretched out flat on the other side, and the joint will return to its place quickly.
et s’elle ne vuet revenir por toutes ces choses que nos avons dit, si fai ceste cure: pren .i. tison de .ij. bras de grant et .iiij. dois de large, qui ait le chief reont por mues entrer em parfont desoz l’assele, selonc ceste forme:	and if it does not want to return due to all these things that we have said, do this cure: take one tision of two arms length and four fingers width, which has its head rounded for easy insertion into the anus, according to this form:
puis lie sus le chief dou fust drapelz souez, que li fust ne blece lou malaide, puis le met desoz l’assele dou malaide; et estende som bras sus le fust dou lonc, et lie l’ajutoire sus le fust, et lou bras au chief de la main, puis met le bras sus .i. eschillon d’une eschiele dou large, et soit estendue li mains aval, et soit laissiez li cors pendans d’autre part: li jointure reva ens maintenant.	then put the head of the rod wrapped in cloth on top, so that it does not hurt the patient, then place it inside the anus of the patient; extend one arm above the rod, and hold the instrument above the rod, and the forearm at the end of the hand, then place the forearm on a small stone of large width, and let the hands hang down below, and let the body hang down from another side: the joint will return in the meantime.
Et quant elle est ens, en quel maniere que ce soit, si covient que tu mettes desoz l’assele une spere de laine igal, puis met l’emplaustre aparilliet de poudre dou molin, avec encens et aubun d’uef, sus toute l’espaule et entor, puis l’estrain desoz l’assele avenanment, et torne le liien sus l’emplaustre, et embraice la main a son col, et soit li mains demorans ensi.	And when it is inside, in whatever manner it may be, it is necessary that you put a spherical piece of linen equal to the size of the instrument, then apply the plaster made of milled powder, with incense and egg white, all over the shoulder and around, then tighten it below the anus appropriately, turn the string around the instrument, and bind the hand to its neck, and let the hands remain in this position.
Et covient qu’il menjuce poc, tant que li membres soit confortez, car il sanera plus tost; et puis menjuce plus aprés .v. jors ou .vij., et le mueve; et s’il est fermeis et il n’est mollifiez, si est sanez.	And it must be fed little by little, until the limb is comforted, for it will heal faster; and then feed more after 5 or 7 days, and move it; and if it becomes firm and is not softened, it is healed.
Et se li jointure est fuer de leu por moistor que i est venue, ou por autre cause, si covient que tu i aministres cauteres a iij. pertus, si com il est mis devant ou chapistre des cauteres.	If the joint is dislocated due to moisture that has come or for other reason, you must administer cauteries at three places, as it is described in the chapter on cauteries.
Et se tu fais tout ceu, et il deslie aprés .vij. jors, et li jointure ne se tient, et ne puet lever som bras amont, adonc saiches que li nerf au chief de l’espaule sont copeit ou estendut ou amollis; et saiches que li jointure n’iert jamais fichie en son leu.	If you do all this and it dislocates again after 7 days, and the joint does not hold, and cannot lift its arm upwards, then know that the nerve at the head of the shoulder is severed or stretched or softened; and know that the joint will never be set in its place.
Li dislocation qui est devers lou pis, et les mameles, ou derrier, si est faite par impulsion, et estendement de mains, et i aministre on autre lieure; et cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	The dislocation which is towards the hip, and limbs, whether front or back, is made by force, and extension of hands, and some other means are administered; and it is treated until it heals.
Et se aprés la sanation vient grietez au membre, et tardemens em movement, si use li malaides bain maintes fois, tant que celle grietez soit alegie, et reviegne a sa premiere nature.	And after healing comes stiffness in the limb, and late movement, the patient should use hot baths many times, until the stiffness is alleviated, and it returns to its original state.
de la dislocation dou coute	of the dislocation cost
Saiches que li jointure dou coute est desaluee a poinnes, et a poinnes revient; et s’est desaluee de toutes pars, et meismement devant et derrier, et li dislocations n’est mie reponue, car on la voit bien et sent bien; et desalue selonc chescune figure.	Know that the joint of the thumb is dislocated at the knuckle, and it comes back at the knuckle; and if it has been dislocated from all sides, both front and back, and the dislocation is not corrected, for it can be clearly seen and felt; and it dislocates according to each shape.
Et quant tu joins le coute malaide avec lou sain, si le pues veoir apertement. Car li jointure est chevee, et ne puet ploier lou bras, ne touchier son espaule a tout.	And when you join the thumb of the patient with the healthy one, make sure it can be clearly seen. For the joint is dislocated, and cannot bend the arm nor touch the shoulder at all.
Et covient que tu le ramoinnes ainsois que apostemes chaus i viegne, car se apostemes chaus i venoit, si seroit grief li ramener; et par aventure ne puet estre ramenez dou tout en tout, meismement quant ele est au derrier; si vaut pis que les autres dislocations, et est de plus grant dolor, et par aventure i vient li mors.	And you must reset it in such a way that the abscess does not come back, for if an abscess comes back, it would be difficult to reset; and it may not be possible to reset it entirely, especially when it is at the back; it is worse than other dislocations, and causes greater pain, and perhaps death.
Et li restauration si est, quant elle est telz c’on la puet ramener, que tu li estendes sa main a tes .ij. mains; et ses bras soit espandus, et les mains dou mire selonc le coute entor, desor et desoz, et boute la jointure a ses peuchas ensamble, ou a la racine de sa palme, tant qu’ele reviegne a son leu.	And the restoration is, when it can be returned to its state, you extend your hand towards his two hands; and his arms should be extended, and his hands facing each other according to the cut around, above and below, and push the joint at his fleshy parts together, or at the root of his palm, until it returns to its place.
Et se li dislocations est au devant, si revient quant il double sa main a sa main, et fier de la racine de la palme lou coute qui est desaluez.	If the dislocation is in front, it returns when you fold your hand over your hand, and press the root of the palm that is dislocated.
Et s’il ne vuet revenir au leu, si aministre fort extension; et est que dui ministre estendent le bras, et le teignent dui ministre, si qu’il ne se mueve a l’estension; puis torne le bras de chescune part, puis que tu as envoloupeit un drapeil double lonc et large;	If it does not return to its place, administer strong extension; and it is that two people extend the arm, and they grip it with two hands so that it does not move during the extension; then turn the arm from both sides, and when you have wrapped a cloth of double length and width around it;
et quant li mires a jointe la jointure a sa main, si l’oigne d’aucun oile por amolir la jointure, puis boute la jointure forment, tant qu’ele reviegne;	And when the master joins the joint with his hand, he should oil it to soften the joint, then press the joint together until it returns to its place.
et quant elle est au leu, si met sus emplaustre sec avec aubun d’uef, et l’estrain forment, et pent le bras au col dou malaide, et le laisse aucuns jors, puis le deslie.	And when it is in its place, he puts on a plaster made with egg white and binds it, then ties the arm to the neck of the patient for some days, then releases it.
Et se li jointure est ferme en son leu, si deslie lou liien, et le laisse; et se tu vois que li jointure n’estrigne bien, si rencomence l’emplaustre et lou lien, et le laisse ensi aucuns jors, tant qu’il soit fermement mis; puis le deslie.	If the joint is closed in its place, release the bindings and leave it; if you see that the joint is not binding well, renew the plaster and bindings, and leave it like this for some days until it is firmly set; then release it.
Et se il sent grieteit aprés le ramenement de la jointe, et elle se muet, si le baigne et frote bellement, et presse tant qu’il soit assouagiez; ou tu met sus la jointure une naige de mouton grasse, puis la laisse .i. jor et une nuit, puis l’oste, et lou fai entrer ou bain;	And if it feels sore after the rejoining of the joint and it swells, bathe and rub it well, and press until it is soothed; or place a sheep's fat pad on the jointure, then leave it for one day and one night, then remove it, and let it enter bath.
et quant il sue, se li frote la jointure tempreement, puis remet la naige sus, et puis entre ou bain; et ensi fai .ij. fois ou .iij., tant qu’il soit sanez; et se tu vues, si met sus fien de vaiche moiste chaufeit avec burre, et l’estrain sus; si revenra a sa disposition.	And when it oozes, rub the jointure gently, then place the fat pad back on, and then enter bath; and do so two or three times until it is healed; and if you see, place warm damp sheep's wool with butter on it and hold it there; it will return to its position.
li dislocation de la main	The dislocation of the hand
Li jointure de la main desalue, et li revenue est legiere, plus que les autres jointures Toutevoie, il la covient ramener au leu hastanment, en l’oure meisme qu’ele est desaluee, ainsois que li leus soit enflez, ou qu’il i viegne aposteme chaut.	The dislocation of the wrist occurs easily and more so than other joints; therefore, it must be returned to its place promptly, immediately when it is dislocated, before the muscles become swollen or an abscess forms in the wound.
Et li ramenemens si est que tu mettes la main malaide sus une tauble, et estende li ministres la main, et li mires la mette igal, ensi que il mette sa paume sus l’aparance de la jointure, et la boute tant qu’elle reviegne.	Then the repositioning is to place the affected hand on a table, and extend the fingers of the minister (the one performing the procedure), and align the hand so that the palm is above the appearance of the jointure, and push until it returns.
Toutevoie, il covient que vos regardez s’il est bien a leu; adonc mette li malaides lou dos de sa main sus une tauble a l’estension et au ramenement.	In addition, you must ensure that it is properly placed; then position the patient's hand, face down on a table for extension and repositioning.
Et se li dislocations est au dos de la main, si mette li malaides son dos de sa main sus la tauble, et li mires mette sa main sus cele aparance de la jointure. S’elle revient maintenant, c’est bien.	And if the dislocation is at the back of the hand, place the patient's hand on the table, and have them put their hand above it over the appearance of the joint. If it returns now, that is good.
Se ce non, si l’estrain d’emplaustres apaisans apostemes chaus, et lou laisse ensi sens rencomencier.	If not, press plasters or hot poultices to the abscesses and let them rest for a while.
Et s’il ne le puet soffrir, et tu ne la pues mettre au leu aprés aucuns jors, si demore li jointure torte;	If he cannot bear it and you are unable to put it back in place after any number of days, the dislocated joint remains.
et ne nuist niant au malaide fuer que tant que li mains est amoillie, et ne puet estraindre aucune chose a tout: adonc saiches que li nerf sont copez, ou li artere; si n’i a autre engien fuer que d’estraindre par cautere delez le cas, et par aventure n’i vaut autre chose.	And it is not necessary for the sick person to endure fire more than when his hand is disabled and cannot tighten anything: therefore know that the nerves are cut, or the arteries; if there is no other means of force except by tightening through fire cautery in such a case, then it serves nothing else.
Et quant li mains est au leu, si met sus l’emplaustre que nos avons dit, puis l’estrain et le laisse .v. jors, puis le deslie et laisse ensi.	And when the hand is at the joint, place it in the plaster that we have mentioned, then tighten and leave for 5 days, then untie and leave so.
Et s’il ne la puet bien movoir, et il i a aucune grieteit, si la moille d’aigue chaude, et le frote tant qu’il soit sanez.	If it cannot move well and there is no inflammation, moisten with warm water and rub until it heals.
de la dislocation des dois de la main	About the dislocation of the fingers of the hand
Aucune fois sont desaluez li doi de la main a chescune part, aucune fois au dos de la palme ou au ventre;	Sometimes the fingers of the hand are dislocated on both sides, sometimes at the back of the palm or the palm.
adonques estent le doi, et boute la dislocation a tes pouchés tant qu’il reviegne, puis sostien lou chief dou doi, et le pent vers la partie ou il est desjoins;	Then you should extend the finger and push back the dislocation until it returns, then hold the finger's head, and pull it towards the part where it is disjointed.
et le laisse .ij. jors, et puis le met igal celui jor; et de nut le lie, si com nos avons dit, et lou deslie de jor, et lou fai movoir, et le relie la nut; et fai ce sovent, tant qu’il soit estroit,	and leave it for 2 days, and then straighten it on the third day; and bind it as we have said, and untie it from time to time, and make it move, and tie it again; and do this often until it becomes tight.
et tout ausi fai, se il est desaluez au ventre de la main, et fai si com tu as fait ci devant, tant qu’il soit sanez; et tout ausi fai, quant il est desaluez d’autre part.	And similarly, if it is dislocated from the stomach of the hand, do as you have done before, until it is healed; and similarly, when it is dislocated from another place.
dou desaluement de l’eschinee dou dos	the dislocation of the vertebrae in the back
Quant l’eschinee dou dos ou dou col est desaluee, ou il en i a plusors desaluees, si n’i a point de cure, car li mors haste le malaide.	When the vertebrae of the back or neck are dislocated, where there is none to cure, death quickly follows the patient.
Et li signes si est que li egestions saut fuer sens volunteit, ne ne la puet tenir, et maintes fois sont mollifiez aucun membre, ou les .ij. cuixes ou li dui bras ou .j.	And the signs are that the excretions jump involuntarily and cannot be held, and many times a limb becomes softened, such as both legs or both arms or one of them.
Et maintes fois se muet li eschinee a iiij. pars; celle qui se muet au derrier si est apelee «gilbositez»:	And often the spine is silent at the fourth part, which is called "kyphosis":
li cure si est que tu rewarde se li gilbositez est venue d’enfance: si n’i ait point de cure ne de sanation dou tot.	the treatment is that you watch if kyphosis has come from childhood; if it has not yet had any cure or healing, it will never do so.
Et celle que vient de cheoir ou de percussions ou de semblans choses, dirent li ancien manieres de cures par grans paroles, ou il n’a mie en toutes grant profit;	And that which comes from falling or blows or similar things, the old ways of treatment used to speak in great words, where there is no benefit in all.
mais je l’ai abregiet selonc mon entention, et ai formez estrumens en diverses manieres.	But I have bandaged it according to my intention, and formed instruments in various ways.
Je dis que en la gilbositeit que vient au pis devant, nen a engien ne santeit;	I say that in the ulceration that comes before, there is neither instrument nor health.
et ausi cele que vient droitement en .ij. costez, et ne puet on curer fuers que celi proprement qui vient au dos, si com je dis;	and similarly the one that comes straight through in both sides, cannot be cured except for the one that comes to the back, as I say.
et est que li malaides soit estendus sus sa faice en .i. leu igal, et ait de l’estrain desoz lui, qu’il ne se blece;	and it is that the patient should lie flat on his back in one even place, and have support underneath him, so he does not bleed.
puis fiche .i. tison au chief en terre forment, et .i. autre as piez, et lie un liien pardesoz les asseles dou malaide, et .i. autre as hainches, et as genous, et as chevilles;	Then insert a needle in the head (into the skull) and one at other limbs, and tie a thread through the patient's shoulders, and another at the hips, and knees, and ankles.
et dui ministre saichent les liiens, li uns au chief et li autres as piez, parmi les .ij. tisons;	And two ministers know the threads, one in the head and others in the limbs, among the two needles.
et soient bien fermez, li tison si com nos avons dit, et li mires mette ses paumes sus l’espinee forment, tant qu’ele reviegne.	and be tightly closed, the needles as we have said, and the mirrors place their hands on the spine formed until it returns.
Et s’elle ne revient par ceste cure, si pren une tauble de .iij. bras de lonc, et chevé desoz la paroit, et li malaides soit en costé, et boute le chief de la tauble desoz la paroit, puis met le mileu de la tauble sus l’espinee;	And if it does not return by this cure, take a beam of 3 cubits in length, and bend it under the patient's side, and place the head of the beam under the side. Then put the middle part of the beam on the spine.
et mette li mires ses piez sus l’autre chief de la tauble, et presse bien, tant qu’il reviegne au leu; et se tu vues, si le fai au tornet qui torne a la main.	And place the limbs on the other end of the beam, press firmly until it returns to its place; and if you see it, do so with the winch that turns by hand.
Et est que tu fiches .ij. tisons au chief dou malaide d’un bras de grant, et devers les piez .ij. autres, et ait entre chescun tison, desoure et desoz, une paume d’espaice de lonc;	And it is that you insert two needles into the head of the patient, one arm's length long, and toward the feet, two others, with a palm's length of space between each needle.
et ait en chescun tison .i. pertus, ou li tornet corre, et soient li tison fermement en terre, si qu’il ne se muevent; et entre chescuns .ij. tisons ait .i. tison tornant, sor coi li liien tornent, et ait en .ij. tornans .ij. petis tisons d’une paume de lonc, por torner le tornet;	And let there be in each splinter or fracture, where the splinters are firmly in the ground so that they do not move; and between two splinters, let there be one turning splinter, like a lien [a kind of tool], and let there be in two turning splinters, two small splinters of a palm's length each, to turn the fracture.
et puis lie lou lien qui est parmi les asseles au tornet devers le chief, et l’autre liien devers les piez a l’autre tornet, et chescuns des ministres torne son tornet a tout le liien, et li maistres mette l’espinee igal si com nos avons dit.	Then tie the lien that is among the bones to the fracture towards the head, and another lien towards the feet at the other fracture, and each of the assistants turns their fracture with all the lien, and the master places the splint evenly as we have said.
Et quant elle est igalz, si met sus emplaustre desiccatif avec abun d’uef, et puis les estoupes, et puis l’estele d’une tablete de .iij. dois de lonc, que porpreigne lou leu de la gilbositeit et la partie de l’espondile sainne, puis le lie d’un liien, si com nos avons dit, et use li malaides de norrissement subtil, tant qu’il soit sanez;	And when it is even, place a plaster with desiccating agent and egg whites on top of it, then bandage it, then place a board of four feet in length along the swelling and the healthy part of the spine, then tie it with a lien as we have said, and use the patient with subtle nursing until he is healed.
et s’aucune chose vient en la fin de la santez, si covient aministrer medicines amollissans et asouajans, avec l’estele que nos avons dit ci devant; et aucune fois i aministre on une piece de plonc,	If any thing comes at the end of health, it is necessary to administer softening and soothing medicines, with the herb that we have mentioned before; and sometimes they administer a piece of wood,
et aucune fois vient li apparance en la derriere spondile dou dos, et cuide on que ce soit dislocations; et c’est li os qui apert, por coi on n’i doit mie avoir presumption: par aventure feroit venir la mort.	And sometimes the appearance of the back spine comes at the end, and it is thought to be a dislocation; but it is the bone that opens, for which reason there should be no presumption: perhaps death will come as a result.
des dislocations de la hainche	the dislocations of the hip
Saiches que as jointures de la hainche et as jointures de l’espaule ne vient fuers que dislocacions soulement, ne n’i vient mie si com as autres jointures; et li jointure de la hainche est desaluee selonc .iiij. parties: dedens et defuer ,et devant et derrier; et plus dedens c’aillors, et poc desalue devant et derrier.	Know that the joints of the hip and shoulder come dislocated only by dislocation, not otherwise like other joints; and the hip joint is dislocated in four parts: within and without, front and back; and more within than out, and less dislocated in front and back.
Et li conoissance de sa dislocations dedens si est que quant on joint la jambe malaide avec la sainne, si est plus longe, et apert plus li malaides genous que li sains, et ne puet li malaides doubler son genoil au feu;	And the knowledge of its dislocation within is that when the sick leg is joined with the healthy one, the thigh is longer and the sick person's thigh joint is more open than the healthy, and the sick person cannot bend their knee in fire.
et est li leus qui est delez enflez d’aposteme chaut, por ceu que li chiés de la cuixe vient lai.	And it is the joint that is swollen with abscess heat, for this reason the thigh joint comes there.
Et li signe de celui cui il vient au defuer, si est que cist accident sont contraire a ces devant.	And the sign of the one who it comes to discharge, is that this incident is contrary to those beforehand.
Et li signes de celui cui avient au devant, si est qu’il estent bien sa jambe selonc l’acomplissement; toutevoie, ne double mie le genoil sens dolor, et s’on le vuet faire aler, si ne puet avant, et retient son urine, et enfle li angre, et quant il vait, si passe sus le talon.	And the signs of the one whose it comes beforehand, is that his leg is well positioned according to completion; however, do not double bend the knee due to pain, and if you wish to make it walk, it cannot move forward, and retains its urine, and when it goes, it passes above the heel.
Et li signes de celui cui il avient derrier, si est qu’il ne puet espandre son genoil, ne doubler, et est celle jambe plus torte de l’autre, et li angre est mollifié, et est li chiés de la cuixe au leu desoz les costes.	And the signs of the one whose it happens behind, is that he cannot extend his knee nor bend it, and this leg is more twisted than the other, and the ankle is softened, and the hip of the calf is in place beneath the ribs.
Li ramenemens de ceste semblance de dislocation si est que tu rewarde se li dislocations est anciainne, et elle demore selonc sa disposition, si n’i a nule cure; et n’i covient mie qu’il ait presumption.	The re-alignments of this type of dislocation are as follows: you examine whether the dislocations are old and remain according to their position without any treatment; and it is not necessary that there should be any presumption.
Et en celi dont li dislocation est fresche, et c’est des .iiij. manieres de dislocation, si te haste que tu tornes la jointe, et l’esten dedens et defuer, et la muef a destre et senestre; par aventure si revenra, et n’a mestier d’autre cure.	And in the one whose dislocation is recent, and it is of the four types of dislocation, you hasten to return the joint, pushing it inward and outward, moving it left and right; by chance if it returns, there is no need for further treatment.
Et s’il ne revient en ceste maniere, si covient que tu apareilles .i. ministre fort, et esten la jambe fort a .ij. mains, ou a .i. liien que soit liiez sus lou genoil;	And if it does not return in this manner, then you must arrange for a strong assistant, and hold the leg firmly with two hands, or one linked above the knee;
et uns autres ministres estende sa main desus en teil maniere qu’il boute ses mains desoz ses asseles, puis l’estrigne d’un souef liien sus la cuixe; et uns autres tigne lou chief dou liien;	and another attendant extends his hand over it in such a way that he pushes his hands under the knees, then tightens a strong rope above the thigh; and another holds the head with the rope;
et estendent amont et aval tuit a une fois, tant que li malaide soit levez de terre a une fois, et demoure pendans.	and they all pull up and down at once, until the patient is raised from the ground once, and remains hanging.
Ceste maniere d’estension si est commune as .iiij. semblances, et se li dislocation est revenue, si com nos avons dit, c’est bien.	This method of extension is common for the four similar cases, and if the dislocation returns, as we have said, it is well.
Se ceu non, si covient mettre cure a sa semblance. Quant li dislocations est au pardedens, si covient que tu sovines le malaide sus son costeit sain, puis met le liien sus la racine de la cuixe, et le leu qui est desoz l’angre, puis estent le liien en haut devers l’angre, et devers la forcele;	If the head is not (dislocated), treatment should be applied to its condition. When dislocation occurs at the shoulders, you must place the patient on his healthy side, then tie a rope around the thigh, and attach it to the root of the pelvis, and pull it up towards the angle (shoulder joint) and towards the forceps (humerus).
puis preigne uns autres ministres ses bras, et embraice le gros leu de la cuixe malaide, et l’estende au defuer forment: si revenra a son leu maintenant; et ceste maniere de dislocation est plus legiere des autres.	Then take another attendant and grasp the large thigh of the affected shoulder, and extend it in a wide-open manner: it will return to its place now; and this method of dislocation is easier than others.
Et se tu ne la pues serrer en ceste maniere que nos avons dit, si covient que tu lies les .ij. piés dou malaide ensamble d’un fort liien souef sus les .ij. talons, et sus les .ij. genous, et soit li jambe malaide estendue .ij. dois plus que li autres;	And if you cannot tie it in this way as we have said, then you must bind the feet of the patient together with a strong rope above the heels and knees, and the affected leg should be extended two feet more than the others;
puis soit pendus sus le chief d’un fust, et soit en sus de terre .ij. bras de lonc; puis comande a .j. ministre qu’il embraice le chief de la cuixe, et soit uns autres ministres pendans avec le malaide, qui embraice forment la cuixe, car li jointure revient maintenant hastanment.	Then let the patient be hung by the neck from a post, and be above the ground by two long arms; then command one minister to embrace the thigh, and let another minister hold with the patient, who will in turn embrace the thigh, as the joints are returning quickly now.
